Were there no practical uniformities in the environment, there would be no economy and only error in the human habit of accepting foresight for sight. But there are uniformities sufficiently accurate, and the need of economizing attention is so inevitable, that the abandonment of all stereotypes for a wholly innocent approach to experience would impoverish human life.

重要的是刻板印象的性质，以及我们运用刻板印象时的轻信程度。而这些最终取决于构成我们人生哲学的包容性模式。如果我们在这种哲学中假设世界是根据我们拥有的一套代码编纂而成的，那么我们很可能会让我们对正在发生的事情的报道描述一个由我们的代码运行的世界。但如果我们的哲学告诉我们，每个人只是世界的一小部分，他的智力最多只能捕捉到粗糙思想网络中的阶段和方面，那么，当我们使用刻板印象时，我们倾向于知道它们只是刻板印象，轻拿轻放，乐于修改它们。我们还倾向于越来越清楚地认识到我们的想法何时开始，从哪里开始，它们是如何来到我们身边的，我们为什么接受它们。所有有用的历史都是以这种方式防腐的。它使我们能够知道什么童话、什么教科书、什么传统、什么小说、戏剧、图片、短语在这个头脑中植入了一个先入之见，在另一个头脑中植入了另一个先入之见。

What matters is the character of the stereotypes, and the gullibility with which we employ them. And these in the end depend upon those inclusive patterns which constitute our philosophy of life. If in that philosophy we assume that the world is codified according to a code which we possess, we are likely to make our reports of what is going on describe a world run by our code. But if our philosophy tells us that each man is only a small part of the world, that his intelligence catches at best only phases and aspects in a coarse net of ideas, then, when we use our stereotypes, we tend to know that they are only stereotypes, to hold them lightly, to modify them gladly. We tend, also, to realize more and more clearly when our ideas started, where they started, how they came to us, why we accepted them. All useful history is antiseptic in this fashion. It enables us to know what fairy tale, what school book, what tradition, what novel, play, picture, phrase, planted one preconception in this mind, another in that mind.





4

4

那些希望审查艺术的人至少没有低估这种影响。他们通常误解了它，而且几乎总是荒谬地一心想阻止其他人发现任何未经他们批准的东西。但无论如何，就像柏拉图在关于诗人的论证中一样，他们隐约感觉到通过虚构获得的类型往往会被强加于现实。因此，毫无疑问，电影正在稳步建立意象，然后人们在报纸上读到的文字会唤起这些意象。在整个人类的经验中，没有任何东西可以像电影一样帮助人们想象。如果一个佛罗伦萨人想想象圣徒，他可以去他教堂的壁画，在那里他可以看到乔托为那个时代标准化的圣徒形象。如果一个雅典人想想象诸神，他会去寺庙。但描绘的物体数量并不多。而在东方，第二条诫命的精神被广泛接受，对具体事物的描绘甚至更加贫乏，也许正是因为这个原因，实际决策的能力才大大减弱。然而，在西方世界，在过去几个世纪里，世俗描述的数量和范围有了巨大的增长，文字图片、叙事、插图叙事，最后是电影，也许还有有声电影。

Those who wish to censor art do not at least underestimate this influence. They generally misunderstand it, and almost always they are absurdly bent on preventing other people from discovering anything not sanctioned by them. But at any rate, like Plato in his argument about the poets, they feel vaguely that the types acquired through fiction tend to be imposed on reality. Thus there can be little doubt that the moving picture is steadily building up imagery which is then evoked by the words people read in their newspapers. In the whole experience of the race there has been no aid to visualization comparable to the cinema. If a Florentine wished to visualize the saints, he could go to the frescoes in his church, where he might see a vision of saints standardized for his time by Giotto. If an Athenian wished to visualize the gods he went to the temples. But the number of objects which were pictured was not great. And in the East, where the spirit of the second commandment was widely accepted, the portraiture of concrete things was even more meager, and for that reason perhaps the faculty of practical decision was by so much reduced. In the western world, however, during the last few centuries there has been an enormous increase in the volume and scope of secular description, the word picture, the narrative, the illustrated narrative, and finally the moving picture and, perhaps, the talking picture.

如今，照片对想象力具有某种权威，就像昨天的印刷文字和更早之前的口语一样。它们看起来十分真实。我们想象它们直接呈现在我们面前，无需人为干预，它们是可以想象的最不费力的心灵食粮。任何文字描述，甚至任何静止的图片，都需要努力记忆，然后才能在脑海中形成图像。但在屏幕上，观察、描述、报道和想象的整个过程都为你完成了。你只需要保持清醒，你的想象力所追求的结果就会在屏幕上一一呈现，而不需要更多的努力。模糊的想法变得生动起来；比如说，当你看到《一个国家的诞生》时，你对三K党的模糊印象，多亏了格里菲思先生，就变得生动起来了。从历史上看，它可能是一种错误的形象，从道德上看，它可能是一种有害的形象，但它是一种形象，而且我怀疑，任何一个看过这部电影的人，如果不比格里菲思先生更了解三K党，在没有看到那些白骑士的情况下，是否会再次听到这个名字。

Photographs have the kind of authority over imagination to-day, which the printed word had yesterday, and the spoken word before that. They seem utterly real. They come, we imagine, directly to us without human meddling, and they are the most effortless food for the mind conceivable. Any description in words, or even any inert picture, requires an effort of memory before a picture exists in the mind. But on the screen the whole process of observing, describing, reporting, and then imagining, has been accomplished for you. Without more trouble than is needed to stay awake the result which your imagination is always aiming at is reeled off on the screen. The shadowy idea becomes vivid; your hazy notion, let us say, of the Ku Klux Klan, thanks to Mr. Griffiths, takes vivid shape when you see the Birth of a Nation. Historically it may be the wrong shape, morally it may be a pernicious shape, but it is a shape, and I doubt whether anyone who has seen the film and does not know more about the Ku Klux Klan than Mr. Griffiths, will ever hear the name again without seeing those white horsemen.





5

5

因此，当我们谈论一群人的思想，法国人的思想，军国主义者的思想，布尔什维克的思想时，我们很容易陷入严重的混乱，除非我们同意将本能的本能与刻板印象、模式和公式区分开来，而这些刻板印象、模式和公式在建立本土性格所适应和响应的精神世界中起着决定性的作用。没有做出这种区分，就会导致大量关于集体思想、民族精神和种族心理的胡言乱语。可以肯定的是，刻板印象可能在每一代中从父母传给孩子，如此一致和权威，以至于它几乎看起来像是一个生物学事实。在某些方面，正如沃拉斯先生所说，我们可能确实在生物学上寄生于我们的社会遗产。但肯定没有任何科学证据能让任何人争辩说，人们生来就具有他们出生的国家的政治习惯。如果一个国家的政治习惯都相同，那么首先要寻找解释的地方就是托儿所、学校和教堂，而不是群体思想和民族灵魂所占据的那个边缘地带。除非你完全看不到父母、教师、牧师和叔叔们传承下来的传统，否则将政治差异归咎于种质是一种最糟糕的错误。

And so when we speak of the mind of a group of people, of the French mind, the militarist mind, the bolshevik mind, we are liable to serious confusion unless we agree to separate the instinctive equipment from the stereotypes, the patterns, and the formulae which play so decisive a part in building up the mental world to which the native character is adapted and responds. Failure to make this distinction accounts for oceans of loose talk about collective minds, national souls, and race psychology. To be sure a stereotype may be so consistently and authoritatively transmitted in each generation from parent to child that it seems almost like a biological fact. In some respects, we may indeed have become, as Mr. Wallas says, biologically parasitic upon our social heritage. But certainly there is not the least scientific evidence which would enable anyone to argue that men are born with the political habits of the country in which they are born. In so far as political habits are alike in a nation, the first places to look for an explanation are the nursery, the school, the church, not in that limbo inhabited by Group Minds and National Souls. Until you have thoroughly failed to see tradition being handed on from parents, teachers, priests, and uncles, it is a solecism of the worst order to ascribe political differences to the germ plasm.

可以尝试性地、谦虚地概括出同一教育和经验类别的比较差异。然而，即便如此，这也是一项棘手的任务。因为几乎没有两个经历是完全相同的，即使是同一个家庭的两个孩子也是如此。大儿子永远不会有做小儿子的经历。因此，在我们能够忽略教养差异之前，我们必须保留对自然差异的判断。就像在知道哪块土地在拉布拉多，哪块土地在爱荷华之前，通过比较它们的产量来判断两块土地的生产力，无论是经过耕种和富饶，还是被耗尽，还是任其荒芜。

It is possible to generalize tentatively and with a decent humility about comparative differences within the same category of education and experience. Yet even this is a tricky enterprise. For almost no two experiences are exactly alike, not even of two children in the same household. The older son never does have the experience of being the younger. And therefore, until we are able to discount the difference in nurture, we must withhold judgment about differences of nature. As well judge the productivity of two soils by comparing their yield before you know which is in Labrador and which in Iowa, whether they have been cultivated and enriched, exhausted, or allowed to run wild.

第七章

CHAPTER VII

以刻板印象作为防御

STEREOTYPES AS DEFENSE





1

1

除了节省精力之外，还有一个原因导致我们经常固守刻板印象，而我们本可以追求更公正的愿景。刻板印象体系可能是我们个人传统的核心，是我们在社会中地位的捍卫者。

THERE is another reason, besides economy of effort, why we so often hold to our stereotypes when we might pursue a more disinterested vision. The systems of stereotypes may be the core of our personal tradition, the defenses of our position in society.

它们是一幅有序的、或多或少一致的世界图景，我们的习惯、品味、能力、舒适和希望都已适应了这个世界。它们可能不是完整的世界图景，但它们是我们适应的一个可能世界的图景。在那个世界里，人和物都有它们熟悉的位置，做着某些预期的事情。我们在那里感到宾至如归。我们融入其中。我们是其中的一员。我们知道周围的路。在那里，我们发现了熟悉的、正常的、可靠的事物的魅力；它的凹槽和形状就是我们习惯的地方。虽然在我们把自己折成那个模子之前，我们已经放弃了许多可能诱惑我们的东西，但一旦我们牢牢地融入其中，它就会像一双旧鞋一样合身。

They are an ordered, more or less consistent picture of the world, to which our habits, our tastes, our capacities, our comforts and our hopes have adjusted themselves. They may not be a complete picture of the world, but they are a picture of a possible world to which we are adapted. In that world people and things have their well-known places, and do certain expected things. We feel at home there. We fit in. We are members. We know the way around. There we find the charm of the familiar, the normal, the dependable; its grooves and shapes are where we are accustomed to find them. And though we have abandoned much that might have tempted us before we creased ourselves into that mould, once we are firmly in, it fits as snugly as an old shoe.

因此，难怪任何对刻板印象的扰乱都像是对宇宙基础的攻击。这是对我们 宇宙基础的攻击，当事关重大时，我们不会轻易承认我们的宇宙和宇宙之间存在任何区别。如果一个世界变成我们所尊敬的人不配，而我们所鄙视的人却高贵，这令人心烦意乱。如果我们的优先顺序不是唯一可能的顺序，就会出现无政府状态。因为如果温顺的人真的应该继承地球，如果第一应该是最后，如果只有那些没有罪的人才能扔石头，如果你只把凯撒的东西交给凯撒，那么对于那些把生活安排得好像这些格言不真实的人来说，自尊的基础就会动摇。刻板印象的模式不是中性的。它不仅仅是一种用秩序来取代现实中繁华喧闹的混乱的方式。它不仅仅是一条捷径。它是所有这些，还有更多的东西。它是我们自尊的保证；它是我们对自身价值、自身地位和自身权利的自我认知在世人的投射。因此，刻板印象中充满了与之相关的情感。它们是我们传统的堡垒，在它的防线后面，我们可以继续在我们所处的位置上感到安全。

No wonder, then, that any disturbance of the stereotypes seems like an attack upon the foundations of the universe. It is an attack upon the foundations of our universe, and, where big things are at stake, we do not readily admit that there is any distinction between our universe and the universe. A world which turns out to be one in which those we honor are unworthy, and those we despise are noble, is nerve-racking. There is anarchy if our order of precedence is not the only possible one. For if the meek should indeed inherit the earth, if the first should be last, if those who are without sin alone may cast a stone, if to Caesar you render only the things that are Caesar's, then the foundations of self-respect would be shaken for those who have arranged their lives as if these maxims were not true. A pattern of stereotypes is not neutral. It is not merely a way of substituting order for the great blooming, buzzing confusion of reality. It is not merely a short cut. It is all these things and something more. It is the guarantee of our self-respect; it is the projection upon the world of our own sense of our own value, our own position and our own rights. The stereotypes are, therefore, highly charged with the feelings that are attached to them. They are the fortress of our tradition, and behind its defenses we can continue to feel ourselves safe in the position we occupy.





2

2

例如，公元前四世纪，亚里士多德在面对日益增长的怀疑时，为奴隶制辩护，当时雅典的奴隶与自由公民几乎没有区别。齐默恩先生引用了《老寡头》中一段有趣的文字，解释了对奴隶的优待。“假设公民可以殴打奴隶，那么雅典人经常会被误认为是奴隶或外来人，并遭到殴打；因为雅典人的衣着并不比奴隶或外来人好，在外表上也没有任何优越性。”这种缺乏区别的现象自然会导致奴隶制的瓦解。如果自由人和奴隶长得一样，那么有什么理由对他们区别对待呢？亚里士多德在《政治学》第一卷中着手消除的就是这种混淆。他凭着敏锐的直觉明白，要证明奴隶制的合理性，就必须教会希腊人一种看待 奴隶的方式，使之与奴隶制的延续相适应。

When, for example, in the fourth century B. C., Aristotle wrote his defense of slavery in the face of increasing skepticism, the Athenian slaves were in great part indistinguishable from free citizens Mr. Zimmern quotes an amusing passage from the Old Oligarch explaining the good treatment of the slaves. "Suppose it were legal for a slave to be beaten by a citizen, it would frequently happen that an Athenian might be mistaken for a slave or an alien and receive a beating;—since the Athenian people is not better clothed than the slave or alien, nor in personal appearance is there any superiority." This absence of distinction would naturally tend to dissolve the institution. If free men and slaves looked alike, what basis was there for treating them so differently? It was this confusion which Aristotle set himself to clear away in the first book of his Politics. With unerring instinct he understood that to justify slavery he must teach the Greeks a way of seeing their slaves that comported with the continuance of slavery.

因此，亚里士多德说，有些人天生就是奴隶。“那么，他天生就是奴隶，适合成为他人的奴隶，因此他就是这样 。”这句话实际上说的是，任何碰巧是奴隶的人天生就注定要成为奴隶。从逻辑上讲，这种说法毫无价值，但事实上它根本不是一个命题，逻辑与它无关。这是一种刻板印象，或者更确切地说，它是刻板印象的一部分。其余的几乎紧接着就出现了。在断言奴隶感知理性，但没有赋予理性使用能力之后，亚里士多德坚持认为“大自然的意图是让奴隶和自由人的身体彼此不同，一个应该强壮以达到他们必要的目的，而另一个应该直立；对于这种卑微的劳动确实毫无用处，但适合平民生活……很明显，有些人天生自由，而另一些人是奴隶。……”

So, said Aristotle, there are beings who are slaves by nature. "He then is by nature formed a slave, who is fitted to become the chattel of another person, and on that account is so ." All this really says is that whoever happens to be a slave is by nature intended to be one. Logically the statement is worthless, but in fact it is not a proposition at all, and logic has nothing to do with it. It is a stereotype, or rather it is part of a stereotype. The rest follows almost immediately. After asserting that slaves perceive reason, but are not endowed with the use of it, Aristotle insists that "it is the intention of nature to make the bodies of slaves and free men different from each other, that the one should be robust for their necessary purposes, but the other erect; useless indeed for such servile labours, but fit for civil life… It is clear then that some men are free by nature, and others are slaves. …"

如果我们自问亚里士多德的论证到底出了什么问题，我们会发现他一开始就在自己和事实之间筑起了一道巨大的屏障。当他说那些奴隶天生就是奴隶时，他一下子排除了一个致命的问题：那些碰巧是奴隶的人是否天生就是奴隶。因为这个问题会让每一起奴隶制案件都充满疑问。而且，由于身为奴隶这一事实并不能证明一个人注定要成为奴隶，因此就没有确定的检验标准了。因此，亚里士多德完全排除了这种破坏性的怀疑。那些奴隶天生就是奴隶。每个奴隶主都应该把他的动产视为天生的奴隶。当他的眼睛被训练成这样看待他们时，他就会注意到他们从事奴役工作、他们有能力做奴役工作、他们有做奴役工作的肌肉，这些事实证实了他们的奴役性质。

If we ask ourselves what is the matter with Aristotle's argument, we find that he has begun by erecting a great barrier between himself and the facts. When he had said that those who are slaves are by nature intended to be slaves, he at one stroke excluded the fatal question whether those particular men who happened to be slaves were the particular men intended by nature to be slaves. For that question would have tainted each case of slavery with doubt. And since the fact of being a slave was not evidence that a man was destined to be one, no certain test would have remained. Aristotle, therefore, excluded entirely that destructive doubt. Those who are slaves are intended to be slaves. Each slave holder was to look upon his chattels as natural slaves. When his eye had been trained to see them that way, he was to note as confirmation of their servile character the fact that they performed servile work, that they were competent to do servile work, and that they had the muscles to do servile work.

这是完美的刻板印象。其特点是先于理性的使用；是一种感知形式，在数据到达智力之前将某种特征强加于我们感官的数据上。刻板印象就像比肯街上的淡紫色窗玻璃，就像化装舞会上判断客人是否穿着合适的化装的门卫。没有什么比刻板印象更难以接受教育或批评了。它在获取证据的过程中就将自己印在证据上。这就是为什么回国旅行者的记述往往是一个有趣的故事，讲述旅行者在旅途中随身携带的东西。如果他主要带着他的胃口，对瓷砖浴室的热爱，对普尔曼车厢是人类舒适度的极致的坚信，以及对给服务员、出租车司机和理发师小费是合理的信念，但绝不给车站工作人员和引座员小费，那么他的奥德赛之旅将充满美食和劣质美食、洗澡冒险、火车车厢冒险和对金钱的贪婪索求。或者如果他是一个更严肃的人，他可能会在旅行中发现自己身处著名景点。到达基地，偷偷瞥了一眼纪念碑，他埋头阅读贝德克尔，从头到尾读完，然后前往下一个著名景点；就这样带着对欧洲紧凑而有序的印象回来了，被评为一星或两星。

This is the perfect stereotype. Its hallmark is that it precedes the use of reason; is a form of perception, imposes a certain character on the data of our senses before the data reach the intelligence. The stereotype is like the lavender window-panes on Beacon Street, like the door-keeper at a costume ball who judges whether the guest has an appropriate masquerade. There is nothing so obdurate to education or to criticism as the stereotype. It stamps itself upon the evidence in the very act of securing the evidence. That is why the accounts of returning travellers are often an interesting tale of what the traveller carried abroad with him on his trip. If he carried chiefly his appetite, a zeal for tiled bathrooms, a conviction that the Pullman car is the acme of human comfort, and a belief that it is proper to tip waiters, taxicab drivers, and barbers, but under no circumstances station agents and ushers, then his Odyssey will be replete with good meals and bad meals, bathing adventures, compartment-train escapades, and voracious demands for money. Or if he is a more serious soul he may while on tour have found himself at celebrated spots. Having touched base, and cast one furtive glance at the monument, he buried his head in Baedeker, read every word through, and moved on to the next celebrated spot; and thus returned with a compact and orderly impression of Europe, rated one star, or two.

在某种程度上，来自外界的刺激，尤其是印刷品或口头文字，会唤起刻板印象系统的某些部分，因此实际感觉和先入之见会同时占据意识。两者混合在一起，就像我们透过蓝色眼镜看红色，却看到绿色一样。如果我们看到的东西与我们的预期相符，刻板印象就会在未来得到强化，就像一个人事先知道日本人很狡猾，却不幸遇到了两个不诚实的日本人一样。

In some measure, stimuli from the outside, especially when they are printed or spoken words, evoke some part of a system of stereotypes, so that the actual sensation and the preconception occupy consciousness at the same time. The two are blended, much as if we looked at red through blue glasses and saw green. If what we are looking at corresponds successfully with what we anticipated, the stereotype is reinforced for the future, as it is in a man who knows in advance that the Japanese are cunning and has the bad luck to run across two dishonest Japanese.

如果体验与刻板印象相矛盾，就会发生两种情况之一。如果这个人不再具有可塑性，或者某种强大的利益使他很难重新安排他的刻板印象，他就会对矛盾嗤之以鼻，认为这是一个例外，证明了规则，抹黑了证人，发现了某个地方的缺陷，并设法忘记了它。但如果他仍然好奇和开放，新奇的东西就会被纳入画面，并被允许修改它。有时，如果事件足够引人注目，如果他对自己既定的计划感到普遍不舒服，他可能会动摇到不信任所有公认的生活观的程度，并认为事情通常不会像人们通常认为的那样。在极端情况下，尤其是如果他是文学家，他可能会发展出一种颠覆道德经典的激情，把犹大、本尼迪克特·阿诺德或凯撒·博尔吉亚塑造成他故事中的英雄。

If the experience contradicts the stereotype, one of two things happens. If the man is no longer plastic, or if some powerful interest makes it highly inconvenient to rearrange his stereotypes, he pooh- poohs the contradiction as an exception that proves the rule, discredits the witness, finds a flaw somewhere, and manages to forget it. But if he is still curious and open-minded, the novelty is taken into the picture, and allowed to modify it. Sometimes, if the incident is striking enough, and if he has felt a general discomfort with his established scheme, he may be shaken to such an extent as to distrust all accepted ways of looking at life, and to expect that normally a thing will not be what it is generally supposed to be. In the extreme case, especially if he is literary, he may develop a passion for inverting the moral canon by making Judas, Benedict Arnold, or Caesar Borgia the hero of his tale.





3

3

这种刻板印象所起的作用可以从德国关于比利时狙击手的传说中看出。奇怪的是，这些传说首先被一个被称为 Pax 的德国天主教牧师组织驳斥。暴行故事的存在本身并不奇怪，德国人民也乐于相信它们。但令人惊讶的是，一大批保守的爱国德国人早在 1914 年 8 月 16 日就已经开始反驳一系列针对敌人的诽谤，尽管这些诽谤对于抚慰同胞不安的良心具有极大的价值。为什么耶稣会会特别着手摧毁对德国战斗士气如此重要的虚构故事呢？

The role played by the stereotype can be seen in the German tales about Belgian snipers. Those tales curiously enough were first refuted by an organization of German Catholic priests known as Pax. The existence of atrocity stories is itself not remarkable, nor that the German people gladly believed them. But it is remarkable that a great conservative body of patriotic Germans should have set out as early as August 16, 1914, to contradict a collection of slanders on the enemy, even though such slanders were of the utmost value in soothing the troubled conscience of their fellow countrymen. Why should the Jesuit order in particular have set out to destroy a fiction so important to the fighting morale of Germany?

我引用 M. van Langenhove 的叙述：

I quote from M. van Langenhove's account:

“德国军队刚进入比利时，奇怪的谣言就开始流传。这些谣言四处传播，被媒体转载，很快就传遍了整个德国。据说比利时人民在牧师的教唆下 背信弃义地介入了敌对行动；出其不意地袭击了孤立的小分队；向敌人透露了部队的驻地；老人甚至孩子对受伤和手无寸铁的德国士兵犯下了可怕的暴行，挖出了他们的眼睛，割掉了手指、鼻子或耳朵；牧师在布道坛上煽动人们犯下这些罪行，许诺他们将进入天国作为奖赏，他们甚至带头实施了这种野蛮行为。

“公众轻信了这些故事。国家最高权力机构毫不犹豫地欢迎它们，并以权威为它们背书……

“这样一来，德国的舆论就被搅乱了，人们表现出强烈的愤慨，尤其是针对那些被认为对比利时人的暴行负责的牧师…… 德国人 自然而然地将 他们所遭受的愤怒转移到了天主教神职人员身上。 新教徒让旧的宗教仇恨在他们心中重新燃起，并开始攻击天主教徒。一场新的文化斗争 由此展开。

“天主教徒毫不迟疑地对这种敌对态度采取行动。”（斜体字是我加的）

"Hardly had the German armies entered Belgium when strange rumors began to circulate. They spread from place to place, they were reproduced by the press, and they soon permeated the whole of Germany. It was said that the Belgian people, instigated by the clergy , had intervened perfidiously in the hostilities; had attacked by surprise isolated detachments; had indicated to the enemy the positions occupied by the troops; that old men, and even children, had been guilty of horrible atrocities upon wounded and defenseless German soldiers, tearing out their eyes and cutting off fingers, nose or ears; that the priests from their pulpits had exhorted the people to commit these crimes, promising them as a reward the kingdom of heaven, and had even taken the lead in this barbarity.

"Public credulity accepted these stories. The highest powers in the state welcomed them without hesitation and endorsed them with their authority…

"In this way public opinion in Germany was disturbed and a lively indignation manifested itself, directed especially against the priests who were held responsible for the barbarities attributed to the Belgians… By a natural diversion the anger to which they were a prey was directed by the Germans against the Catholic clergy generally. Protestants allowed the old religious hatred to be relighted in their minds and delivered themselves to attacks against Catholics. A new Kulturkampf was let loose.

"The Catholics did not delay in taking action against this hostile attitude." (Italics mine)

或许有人会进行攻击。如果每个愤怒的比利时人都冲到图书馆，打开国际法手册，了解自己是否有权对在街头游荡的可恶的滋扰者进行射击，那将是不可思议的。如果一支从未遭受过炮火的军队不认为每颗射向它的子弹都是未经授权的，因为这很不方便，而且实际上在某种程度上违反了当时构成其唯一战争经验的战争游戏规则，那也同样不可思议。可以想象，更敏感的人会一心想说服自己，他们所针对的人一定是可怕的人。因此，这个传说可能被编造出来，直到它传到审查者和宣传者手中，无论他们是否相信，他们都看到了它的价值，并把它传给了德国平民。他们也不会完全为发现自己所激怒的人是非人类而感到难过。最重要的是，由于传说源自他们的英雄，他们不仅有权相信它，而且如果他们不相信，他们就是不爱国的。

There may have been some sniping. It would be extraordinary if every angry Belgian had rushed to the library, opened a manual of international law, and had informed himself whether he had a right to take potshot at the infernal nuisance tramping through his streets. It would be no less extraordinary if an army that had never been under fire, did not regard every bullet that came its way as unauthorized, because it was inconvenient, and indeed as somehow a violation of the rules of the Kriegspiel, which then constituted its only experience of war. One can imagine the more sensitive bent on convincing themselves that the people to whom they were doing such terrible things must be terrible people. And so the legend may have been spun until it reached the censors and propagandists, who, whether they believed it or not, saw its value, and let it loose on the German civilians. They too were not altogether sorry to find that the people they were outraging were sub-human. And, above all, since the legend came from their heroes, they were not only entitled to believe it, they were unpatriotic if they did not.

但是，由于战争的场景被战争的迷雾所笼罩，人们只能在想象中看到很多东西，因此无法制止和控制。凶残的比利时牧师的传说很快唤起了人们的旧恨。因为在大多数爱国的德国新教徒，尤其是上层阶级的爱国新教徒的心中，俾斯麦的胜利包括与罗马天主教徒的长期争吵。通过交往，比利时牧师成为了牧师，对比利时人的仇恨成为了他们所有仇恨的发泄口。这些德国新教徒所做的和一些美国人一样，在战争的压力下，他们把国外的敌人和国内的所有对手都变成了仇恨的复合对象。他们把内心的所有仇恨都发泄在了德国和门内的匈奴人这个合成的敌人身上。

But where so much is left to the imagination because the scene of action is lost in the fog of war, there is no check and no control. The legend of the ferocious Belgian priests soon tapped an old hatred. For in the minds of most patriotic protestant Germans, especially of the upper classes, the picture of Bismarck's victories included a long quarrel with the Roman Catholics. By a process of association, Belgian priests became priests, and hatred of Belgians a vent for all their hatreds. These German protestants did what some Americans did when under the stress of war they created a compound object of hatred out of the enemy abroad and all their opponents at home. Against this synthetic enemy, the Hun in Germany and the Hun within the Gate, they launched all the animosity that was in them.

当然，天主教徒对暴行故事的抵制是出于防御。它针对的是那些引起对所有天主教徒的仇恨的特定虚构故事，而不仅仅是针对比利时天主教徒。M . van Langenhove 说， 《和平信息》 只具有教会意义，“几乎只关注牧师的应受谴责的行为”。然而，人们不禁想知道，德国天主教徒在得知俾斯麦帝国对他们意味着什么后，他们的脑海中会浮现出什么；以及这种了解与愿意在停战协议中签署帝国死刑令的著名德国政治家是天主教中央党领袖埃茨贝格尔这一事实之间是否存在任何模糊的联系。

The Catholic resistance to the atrocity tales was, of course, defensive. It was aimed at those particular fictions which aroused animosity against all Catholics, rather than against Belgian Catholics alone. The Informations Pax , says M. van Langenhove, had only an ecclesiastical bearing and "confined their attention almost exclusively to the reprehensible acts attributed to the priests." And yet one cannot help wondering a little about what was set in motion in the minds of German Catholics by this revelation of what Bismarck's empire meant in relation to them; and also whether there was any obscure connection between that knowledge and the fact that the prominent German politician who was willing in the armistice to sign the death warrant of the empire was Erzberger, the leader of the Catholic Centre Party.

第八章

CHAPTER VIII

盲点及其价值

BLIND SPOTS AND THEIR VALUE





1

1

我一直在谈论刻板印象而不是理想，因为“理想”这个词通常用于指代我们认为的善、真和美。因此，它暗示着这里有一些东西需要复制或实现。但我们固定印象的储备远不止于此。它包含理想的骗子、理想的坦慕尼政客、理想的沙文主义者、理想的煽动者、理想的敌人。我们刻板印象中的世界不一定是我们希望的世界。它只是我们期望的世界。如果事件相符，就会有一种熟悉感，我们会觉得我们正在随着事件的发展而前进。如果我们是希望没有疑虑的雅典人，我们的奴隶必须是天生的奴隶。如果我们告诉朋友我们在 95 年打了 18 洞高尔夫球，我们会在 110 年打完一场比赛后告诉他们，我们今天不是我们自己。也就是说，我们不认识那个打了 15 杆的笨蛋。

I HAVE been speaking of stereotypes rather than ideals, because the word ideal is usually reserved for what we consider the good, the true and the beautiful. Thus it carries the hint that here is something to be copied or attained. But our repertory of fixed impressions is wider than that. It contains ideal swindlers, ideal Tammany politicians, ideal jingoes, ideal agitators, ideal enemies. Our stereotyped world is not necessarily the world we should like it to be. It is simply the kind of world we expect it to be. If events correspond there is a sense of familiarity, and we feel that we are moving with the movement of events. Our slave must be a slave by nature, if we are Athenians who wish to have no qualms. If we have told our friends that we do eighteen holes of golf in 95, we tell them after doing the course in 110, that we are not ourselves to-day. That is to say, we are not acquainted with the duffer who foozled fifteen strokes.

如果每一代人中没有相对较少的人不断将事物整理、标准化和改进为逻辑系统（即政治经济学法则、政治学原理等），我们大多数人都会通过相当随意和不断变化的各种刻板印象来处理事务。一般来说，当我们写到文化、传统和群体思维时，我们想到的是这些由天才完善的体系。现在，毫无疑问有必要不断研究和批评这些理想化的版本，但历史学家、政治家和宣传人员不能止步于此。因为在历史中起作用的不是天才所制定的系统思想，而是个人头脑中不断变化的模仿、复制品、伪造品、类比和扭曲。

Most of us would deal with affairs through a rather haphazard and shifting assortment of stereotypes, if a comparatively few men in each generation were not constantly engaged in arranging, standardizing, and improving them into logical systems, known as the Laws of Political Economy, the Principles of Politics, and the like. Generally when we write about culture, tradition, and the group mind, we are thinking of these systems perfected by men of genius. Now there is no disputing the necessity of constant study and criticism of these idealized versions, but the historian of people, the politician, and the publicity man cannot stop there. For what operates in history is not the systematic idea as a genius formulated it, but shifting imitations, replicas, counterfeits, analogies, and distortions in individual minds.

因此，马克思主义不一定是卡尔·马克思在《资本论》中所写的内容，而是所有自称是信徒的敌对教派所信仰的任何东西。你无法从福音书中推断出基督教的历史，也无法从宪法中推断出美国的政治历史。你必须遵循的是《资本论》的构想、福音书的宣讲和对宣讲的理解、宪法的解释和执行。因为虽然标准版本和当前版本之间存在相互影响，但正是这些在人们中传播的当前版本影响了他们的行为。

Thus Marxism is not necessarily what Karl Marx wrote in Das Kapital, but whatever it is that all the warring sects believe, who claim to be the faithful. From the gospels you cannot deduce the history of Christianity, nor from the Constitution the political history of America. It is Das Kapital as conceived, the gospels as preached and the preachment as understood, the Constitution as interpreted and administered, to which you have to go. For while there is a reciprocating influence between the standard version and the current versions, it is these current versions as distributed among men which affect their behavior.

一位眼皮和丽莎夫人一样有些疲惫的评论家说：“相对论有望发展成为一种像进化论一样适用于全世界的理论。进化论从一种技术性的生物学假设，变成了几乎所有知识领域工作者的鼓舞人心的指南：风俗习惯、道德、宗教、哲学、艺术、蒸汽机、电车——一切都在‘进化’。” “进化”成为一个非常笼统的术语；它也变得不精确，直到在许多情况下，这个词最初的明确含义已经消失，它所描述的理论被误解。我们有足够的勇气预言相对论的类似发展和命运。目前尚未完全理解的技术物理理论将变得更加模糊和晦涩。历史会重演，相对论就像进化论一样，在其科学方面得到许多可理解但有些不准确的流行阐述后，将开始征服世界的历程。我们认为，到那时，它可能会被称为相对论 。这些较大的应用中的许多无疑将得到证实；有些将是荒谬的，我们想象，相当多的应用将沦为真理。而物理理论，这一巨大增长的种子，将再次成为科学家纯粹的技术关注点。”

"The theory of Relativity," says a critic whose eyelids, like the Lady Lisa's, are a little weary, "promises to develop into a principle as adequate to universal application as was the theory of Evolution. This latter theory, from being a technical biological hypothesis, became an inspiring guide to workers in practically every branch of knowledge: manners and customs, morals, religions, philosophies, arts, steam engines, electric tramways—everything had 'evolved.' 'Evolution' became a very general term; it also became imprecise until, in many cases, the original, definite meaning of the word was lost, and the theory it had been evoked to describe was misunderstood. We are hardy enough to prophesy a similar career and fate for the theory of Relativity. The technical physical theory, at present imperfectly understood, will become still more vague and dim. History repeats itself, and Relativity, like Evolution, after receiving a number of intelligible but somewhat inaccurate popular expositions in its scientific aspect, will be launched on a world-conquering career. We suggest that, by that time, it will probably be called Relativismus . Many of these larger applications will doubtless be justified; some will be absurd and a considerable number will, we imagine, reduce to truisms. And the physical theory, the mere seed of this mighty growth, will become once more the purely technical concern of scientific men."

但是，对于这样一个征服世界的事业，一个想法必须与某种东西相对应，无论这种相对应是多么不精确。伯里教授表明，进步的观念在很长一段时间内仍然是一种推测性的玩物。他写道：“一个新的推测秩序的观念要渗透并影响一个社会的普遍意识，并不容易，除非它已经呈现出一些外在的具体体现，或者得到了一些引人注目的物质证据的推荐。就进步而言，这两个条件在 1820-1850 年期间（在英国）都得到了满足。”最引人注目的证据是由机械革命提供的。“出生于本世纪初的人，在他们三十岁之前，就见证了蒸汽航行的快速发展、城镇和房屋被煤气照亮、第一条铁路的开通。”在普通家庭的意识中，像这样的奇迹形成了他对人类可完善性的信仰的模式。

But for such a world-conquering career an idea must correspond, however imprecisely, to something. Professor Bury shows for how long a time the idea of progress remained a speculative toy. "It is not easy," he writes, "for a new idea of the speculative order to penetrate and inform the general consciousness of a community until it has assumed some external and concrete embodiment, or is recommended by some striking material evidence. In the case of Progress both these conditions were fulfilled (in England) in the period 1820-1850." The most striking evidence was furnished by the mechanical revolution. "Men who were born at the beginning of the century had seen, before they had passed the age of thirty, the rapid development of steam navigation, the illumination of towns and houses by gas, the opening of the first railway." In the consciousness of the average householder miracles like these formed the pattern of his belief in the perfectibility of the human race.

丁尼生在哲学上是个相当正常的人，他告诉我们，当他乘坐从利物浦开往曼彻斯特的第一列火车（1830 年）时，他觉得车轮在凹槽里转动。然后他写下了这样一句话：

Tennyson, who was in philosophical matters a fairly normal person, tells us that when he went by the first train from Liverpool to Manchester (1830) he thought that the wheels ran in grooves. Then he wrote this line:

“让伟大的世界永远在变化的洪流中旋转。”

"Let the great world spin forever down the ringing grooves of change."

于是，一个或多或少适用于利物浦和曼彻斯特之间旅程的概念被推广为“永恒”的宇宙模式。这种模式被其他人所接受，并通过令人眼花缭乱的发明得到强化，使进化论变得乐观起来。当然，正如伯里教授所说，进化论在悲观主义和乐观主义之间是中立的。但它承诺不断变化，世界上可见的变化标志着大自然如此非凡的征服，以至于大众的思想将两者融合在一起。进化论首先出现在达尔文本人身上，然后出现在赫伯特·斯宾塞身上，是一种“走向完美的进步”。

And so a notion more or less applicable to a journey between Liverpool and Manchester was generalized into a pattern of the universe "for ever." This pattern, taken up by others, reinforced by dazzling inventions, imposed an optimistic turn upon the theory of evolution. That theory, of course, is, as Professor Bury says, neutral between pessimism and optimism. But it promised continual change, and the changes visible in the world marked such extraordinary conquests of nature, that the popular mind made a blend of the two. Evolution first in Darwin himself, and then more elaborately in Herbert Spencer, was a "progress towards perfection."





2

2

“进步”和“完美”等词语所代表的刻板印象从根本上来说就是机械发明。而且，从总体上讲，这种刻板印象至今仍然如此。在美国，机械进步的景象给人留下了比在其他地方更深刻的印象，以至于它渗透到了整个道德准则中。美国人几乎可以忍受任何侮辱，除了指责他不进步。无论是拥有悠久的本土血统，还是新移民，美国文明的巨大物质增长总是让他印象深刻。这构成了他看待世界的基本刻板印象：乡村将成为大都市，朴素的建筑将成为摩天大楼，小的将成为大；慢的将成为快的；贫穷的将成为富裕的；少的将成为多的；任何事物都将更加多。

The stereotype represented by such words as "progress" and "perfection" was composed fundamentally of mechanical inventions. And mechanical it has remained, on the whole, to this day. In America more than anywhere else, the spectacle of mechanical progress has made so deep an impression, that it has suffused the whole moral code. An American will endure almost any insult except the charge that he is not progressive. Be he of long native ancestry, or a recent immigrant, the aspect that has always struck his eye is the immense physical growth of American civilization. That constitutes a fundamental stereotype through which he views the world: the country village will become the great metropolis, the modest building a skyscraper, what is small shall be big; what is slow shall be fast; what is poor shall be rich; what is few shall be many; whatever is shall be more so.

当然，并非每个美国人都这样看世界。亨利·亚当斯不是，威廉·艾伦·怀特也不是。但那些在宣扬成功宗教的杂志上被称为美国缔造者的人们却是这样的。他们宣扬进化、进步、繁荣、建设性、美国做事的方式，大概就是这个意思。这很容易让人发笑，但事实上，他们运用了一种非常伟大的人类努力模式。一方面，它采用了一种非个人的标准；另一方面，它采用了一种世俗的标准；第三，它使人们习惯于定量思考。诚然，这种理想混淆了卓越与规模、幸福与速度、人性与机械装置。然而，起作用的动机与任何道德准则都是相同的，而且这些道德准则曾经或将来也会如此。渴望最大、最快、最高，或者如果你是手表或显微镜制造商，渴望最小；简而言之，最高级和“无与伦比的”爱情，本质上可能是一种高尚的激情。

Not every American, of course, sees the world this way. Henry Adams didn't, and William Allen White doesn't. But those men do, who in the magazines devoted to the religion of success appear as Makers of America. They mean just about that when they preach evolution, progress, prosperity, being constructive, the American way of doing things. It is easy to laugh, but, in fact, they are using a very great pattern of human endeavor. For one thing it adopts an impersonal criterion; for another it adopts an earthly criterion; for a third it is habituating men to think quantitatively. To be sure the ideal confuses excellence with size, happiness with speed, and human nature with contraption. Yet the same motives are at work which have ever actuated any moral code, or ever will. The desire for the biggest, the fastest, the highest, or if you are a maker of wristwatches or microscopes the smallest; the love in short of the superlative and the "peerless," is in essence and possibility a noble passion.

当然，美国版的进步与经济状况和人性中大量的事实相吻合。它把异常多的好斗、贪婪和权力欲转化为生产性工作。直到最近，它才严重挫败了社区积极成员的积极性。他们创造了一种文明，为创造它的人提供了他们认为在工作、交配和娱乐中充分满足的东西，他们战胜高山、荒野、距离和人类竞争的冲动甚至使宗教情感的一部分成为一种与宇宙目的相通的感觉。这种模式在理想、实践和结果的顺序上取得了近乎完美的成功，以至于任何对它的挑战都被称为非美国式的。

Certainly the American version of progress has fitted an extraordinary range of facts in the economic situation and in human nature. It turned an unusual amount of pugnacity, acquisitiveness, and lust of power into productive work. Nor has it, until more recently perhaps, seriously frustrated the active nature of the active members of the community. They have made a civilization which provides them who made it with what they feel to be ample satisfaction in work, mating and play, and the rush of their victory over mountains, wildernesses, distance, and human competition has even done duty for that part of religious feeling which is a sense of communion with the purpose of the universe. The pattern has been a success so nearly perfect in the sequence of ideals, practice, and results, that any challenge to it is called un-American.

然而，这种模式是一种非常片面和不充分的描述世界的方式。习惯于将进步视为“发展”，这意味着环境的许多方面被忽视了。由于“进步”的刻板印象，美国人在大众眼中几乎没有看到与这种进步不符的东西。他们看到城市的扩张，但没有看到贫民窟的增加；他们为人口普查数据欢呼，但拒绝考虑过度拥挤的问题；他们自豪地指出他们的增长，但看不到离开家乡的人口或未被同化的移民。他们疯狂地扩张工业，不计后果地消耗自然资源；他们建立了巨型公司，却没有安排好劳资关系。他们成长为地球上最强大的国家之一，却没有为结束孤立状态做好机构或思想准备。他们在道德和身体上都没有做好准备就跌跌撞撞地卷入了世界大战，他们再次跌跌撞撞地退出，大失所望，但经验却没有增加多少。

And yet, this pattern is a very partial and inadequate way of representing the world. The habit of thinking about progress as "development" has meant that many aspects of the environment were simply neglected. With the stereotype of "progress" before their eyes, Americans have in the mass seen little that did not accord with that progress. They saw the expansion of cities, but not the accretion of slums; they cheered the census statistics, but refused to consider overcrowding; they pointed with pride to their growth, but would not see the drift from the land, or the unassimilated immigration. They expanded industry furiously at reckless cost to their natural resources; they built up gigantic corporations without arranging for industrial relations. They grew to be one of the most powerful nations on earth without preparing their institutions or their minds for the ending of their isolation. They stumbled into the World War morally and physically unready, and they stumbled out again, much disillusioned, but hardly more experienced.

在世界大战中，美国刻板印象的正反两方面影响显而易见。认为只要招募无限数量的军队、筹集无限数量的贷款、建造无限数量的舰船、生产无限数量的军火，并无限集中精力于这些就能赢得战争的想法符合传统的刻板印象，并产生了类似物理奇迹的东西。但在那些受刻板印象影响最深的人中，没有空间去考虑胜利的果实是什么，或者如何实现它们。因此，目标被忽视，或被视为自动实现，胜利被认为是战场上的毁灭性胜利，因为刻板印象要求如此。在和平时期，你不会问最快的汽车有什么用，在战争中，你也不会问最彻底的胜利有什么用。然而，在巴黎，这种模式并不符合事实。在和平时期，你可以无休止地用大的东西取代小的东西，用更大的东西取代大的东西；在战争中，当你赢得了绝对的胜利时，你就不可能再取得更绝对的胜利。你必须按照完全不同的模式做事。如果你没有这样的模式，战争的结束对你来说就像对许多好人一样，是一个沉闷而毫无趣味的世界里的败笔。

In the World War the good and the evil influence of the American stereotype was plainly visible. The idea that the war could be won by recruiting unlimited armies, raising unlimited credits, building an unlimited number of ships, producing unlimited munitions, and concentrating without limit on these alone, fitted the traditional stereotype, and resulted in something like a physical miracle. But among those most affected by the stereotype, there was no place for the consideration of what the fruits of victory were, or how they were to be attained. Therefore, aims were ignored, or regarded as automatic, and victory was conceived, because the stereotype demanded it, as nothing but an annihilating victory in the field. In peace time you did not ask what the fastest motor car was for, and in war you did not ask what the completest victory was for. Yet in Paris the pattern did not fit the facts. In peace you can go on endlessly supplanting small things with big ones, and big ones with bigger ones; in war when you have won absolute victory, you cannot go on to a more absolute victory. You have to do something on an entirely different pattern. And if you lack such a pattern, the end of the war is to you what it was to so many good people, an anticlimax in a dreary and savorless world.

这标志着刻板印象和不容忽视的事实最终分道扬镳的临界点。总是存在这样的临界点，因为我们对事物行为的想象比事物的涨落更简单、更固定。因此，总有那么一个时刻，盲点会从视野的边缘延伸到中心。那时，除非有敢于发出警报的批评家、能够理解变化的领导人和习惯宽容的人民，否则刻板印象不但不能像 1917 年和 1918 年那样节省精力、集中精力，反而可能会使努力受挫、浪费人们的精力，就像它对那些在 1919 年呼吁迦太基和平、在 1921 年谴责凡尔赛条约的人所做的那样。

This marks the point where the stereotype and the facts, that cannot be ignored, definitely part company. There is always such a point, because our images of how things behave are simpler and more fixed than the ebb and flow of affairs. There comes a time, therefore, when the blind spots come from the edge of vision into the center. Then unless there are critics who have the courage to sound an alarm, and leaders capable of understanding the change, and a people tolerant by habit, the stereotype, instead of economizing effort, and focussing energy as it did in 1917 and 1918, may frustrate effort and waste men's energy by blinding them, as it did for those people who cried for a Carthaginian peace in 1919 and deplored the Treaty of Versailles in 1921.





3

3

如果不加批判地坚持这种刻板印象，它不仅会屏蔽掉许多需要考虑的因素，而且当清算日到来时，这种刻板印象被打破，它所明智考虑的因素很可能也会随之崩塌。这就是萧伯纳先生对自由贸易、自由契约、自由竞争、自然自由、自由放任和达尔文主义的惩罚。一百年前，当他肯定是这些学说最尖锐的拥护者之一时，他不会像今天，在异教徒半个世纪中那样，认为这些学说是“肆无忌惮地‘打压他人’的借口，指导政府的一切干预，除警察组织之外的所有组织，以保护合法欺诈免受殴打，所有试图将人类的目的、设计和深思熟虑引入工业混乱的行为都是‘违反政治经济规律’”。那么，作为向天堂平原进军的先驱之一，他会看到，在像维多利亚女王叔叔那样的政府中，人类的目的、设计和深思熟虑越少越好。他会看到，不是强者打压弱者，而是愚蠢的人打压强者。他会看到，目的、设计和深思熟虑在起作用，阻碍发明，阻碍企业，阻碍他肯定会认识到的创造进化的下一步。

Uncritically held, the stereotype not only censors out much that needs to be taken into account, but when the day of reckoning comes, and the stereotype is shattered, likely as not that which it did wisely take into account is ship-wrecked with it. That is the punishment assessed by Mr. Bernard Shaw against Free Trade, Free Contract, Free Competition, Natural Liberty, Laissez-faire, and Darwinism. A hundred years ago, when he would surely have been one of the tartest advocates of these doctrines, he would not have seen them as he sees them to-day, in the Infidel Half Century, to be excuses for "'doing the other fellow down' with impunity, all interference by a guiding government, all organization except police organization to protect legalized fraud against fisticuffs, all attempt to introduce human purpose and design and forethought into the industrial welter being 'contrary to the laws of political economy'" He would have seen, then, as one of the pioneers of the march to the plains of heaven that, of the kind of human purpose and design and forethought to be found in a government like that of Queen Victoria's uncles, the less the better. He would have seen, not the strong doing the weak down, but the foolish doing the strong down. He would have seen purposes, designs and forethoughts at work, obstructing invention, obstructing enterprise, obstructing what he would infallibly have recognized as the next move of Creative Evolution.

即便现在，萧伯纳也不太热衷于他所知道的任何指导性政府的指导，但在理论上，他完全反对自由放任主义。战前最先进的思想也同样反对既定观念，即如果你放开一切，智慧就会涌现，建立和谐。战后，在审查员、宣传员和间谍的帮助下，罗巴克·拉姆斯登和自然自由主义以其明确的指导性政府表现重新被纳入严肃思想家的行列。

Even now Mr. Shaw is none too eager for the guidance of any guiding government he knows, but in theory he has turned a full loop against laissez-faire. Most advanced thinking before the war had made the same turn against the established notion that if you unloosed everything, wisdom would bubble up, and establish harmony. Since the war, with its definite demonstration of guiding governments, assisted by censors, propagandists, and spies, Roebuck Ramsden and Natural Liberty have been readmitted to the company of serious thinkers.

这些周期有一个共同点。在每一套刻板印象中，都有一个点，在这个点上，努力停止，事情自然发生，就像你希望的那样。进步的刻板印象，有力地激励工作，几乎完全抹杀了决定做什么工作和为什么工作的尝试。自由放任主义，一种摆脱愚蠢官僚主义的幸运，认为人们会自发地走向预先确定的和谐。集体主义，一种对抗无情自私的解药，在马克思主义者看来，它似乎假设了一种经济决定论，即社会主义官员的效率和智慧。强大的政府，国内外的帝国主义，在最好的情况下，深刻意识到混乱的代价，最终依赖于这样一种观念，即被统治者所关心的一切都会被统治者知道。在每一种理论中，都有一丝盲目的自动化。

One thing is common to these cycles. There is in each set of stereotypes a point where effort ceases and things happen of their own accord, as you would like them to. The progressive stereotype, powerful to incite work, almost completely obliterates the attempt to decide what work and why that work. Laissez-faire, a blessed release from stupid officialdom, assumes that men will move by spontaneous combustion towards a pre-established harmony. Collectivism, an antidote to ruthless selfishness, seems, in the Marxian mind, to suppose an economic determinism towards efficiency and wisdom on the part of socialist officials. Strong government, imperialism at home and abroad, at its best deeply conscious of the price of disorder, relies at last on the notion that all that matters to the governed will be known by the governors. In each theory there is a spot of blind automatism.

那个盲点掩盖了一些事实，如果考虑到这一点，就会抑制刻板印象所激发的重大运动。如果进步人士必须像笑话中的中国人一样扪心自问，他想用打破纪录节省下来的时间做什么，如果自由放任主义的倡导者不仅要考虑人类自由和旺盛的能量，还要考虑一些人所说的人类本性，如果集体主义者将注意力集中在如何保护官员的问题上，如果帝国主义者敢于怀疑自己的灵感，那么你会发现更多的哈姆雷特而不是亨利五世。因为这些盲点可以避免分散注意力的形象，这些形象及其伴随的情绪可能会导致犹豫和目标不明确。因此，刻板印象不仅可以在忙碌的生活中节省时间，捍卫我们在社会中的地位，而且还可以保护我们免受试图稳定地看待世界和看待世界整体所带来的所有令人困惑的影响。

That spot covers up some fact, which if it were taken into account, would check the vital movement that the stereotype provokes. If the progressive had to ask himself, like the Chinaman in the joke, what he wanted to do with the time he saved by breaking the record, if the advocate of laissez-faire had to contemplate not only free and exuberant energies of men, but what some people call their human nature, if the collectivist let the center of his attention be occupied with the problem of how he is to secure his officials, if the imperialist dared to doubt his own inspiration, you would find more Hamlet and less Henry the Fifth. For these blind spots keep away distracting images, which with their attendant emotions, might cause hesitation and infirmity of purpose. Consequently the stereotype not only saves time in a busy life and is a defense of our position in society, but tends to preserve us from all the bewildering effect of trying to see the world steadily and see it whole.

第九章

CHAPTER IX

守则及其敌人

CODES AND THEIR ENEMIES





1

1

任何曾经站在火车站台尽头等朋友的人都会记得自己曾把哪些奇怪的人误认为是他。帽子的形状、略带特征的步态，都会在他的脑海中唤起生动的画面。在睡梦中，叮当声可能听起来像大钟的鸣响；远处锤子的敲击声像雷声。因为我们的想象星座会随着可能与它们某些方面模糊相似的刺激而震动。它们可能在幻觉中充斥整个意识。它们可能很少进入感知，尽管我倾向于认为这种体验极为罕见且高度复杂，就像我们茫然地凝视一个熟悉的单词或物体，它逐渐不再熟悉。当然，在大多数情况下，我们看待事物的方式是既有的东西与我们期望找到的东西的结合。天文学家和恋人眼中的天空是不一样的；康德的一页著作将会在康德主义者和激进经验主义者的思想中引发不同的思路；大溪地美女对大溪地追求者来说比对《国家地理杂志》的读者来说更漂亮 。

ANYONE who has stood at the end of a railroad platform waiting for a friend, will recall what queer people he mistook for him. The shape of a hat, a slightly characteristic gait, evoked the vivid picture in his mind's eye. In sleep a tinkle may sound like the pealing of a great bell; the distant stroke of a hammer like a thunderclap. For our constellations of imagery will vibrate to a stimulus that is perhaps but vaguely similar to some aspect of them. They may, in hallucination, flood the whole consciousness. They may enter very little into perception, though I am inclined to think that such an experience is extremely rare and highly sophisticated, as when we gaze blankly at a familiar word or object, and it gradually ceases to be familiar. Certainly for the most part, the way we see things is a combination of what is there and of what we expected to find. The heavens are not the same to an astronomer as to a pair of lovers; a page of Kant will start a different train of thought in a Kantian and in a radical empiricist; the Tahitian belle is a better looking person to her Tahitian suitor than to the readers of the National Geographic Magazine .

事实上，任何学科的专业知识都是我们准备发现的方面数量的乘积，加上低估我们期望的习惯。对于无知的人来说，所有事物看起来都一样，生活就是一件接一件的事情，而对于专家来说，事物是高度个性化的。对于司机、美食家、鉴赏家、总统内阁成员或教授的妻子来说，存在着明显的差异和品质，而对于讨论汽车、葡萄酒、老大师、共和党人和大学教职员工的普通人来说，这些差异和品质根本不明显。

Expertness in any subject is, in fact, a multiplication of the number of aspects we are prepared to discover, plus the habit of discounting our expectations. Where to the ignoramus all things look alike, and life is just one thing after another, to the specialist things are highly individual. For a chauffeur, an epicure, a connoisseur, a member of the President's cabinet, or a professor's wife, there are evident distinctions and qualities, not at all evident to the casual person who discusses automobiles, wines, old masters, Republicans, and college faculties.

但在我们的公众舆论中，很少有人能成为专家，而正如萧伯纳先生所言，生命如此短暂。那些专家只精通少数几个话题。即使在专家士兵中，正如我们在战争期间所了解到的，精通骑兵的人也不一定擅长堑壕战和坦克。事实上，有时对一个小话题的一点点精通可能只是夸大了我们正常的人类习惯，即试图把所有能挤进我们刻板印象的东西塞进去，把不合适的东西抛到外面的黑暗中。

But in our public opinions few can be expert, while life is, as Mr. Bernard Shaw has made plain, so short. Those who are expert are so on only a few topics. Even among the expert soldiers, as we learned during the war, expert cavalrymen were not necessarily brilliant with trench-warfare and tanks. Indeed, sometimes a little expertness on a small topic may simply exaggerate our normal human habit of trying to squeeze into our stereotypes all that can be squeezed, and of casting into outer darkness that which does not fit.

如果不仔细观察，我们就会倾向于借助于我们脑海中已有的图像来想象我们所熟悉的一切。因此，美国人对进步和成功的看法中，对人性和社会有着明确的描述。正是这种人性和这种社会逻辑上产生了被认为是理想的进步。然后，当我们试图描述或解释真正成功的人和真正发生的事件时，我们会从他们身上读出刻板印象中预设的品质。

Whatever we recognize as familiar we tend, if we are not very careful, to visualize with the aid of images already in our mind. Thus in the American view of Progress and Success there is a definite picture of human nature and of society. It is the kind of human nature and the kind of society which logically produce the kind of progress that is regarded as ideal. And then, when we seek to describe or explain actually successful men, and events that have really happened, we read back into them the qualities that are presupposed in the stereotypes.

老一辈经济学家对这些品质进行了相当天真的标准化。他们开始描述他们所处的社会制度，发现它太复杂了，无法用语言描述。因此，他们构建了一个他们真诚希望简化的图表，在原则和真实性上与儿童画的复杂奶牛的有腿和头的平行四边形没有太大区别。该方案由一位努力从自己的劳动中节省资本的资本家、一位设想社会有用需求并组织工厂的企业家、一群自由签订劳动合同、接受或放弃劳动的工人、一位房东和一群消费者组成，他们在最便宜的市场上购买那些通过现成的快乐-痛苦计算而知道会给他们带来最大快乐的商品。这个模型奏效了。在描述该模型的书中，模型所假设的那种人生活在模型所假设的那种世界中，总是和谐地合作。

These qualities were standardized rather innocently by the older economists. They set out to describe the social system under which they lived, and found it too complicated for words. So they constructed what they sincerely hoped was a simplified diagram, not so different in principle and in veracity from the parallelogram with legs and head in a child's drawing of a complicated cow. The scheme consisted of a capitalist who had diligently saved capital from his labor, an entrepreneur who conceived a socially useful demand and organized a factory, a collection of workmen who freely contracted, take it or leave it, for their labor, a landlord, and a group of consumers who bought in the cheapest market those goods which by the ready use of the pleasure-pain calculus they knew would give them the most pleasure. The model worked. The kind of people, which the model assumed, living in the sort of world the model assumed, invariably cooperated harmoniously in the books where the model was described.

经济学家们为了简化思维而对这一纯粹的虚构进行了修改和粉饰，然后将其传播开来，直到它成为当时大部分人的经济神话。它为资本家、推动者、工人和消费者提供了一个标准版本，而这个社会自然更热衷于获得成功，而不是解释成功。不断拔地而起的大楼和不断增加的银行账户证明了人们对成功的看法是正确的。而那些从成功中获益最多的人开始相信他们就是他们应该成为的那种人。难怪成功人士的真诚朋友在阅读官方传记和讣告时，不得不克制自己不去问这是否真的是他们的朋友。

With modification and embroidery, this pure fiction, used by economists to simplify their thinking, was retailed and popularized until for large sections of the population it prevailed as the economic mythology of the day. It supplied a standard version of capitalist, promoter, worker and consumer in a society that was naturally more bent on achieving success than on explaining it. The buildings which rose, and the bank accounts which accumulated, were evidence that the stereotype of how the thing had been done was accurate. And those who benefited most by success came to believe they were the kind of men they were supposed to be. No wonder that the candid friends of successful men, when they read the official biography and the obituary, have to restrain themselves from asking whether this is indeed their friend.





2

2

对于失败者和受害者来说，官方的描绘当然是无法辨认的。因为那些代表进步的人往往不会停下来思考他们是否按照经济学家或其他同样值得称道的人所制定的路线前进，而那些失败的人却在思考。威廉·詹姆斯说：“没有人能比自己对细节的了解更深入地理解概括。”工业巨头们把大托拉斯看作是他们成功的纪念碑；他们失败的竞争对手则认为是他们失败的纪念碑。因此，大企业主们阐述大企业的节约和美德，要求不受干扰，说他们是繁荣的推动者和贸易的开发者。失败者坚持托拉斯的浪费和残酷，并大声呼吁司法部将企业从阴谋中解放出来。在同样的情形下，一方看到了进步、节约和辉煌的发展；另一方看到了反动、奢侈和贸易的限制。大量的统计数据和有关真实真相和内部真相、更深层和更大的真相的轶事被发表出来以证明双方的论点。

To the vanquished and the victims, the official portraiture was, of course, unrecognizable. For while those who exemplified progress did not often pause to inquire whether they had arrived according to the route laid down by the economists, or by some other just as creditable, the unsuccessful people did inquire. "No one," says William James, "sees further into a generalization than his own knowledge of detail extends." The captains of industry saw in the great trusts monuments of (their) success; their defeated competitors saw the monuments of (their) failure. So the captains expounded the economies and virtues of big business, asked to be let alone, said they were the agents of prosperity, and the developers of trade. The vanquished insisted upon the wastes and brutalities of the trusts, and called loudly upon the Department of Justice to free business from conspiracies. In the same situation one side saw progress, economy, and a splendid development; the other, reaction, extravagance, and a restraint of trade. Volumes of statistics, anecdotes about the real truth and the inside truth, the deeper and the larger truth, were published to prove both sides of the argument.

因为当一套刻板印象体系牢固确立时，我们的注意力就会被吸引到那些支持它的事实上，而远离那些与之相反的事实。所以，也许正是因为他们善于发现这一点，善良的人才会发现善良的那么多理由，恶意的人才会发现恶意的那么多理由。我们说得非常准确，就是戴着玫瑰色的眼镜，或者带着偏见看问题。如果像菲利普·利特尔曾经写过一位杰出教授那样，我们透过一个黑暗的阶级来看待生活，我们对最优秀人和下层阶级的刻板印象就不会被理解所污染。陌生的东西会被拒绝，不同的东西会落在无知的眼睛上。我们看不到我们的眼睛不习惯考虑的东西。有时是有意识的，更多的时候是无意识的，我们会对那些符合我们哲学的事实印象深刻。

For when a system of stereotypes is well fixed, our attention is called to those facts which support it, and diverted from those which contradict. So perhaps it is because they are attuned to find it, that kindly people discover so much reason for kindness, malicious people so much malice. We speak quite accurately of seeing through rose-colored spectacles, or with a jaundiced eye. If, as Philip Littell once wrote of a distinguished professor, we see life as through a class darkly, our stereotypes of what the best people and the lower classes are like will not be contaminated by understanding. What is alien will be rejected, what is different will fall upon unseeing eyes. We do not see what our eyes are not accustomed to take into account. Sometimes consciously, more often without knowing it, we are impressed by those facts which fit our philosophy.





3

3

这种哲学是一系列或多或少有组织的图像，用于描述看不见的世界。但不仅用于描述它。也用于判断它。因此，刻板印象充满了偏爱，充满了爱或厌恶，与恐惧、欲望、强烈的愿望、骄傲、希望联系在一起。任何引起刻板印象的事物都会以适当的情绪来判断。除非我们故意保持偏见，否则我们不会研究一个人并判断他是坏人。我们看到一个坏人。我们看到一个露水的早晨，一个脸红的少女，一个圣洁的牧师，一个没有幽默感的英国人，一个危险的红色人，一个无忧无虑的波西米亚人，一个懒惰的印度人，一个狡猾的东方人，一个做梦的斯拉夫人，一个反复无常的爱尔兰人，一个贪婪的犹太人，一个 100% 的美国人。在日常世界中，这往往是真正的判断，远远领先于证据，它本身就包含了证据肯定会证实的结论。正义、仁慈和真理都不能参与这样的判断，因为判断先于证据。然而，一个没有偏见的民族，一个具有完全中立观点的民族，在任何值得思考的文明中都是不可想象的，以至于任何教育方案都不可能建立在这种理想之上。偏见可以被发现、消除和提炼，但只要有限的人必须将应对广阔文明的准备压缩到短期学校教育中，他们就必须随身携带这种文明的形象，并有偏见。他们思考和行动的质量将取决于这些偏见是否友好，是否对其他人、对其他思想友好，是否唤起对他们认为是积极善的事物的热爱，而不是对他们认为的善中没有的东西的仇恨。

This philosophy is a more or less organized series of images for describing the unseen world. But not only for describing it. For judging it as well. And, therefore, the stereotypes are loaded with preference, suffused with affection or dislike, attached to fears, lusts, strong wishes, pride, hope. Whatever invokes the stereotype is judged with the appropriate sentiment. Except where we deliberately keep prejudice in suspense, we do not study a man and judge him to be bad. We see a bad man. We see a dewy morn, a blushing maiden, a sainted priest, a humorless Englishman, a dangerous Red, a carefree bohemian, a lazy Hindu, a wily Oriental, a dreaming Slav, a volatile Irishman, a greedy Jew, a 100% American. In the workaday world that is often the real judgment, long in advance of the evidence, and it contains within itself the conclusion which the evidence is pretty certain to confirm. Neither justice, nor mercy, nor truth, enter into such a judgment, for the judgment has preceded the evidence. Yet a people without prejudices, a people with altogether neutral vision, is so unthinkable in any civilization of which it is useful to think, that no scheme of education could be based upon that ideal. Prejudice can be detected, discounted, and refined, but so long as finite men must compress into a short schooling preparation for dealing with a vast civilization, they must carry pictures of it around with them, and have prejudices. The quality of their thinking and doing will depend on whether those prejudices are friendly, friendly to other people, to other ideas, whether they evoke love of what is felt to be positively good, rather than hatred of what is not contained in their version of the good.

道德、良好品味和良好形式首先规范化，然后强调某些潜在的偏见。当我们调整自己以适应我们的准则时，我们也会调整我们看到的事实以适应该准则。理性地说，事实对于我们对是非的所有看法都是中立的。实际上，我们的准则在很大程度上决定了我们将感知什么以及如何感知。

Morality, good taste and good form first standardize and then emphasize certain of these underlying prejudices. As we adjust ourselves to our code, we adjust the facts we see to that code. Rationally, the facts are neutral to all our views of right and wrong. Actually, our canons determine greatly what we shall perceive and how.

因为道德准则是一套适用于许多典型情况的行为体系。按照准则行事就是服务于准则所追求的任何目的。它可能是上帝的旨意，也可能是国王的意志，也可能是个人在一个美好、坚实、立体的天堂中的救赎，也可能是人间的成功，也可能是为人类服务。无论如何，准则的制定者会确定某些典型情况，然后通过某种形式的推理或直觉，推断出会产生他们认可的目标的行为类型。规则适用于适用的地方。

For a moral code is a scheme of conduct applied to a number of typical instances. To behave as the code directs is to serve whatever purpose the code pursues. It may be God's will, or the king's, individual salvation in a good, solid, three dimensional paradise, success on earth, or the service of mankind. In any event the makers of the code fix upon certain typical situations, and then by some form of reasoning or intuition, deduce the kind of behavior which would produce the aim they acknowledge. The rules apply where they apply.

但在日常生活中，一个人如何知道他所处的困境是否正是立法者所设想的？他被告知不要杀人。但如果他的孩子受到袭击，他可以杀人来阻止杀戮吗？十诫对这一点只字未提。因此，围绕每一条法典，都有一群解释者推断出更具体的案例。那么，假设法律博士决定他可以出于自卫而杀人。对于下一个人来说，疑问几乎同样巨大；他如何知道他对自卫的定义是正确的，或者他没有误判事实，没有想象出袭击，他真的是侵略者？也许他挑起了袭击。但什么是挑衅？正是这些混乱在 1914 年 8 月感染了大多数德国人的思想。

But in daily living how does a man know whether his predicament is the one the law-giver had in mind? He is told not to kill. But if his children are attacked, may he kill to stop a killing? The Ten Commandments are silent on the point. Therefore, around every code there is a cloud of interpreters who deduce more specific cases. Suppose, then, that the doctors of the law decide that he may kill in self-defense. For the next man the doubt is almost as great; how does he know that he is defining self-defense correctly, or that he has not misjudged the facts, imagined the attack, and is really the aggressor? Perhaps he has provoked the attack. But what is a provocation? Exactly these confusions infected the minds of most Germans in August, 1914.

在现代社会，比任何道德准则的差异更为严重的是，对准则所适用的事实的假设存在差异。宗教、道德和政治公式之间的差异，并不比其信奉者所假设的事实大。因此，有益的讨论不是比较理想，而是重新审视事实的观点。因此，己所不欲勿施于人这一规则基于人性是一致的这一信念。萧伯纳先生说，己所不欲勿施于人，因为他们的品味可能不同，这一说法基于人性不是一致的这一信念。竞争是贸易的生命这一格言包含了大量关于经济动机、劳资关系和特定商业体系运作的假设。除非商船是私人所有和管理的，否则美国永远不会拥有商船队，这一说法假设了某种盈利和激励之间存在某种已证实的联系。布尔什维克宣传家为独裁、间谍和恐怖进行辩护，因为“每个国家都是暴力机器”，这是一个历史判断，其真实性对于非共产主义者来说绝非不言而喻。

Far more serious in the modern world than any difference of moral code is the difference in the assumptions about facts to which the code is applied. Religious, moral and political formulae are nothing like so far apart as the facts assumed by their votaries. Useful discussion, then, instead of comparing ideals, reexamines the visions of the facts. Thus the rule that you should do unto others as you would have them do unto you rests on the belief that human nature is uniform. Mr. Bernard Shaw's statement that you should not do unto others what you would have them do unto you, because their tastes may be different, rests on the belief that human nature is not uniform. The maxim that competition is the life of trade consists of a whole tome of assumptions about economic motives, industrial relations, and the working of a particular commercial system. The claim that America will never have a merchant marine, unless it is privately owned and managed, assumes a certain proved connection between a certain kind of profit-making and incentive. The justification by the bolshevik propagandist of the dictatorship, espionage, and the terror, because "every state is an apparatus of violence" is an historical judgment, the truth of which is by no means self-evident to a non-communist.

每一条道德准则的核心都是一幅人性的图景、一幅宇宙地图和一段历史。道德准则的规则适用于人性（构想的那种）、宇宙（想象的那种）、历史（如此理解的那种）。只要人格、环境和记忆的事实不同，道德准则的规则就很难成功应用。现在，每一条道德准则都必须以某种方式构想人类心理、物质世界和传统。但在受科学影响的准则中，概念被认为是一种假设，而在未经检验的过去或从思想洞穴中冒出来的准则中，概念并不被视为需要证明或反驳的假设，而是一种毫无疑问接受的虚构。在前一种情况下，人类对自己的信仰很谦虚，因为他知道这些信仰是暂时的和不完整的；在另一种情况下，人类很武断，因为他的信仰是一个完整的神话。服从科学纪律的道德家知道，尽管他并非无所不知，但他正在阻碍了解某些事物；教条主义者利用神话，相信自己分享了部分全知的洞察力，尽管他缺乏区分真相和谬误的标准。因为神话的显著特征是，真理和谬误、事实和寓言、报道和幻想都处于同一可信度水平。

At the core of every moral code there is a picture of human nature, a map of the universe, and a version of history. To human nature (of the sort conceived), in a universe (of the kind imagined), after a history (so understood), the rules of the code apply. So far as the facts of personality, of the environment and of memory are different, by so far the rules of the code are difficult to apply with success. Now every moral code has to conceive human psychology, the material world, and tradition some way or other. But in the codes that are under the influence of science, the conception is known to be an hypothesis, whereas in the codes that come unexamined from the past or bubble up from the caverns of the mind, the conception is not taken as an hypothesis demanding proof or contradiction, but as a fiction accepted without question. In the one case, man is humble about his beliefs, because he knows they are tentative and incomplete; in the other he is dogmatic, because his belief is a completed myth. The moralist who submits to the scientific discipline knows that though he does not know everything, he is in the way of knowing something; the dogmatist, using a myth, believes himself to share part of the insight of omniscience, though he lacks the criteria by which to tell truth from error. For the distinguishing mark of a myth is that truth and error, fact and fable, report and fantasy, are all on the same plane of credibility.

那么，神话不一定是假的。它可能完全真实。也可能部分真实。如果它长期影响了人类的行为，那么它几乎肯定会包含许多深刻而重要的真实内容。神话从来不具备区分真相与谬误的批判能力。因为只有认识到没有任何人类观点，无论其假定来源如何，都过于崇高而无法通过证据检验，每种观点都只是某人的观点，才能获得这种能力。如果你问为什么证据检验比其他任何检验都更好，除非你愿意使用检验来检验它，否则没有答案。

The myth is, then, not necessarily false. It might happen to be wholly true. It may happen to be partly true. If it has affected human conduct a long time, it is almost certain to contain much that is profoundly and importantly true. What a myth never contains is the critical power to separate its truths from its errors. For that power comes only by realizing that no human opinion, whatever its supposed origin, is too exalted for the test of evidence, that every opinion is only somebody's opinion. And if you ask why the test of evidence is preferable to any other, there is no answer unless you are willing to use the test in order to test it.





4

4

我认为，有充分的证据证明，道德准则假定了对事实的特定看法。道德准则包括所有类型的准则：个人、家庭、经济、职业、法律、爱国和国际。每种准则的核心都是关于心理学、社会学和历史的刻板印象。我们所有的准则很少都坚持相同的人性、制度或传统观点。例如，比较一下经济准则和爱国准则。有一场战争应该对所有人产生同样的影响。两个人是生意伙伴。一个参军，另一个签订了战争合同。士兵牺牲了一切，甚至牺牲了自己的生命。他每天只得到一美元，没有人说，也没有人相信，任何形式的经济激励都能让他成为一名更好的士兵。这种动机从他的人性中消失了。承包商牺牲很少，得到的利润远高于成本，几乎没有人说或相信，如果没有经济激励，他会生产军火。这对他来说可能不公平。关键在于，公认的爱国准则假定了一种人性，而商业准则则假定了另一种人性。这些准则可能在某种程度上建立在真实的期望之上，即当一个人采用某种准则时，他往往会表现出准则所要求的那种人性。

The statement is, I think, susceptible of overwhelming proof, that moral codes assume a particular view of the facts. Under the term moral codes I include all kinds: personal, family, economic, professional, legal, patriotic, international. At the center of each there is a pattern of stereotypes about psychology, sociology, and history. The same view of human nature, institutions or tradition rarely persists through all our codes. Compare, for example, the economic and the patriotic codes. There is a war supposed to affect all alike. Two men are partners in business. One enlists, the other takes a war contract. The soldier sacrifices everything, perhaps even his life. He is paid a dollar a day, and no one says, no one believes, that you could make a better soldier out of him by any form of economic incentive. That motive disappears out of his human nature. The contractor sacrifices very little, is paid a handsome profit over costs, and few say or believe that he would produce the munitions if there were no economic incentive. That may be unfair to him. The point is that the accepted patriotic code assumes one kind of human nature, the commercial code another. And the codes are probably founded on true expectations to this extent, that when a man adopts a certain code he tends to exhibit the kind of human nature which the code demands.

这就是为什么对人性进行概括是如此危险的原因之一。慈爱的父亲可能是一个脾气暴躁的老板，一个热心的市政改革者，一个贪婪的海外沙文主义者。他的家庭生活、他的商业生涯、他的政治和外交政策都基于对他人的看法和他应该如何行事的完全不同的理解。这些看法在同一个人身上因准则而异，同一社会群体中的人之间准则略有不同，不同社会群体之间准则也大不相同，两个国家或两种肤色之间的差异可能大到没有任何共同的假设。这就是为什么信奉相同宗教信仰的人会开战的原因。他们的信仰中决定行为的因素是他们对事实的看法。

That is one reason why it is so dangerous to generalize about human nature. A loving father can be a sour boss, an earnest municipal reformer, and a rapacious jingo abroad. His family life, his business career, his politics, and his foreign policy rest on totally different versions of what others are like and of how he should act. These versions differ by codes in the same person, the codes differ somewhat among persons in the same social set, differ widely as between social sets, and between two nations, or two colors, may differ to the point where there is no common assumption whatever. That is why people professing the same stock of religious beliefs can go to war. The element of their belief which determines conduct is that view of the facts which they assume.

正是在这里，规范如此巧妙而广泛地介入了舆论的形成。正统理论认为，舆论构成了对一组事实的道德判断。我提出的理论是，在目前的教育状态下，舆论主要是事实的道德化和规范化版本。我认为，我们规范核心的刻板印象模式在很大程度上决定了我们将看到哪一组事实，以及我们将以何种眼光看待它们。这就是为什么，尽管怀着世界上最好的意愿，杂志的新闻政策倾向于支持其编辑政策；为什么资本家看到一组事实，而人性的某些方面确实看到了这些事实；他的社会主义对手看到另一组事实和其他方面，为什么每个人都认为对方是不合理或不正当的，而他们之间的真正区别只是感知的不同。这种差异是由资本主义和社会主义刻板印象模式的差异造成的。“美国没有阶级，”一位美国编辑写道。 《共产党宣言》说：“迄今为止现存社会的历史都是阶级斗争的历史。”如果你的头脑中有编辑的模式，你就会清楚地看到证实它的事实，而与之相反的事实则会模糊而无效地看到。如果你有共产主义模式，你不仅会寻找不同的东西，而且你会以完全不同的重点看到你和编辑碰巧看到的共同点。

That is where codes enter so subtly and so pervasively into the making of public opinion. The orthodox theory holds that a public opinion constitutes a moral judgment on a group of facts. The theory I am suggesting is that, in the present state of education, a public opinion is primarily a moralized and codified version of the facts. I am arguing that the pattern of stereotypes at the center of our codes largely determines what group of facts we shall see, and in what light we shall see them. That is why, with the best will in the world, the news policy of a journal tends to support its editorial policy; why a capitalist sees one set of facts, and certain aspects of human nature, literally sees them; his socialist opponent another set and other aspects, and why each regards the other as unreasonable or perverse, when the real difference between them is a difference of perception. That difference is imposed by the difference between the capitalist and socialist pattern of stereotypes. "There are no classes in America," writes an American editor. "The history of all hitherto existing society is the history of class struggles," says the Communist Manifesto. If you have the editor's pattern in your mind, you will see vividly the facts that confirm it, vaguely and ineffectively those that contradict. If you have the communist pattern, you will not only look for different things, but you will see with a totally different emphasis what you and the editor happen to see in common.





5

5

而且，由于我的道德体系建立在我接受的事实版本之上，所以，对我而言，否认我的道德判断或事实版本的人是反常的、异类的、危险的。我该如何解释他呢？对手总是需要解释的，而我们寻求的最后一个解释是，他看到了一组不同的事实。我们避免这样的解释，因为它削弱了我们对自己已经稳定地、全面地看待生活的基础的信心。只有当我们习惯于将我们的观点视为通过刻板印象看到的部分经验时，我们才会真正容忍对手。如果没有这种习惯，我们就会相信我们自己观点的绝对主义，从而相信所有反对意见的危险性。因为虽然人们愿意承认“问题”有两面，但他们不相信他们所认为的“事实”有两面。他们从来不相信这一点，直到经过长期的批判性教育，他们才充分意识到自己对社会数据的理解是多么的二手和主观。

And since my moral system rests on my accepted version of the facts, he who denies either my moral judgments or my version of the facts, is to me perverse, alien, dangerous. How shall I account for him? The opponent has always to be explained, and the last explanation that we ever look for is that he sees a different set of facts. Such an explanation we avoid, because it saps the very foundation of our own assurance that we have seen life steadily and seen it whole. It is only when we are in the habit of recognizing our opinions as a partial experience seen through our stereotypes that we become truly tolerant of an opponent. Without that habit, we believe in the absolutism of our own vision, and consequently in the treacherous character of all opposition. For while men are willing to admit that there are two sides to a "question," they do not believe that there are two sides to what they regard as a "fact." And they never do believe it until after long critical education, they are fully conscious of how second-hand and subjective is their apprehension of their social data.

因此，当两派都清楚地看到各自的方面，并对他们所看到的事物做出自己的解释时，他们几乎不可能诚实地相信对方。如果模式在关键时刻符合他们的经验，他们就不再将其视为一种解释。他们将其视为“现实”。它可能与现实并不相似，除非它最终得出一个符合真实经验的结论。我可以用地图上的一条直线来表示我从纽约到波士顿的旅程，就像一个人可能把他的胜利视为一条笔直狭窄的道路的终点一样。我实际去波士顿的那条路可能绕了很多弯路，拐了很多弯，就像他的道路可能除了纯粹的进取、劳动和节俭之外还涉及很多事情。但只要我到达波士顿，他也能成功，那条航线和那条笔直的道路就可以作为现成的图表。只有当有人试图追随它们，却没有到达时，我们才必须回答反对意见。如果我们坚持我们的图表，而他坚持拒绝，我们很快就会认为他是个危险的傻瓜，而他会认为我们是骗子和伪君子。因此，我们逐渐互相描绘。因为对手将自己表现为说“恶即是善”的人。他是一个不适合事物计划的讨厌鬼。然而他却干扰了。而且由于该计划在我们心中是建立在无可辩驳的事实之上，并以不可抗拒的逻辑为后盾，所以必须在计划中为他找到一些位置。在政治或劳资纠纷中，很少会因为简单承认他看待过同样的现实，但看到了它的另一个方面而为他找到一席之地。那会动摇整个计划。

So where two factions see vividly each its own aspect, and contrive their own explanations of what they see, it is almost impossible for them to credit each other with honesty. If the pattern fits their experience at a crucial point, they no longer look upon it as an interpretation. They look upon it as "reality." It may not resemble the reality, except that it culminates in a conclusion which fits a real experience. I may represent my trip from New York to Boston by a straight line on a map, just as a man may regard his triumph as the end of a straight and narrow path. The road by which I actually went to Boston may have involved many detours, much turning and twisting, just as his road may have involved much besides pure enterprise, labor and thrift. But provided I reach Boston and he succeeds, the airline and the straight path will serve as ready made charts. Only when somebody tries to follow them, and does not arrive, do we have to answer objections. If we insist on our charts, and he insists on rejecting them, we soon tend to regard him as a dangerous fool, and he to regard us as liars and hypocrites. Thus we gradually paint portraits of each other. For the opponent presents himself as the man who says, evil be thou my good. He is an annoyance who does not fit into the scheme of things. Nevertheless he interferes. And since that scheme is based in our minds on incontrovertible fact fortified by irresistible logic, some place has to be found for him in the scheme. Rarely in politics or industrial disputes is a place made for him by the simple admission that he has looked upon the same reality and seen another aspect of it. That would shake the whole scheme.

因此，对在巴黎的意大利人来说，阜姆是意大利的。它不仅仅是一个值得纳入意大利王国的城市。它本身就是意大利的。他们把全部注意力都集中在城市合法边界内的意大利多数人群身上。美国代表在纽约见到的意大利人比在阜姆见到的还多，但他们并不认为纽约是意大利的，而是把目光投向了阜姆，将其视为欧洲中部的入境口岸。他们清楚地看到了郊区和非意大利腹地的南斯拉夫人。因此，巴黎的一些意大利人需要对美国人的乖僻行为给出令人信服的解释。他们在一个谣言中找到了答案，这个谣言的起源无人知晓，说一位有影响力的美国外交官被一位南斯拉夫情妇所蒙蔽。有人见过她……有人见过他……就在凡尔赛大道旁……那座长满大树的别墅。

Thus to the Italians in Paris Fiume was Italian It was not merely a city that it would be desirable to include within the Italian kingdom. It was Italian. They fixed their whole mind upon the Italian majority within the legal boundaries of the city itself. The American delegates, having seen more Italians in New York than there are in Fiume, without regarding New York as Italian, fixed their eyes on Fiume as a central European port of entry. They saw vividly the Jugoslavs in the suburbs and the non-Italian hinterland. Some of the Italians in Paris were therefore in need of a convincing explanation of the American perversity. They found it in a rumor which started, no one knows where, that an influential American diplomat was in the snares of a Jugoslav mistress. She had been seen…. He had been seen…. At Versailles just off the boulevard. … The villa with the large trees.

这是为反对意见辩解的常用方式。这些指控在诽谤性更强的形式下很少出现在报纸上，罗斯福可能要等上几年，哈丁可能要等上几个月，才能迫使政府采取行动，结束已经渗透到各个谈话圈子的流言蜚语。公众人物必须忍受大量恶毒的俱乐部、餐桌和闺房诽谤，这些诽谤被反复提及、详细阐述、引人发笑，并被视为美味佳肴。虽然我认为这种事情在美国不如在欧洲普遍，但很少有美国官员不被人重复丑闻。

This is a rather common way of explaining away opposition. In their more libelous form such charges rarely reach the printed page, and a Roosevelt may have to wait years, or a Harding months, before he can force an issue, and end a whispering campaign that has reached into every circle of talk. Public men have to endure a fearful amount of poisonous clubroom, dinner table, boudoir slander, repeated, elaborated, chuckled over, and regarded as delicious. While this sort of thing is, I believe, less prevalent in America than in Europe, yet rare is the American official about whom somebody is not repeating a scandal.

我们把反对派塑造成恶棍和阴谋家。如果物价无情上涨，奸商们就密谋了；如果报纸歪曲新闻，那就有资本主义的阴谋；如果富人太富有，他们就一直在偷窃；如果一场势均力敌的选举失败了，那选民就被腐蚀了；如果一个政客做了你不赞成的事情，那他就是被某个声名狼藉的人收买或影响了。如果工人焦躁不安，那他们就是煽动者的受害者；如果他们在广大地区焦躁不安，那一定有阴谋在酝酿。如果你生产的飞机不够，那是间谍干的；如果爱尔兰出现问题，那是德国或布尔什维克的“黄金”。如果你仔细观察，疯狂地寻找阴谋，你会发现，所有的罢工、普拉姆计划、爱尔兰叛乱、穆罕默德暴动、康斯坦丁国王复辟、国际联盟、墨西哥动乱、裁军运动、周日电影、短裙、逃避酒类管制法、黑人自强不息，都是莫斯科、罗马、共济会、日本人或锡安长老会策划的宏伟阴谋下的子阴谋。

Out of the opposition we make villains and conspiracies. If prices go up unmercifully the profiteers have conspired; if the newspapers misrepresent the news, there is a capitalist plot; if the rich are too rich, they have been stealing; if a closely fought election is lost, the electorate was corrupted; if a statesman does something of which you disapprove, he has been bought or influenced by some discreditable person. If workingmen are restless, they are the victims of agitators; if they are restless over wide areas, there is a conspiracy on foot. If you do not produce enough aeroplanes, it is the work of spies; if there is trouble in Ireland, it is German or Bolshevik "gold." And if you go stark, staring mad looking for plots, you see all strikes, the Plumb plan, Irish rebellion, Mohammedan unrest, the restoration of King Constantine, the League of Nations, Mexican disorder, the movement to reduce armaments, Sunday movies, short skirts, evasion of the liquor laws, Negro self-assertion, as sub-plots under some grandiose plot engineered either by Moscow, Rome, the Free Masons, the Japanese, or the Elders of Zion.

第十章

CHAPTER X

刻板印象的检测

THE DETECTION OF STEREOTYPES





1

1

经验丰富的外交官被迫大声向交战的人民讲话，学会了如何使用大量的陈词滥调。他们面对的是岌岌可危的强国联盟，每个联盟都只能靠最谨慎的领导来维持其战争团结。普通士兵和他的妻子，英勇无私，超越了英雄史册上的任何记载，但他们仍然没有足够的英雄气概，无法为了外国驻外机构所说的对文明未来至关重要的所有理念而欣然面对死亡。那里有港口、矿山、岩石山口和村庄，很少有士兵愿意穿越无人区为他们的盟友夺取这些地方。

Skilled diplomatists, compelled to talk out loud to the warring peoples, learned how to use a large repertory of stereotypes. They were dealing with a precarious alliance of powers, each of which was maintaining its war unity only by the most careful leadership. The ordinary soldier and his wife, heroic and selfless beyond anything in the chronicles of courage, were still not heroic enough to face death gladly for all the ideas which were said by the foreign offices of foreign powers to be essential to the future of civilization. There were ports, and mines, rocky mountain passes, and villages that few soldiers would willingly have crossed No Man's Land to obtain for their allies.

现在，在一个国家，控制着外交部、最高指挥部和大多数媒体的主战派，对几个邻国的领土提出了主权要求。有教养的阶层把这些领土称为大鲁里塔尼亚，他们认为吉卜林、特赖奇克和莫里斯·巴雷斯是百分之百的鲁里塔尼亚人。但这个宏伟的想法并没有在国外引起热情。因此，正如他们的桂冠诗人所说，鲁里塔尼亚的政治家们把鲁里塔尼亚天才的这朵最优秀的花朵放在心上，开始分而治之。他们把领土划分成几个部分。对于每一部分，他们都援引了他们的一个或多个盟友难以抗拒的刻板印象，因为这个盟友有自己的主权要求，希望通过使用同样的刻板印象来获得认可。

Now it happened in one nation that the war party which was in control of the foreign office, the high command, and most of the press, had claims on the territory of several of its neighbors. These claims were called the Greater Ruritania by the cultivated classes who regarded Kipling, Treitschke, and Maurice Barres as one hundred percent Ruritanian. But the grandiose idea aroused no enthusiasm abroad. So holding this finest flower of the Ruritanian genius, as their poet laureate said, to their hearts, Ruritania's statesmen went forth to divide and conquer. They divided the claim into sectors. For each piece they invoked that stereotype which some one or more of their allies found it difficult to resist, because that ally had claims for which it hoped to find approval by the use of this same stereotype.

第一部分恰好是一片居住着外来农民的山区。鲁里塔尼亚要求将其作为其自然地理边界的补充。如果你长时间关注自然的不可言喻的价值，那些外来农民就会消失在雾中，只能看到山坡。下一个部分居住着鲁里塔尼亚人，根据任何民族都不应生活在外来统治下的原则，他们被重新吞并。接下来是一个具有相当重要商业意义的城市，鲁里塔尼亚人并没有居住。但直到十八世纪，它一直是鲁里塔尼亚的一部分，根据历史权利的原则，它被吞并。再往前，有一个由外国人拥有和开采的优质矿藏。根据损害赔偿的原则，它被吞并。在此之外，有一块 97% 的领土居住着外国人，构成了另一个国家的自然地理边界，历史上从未成为鲁里塔尼亚的一部分。但鲁里塔尼亚联邦中的一个省份以前曾在这些市场上进行贸易，上层阶级的文化是鲁里塔尼亚文化。基于文化优越性和捍卫文明的必要性，这些土地被占领。最后，有一个港口在地理、种族、经济、历史和传统上与鲁里塔尼亚完全脱节。要求建立这个港口的理由是需要国防。

The first sector happened to be a mountainous region inhabited by alien peasants. Ruritania demanded it to complete her natural geographical frontier. If you fixed your attention long enough on the ineffable value of what is natural, those alien peasants just dissolved into fog, and only the slope of the mountains was visible. The next sector was inhabited by Ruritanians, and on the principle that no people ought to live under alien rule, they were re-annexed. Then came a city of considerable commercial importance, not inhabited by Ruritanians. But until the Eighteenth Century it had been part of Ruritania, and on the principle of Historic Right it was annexed. Farther on there was a splendid mineral deposit owned by aliens and worked by aliens. On the principle of reparation for damage it was annexed. Beyond this there was a territory inhabited 97% by aliens, constituting the natural geographical frontier of another nation, never historically a part of Ruritania. But one of the provinces which had been federated into Ruritania had formerly traded in those markets, and the upper class culture was Ruritanian. On the principle of cultural superiority and the necessity of defending civilization, the lands were claimed. Finally, there was a port wholly disconnected from Ruritania geographically, ethnically, economically, historically, traditionally. It was demanded on the ground that it was needed for national defense.

在结束第一次世界大战的条约中，你可以举出很多这样的例子。现在，我并不想暗示我认为可以始终如一地按照这些原则中的任何一个来重新安置欧洲。我确信不可能。这些如此自命不凡和绝对的原则的使用本身就意味着和解的精神没有占上风，因此，和平的实质并不存在。当你开始讨论工厂、矿山、山脉甚至政治权威作为某个永恒原则的完美例子时，你不是在争论，而是在战斗。那个永恒的原则会排除所有的反对意见，将问题与其背景和环境隔离开来，并在你心中激起某种强烈的情感，这种情感与原则相符，与码头、仓库和房地产极不相符。从这种情绪开始，你就无法停止。存在着真正的危险。为了应对它，你必须援引更绝对的原则来捍卫那些可能受到攻击的东西。然后你必须保卫防线，建立缓冲区，并为缓冲区建立缓冲区，直到整个事件变得如此混乱，以至于打架似乎比继续谈话更不危险。

In the treaties that concluded the Great War you can multiply examples of this kind. Now I do not wish to imply that I think it was possible to resettle Europe consistently on any one of these principles. I am certain that it was not. The very use of these principles, so pretentious and so absolute, meant that the spirit of accommodation did not prevail and that, therefore, the substance of peace was not there. For the moment you start to discuss factories, mines, mountains, or even political authority, as perfect examples of some eternal principle or other, you are not arguing, you are fighting. That eternal principle censors out all the objections, isolates the issue from its background and its context, and sets going in you some strong emotion, appropriate enough to the principle, highly inappropriate to the docks, warehouses, and real estate. And having started in that mood you cannot stop. A real danger exists. To meet it you have to invoke more absolute principles in order to defend what is open to attack. Then you have to defend the defenses, erect buffers, and buffers for the buffers, until the whole affair is so scrambled that it seems less dangerous to fight than to keep on talking.
