某些线索通常有助于发现刻板印象的虚假绝对主义。在鲁里塔尼亚宣传中，各种原则如此迅速地相互覆盖，以至于人们很容易看出论点是如何构建的。一系列矛盾表明，对于每个领域，都采用了刻板印象，这将抹杀所有干扰主张的事实。这种矛盾通常是一个很好的线索。

There are certain clues which often help in detecting the false absolutism of a stereotype. In the case of the Ruritanian propaganda the principles blanketed each other so rapidly that one could readily see how the argument had been constructed. The series of contradictions showed that for each sector that stereotype was employed which would obliterate all the facts that interfered with the claim. Contradiction of this sort is often a good clue.





2

2

另一个原因是无法考虑空间因素。例如，1918 年春，许多人对俄国撤退感到震惊，要求“重建东线”。他们设想的战争是两条战线，当其中一条战线消失时，立即有人要求重建。失业的日本军队将代替俄国军队驻守前线。但有一个无法克服的障碍。符拉迪沃斯托克和东线战线之间有五千英里的国土，一条铁路断了。然而，这五千英里不会留在狂热分子的脑海中。他们坚信东线战线是必要的，他们对日本军队的英勇无畏充满信心，以至于在心理上，他们把这支军队从符拉迪沃斯托克投射到波兰，就像是乘坐魔毯一样。我们的军事当局徒劳地争辩说，将军队登陆西伯利亚边缘与到达德国人几乎没有关系，就像从地下室爬到伍尔沃斯大楼的屋顶与到达月球几乎没有关系一样。

Inability to take account of space is another. In the spring of 1918, for example, large numbers of people, appalled by the withdrawal of Russia, demanded the "reestablishment of an Eastern Front." The war, as they had conceived it, was on two fronts, and when one of them disappeared there was an instant demand that it be recreated. The unemployed Japanese army was to man the front, substituting for the Russian. But there was one insuperable obstacle. Between Vladivostok and the eastern battleline there were five thousand miles of country, spanned by one broken down railway. Yet those five thousand miles would not stay in the minds of the enthusiasts. So overwhelming was their conviction that an eastern front was needed, and so great their confidence in the valor of the Japanese army, that, mentally, they had projected that army from Vladivostok to Poland on a magic carpet. In vain our military authorities argued that to land troops on the rim of Siberia had as little to do with reaching the Germans, as climbing from the cellar to the roof of the Woolworth building had to do with reaching the moon.

这次战争的刻板印象是两线作战。自从人们开始想象第一次世界大战以来，他们就认为德国夹在法国和俄罗斯之间。一代或两代战略家一直以这种视觉形象作为他们所有计算的起点。近四年来，他们看到的每一张作战地图都加深了他们这就是战争的印象。当事态发生新的转变时，很难再像当时那样看待它们。人们是通过刻板印象来看待它们的，与之相矛盾的事实，例如从日本到波兰的距离，无法生动地进入人们的意识。

The stereotype in this instance was the war on two fronts. Ever since men had begun to imagine the Great War they had conceived Germany held between France and Russia. One generation of strategists, and perhaps two, had lived with that visual image as the starting point of all their calculations. For nearly four years every battle-map they saw had deepened the impression that this was the war. When affairs took a new turn, it was not easy to see them as they were then. They were seen through the stereotype, and facts which conflicted with it, such as the distance from Japan to Poland, were incapable of coming vividly into consciousness.

值得注意的是，美国当局比法国当局更现实地处理新事实。部分原因是（1914 年之前）他们没有对大陆上发生战争的先入为主的观念；部分原因是美国人全神贯注于动员军队，对西线的看法本身就是刻板印象，使他们 对其他战场没有任何生动的认识。1918 年春天，这种美国观点无法与传统的法国观点相抗衡，因为虽然美国人对自己的力量深信不疑，但当时的法国人（在康蒂尼和第二次马恩河战役之前）却对此深表怀疑。美国人的自信弥漫在美国刻板印象中，赋予它拥有意识的力量、活力和明智的刺激、对意志的刺激作用、作为欲望对象的情感兴趣、与手头活动的一致性，詹姆斯指出，这些都是我们认为“真实”的特征。法国人绝望地坚持他们所接受的形象。当事实、粗略的地理事实与先入之见不符时，他们要么被排除在外，要么事实本身被扭曲。因此，日本人到达五千英里外的德国人的困难在一定程度上被德国人带往半路以外的地区所克服。1918 年 3 月至 6 月间，据说有一支德国军队在东西伯利亚作战。这支幻影军队由一些实际看到的德国战俘、更多想象中的德国战俘组成，主要是因为人们误以为这五千英里的距离并不存在。

It is interesting to note that the American authorities dealt with the new facts more realistically than the French. In part, this was because (previous to 1914) they had no preconception of a war upon the continent; in part because the Americans, engrossed in the mobilization of their forces, had a vision of the western front which was itself a stereotype that excluded from their consciousness any very vivid sense of the other theatres of war. In the spring of 1918 this American view could not compete with the traditional French view, because while the Americans believed enormously in their own powers, the French at that time (before Cantigny and the Second Marne) had the gravest doubts. The American confidence suffused the American stereotype, gave it that power to possess consciousness, that liveliness and sensible pungency, that stimulating effect upon the will, that emotional interest as an object of desire, that congruity with the activity in hand, which James notes as characteristic of what we regard as "real." The French in despair remained fixed on their accepted image. And when facts, gross geographical facts, would not fit with the preconception, they were either censored out of mind, or the facts were themselves stretched out of shape. Thus the difficulty of the Japanese reaching the Germans five thousand miles away was, in measure, overcome by bringing the Germans more than half way to meet them. Between March and June 1918, there was supposed to be a German army operating in Eastern Siberia. This phantom army consisted of some German prisoners actually seen, more German prisoners thought about, and chiefly of the delusion that those five thousand intervening miles did not really exist.





3

3

真正理解空间并非易事。如果我在地图上从孟买到香港画一条直线并测量距离，我根本无法知道我航行需要经过的距离。即使我测量了必须穿越的实际距离，在知道有哪些船只在运行、它们何时开航、它们行驶的速度有多快、我是否能找到住处并支付得起费用之前，我仍然一无所知。在实际生活中，空间是一个可用的交通工具问题，而不是几何平面问题，就像那位老铁路大亨在威胁要让一个冒犯他的城市的街道上长草时所知道的那样。如果我开车问离目的地有多远，我会骂那个告诉我有三英里却没有提到六英里绕行路线的人是个十足的傻瓜。如果告诉我步行距离是三英里，那对我来说毫无意义。我还不如告诉我直线距离是一英里。我不会像乌鸦一样飞，也不会像步行一样。我必须知道，对于汽车来说，这是九英里，而且，如果是这样的话，其中六英里是车辙和水坑。我会把告诉我是三英里的行人称为讨厌鬼，并认为告诉我是一英里的飞行员是可恶的。他们俩都在谈论他们必须覆盖的空间，而不是我必须覆盖的空间。

A true conception of space is not a simple matter. If I draw a straight line on a map between Bombay and Hong Kong and measure the distance, I have learned nothing whatever about the distance I should have to cover on a voyage. And even if I measure the actual distance that I must traverse, I still know very little until I know what ships are in the service, when they run, how fast they go, whether I can secure accommodation and afford to pay for it. In practical life space is a matter of available transportation, not of geometrical planes, as the old railroad magnate knew when he threatened to make grass grow in the streets of a city that had offended him. If I am motoring and ask how far it is to my destination, I curse as an unmitigated booby the man who tells me it is three miles, and does not mention a six mile detour. It does me no good to be told that it is three miles if you walk. I might as well be told it is one mile as the crow flies. I do not fly like a crow, and I am not walking either. I must know that it is nine miles for a motor car, and also, if that is the case, that six of them are ruts and puddles. I call the pedestrian a nuisance who tells me it is three miles and think evil of the aviator who told me it was one mile. Both of them are talking about the space they have to cover, not the space I must cover.

在划定边界线时，由于未能了解一个地区的实际地理情况，出现了荒谬的复杂情况。根据自决等一般公式，政治家们在不同时期在地图上划线，当现场测量时，这些线穿过工厂中间、村庄街道中心、教堂中殿对角线或农民小屋厨房和卧室之间。在放牧国家，有将牧场与水、牧场与市场分开的边界，在工业国家，有将铁路终点站与铁路分开的边界。在彩色民族地图上，这条线在民族上是公正的，也就是说，在那个民族地图的世界中是公正的。

In the drawing of boundary lines absurd complications have arisen through failure to conceive the practical geography of a region. Under some general formula like self-determination statesmen have at various times drawn lines on maps, which, when surveyed on the spot, ran through the middle of a factory, down the center of a village street, diagonally across the nave of a church, or between the kitchen and bedroom of a peasant's cottage. There have been frontiers in a grazing country which separated pasture from water, pasture from market, and in an industrial country, railheads from railroad. On the colored ethnic map the line was ethnically just, that is to say, just in the world of that ethnic map.





4

4

但是时间，和空间一样，情况很糟糕。一个常见的例子是，一个人试图通过制定一份详尽的遗嘱来控制他死后的钱财。他的曾孙亨利·詹姆斯写道：“威廉·詹姆斯一世的目的是让他的孩子们（他去世时，其中几个还未成年）通过勤奋和经验获得资格，享受他希望留给他们的大笔遗产，为此，他留下了一份遗嘱，里面充满了限制和指示。他由此表明，他对自己判断的信心和对后代道德福祉的关心是多么强烈。”法院推翻了遗嘱。因为法律在反对永久继承时，承认允许任何人将自己的道德模板强加于未知的未来，其用处是有明显的限制的。但强加这种模板的愿望是一种非常人性化的特性，如此人性化以至于法律允许它在死后有限的时间内发挥作用。

But time, no less than space, fares badly. A common example is that of the man who tries by making an elaborate will to control his money long after his death. "It had been the purpose of the first William James," writes his great-grandson Henry James, "to provide that his children (several of whom were under age when he died) should qualify themselves by industry and experience to enjoy the large patrimony which he expected to bequeath to them, and with that in view he left a will which was a voluminous compound of restraints and instructions. He showed thereby how great were both his confidence in his own judgment and his solicitude for the moral welfare of his descendants." The courts upset the will. For the law in its objection to perpetuities recognizes that there are distinct limits to the usefulness of allowing anyone to impose his moral stencil upon an unknown future. But the desire to impose it is a very human trait, so human that the law permits it to operate for a limited time after death.

任何宪法的修正条款都是作者对其观点在后代影响范围的信心的一个很好的指标。我相信，美国有些州的宪法几乎无法修正。制定这些宪法的人可能对时间的变迁知之甚少：对他们来说，此时此刻是如此确定，而来世是如此模糊或可怕，以至于他们有勇气说出他们死后的生活应该如何过。而且由于宪法难以修正，热心于永生的人喜欢在这块不朽的铜板上写下各种规则和限制，只要对未来保持一点谦逊的态度，这些规则和限制就不应该比普通的法令更永久。

The amending clause of any constitution is a good index of the confidence the authors entertained about the reach of their opinions in the succeeding generations. There are, I believe, American state constitutions which are almost incapable of amendment. The men who made them could have had but little sense of the flux of time: to them the Here and Now was so brilliantly certain, the Hereafter so vague or so terrifying, that they had the courage to say how life should run after they were gone. And then because constitutions are difficult to amend, zealous people with a taste for mortmain have loved to write on this imperishable brass all kinds of rules and restrictions that, given any decent humility about the future, ought to be no more permanent than an ordinary statute.

我们普遍持有一种关于时间的假设。对一个人来说，一个在他的整个有意识的生活中一直存在的制度是宇宙中永恒不变的家具的一部分；对另一个人来说，它却是短暂的。地质时间与生物时间截然不同。社会时间是最复杂的。政治家必须决定是为紧急情况计算还是为长远考虑。有些决定必须根据接下来两个小时会发生什么来做出；其他决定则要根据一周、一个月、一个季节、十年后会发生什么，当孩子长大成人或他们的孩子的孩子长大成人时。智慧的一个重要部分是能够区分真正属于手头事物的时间概念。使用错误时间概念的人从忽视现在的梦想家到什么都看不见的庸人。真正的价值尺度对相对时间有着非常敏锐的感觉。

A presumption about time enters widely into our opinions. To one person an institution which has existed for the whole of his conscious life is part of the permanent furniture of the universe: to another it is ephemeral. Geological time is very different from biological time. Social time is most complex. The statesman has to decide whether to calculate for the emergency or for the long run. Some decisions have to be made on the basis of what will happen in the next two hours; others on what will happen in a week, a month, a season, a decade, when the children have grown up, or their children's children. An important part of wisdom is the ability to distinguish the time-conception that properly belongs to the thing in hand. The person who uses the wrong time-conception ranges from the dreamer who ignores the present to the philistine who can see nothing else. A true scale of values has a very acute sense of relative time.

遥远的时间，过去和未来，必须以某种方式来构想。但正如詹姆斯所说，“对于较长的时间，我们没有直接的‘实现’感。”我们立即感受到的最长的时间是所谓的“似是而非的现在”。根据铁钦纳的说法，它持续了大约六秒钟。“这段时间内的所有印象都同时呈现在我们 面前。这使我们能够感知变化和事件以及静止的物体。感知的现在由概念的现在补充。通过将感知与记忆图像相结合，过去的整天、整月甚至整年都被带入现在。”

Distant time, past and future, has somehow to be conceived. But as James says, "of the longer duration we have no direct 'realizing' sense." The longest duration which we immediately feel is what is called the "specious present." It endures, according to Titchener, for about six seconds. "All impressions within this period of time are present to us at once . This makes it possible for us to perceive changes and events as well as stationary objects. The perceptual present is supplemented by the ideational present. Through the combination of perceptions with memory images, entire days, months, and even years of the past are brought together into the present."

在这种观念上的现在，正如詹姆斯所说，生动性与我们在其中感知到的辨别数量成正比。因此，一个我们无聊无所事事的假期在我们度过时过得很慢，但在记忆中却似乎很短暂。大活动会迅速消磨时间，但在记忆中它持续的时间很长。关于我们辨别的数量和我们的时间观之间的关系，詹姆斯有一段有趣的文字：

In this ideational present, vividness, as James said, is proportionate to the number of discriminations we perceive within it. Thus a vacation in which we were bored with nothing to do passes slowly while we are in it, but seems very short in memory. Great activity kills time rapidly, but in memory its duration is long. On the relation between the amount we discriminate and our time perspective James has an interesting passage:

“我们有充分的理由认为，生物在直觉上感觉到的持续时间长度和可能填充的事件的精细程度上可能存在巨大差异。冯·贝尔对这种差异对自然面貌的影响进行了一些有趣的计算。假设我们能够在一秒钟的时间内清楚地注意到 10,000 个事件，而不是像现在这样仅仅 10 个；如果我们的生命注定要容纳相同数量的印象，那么它可能会短 1000 倍。我们的寿命应该不到一个月，而且个人对季节的变化一无所知。如果出生在冬天，我们应该相信夏天，就像我们现在相信石炭纪的炎热一样。有机生物的运动对于我们的感觉来说是如此缓慢，以至于只能推断，而不能看到。太阳会在天空中静止不动，月亮几乎没有变化，等等。但现在反过来假设，假设一个生物只得到我们感觉的千分之一在他看来，冬天和夏天就像一刻钟那么短。蘑菇和生长更快的植物会迅速生长，看起来像是瞬间的产物；一年生灌木会像不停沸腾的泉水一样从地上升起和落下；动物的运动就像我们看不见子弹和炮弹的运动一样；太阳会像流星一样划过天空，身后留下一条火红的轨迹，等等。”

"We have every reason to think that creatures may possibly differ enormously in the amounts of duration which they intuitively feel, and in the fineness of the events that may fill it. Von Baer has indulged in some interesting computations of the effect of such differences in changing the aspect of Nature. Suppose we were able, within the length of a second, to note 10,000 events distinctly, instead of barely 10 as now; if our life were then destined to hold the same number of impressions, it might be 1000 times as short. We should live less than a month, and personally know nothing of the change of seasons. If born in winter, we should believe in summer as we now believe in the heats of the carboniferous era. The motions of organic beings would be so slow to our senses as to be inferred, not seen. The sun would stand still in the sky, the moon be almost free from change, and so on. But now reverse the hypothesis and suppose a being to get only one 1000th part of the sensations we get in a given time, and consequently to live 1000 times as long. Winters and summers will be to him like quarters of an hour. Mushrooms and the swifter growing plants will shoot into being so rapidly as to appear instantaneous creations; annual shrubs will rise and fall from the earth like restless boiling water springs; the motions of animals will be as invisible as are to us the movements of bullets and cannon-balls; the sun will scour through the sky like a meteor, leaving a fiery trail behind him, etc."





5

5

在他的《历史大纲》中，韦尔斯先生做出了巨大的努力，试图形象化“历史时间与地质时间的真实比例”。如果用三英寸的空间来表示从哥伦布到我们今天的时间，读者必须走 55 英尺才能看到阿尔塔马拉洞穴画家的年代，走 550 英尺才能看到更早的尼安德特人，走一英里左右才能看到最后的恐龙。或多或少精确的年代学直到公元前 1000 年之后才开始，而那时“阿卡德-苏美尔帝国的萨尔贡一世是一个遥远的记忆，……比君士坦丁大帝离当今世界还要遥远……汉谟拉比已经死了一千年……英格兰的巨石阵已经有一千年的历史了。”

In his Outline of History Mr. Wells has made a gallant effort to visualize "the true proportions of historical to geological time" On a scale which represents the time from Columbus to ourselves by three inches of space, the reader would have to walk 55 feet to see the date of the painters of the Altamara caves, 550 feet to see the earlier Neanderthalers, a mile or so to the last of the dinosaurs. More or less precise chronology does not begin until after 1000 B.C., and at that time "Sargon I of the Akkadian-Sumerian Empire was a remote memory,… more remote than is Constantine the Great from the world of the present day…. Hammurabi had been dead a thousand years… Stonehedge in England was already a thousand years old."

威尔斯先生的写作是有目的的。“在短短的一万年中，这些单位（人类结合而成的单位）从早期新石器文化的小家族部落发展成为当今庞大的联合王国——虽然庞大，但仍然太小，太片面。”威尔斯先生希望通过改变我们当前问题的时间观来改变道德观。然而，天文时间测量、地质时间、生物时间，任何将现在最小化的望远镜测量并不比微观时间“更真实”。西米恩·斯特伦斯基先生坚持认为“如果威尔斯先生正在考虑他的副标题《人类可能的未来》，他有权要求用多少个世纪来解决问题。如果他正在考虑挽救这个在第一次世界大战的影响下摇摇欲坠的西方文明，他必须考虑几十年和几十年。”这完全取决于你采用这种测量的实际目的。有些情况下需要延长时间视角，而其他情况下则需要缩短时间视角。

Mr. Wells was writing with a purpose. "In the brief period of ten thousand years these units (into which men have combined) have grown from the small family tribe of the early neolithic culture to the vast united realms—vast yet still too small and partial—of the present time." Mr. Wells hoped by changing the time perspective on our present problems to change the moral perspective. Yet the astronomical measure of time, the geological, the biological, any telescopic measure which minimizes the present is not "more true" than a microscopic. Mr. Simeon Strunsky is right when he insists that "if Mr. Wells is thinking of his subtitle, The Probable Future of Mankind, he is entitled to ask for any number of centuries to work out his solution. If he is thinking of the salvaging of this western civilization, reeling under the effects of the Great War, he must think in decades and scores of years." It all depends upon the practical purpose for which you adopt the measure. There are situations when the time perspective needs to be lengthened, and others when it needs to be shortened.

有人说，即使有 1500 万中国人死​​于饥荒，也无所谓，因为两代人之后，出生率就会弥补这一损失。这个人用时间观念来为自己的惰性辩解。一个人因为眼前的困难而让一个健康的年轻人陷入贫困，他忘记了这个乞丐的生命有多长。那些为了眼前的和平，愿意放纵侵略性帝国的胃口来收买它的人们，让一个华而不实的现实干扰了他们孩子的和平。那些对麻烦的邻居没有耐心，想把一切都“摊牌”的人，同样也是华而不实的现实的受害者。

The man who says that it does not matter if 15,000,000 Chinese die of famine, because in two generations the birthrate will make up the loss, has used a time perspective to excuse his inertia. A person who pauperizes a healthy young man because he is sentimentally overimpressed with an immediate difficulty has lost sight of the duration of the beggar's life. The people who for the sake of an immediate peace are willing to buy off an aggressive empire by indulging its appetite have allowed a specious present to interfere with the peace of their children. The people who will not be patient with a troublesome neighbor, who want to bring everything to a "showdown" are no less the victims of a specious present.





6

6

几乎每一个社会问题都涉及到时间的正确计算。假设，例如，这是一个木材问题。有些树长得比其他树快。那么，一个合理的森林政策就是，每个季节砍伐的每种树种和每种树龄的树木数量，都通过重新种植来弥补。只要这个计算正确，就达到了最真实的节约。砍伐少是浪费，砍伐多是剥削。但可能会出现紧急情况，比如战争中需要飞机云杉，这时必须超过一年的限额。一个警觉的政府会认识到这一点，并把恢复平衡视为对未来的负担。

Into almost every social problem the proper calculation of time enters. Suppose, for example, it is a question of timber. Some trees grow faster than others. Then a sound forest policy is one in which the amount of each species and of each age cut in each season is made good by replanting. In so far as that calculation is correct the truest economy has been reached. To cut less is waste, and to cut more is exploitation. But there may come an emergency, say the need for aeroplane spruce in a war, when the year's allowance must be exceeded. An alert government will recognize that and regard the restoration of the balance as a charge upon the future.

煤炭涉及不同的时间理论，因为煤炭与树木不同，是按照地质时间尺度生产的。煤炭的供应是有限的。因此，正确的社会政策需要对世界可用储量、预计的可能性、目前的使用率、目前的使用经济性和替代燃料进行复杂的计算。但是，当计算结果出来后，它必须最终与涉及时间的理想标准相一致。例如，假设工程师得出结论，目前的燃料正在以一定的速度耗尽；除非有新的发现，否则工业将不得不在未来某个确定的时间进入收缩阶段。那么，我们必须确定，在采取了所有可行的经济措施之后，我们将使用多少节俭和自我克制，以免掠夺后代。但是，我们应该把后代看作什么呢？我们的孙子？我们的曾孙？也许我们会决定以一百年为单位来计算，相信如果立即明确了必要性，那么这足以发现替代燃料。当然，这些数字是假设的。但是，在这样计算时，我们将运用我们拥有的理由。我们将在公众舆论中赋予社会时间一席之地。现在让我们想象一个略有不同的情况：一个城市与一家有轨电车公司之间的合同。该公司表示，除非获得主干道九十九年的垄断权，否则它不会投资。在提出这一要求的人看来，九十九年的时间太长，意味着“永远”。但是，假设有理由认为，由轨道上的中央发电厂运行的地面车将在二十年后过时。那么，这是一份最不明智的合同，因为你实际上是在让后代不得不使用劣质的交通工具。在签订这样的合同时，城市官员缺乏对九十九年的现实意识。现在给公司补贴以吸引资本远比通过放纵虚假的永恒感来刺激投资要好得多。没有哪个城市官员和公司官员在谈论九十九年时有真正的时间感。

Coal involves a different theory of time, because coal, unlike a tree, is produced on the scale of geological time. The supply is limited. Therefore a correct social policy involves intricate computation of the available reserves of the world, the indicated possibilities, the present rate of use, the present economy of use, and the alternative fuels. But when that computation has been reached it must finally be squared with an ideal standard involving time. Suppose, for example, that engineers conclude that the present fuels are being exhausted at a certain rate; that barring new discoveries industry will have to enter a phase of contraction at some definite time in the future. We have then to determine how much thrift and self-denial we will use, after all feasible economies have been exercised, in order not to rob posterity. But what shall we consider posterity? Our grandchildren? Our great grandchildren? Perhaps we shall decide to calculate on a hundred years, believing that to be ample time for the discovery of alternative fuels if the necessity is made clear at once. The figures are, of course, hypothetical. But in calculating that way we shall be employing what reason we have. We shall be giving social time its place in public opinion. Let us now imagine a somewhat different case: a contract between a city and a trolley-car company. The company says that it will not invest its capital unless it is granted a monopoly of the main highway for ninety-nine years. In the minds of the men who make that demand ninety-nine years is so long as to mean "forever." But suppose there is reason to think that surface cars, run from a central power plant on tracks, are going out of fashion in twenty years. Then it is a most unwise contract to make, for you are virtually condemning a future generation to inferior transportation. In making such a contract the city officials lack a realizing sense of ninety-nine years. Far better to give the company a subsidy now in order to attract capital than to stimulate investment by indulging a fallacious sense of eternity. No city official and no company official has a sense of real time when he talks about ninety-nine years.

通俗历史是时间混淆的快乐猎场。例如，对于普通英国人来说，克伦威尔的行为、《联合法案》的腐败、1847 年的大饥荒都是早已去世的人所遭受的苦难，而这些苦难是由早已去世的行动者所为，与这些在世的人（无论是爱尔兰人还是英国人）没有任何真正的联系。但在一位爱国的爱尔兰人的心目中，这些相同的事件几乎是同时发生的。他的记忆就像一幅历史画，维吉尔和但丁并肩坐在一起交谈。这些远景和缩短是民族之间的巨大障碍。对于一个传统的人来说，记住另一个传统中同时发生的事情是非常困难的。

Popular history is a happy hunting ground of time confusions. To the average Englishman, for example, the behavior of Cromwell, the corruption of the Act of Union, the Famine of 1847 are wrongs suffered by people long dead and done by actors long dead with whom no living person, Irish or English, has any real connection. But in the mind of a patriotic Irishman these same events are almost contemporary. His memory is like one of those historical paintings, where Virgil and Dante sit side by side conversing. These perspectives and foreshortenings are a great barrier between peoples. It is ever so difficult for a person of one tradition to remember what is contemporary in the tradition of another.

几乎没有任何所谓的历史权利或历史错误可以称为对过去的真正客观的看法。以法德关于阿尔萨斯-洛林的辩论为例。这完全取决于您选择的原始日期。如果您从 Rauraci 和 Sequani 开始，这些土地在历史上是古高卢的一部分。如果您更喜欢亨利一世，它们在历史上是德国领土；如果您选择 1273 年，它们属于奥地利王朝；如果您选择 1648 年和威斯特伐利亚和约，它们大部分是法国的；如果您选择路易十四和 1688 年，它们几乎都是法国的。如果您使用历史论据，您相当肯定地会选择过去的那些日期来支持您对现在应该做什么的看法。

Almost nothing that goes by the name of Historic Rights or Historic Wrongs can be called a truly objective view of the past. Take, for example, the Franco-German debate about Alsace-Lorraine. It all depends on the original date you select. If you start with the Rauraci and Sequani, the lands are historically part of Ancient Gaul. If you prefer Henry I, they are historically a German territory; if you take 1273 they belong to the House of Austria; if you take 1648 and the Peace of Westphalia, most of them are French; if you take Louis XIV and the year 1688 they are almost all French. If you are using the argument from history you are fairly certain to select those dates in the past which support your view of what should be done now.

关于“种族”和民族的争论常常暴露出同样武断的时间观。在战争期间，在强烈情感的影响下，人们普遍认为“日耳曼人”与“盎格鲁-撒克逊人”和法国人之间的差异是永恒的。他们一直是对立的种族。然而，一代人之前，像弗里曼这样的历史学家强调西欧各民族的共同日耳曼血统，民族学家肯定会坚持认为德国人、英国人和大部分法国人都是曾经共同血统的分支。一般规则是：如果你喜欢今天的某个民族，你会顺着枝条追溯到主干；如果你不喜欢他们，你会坚持认为不同的枝条是不同的主干。在一种情况下，你会把注意力集中在他们变得可区分之前的时期；在另一种情况下，你会把注意力集中在他们变得不同的时期之后。符合这种情绪的观点被认为是“真理”。

Arguments about "races" and nationalities often betray the same arbitrary view of time. During the war, under the influence of powerful feeling, the difference between "Teutons" on the one hand, and "Anglo-Saxons" and French on the other, was popularly believed to be an eternal difference. They had always been opposing races. Yet a generation ago, historians, like Freeman, were emphasizing the common Teutonic origin of the West European peoples, and ethnologists would certainly insist that the Germans, English, and the greater part of the French are branches of what was once a common stock. The general rule is: if you like a people to-day you come down the branches to the trunk; if you dislike them you insist that the separate branches are separate trunks. In one case you fix your attention on the period before they were distinguishable; in the other on the period after which they became distinct. And the view which fits the mood is taken as the "truth."

一个可爱的变体是家谱。通常有一对夫妇被指定为原始祖先，如果可能的话，这对夫妇与诺曼征服等光荣事件有关。这对夫妇没有祖先。他们不是后代。然而他们是祖先的后代，而某某是他家的创始人这一表述并不意味着他是他家的亚当，而是他是理想的特定祖先，或者可能是有记录的最早祖先。但家谱表表现出更深的偏见。除非女性血统恰好是特别显着的，否则血统是通过男性追溯的。这棵树是雄性的。在不同的时刻，雌性会加入其中，就像流动的蜜蜂落在一棵古老的苹果树上一样。

An amiable variation is the family tree. Usually one couple are appointed the original ancestors, if possible, a couple associated with an honorific event like the Norman Conquest. That couple have no ancestors. They are not descendants. Yet they were the descendants of ancestors, and the expression that So-and-So was the founder of his house means not that he is the Adam of his family, but that he is the particular ancestor from whom it is desirable to start, or perhaps the earliest ancestor of which there is a record. But genealogical tables exhibit a deeper prejudice. Unless the female line happens to be especially remarkable descent is traced down through the males. The tree is male. At various moments females accrue to it as itinerant bees light upon an ancient apple tree.





7

7

但未来是最虚幻的时期。我们在这里很容易跳过必要的步骤，而且由于我们受希望或怀疑的支配，我们很容易夸大或最小化完成过程各个部分所需的时间。关于工薪阶层在工业管理中应发挥的作用的讨论充满了这种困难。因为管理这个词涵盖了许多功能。其中一些不需要培训；一些需要一点培训；其他一些只能在一生中学会。而真正有辨别力的工业民主化计划将基于适当的时间顺序，这样承担责任将与补充的工业培训计划并行。无产阶级突然专政的提议是试图取消中间的准备时间；抵制所有责任分担是试图否认人类能力随着时间的推移而改变。民主的原始观念，例如轮换任职、蔑视专家，其实不过是古老神话中的一个说法，即智慧女神从朱庇特的额头上诞生，成熟且全副武装。他们认为，需要多年学习的东西根本不需要学习。

But the future is the most illusive time of all. Our temptation here is to jump over necessary steps in the sequence; and as we are governed by hope or doubt, to exaggerate or to minimize the time required to complete various parts of a process. The discussion of the role to be exercised by wage-earners in the management of industry is riddled with this difficulty. For management is a word that covers many functions. Some of these require no training; some require a little training; others can be learned only in a lifetime. And the truly discriminating program of industrial democratization would be one based on the proper time sequence, so that the assumption of responsibility would run parallel to a complementary program of industrial training. The proposal for a sudden dictatorship of the proletariat is an attempt to do away with the intervening time of preparation; the resistance to all sharing of responsibility an attempt to deny the alteration of human capacity in the course of time. Primitive notions of democracy, such as rotation in office, and contempt for the expert, are really nothing but the old myth that the Goddess of Wisdom sprang mature and fully armed from the brow of Jove. They assume that what it takes years to learn need not be learned at all.

每当“落后民族”一词被用作政策依据时，时间观念就是决定性因素。例如，《国际联盟盟约》规定，“托管性质必须根据民族发展阶段的不同而不同”，以及其他理由。它断言，某些社区“已经达到了发展阶段”，可以暂时承认其独立，并接受建议和援助，“直到他们能够独立”。托管国和受托管国对时间观念的方式将深刻影响他们的关系。因此，在古巴问题上，美国政府的判断实际上与古巴爱国者的判断一致，尽管存在麻烦，但在强国如何对待弱国的历史上，没有比这更好的一页了。在那段历史中，估计往往不一致。无论帝国人民如何公开表达自己的观点，他们深信落后的落后是如此无望，不值得补救，或者如此有利可图，以至于补救它是不值得的，这种束缚已经恶化并毒害了世界和平。在少数情况下，落后意味着统治者需要一个前进的计划，一个具有明确标准和明确时间估计的计划。更常见的情况是，事实上，这种情况如此频繁，以至于似乎已经成为常态，落后被认为是自卑的内在和永恒标志。然后，任何减少落后的尝试都被看作是煽动，在这种情况下，它无疑是煽动。在我们自己的种族战争中，我们可以看到未能意识到时间会逐渐抹去黑人的奴隶道德，而基于这种道德的社会调节将开始崩溃的一些后果。

Whenever the phrase "backward people" is used as the basis of a policy, the conception of time is a decisive element. The Covenant of the League of Nations says, for example, that "the character of the mandate must differ according to the stage of the development of the people," as well as on other grounds. Certain communities, it asserts, "have reached a stage of development" where their independence can be provisionally recognized, subject to advice and assistance "until such time as they are able to stand alone." The way in which the mandatories and the mandated conceive that time will influence deeply their relations. Thus in the case of Cuba the judgment of the American government virtually coincided with that of the Cuban patriots, and though there has been trouble, there is no finer page in the history of how strong powers have dealt with the weak. Oftener in that history the estimates have not coincided. Where the imperial people, whatever its public expressions, has been deeply convinced that the backwardness of the backward was so hopeless as not to be worth remedying, or so profitable that it was not desirable to remedy it, the tie has festered and poisoned the peace of the world. There have been a few cases, very few, where backwardness has meant to the ruling power the need for a program of forwardness, a program with definite standards and definite estimates of time. Far more frequently, so frequently in fact as to seem the rule, backwardness has been conceived as an intrinsic and eternal mark of inferiority. And then every attempt to be less backward has been frowned upon as the sedition, which, under these conditions, it undoubtedly is. In our own race wars we can see some of the results of the failure to realize that time would gradually obliterate the slave morality of the Negro, and that social adjustment based on this morality would begin to break down.

我们很难不去想象未来会遵循我们现在的目标，消灭一切阻碍我们实现愿望的事物，或者使一切阻碍我们克服恐惧的事物永远存在。

It is hard not to picture the future as if it obeyed our present purposes, to annihilate whatever delays our desire, or immortalize whatever stands between us and our fears.





8

8

在整理舆论时，我们不仅要描绘比我们眼睛所能看到的更多的空间，比我们所能感受到的更多的时间，还要描述和判断比我们所能计算或生动想象的更多的人、更多的行为、更多的事物。我们必须总结和概括。我们必须挑选样本，并将它们视为典型。

In putting together our public opinions, not only do we have to picture more space than we can see with our eyes, and more time than we can feel, but we have to describe and judge more people, more actions, more things than we can ever count, or vividly imagine. We have to summarize and generalize. We have to pick out samples, and treat them as typical.

从一大类人中挑选出一个相当好的样本并不容易。这个问题属于统计学，对于数学基础不深的人来说，这是一件最困难的事情，尽管我曾经虔诚地想象自己能理解六本手册，但我的数学仍然很幼稚。它们对我所做的一切就是让我更加意识到分类和抽样有多么困难，我们多么容易将一点黄油涂满整个宇宙。

To pick fairly a good sample of a large class is not easy. The problem belongs to the science of statistics, and it is a most difficult affair for anyone whose mathematics is primitive, and mine remain azoic in spite of the half dozen manuals which I once devoutly imagined that I understood. All they have done for me is to make me a little more conscious of how hard it is to classify and to sample, how readily we spread a little butter over the whole universe.

不久前，英国谢菲尔德的一群社会工作者开始用对该市工人心理素质的准确描述来取代他们印象派的描述。他们想说谢菲尔德工人的心理素质如何，并有充分的理由这么说。他们发现，正如我们所有人在拒绝让最初的想法占上风时所发现的那样，他们被复杂的情况所困扰。关于他们使用的测试，这里无需多言，只是这是一个很大的问卷。为了便于说明，假设这些问题是对英国城市生活心理素质的公平测试。那么，从理论上讲，这些问题应该向工人阶级的每一位成员提出。但要知道谁是工人阶级并不容易。然而，再次假设人口普查知道如何对他们进行分类。那么，大约有 104,000 名男性和 107,000 名女性应该接受调查。他们有答案可以证明或驳斥关于“无知工人”或“聪明工人”的随意说法。但没人能想到要质疑全部二十万人。

Some time ago a group of social workers in Sheffield, England, started out to substitute an accurate picture of the mental equipment of the workers of that city for the impressionistic one they had. They wished to say, with some decent grounds for saying it, how the workers of Sheffield were equipped. They found, as we all find the moment we refuse to let our first notion prevail, that they were beset with complications. Of the test they employed nothing need be said here except that it was a large questionnaire. For the sake of the illustration, assume that the questions were a fair test of mental equipment for English city life. Theoretically, then, those questions should have been put to every member of the working class. But it is not so easy to know who are the working class. However, assume again that the census knows how to classify them. Then there were roughly 104,000 men and 107,000 women who ought to have been questioned. They possessed the answers which would justify or refute the casual phrase about the "ignorant workers" or the "intelligent workers." But nobody could think of questioning the whole two hundred thousand.

因此，社会工作者咨询了一位著名的统计学家鲍利教授。他建议他们，至少 408 名男性和 408 名女性将是一个公平的样本。根据数学计算，这个数字与平均水平的偏差不会超过 1/22。因此，他们必须询问至少 816 人，才能假装谈论普通工人。但他们应该联系哪 816 人呢？“我们可能已经收集了有关我们其中一人事先调查过的工人的详细信息；我们可能通过与俱乐部、传教所、医务室、礼拜场所、定居点的某些工人有联系的慈善绅士和女士来开展工作。但这种选择方法会产生完全没有价值的成果。这样挑选出来的工人根本不代表人们通常所说的‘普通工人’；他们只代表他们所属的小圈子。

So the social workers consulted an eminent statistician, Professor Bowley. He advised them that not less than 408 men and 408 women would prove to be a fair sample. According to mathematical calculation this number would not show a greater deviation from the average than 1 in 22. They had, therefore, to question at least 816 people before they could pretend to talk about the average workingman. But which 816 people should they approach? "We might have gathered particulars concerning workers to whom one or another of us had a pre-inquiry access; we might have worked through philanthropic gentlemen and ladies who were in contact with certain sections of workers at a club, a mission, an infirmary, a place of worship, a settlement. But such a method of selection would produce entirely worthless results. The workers thus selected would not be in any sense representative of what is popularly called 'the average run of workers;' they would represent nothing but the little coteries to which they belonged.

“我们花费了大量的时间和精力，严格遵守确保‘受害者’的正确方法，即通过某种‘中立’、‘偶然’或‘随机’的方法抓住工人。”他们这样做了。在采取了所有这些预防措施之后，他们得出的结论并不明确，只是根据他们的分类和调查问卷，在谢菲尔德 20 万名工人中，“约四分之一”的人“装备精良”，“接近四分之三”的人“装备不足”，“约十五分之一”的人“装备不良”。

"The right way of securing 'victims,' to which at immense cost of time and labour we rigidly adhered, is to get hold of your workers by some 'neutral' or 'accidental' or 'random' method of approach." This they did. And after all these precautions they came to no more definite conclusion than that on their classification and according to their questionnaire, among 200,000 Sheffield workers "about one quarter" were "well equipped," "approaching three-quarters" were "inadequately equipped" and that "about one-fifteenth" were "mal-equipped."

将这种认真、近乎迂腐的得出意见的方法与我们通常对大众的判断进行比较，对反复无常的爱尔兰人、逻辑严密的法国人、纪律严明的德国人、无知的斯拉夫人、诚实的中国人、不值得信任的日本人等等。所有这些都是从样本中得出的概括，但样本的选择方法在统计上完全不合理。因此，雇主将根据他所认识的最麻烦的雇员或最温顺的雇员来判断劳动力，许多激进团体都认为这是工人阶级的公平样本。有多少女性对“仆人问题”的看法只不过是她们自己对待仆人的方式的反映？随意的思维倾向于挑选或偶然发现一个支持或违背其偏见的样本，然后使其成为整个阶级的代表。

Compare this conscientious and almost pedantic method of arriving at an opinion, with our usual judgments about masses of people, about the volatile Irish, and the logical French, and the disciplined Germans, and the ignorant Slavs, and the honest Chinese, and the untrustworthy Japanese, and so on and so on. All these are generalizations drawn from samples, but the samples are selected by a method that statistically is wholly unsound. Thus the employer will judge labor by the most troublesome employee or the most docile that he knows, and many a radical group has imagined that it was a fair sample of the working class. How many women's views on the "servant question" are little more than the reflection of their own treatment of their servants? The tendency of the casual mind is to pick out or stumble upon a sample which supports or defies its prejudices, and then to make it the representative of a whole class.

当人们拒绝按照我们给他们的分类进行自我分类时，就会产生很多混乱。如果他们能保持我们给他们的分类，那么预言就会容易得多。但事实上，像工人阶级这样的短语只能在部分时间内涵盖部分事实。当你把所有收入低于一定水平的人都称为工人阶级时，你不得不假设，这样分类的人会按照你的刻板印象行事。至于这些人到底是谁，你不太清楚。工厂工人和矿工或多或少都符合，但农场工人、小农、小贩、小店主、办事员、仆人、士兵、警察、消防员则不在名单之列。当你呼吁“工人阶级”时，往往会将注意力集中在或多或少坚定的工会主义者身上，并将他们视为劳工；另外一千七百或一千八百万可能符合统计要求的人，则被默认为具有组织核心的观点。把工会代表大会的决议或知识分子撰写的小册子中表达的观点归咎于1918年至1921年的英国工人阶级是多么具有误导性。

A great deal of confusion arises when people decline to classify themselves as we have classified them. Prophecy would be so much easier if only they would stay where we put them. But, as a matter of fact, a phrase like the working class will cover only some of the truth for a part of the time. When you take all the people, below a certain level of income, and call them the working class, you cannot help assuming that the people so classified will behave in accordance with your stereotype. Just who those people are you are not quite certain. Factory hands and mine workers fit in more or less, but farm hands, small farmers, peddlers, little shop keepers, clerks, servants, soldiers, policemen, firemen slip out of the net. The tendency, when you are appealing to the "working class," is to fix your attention on two or three million more or less confirmed trade unionists, and treat them as Labor; the other seventeen or eighteen million, who might qualify statistically, are tacitly endowed with the point of view ascribed to the organized nucleus. How very misleading it was to impute to the British working class in 1918-1921 the point of view expressed in the resolutions of the Trades Union Congress or in the pamphlets written by intellectuals.

劳动者作为解放者的刻板印象选择了支持自己的证据，而拒绝了其他证据。因此，与工人的真实运动并行的，还有一种劳工运动的虚构，其中理想化的群众朝着理想的目标前进。这种虚构与未来有关。在未来，可能性几乎与概率、概率与确定性难以区分。如果未来足够长，人类的意志可能会把可以想象的事情变成非常可能的事情，把可能的事情变成肯定会发生的事情。詹姆斯称之为信仰阶梯，并说“它是善意的斜坡，人们习惯于在更大的人生问题上生活于此。”

The stereotype of Labor as Emancipator selects the evidence which supports itself and rejects the other. And so parallel with the real movements of working men there exists a fiction of the Labor Movement, in which an idealized mass moves towards an ideal goal. The fiction deals with the future. In the future possibilities are almost indistinguishable from probabilities and probabilities from certainties. If the future is long enough, the human will might turn what is just conceivable into what is very likely, and what is likely into what is sure to happen. James called this the faith ladder, and said that "it is a slope of goodwill on which in the larger questions of life men habitually live."

“1. 某种世界观是正确的，这并不荒谬，也不矛盾；

"1. There is nothing absurd in a certain view of the world being true, nothing contradictory;

2. 在某些条件下它可能 是正确的；

2. It might have been true under certain conditions;

3.现在可能 还是这样；

3. It may be true even now;

4. 它是真实 的；

4. It is fit to be true;

5. 这应该 是真的；

5. It ought to be true;

6.必须 是真实的；

6. It must be true;

7.这应 是真的，至少对我来说是真的。

7. It shall be true, at any rate true for me."

而且，正如他在另一处所补充说的，“在某些特殊情况下，你的行动可能是一种确保最终实现目标的手段。”然而，没有人比他更坚持，就我们所知，我们必须避免用目标代替起点，必须避免将勇气、努力和技能在未来可能创造的东西重新解读到现在。然而，这个真理很难实现，因为我们每个人都没有受过太多关于样本选择的训练。

And, as he added in another place, "your acting thus may in certain special cases be a means of making it securely true in the end." Yet no one would have insisted more than he, that, so far as we know how, we must avoid substituting the goal for the starting point, must avoid reading back into the present what courage, effort and skill might create in the future. Yet this truism is inordinately difficult to live by, because every one of us is so little trained in the selection of our samples.

如果我们相信某件事应该是真的，我们几乎总能找到一个事实，或者找到一个相信它应该是真的人。当一个具体的事实表明希望正确地衡量这一事实时，就很难做到这一点。当我们遇到的前六个人同意我们的观点时，很难记住他们可能都在早餐时读了同一份报纸。然而，我们不可能每次想估计一个概率时都向 816 个随机样本发送问卷。在处理任何大量事实时，如果我们是根据偶然的印象行事，那么就假设我们挑选了真实的样本。

If we believe that a certain thing ought to be true, we can almost always find either an instance where it is true, or someone who believes it ought to be true. It is ever so hard when a concrete fact illustrates a hope to weigh that fact properly. When the first six people we meet agree with us, it is not easy to remember that they may all have read the same newspaper at breakfast. And yet we cannot send out a questionnaire to 816 random samples every time we wish to estimate a probability. In dealing with any large mass of facts, the presumption is against our having picked true samples, if we are acting on a casual impression.





9

9

当我们试图更进一步寻找看不见的复杂事件的因果时，随意的意见是非常棘手的。公共生活中很少有大问题的因果关系一目了然。对于那些花了数年时间研究商业周期、价格和工资变动、人民的移民和同化或外国外交目的的学者来说，它们并不明显。然而，不知何故，我们都应该对这些问题有自己的看法，最常见的推理形式是直觉的，事后诸葛亮，这并不奇怪。

And when we try to go one step further in order to seek the causes and effects of unseen and complicated affairs, haphazard opinion is very tricky. There are few big issues in public life where cause and effect are obvious at once. They are not obvious to scholars who have devoted years, let us say, to studying business cycles, or price and wage movements, or the migration and the assimilation of peoples, or the diplomatic purposes of foreign powers. Yet somehow we are all supposed to have opinions on these matters, and it is not surprising that the commonest form of reasoning is the intuitive, post hoc ergo propter hoc.

一个人的头脑越是缺乏训练，就越容易得出这样的理论：两件同时引起他注意的事情之间是有因果关系的。我们已经详细讨论了事物引起我们注意的方式。我们已经看到，我们获取信息的渠道是受阻和不确定的，我们的理解力深受刻板印象的控制；我们理性所能获得的证据受到防御、威望、道德、空间、时间和取样的幻觉的影响。我们现在必须注意到，随着这一最初的污染，公众舆论进一步受到困扰，因为在一系列主要通过刻板印象看到的事件中，我们很容易接受顺序或平行性等同于因果关系。

The more untrained a mind, the more readily it works out a theory that two things which catch its attention at the same time are causally connected. We have already dwelt at some length on the way things reach our attention. We have seen that our access to information is obstructed and uncertain, and that our apprehension is deeply controlled by our stereotypes; that the evidence available to our reason is subject to illusions of defense, prestige, morality, space, time, and sampling. We must note now that with this initial taint, public opinions are still further beset, because in a series of events seen mostly through stereotypes, we readily accept sequence or parallelism as equivalent to cause and effect.

当两个想法结合在一起引起相同的感觉时，这种情况最有可能发生。如果它们结合在一起，它们很可能会引起相同的感觉；即使它们没有结合在一起，附着在其中一个想法上的强烈感觉也可能从记忆的所有角落吸走任何感觉大致相同的想法。因此，一切痛苦的事情都倾向于聚集到一个因果系统中，一切愉快的事情也是如此。

This is most likely to happen when two ideas that come together arouse the same feeling. If they come together they are likely to arouse the same feeling; and even when they do not arrive together a powerful feeling attached to one is likely to suck out of all the corners of memory any idea that feels about the same. Thus everything painful tends to collect into one system of cause and effect, and likewise everything pleasant.

“IId IIm (1675) 今天我听说上帝向这个城镇的中心射了一支箭。天花出现在天鹅的普通标志中，普通守护者的名字是温莎。他的女儿患上了这种疾病。可以看出，这种疾病始于一家酒馆，这证明了上帝对酗酒和酒馆增多的罪恶的不满！”

"IId IIm (1675) This day I hear that God has shot an arrow into the midst of this Town. The small pox is in an ordinary ye sign of the Swan, the ordinary Keepers name is Windsor. His daughter is sick of the disease. It is observable that this disease begins at an alehouse, to testify God's displeasure agt the sin of drunkenness & yt of multiplying alehouses!"

因此，英克利斯·马瑟，以及 1919 年一位杰出的天体力学教授在讨论爱因斯坦理论时说道：

Thus Increase Mather, and thus in the year 1919 a distinguished Professor of Celestial Mechanics discussing the Einstein theory:

“很有可能……布尔什维克起义实际上是某种潜在的、深层的、精神混乱的明显表现，这种混乱具有世界性……同样的不安情绪已经侵入了科学。”

"It may well be that…. Bolshevist uprisings are in reality the visible objects of some underlying, deep, mental disturbance, world-wide in character…. This same spirit of unrest has invaded science."

当我们极度憎恨某件事时，我们很容易将我们极度憎恨或恐惧的其他大多数事情与它联系起来，认为它们是原因或结果。它们之间的联系可能并不比天花和酒馆、相对论和布尔什维克主义之间的联系更紧密，但它们却因同一种情感而紧密相连。在像天体力学教授那样的迷信思想中，情感是一股熔岩流，它捕捉并嵌入它所接触的一切。当你在其中挖掘时，你会发现，就像在一座被埋葬的城市中一样，各种各样的物体荒谬地纠缠在一起。任何事物都可以与其他事物相关联，只要它有这种感觉。处于这种状态的思想也无法知道它有多么荒谬。古老的恐惧，加上最近的恐惧，凝结成一连串的恐惧，任何令人恐惧的事物都是其他令人恐惧的事物的原因。

In hating one thing violently, we readily associate with it as cause or effect most of the other things we hate or fear violently. They may have no more connection than smallpox and alehouses, or Relativity and Bolshevism, but they are bound together in the same emotion. In a superstitious mind, like that of the Professor of Celestial Mechanics, emotion is a stream of molten lava which catches and imbeds whatever it touches. When you excavate in it you find, as in a buried city, all sorts of objects ludicrously entangled in each other. Anything can be related to anything else, provided it feels like it. Nor has a mind in such a state any way of knowing how preposterous it is. Ancient fears, reinforced by more recent fears, coagulate into a snarl of fears where anything that is dreaded is the cause of anything else that is dreaded.





10

10

一般而言，这一切最终都会形成一个万恶体系，以及另一个万善体系。然后，我们对绝对的热爱就显露出来了。因为我们不喜欢限定副词。它们使句子变得杂乱，干扰了不可抗拒的感觉。我们喜欢“最多”胜过“更多”，喜欢“最少”胜过“更少”，我们不喜欢“宁愿”、“也许”、“如果”、“或者”、“但是”、“向着”、“不完全”、“几乎”、“暂时”、“部分”等词。然而，几乎每一种关于公共事务的观点都需要用这种词来打消。但在我们自由的时刻，一切都倾向于绝对地表现——百分之百，无处不在，永远如此。

Generally it all culminates in the fabrication of a system of all evil, and of another which is the system of all good. Then our love of the absolute shows itself. For we do not like qualifying adverbs. They clutter up sentences, and interfere with irresistible feeling. We prefer most to more, least to less, we dislike the words rather, perhaps, if, or, but, toward, not quite, almost, temporarily, partly. Yet nearly every opinion about public affairs needs to be deflated by some word of this sort. But in our free moments everything tends to behave absolutely,—one hundred percent, everywhere, forever.

仅仅说我们比敌人更正确，我们的胜利比敌人更有利于民主是不够的。我们必须坚持我们的胜利将永远结束战争，让世界安全，实现民主。战争结束后，虽然我们挫败了比现在困扰我们的邪恶更大的邪恶，但结果的相对性会逐渐消失，当前邪恶的绝对性会战胜我们的精神，我们会感到无助，因为我们并非不可抗拒。钟摆在无所不能和无能之间摇摆。

It is not enough to say that our side is more right than the enemy's, that our victory will help democracy more than his. One must insist that our victory will end war forever, and make the world safe for democracy. And when the war is over, though we have thwarted a greater evil than those which still afflict us, the relativity of the result fades out, the absoluteness of the present evil overcomes our spirit, and we feel that we are helpless because we have not been irresistible. Between omnipotence and impotence the pendulum swings.

真实的空间、真实的时间、真实的数字、真实的联系、真实的重量都消失了。视角、背景和行动的维度都被刻板地剪裁和冻结了。

Real space, real time, real numbers, real connections, real weights are lost. The perspective and the background and the dimensions of action are clipped and frozen in the stereotype.

第四部分：利益

PART IV: INTERESTS

第十一章

CHAPTER XI

引起关注

THE ENLISTING OF INTEREST





1

1

但人类的心灵并不是一部电影，它不会一劳永逸地记录下通过快门和镜头所呈现的每一个印象。人类的心灵具有无休止的、持续的创造力。随着我们使这些画面更加完整地融入我们自己，这些画面会淡化或融合，在这里变得清晰，在那里变得浓缩。它们不会静止地停留在心灵的表面，而是被诗意的能力重新加工成我们自己的个人表达。我们分配重点并参与行动。

BUT the human mind is not a film which registers once and for all each impression that comes through its shutters and lenses. The human mind is endlessly and persistently creative. The pictures fade or combine, are sharpened here, condensed there, as we make them more completely our own. They do not lie inert upon the surface of the mind, but are reworked by the poetic faculty into a personal expression of ourselves. We distribute the emphasis and participate in the action.

为了做到这一点，我们倾向于将数量人格化，将关系戏剧化。除了极其复杂的头脑之外，世界事务被表现为某种寓言。社会运动、经济力量、国家利益、公众舆论被视为人，或者像教皇、总统、列宁、摩根或国王这样的人被视为思想和制度。所有刻板印象中最深刻的是人类刻板印象，它将人性归因于无生命或集体的事物。

In order to do this we tend to personalize quantities, and to dramatize relations. As some sort of allegory, except in acutely sophisticated minds, the affairs of the world are represented. Social Movements, Economic Forces, National Interests, Public Opinion are treated as persons, or persons like the Pope, the President, Lenin, Morgan or the King become ideas and institutions. The deepest of all the stereotypes is the human stereotype which imputes human nature to inanimate or collective things.

即使经过各种方式的审查，我们的印象仍然千差万别，令人眼花缭乱，这迫使我们采用更经济的寓言。事物如此之多，我们无法清楚地记住它们。通常，我们给它们命名，让名字代表整个印象。但名字是多孔的。旧的含义会溜走，新的含义会溜进来，试图保留名字的完整含义几乎和试图回忆原始印象一样令人疲惫。然而，名字并不是思想的廉价货币。它们太空洞、太抽象、太不人性化。因此，我们开始通过一些个人刻板印象来看待名字，对其进行解读，最终在名字中看到某种人类品质的化身。

The bewildering variety of our impressions, even after they have been censored in all kinds of ways, tends to force us to adopt the greater economy of the allegory. So great is the multitude of things that we cannot keep them vividly in mind. Usually, then, we name them, and let the name stand for the whole impression. But a name is porous. Old meanings slip out and new ones slip in, and the attempt to retain the full meaning of the name is almost as fatiguing as trying to recall the original impressions. Yet names are a poor currency for thought. They are too empty, too abstract, too inhuman. And so we begin to see the name through some personal stereotype, to read into it, finally to see in it the incarnation of some human quality.

然而，人类的品质本身是模糊和波动的。它们最好通过物理符号来记住。因此，我们倾向于将人类的品质归因于我们印象的名称，而这些品质本身往往以物理隐喻的形式来形象化。英国人民、英国历史都浓缩在英格兰，英格兰变成了约翰牛，他快活而肥胖，不太聪明，但能很好地照顾自己。人民的迁徙对某些人来说可能像河流的蜿蜒曲折，对另一些人来说则像毁灭性的洪水。人们表现出的勇气可以具体化为一块岩石；他们的目标可以具体化为一条道路，他们的疑虑可以具体化为道路的分叉，他们的困难可以具体化为车辙和岩石，他们的进步可以具体化为一片肥沃的山谷。如果他们动员他们的无畏之心，他们就会拔出宝剑。如果他们的军队投降，他们就会被打倒在地。如果他们受到压迫，他们就会被折磨或被折磨。

Yet human qualities are themselves vague and fluctuating. They are best remembered by a physical sign. And therefore, the human qualities we tend to ascribe to the names of our impressions, themselves tend to be visualized in physical metaphors. The people of England, the history of England, condense into England, and England becomes John Bull, who is jovial and fat, not too clever, but well able to take care of himself. The migration of a people may appear to some as the meandering of a river, and to others like a devastating flood. The courage people display may be objectified as a rock; their purpose as a road, their doubts as forks of the road, their difficulties as ruts and rocks, their progress as a fertile valley. If they mobilize their dread-naughts they unsheath a sword. If their army surrenders they are thrown to earth. If they are oppressed they are on the rack or under the harrow.

当公共事务通过演讲、标题、戏剧、电影、漫画、小说、雕像或绘画等形式普及时，要将其转化为人类的兴趣，首先需要从原作中抽象出来，然后使抽象的内容生动起来。我们不会对我们看不到的东西产生太大的兴趣，也不会被它打动。我们每个人对公共事务了解甚少，因此，它们仍然枯燥乏味，直到某个具有艺术家气质的人将它们转化为生动的画面。因此，由于我们接触的渠道和偏见的限制，我们对现实的认识被强加了抽象，这种抽象得到了补偿。由于我们不是无所不在、无所不知的，我们看不到很多我们要思考和谈论的东西。作为有血有肉的人，我们不会靠文字、名字和灰色理论来维持生活。作为某种艺术家，我们用抽象来绘画、上演戏剧和画漫画。

When public affairs are popularized in speeches, headlines, plays, moving pictures, cartoons, novels, statues or paintings, their transformation into a human interest requires first abstraction from the original, and then animation of what has been abstracted. We cannot be much interested in, or much moved by, the things we do not see. Of public affairs each of us sees very little, and therefore, they remain dull and unappetizing, until somebody, with the makings of an artist, has translated them into a moving picture. Thus the abstraction, imposed upon our knowledge of reality by all the limitations of our access and of our prejudices, is compensated. Not being omnipresent and omniscient we cannot see much of what we have to think and talk about. Being flesh and blood we will not feed on words and names and gray theory. Being artists of a sort we paint pictures, stage dramas and draw cartoons out of the abstractions.

或者，如果可能的话，我们会找到有天赋的人，他们可以为我们进行想象。因为每个人的绘画能力并不相同。但我想，人们可以像柏格森一样断言，实践智力与空间品质最为密切相关。一个“清晰”的思想者几乎总是一个优秀的视觉家。但出于同样的原因，因为他是“电影摄影师”，所以他往往过于外在和不敏感。因为有直觉的人，这可能是音乐或肌肉感知的另一个名称，他们往往比视觉家更能欣赏事件的质量和行为的内在性。当关键因素是一种从不粗暴公开的欲望时，他们有更多理解，这种欲望只出现在表面上，以一种隐晦的手势或一种语言节奏。视觉化可以捕捉刺激和结果。但中间和内部往往被视觉化者严重地讽刺，就像作曲家的意图被一个伟大的女高音在甜美少女的角色中讽刺一样。

Or, if possible, we find gifted men who can visualize for us. For people are not all endowed to the same degree with the pictorial faculty. Yet one may, I imagine, assert with Bergson that the practical intelligence is most closely adapted to spatial qualities. A "clear" thinker is almost always a good visualizer. But for that same reason, because he is "cinematographic," he is often by that much external and insensitive. For the people who have intuition, which is probably another name for musical or muscular perception, often appreciate the quality of an event and the inwardness of an act far better than the visualizer. They have more understanding when the crucial element is a desire that is never crudely overt, and appears on the surface only in a veiled gesture, or in a rhythm of speech. Visualization may catch the stimulus and the result. But the intermediate and internal is often as badly caricatured by a visualizer, as is the intention of the composer by an enormous soprano in the sweet maiden's part.

然而，尽管直觉往往具有一种特殊的正义性，但它仍然是高度私密的，而且在很大程度上是不可交流的。但社会交往依赖于交流，虽然一个人常常可以凭借直觉以最大的优雅掌控自己的生活，但他通常很难让别人相信直觉。当他谈论直觉时，直觉听起来就像一团雾。因为虽然直觉确实能更公正地感知人类的感觉，但理性的空间和触觉偏见却对这种感知无能为力。因此，当行动取决于许多人是否意见一致时，可能首先没有一个想法在具有视觉或触觉价值之前是无法清晰地做出实际决定的。但同样真实的是，没有一个视觉想法对我们来说是重要的，除非它包裹了我们自己个性的一些压力。在它释放或抵抗、抑制或增强我们自己的一些渴望之前，它仍然是无关紧要的对象之一。

Nevertheless, though they have often a peculiar justice, intuitions remain highly private and largely incommunicable. But social intercourse depends on communication, and while a person can often steer his own life with the utmost grace by virtue of his intuitions, he usually has great difficulty in making them real to others. When he talks about them they sound like a sheaf of mist. For while intuition does give a fairer perception of human feeling, the reason with its spatial and tactile prejudice can do little with that perception. Therefore, where action depends on whether a number of people are of one mind, it is probably true that in the first instance no idea is lucid for practical decision until it has visual or tactile value. But it is also true, that no visual idea is significant to us until it has enveloped some stress of our own personality. Until it releases or resists, depresses or enhances, some craving of our own, it remains one of the objects which do not matter.





2

2

图像一直是传达思想的最可靠方式，其次是唤起记忆中图像的文字。但是，除非我们将自己与图像的某个方面联系起来，否则所传达的思想并不完全属于我们自己。这种认同，或者弗农·李所说的移情，可能几乎是无限微妙和象征性的。模仿可能在我们不知情的情况下进行，有时甚至会以一种让我们的个性中支持自尊的部分感到恐惧的方式进行。对于成熟的人而言，他们参与的可能不是英雄的命运，而是整个思想的命运，而英雄和恶棍都是必不可少的。但这些都是精妙之处。

Pictures have always been the surest way of conveying an idea, and next in order, words that call up pictures in memory. But the idea conveyed is not fully our own until we have identified ourselves with some aspect of the picture. The identification, or what Vernon Lee has called empathy, may be almost infinitely subtle and symbolic. The mimicry may be performed without our being aware of it, and sometimes in a way that would horrify those sections of our personality which support our self-respect. In sophisticated people the participation may not be in the fate of the hero, but in the fate of the whole idea to which both hero and villain are essential. But these are refinements.

在通俗作品中，识别的把柄几乎总是被标记出来。你立刻就知道谁是英雄。如果标记不明确，选择不明确，那么任何作品都不可能轻易流行。但这还不够。观众必须有事可做，而对真善美的沉思不是一件可以做的事情。为了不呆呆地坐在画面前，这既适用于报纸故事，也适用于小说和电影，观众必须通过画面来锻炼。现在有两种锻炼形式远远超越其他所有形式，既容易被唤起，又渴望寻求刺激。它们是性激情和打斗，两者之间有着如此多的联系，如此紧密地融合在一起，以至于关于性的打斗在吸引力方面胜过其他任何主题。没有哪一种如此引人入胜，也没有哪一种如此不顾文化和边界的所有区别。

In popular representation the handles for identification are almost always marked. You know who the hero is at once. And no work promises to be easily popular where the marking is not definite and the choice clear. But that is not enough. The audience must have something to do, and the contemplation of the true, the good and the beautiful is not something to do. In order not to sit inertly in the presence of the picture, and this applies as much to newspaper stories as to fiction and the cinema, the audience must be exercised by the image. Now there are two forms of exercise which far transcend all others, both as to ease with which they are aroused, and eagerness with which stimuli for them are sought. They are sexual passion and fighting, and the two have so many associations with each other, blend into each other so intimately, that a fight about sex outranks every other theme in the breadth of its appeal. There is none so engrossing or so careless of all distinctions of culture and frontiers.

性主题几乎不出现在美国政治形象中。除了战争的某些小高潮、偶尔的丑闻或与黑人或亚洲人的种族冲突阶段外，谈论它似乎有些牵强。只有在电影、小说和一些杂志小说中，劳资关系、商业竞争、政治和外交才会与女孩和另一个女人纠缠在一起。但战斗主题随处可见。当有战斗，或者我们所说的有争议时，政治才有趣。为了让政治流行，必须找到争议，即使在真理和正义中没有争议——没有争议，因为判断、原则或事实的差异不需要征召好斗。

The sexual motif figures hardly at all in American political imagery. Except in certain minor ecstasies of war, in an occasional scandal, or in phases of the racial conflict with Negroes or Asiatics, to speak of it at all would seem far-fetched. Only in moving pictures, novels, and some magazine fiction are industrial relations, business competition, politics, and diplomacy tangled up with the girl and the other woman. But the fighting motif appears at every turn. Politics is interesting when there is a fight, or as we say, an issue. And in order to make politics popular, issues have to be found, even when in truth and justice, there are none,—none, in the sense that the differences of judgment, or principle, or fact, do not call for the enlistment of pugnacity.

但是，如果没有好斗精神，我们这些没有直接参与的人很难保持兴趣。对于那些参与其中的人来说，即使没有问题，这种专注也可能足以让他们保持兴趣。他们可能因为活动中的纯粹乐趣，或者因为微妙的竞争或发明而锻炼了这种专注。但对于那些整个问题都是外部和遥远的人来说，这些其他能力不容易发挥作用。为了让事情的模糊形象对他们有意义，必须允许他们锻炼对斗争、悬念和胜利的热爱。

But where pugnacity is not enlisted, those of us who are not directly involved find it hard to keep up our interest. For those who are involved the absorption may be real enough to hold them even when no issue is involved. They may be exercised by sheer joy in activity, or by subtle rivalry or invention. But for those to whom the whole problem is external and distant, these other faculties do not easily come into play. In order that the faint image of the affair shall mean something to them, they must be allowed to exercise the love of struggle, suspense, and victory.

帕特森小姐坚持认为“悬念……是大都会艺术博物馆的杰作与里沃利或里亚托剧院的影片之间的区别。”如果她明确表示这些杰作既缺乏简单的识别方式，又缺乏对这一代人受欢迎的主题，那么她完全可以正确地说，这“解释了为什么人们三三两两地涌入大都会，数百人挤进里亚托和里沃利。三三两两的人在艺术博物馆看一幅画的时间不到十分钟——除非他们是艺术学生、评论家或鉴赏家。里沃利或里亚托的数百人看画的时间超过一个小时。就美感而言，这两幅画的优点是无法比较的。然而，这部电影比杰作吸引了更多的人，并让他们的注意力停留更长时间，这并不是因为它本身有什么内在的优点，而是因为它描绘了正在展开的事件，观众正屏息等待着结果。它具有斗争的元素，这总能引起悬念。”

Miss Patterson insists that "suspense… constitutes the difference between the masterpieces in the Metropolitan Museum of Art and the pictures at the Rivoli or the Rialto Theatres." Had she made it clear that the masterpieces lack either an easy mode of identification or a theme popular for this generation, she would be wholly right in saying that this "explains why the people straggle into the Metropolitan by twos and threes and struggle into the Rialto and Rivoli by hundreds. The twos and threes look at a picture in the Art Museum for less than ten minutes—unless they chance to be art students, critics, or connoisseurs. The hundreds in the Rivoli or the Rialto look at the picture for more than an hour. As far as beauty is concerned there can be no comparison of the merits of the two pictures. Yet the motion picture draws more people and holds them at attention longer than do the masterpieces, not through any intrinsic merit of its own, but because it depicts unfolding events, the outcome of which the audience is breathlessly waiting. It possesses the element of struggle, which never fails to arouse suspense."

为了使遥远的情景不成为注意力边缘的灰色闪烁，它应该能够转化为可以识别的画面。除非发生这种情况，否则它只会在短时间内引起少数人的兴趣。它将属于看到但感觉不到的景象，属于敲击我们感官却不被承认的感觉。我们必须站队。我们必须能够站队。在我们内心深处，我们必须走出观众席，走上舞台，像英雄一样为正义战胜邪恶而奋斗。我们必须将我们生命的气息注入寓言中。

In order then that the distant situation shall not be a gray flicker on the edge of attention, it should be capable of translation into pictures in which the opportunity for identification is recognizable. Unless that happens it will interest only a few for a little while. It will belong to the sights seen but not felt, to the sensations that beat on our sense organs, and are not acknowledged. We have to take sides. We have to be able to take sides. In the recesses of our being we must step out of the audience on to the stage, and wrestle as the hero for the victory of good over evil. We must breathe into the allegory the breath of our life.





3

3

因此，尽管有批评者，但关于现实主义和浪漫主义的古老争论还是得出了结论。我们的大众品味是让戏剧以足够现实的场景开始，使认同变得可信，并让戏剧以足够浪漫的场景结束，使其令人向往，但又不至于浪漫到不可想象。在开始和结束之间，经典是自由的，但真正的开始和幸福的结局是里程碑。电影观众拒绝逻辑上发展的幻想，因为在纯粹的幻想中，在机器时代没有熟悉的立足点。它拒绝不懈追求的现实主义，因为它不喜欢在已经成为自己的斗争中失败。

And so, in spite of the critics, a verdict is rendered in the old controversy about realism and romanticism. Our popular taste is to have the drama originate in a setting realistic enough to make identification plausible and to have it terminate in a setting romantic enough to be desirable, but not so romantic as to be inconceivable. In between the beginning and the end the canons are liberal, but the true beginning and the happy ending are landmarks. The moving picture audience rejects fantasy logically developed, because in pure fantasy there is no familiar foothold in the age of machines. It rejects realism relentlessly pursued because it does not enjoy defeat in a struggle that has become its own.

什么才是真实的、现实的、善的、恶的、令人向往的，并不是永恒不变的。这些是由刻板印象决定的，这些刻板印象是从早期经验中获得的，并延续到后来的判断中。因此，如果对每部电影和流行杂志的财务投资不是那么高昂，以至于需要立即获得广泛的欢迎，那么有精神和想象力的人就可以像人们梦想的那样，利用银幕和期刊来扩大和完善、验证和批评我们想象力所运用的图像库。但是，考虑到目前的成本，制作电影的人，就像其他时代的教堂和宫廷画家一样，必须坚持他们发现的刻板印象，否则就会付出令人失望的代价。刻板印象可以改变，但不能及时保证六个月后电影上映时的成功。

What will be accepted as true, as realistic, as good, as evil, as desirable, is not eternally fixed. These are fixed by stereotypes, acquired from earlier experiences and carried over into judgment of later ones. And, therefore, if the financial investment in each film and in popular magazines were not so exorbitant as to require instant and widespread popularity, men of spirit and imagination would be able to use the screen and the periodical, as one might dream of their being used, to enlarge and to refine, to verify and criticize the repertory of images with which our imaginations work. But, given the present costs, the men who make moving pictures, like the church and the court painters of other ages, must adhere to the stereotypes that they find, or pay the price of frustrating expectation. The stereotypes can be altered, but not in time to guarantee success when the film is released six months from now.

那些真正改变刻板印象的人，那些先锋艺术家和评论家，自然会对保护他们投资的经理和编辑感到沮丧和愤怒。他们冒着一切风险，那么其他人为什么不呢？这不太公平，因为他们在义愤填膺中忘记了自己的回报，而这些回报是他们的雇主无法想象的。他们不能，即使可以也不会换位置。在与非利士人的无休止的战争中，他们还忘记了另一件事。他们忘记了他们衡量自己成功的标准是过去的艺术家和智者做梦也想不到的。他们要求的是直到最近几代艺术家才考虑过的发行量和观众。当他们得不到这些时，他们就会失望。

The men who do alter the stereotypes, the pioneering artists and critics, are naturally depressed and angered at managers and editors who protect their investments. They are risking everything, then why not the others? That is not quite fair, for in their righteous fury they have forgotten their own rewards, which are beyond any that their employers can hope to feel. They could not, and would not if they could, change places. And they have forgotten another thing in the unceasing war with Philistia. They have forgotten that they are measuring their own success by standards that artists and wise men of the past would never have dreamed of invoking. They are asking for circulations and audiences that were never considered by any artist until the last few generations. And when they do not get them, they are disappointed.

那些像《大街》中的辛克莱·刘易斯一样的人，成功地将大量其他人在脑海中试图表达的东西明确地投射出来。“你已经为我说出来了。”他们建立了一种新的形式，然后被无休止地复制，直到它也成为一种刻板印象。下一位先驱者很难让公众以其他方式看待大街。他和辛克莱·刘易斯的先驱们一样，与公众发生了争执。

Those who catch on, like Sinclair Lewis in "Main Street," are men who have succeeded in projecting definitely what great numbers of other people were obscurely trying to say inside their heads. "You have said it for me." They establish a new form which is then endlessly copied until it, too, becomes a stereotype of perception. The next pioneer finds it difficult to make the public see Main Street any other way. And he, like the forerunners of Sinclair Lewis, has a quarrel with the public.

这场争论不仅源于刻板印象的冲突，还源于先锋艺术家对其素材的崇敬。无论他选择哪个层面，他都会坚持那个层面。如果他处理的是事件的内在性，他会不顾它造成的痛苦，将其一直延续到最后。他不会用幻想来帮助任何人，也不会在没有和平的地方高呼和平。这就是他的美国。但广大观众无法忍受这种严肃。他们对自己比对世界上任何其他事物都更感兴趣。他们感兴趣的自我是学校和传统所揭示的自我。他们坚持认为，艺术作品应该是一辆有踏板的车辆，他们可以爬上去，他们应该乘坐的不是国家的轮廓，而是一片土地，在那里一个小时内没有钟表要打卡，也没有盘子要洗。为了满足这些要求，存在着一个中间阶层的艺术家，他们能够并且愿意混淆各个层面，将更伟大的人物的发明拼凑成一个现实主义-浪漫主义的混合体，并且正如帕特森小姐所建议的那样，给出“现实生活中很少能做到的事情——一系列困难的胜利解决；美德的痛苦和罪恶的胜利……转变为对美德的颂扬和对其敌人的永恒惩罚。”

This quarrel is due not only to the conflict of stereotypes, but to the pioneering artist's reverence for his material. Whatever the plane he chooses, on that plane he remains. If he is dealing with the inwardness of an event he follows it to its conclusion regardless of the pain it causes. He will not tag his fantasy to help anyone, or cry peace where there is no peace. There is his America. But big audiences have no stomach for such severity. They are more interested in themselves than in anything else in the world. The selves in which they are interested are the selves that have been revealed by schools and by tradition. They insist that a work of art shall be a vehicle with a step where they can climb aboard, and that they shall ride, not according to the contours of the country, but to a land where for an hour there are no clocks to punch and no dishes to wash. To satisfy these demands there exists an intermediate class of artists who are able and willing to confuse the planes, to piece together a realistic-romantic compound out of the inventions of greater men, and, as Miss Patterson advises, give "what real life so rarely does-the triumphant resolution of a set of difficulties; the anguish of virtue and the triumph of sin… changed to the glorifications of virtue and the eternal punishment of its enemy."





4

4

政治意识形态遵循这些规则。现实主义的立足点始终存在。在论证中，可以辨认出一些真实的邪恶，如德国威胁或阶级冲突。对世界某些方面的描述令人信服，因为它与熟悉的想法一致。但是，由于意识形态既涉及看不见的未来，也涉及有形的现在，它很快就会不知不觉地跨越验证的边界。在描述现在时，你或多或少地被束缚在共同的经验中。在描述没有人经历过的事情时，你注定要放手。你或多或少站在世界末日，但你也许在为上帝而战……一个真正的开始，按照现行的标准来看是真实的，还有一个幸福的结局。每一个马克思主义者都对当前的残酷无情非常坚定，而对独裁统治后的一天则大多持乐观态度。战争宣传家也是如此：在莱茵河以东的任何地方，或者如果他们是德国人，在莱茵河以西的任何地方，他们都发现了人性中没有一种兽性。确实，兽性确实存在。但胜利之后，就是永恒的和平。很多这样的事情都是经过深思熟虑的。因为熟练的宣传家知道，虽然你必须从合理的分析开始，但你不能一直分析下去，因为真正的政治成就的乏味很快就会摧毁人们的兴趣。因此，宣传家用一个相当合理的开头来耗尽人们对现实的兴趣，然后挥舞着通往天堂的护照，为长途旅行积蓄能量。

The ideologies of politics obey these rules. The foothold of realism is always there. The picture of some real evil, such as the German threat or class conflict, is recognizable in the argument. There is a description of some aspect of the world which is convincing because it agrees with familiar ideas. But as the ideology deals with an unseen future, as well as with a tangible present, it soon crosses imperceptibly the frontier of verification. In describing the present you are more or less tied down to common experience. In describing what nobody has experienced you are bound to let go. You stand at Armageddon, more or less, but you battle for the Lord, perhaps…. A true beginning, true according to the standards prevailing, and a happy ending. Every Marxist is hard as nails about the brutalities of the present, and mostly sunshine about the day after the dictatorship. So were the war propagandists: there was not a bestial quality in human nature they did not find everywhere east of the Rhine, or west of it if they were Germans. The bestiality was there all right. But after the victory, eternal peace. Plenty of this is quite cynically deliberate. For the skilful propagandist knows that while you must start with a plausible analysis, you must not keep on analyzing, because the tedium of real political accomplishment will soon destroy interest. So the propagandist exhausts the interest in reality by a tolerably plausible beginning, and then stokes up energy for a long voyage by brandishing a passport to heaven.

当公众虚构与私人紧迫感交织在一起时，这一公式便会奏效。但一旦交织在一起，在激烈的斗争中，最初的自我和最初的刻板印象可能会完全消失。

The formula works when the public fiction enmeshes itself with a private urgency. But once enmeshed, in the heat of battle, the original self and the original stereotype which effected the junction may be wholly lost to sight.

第十二章

CHAPTER XII

重新考虑自身利益

SELF-INTEREST RECONSIDERED





1

1

因此，对于所有听到同一个故事的人来说，故事并不是同一个。每个人进入故事的起点都会略有不同，因为没有两个经历是完全相同的；他会以自己的方式重演这个故事，并注入自己的感情。有时，一位技艺高超的艺术家会迫使我们进入与我们完全不同的生活，这些生活乍一看似乎枯燥、令人厌恶或古怪。但这种情况很少见。在几乎每一个引起我们注意的故事中，我们都变成了一个角色，用我们自己的哑剧表演这个角色。哑剧可能是微妙的或粗俗的，可能是对故事的共鸣，也可能只是粗略地类似；但它将包含我们对角色的构想所引起的那些感情。因此，原始主题在流传过程中，被所有经历它的人的思想所强调、扭曲和修饰。就好像莎士比亚的戏剧每次演出时都会被重写，演员和观众激发的重点和意义都会发生变化。

THEREFORE, the identical story is not the same story to all who hear it. Each will enter it at a slightly different point, since no two experiences are exactly alike; he will reenact it in his own way, and transfuse it with his own feelings. Sometimes an artist of compelling skill will force us to enter into lives altogether unlike our own, lives that seem at first glance dull, repulsive, or eccentric. But that is rare. In almost every story that catches our attention we become a character and act out the role with a pantomime of our own. The pantomime may be subtle or gross, may be sympathetic to the story, or only crudely analogous; but it will consist of those feelings which are aroused by our conception of the role. And so, the original theme as it circulates, is stressed, twisted, and embroidered by all the minds through which it goes. It is as if a play of Shakespeare's were rewritten each time it is performed with all the changes of emphasis and meaning that the actors and audience inspired.

在传奇故事被最终记录下来之前，似乎也发生了类似的事情。在我们这个时代，印刷记录会抑制每个人的想象力。但对于谣言，几乎没有或根本没有抑制，原始故事，无论是真实的还是虚构的，都会随着每个流言的艺术家对其进行创作而长出翅膀和角、蹄子和喙。第一个叙述者的叙述不会保持其形状和比例。所有听到它的人都会对其进行编辑和修改，将其用于白日梦并流传下去。

Something very like that seems to have happened to the stories in the sagas before they were definitively written down. In our time the printed record, such as it is, checks the exuberance of each individual's fancy. But against rumor there is little or no checks and the original story, true or invented, grows wings and horns, hoofs and beaks, as the artist in each gossip works upon it. The first narrator's account does not keep its shape and proportions. It is edited and revised by all who played with it as they heard it, used it for day dreams, and passed it on.

因此，听众越复杂，反应的变化就越大。因为随着听众的增多，常用词的数量就会减少。因此，故事中的共同因素变得更加抽象。这个故事缺乏自己的明确特征，但听故事的人却各不相同。他们赋予它自己的特征。

Consequently the more mixed the audience, the greater will be the variation in the response. For as the audience grows larger, the number of common words diminishes. Thus the common factors in the story become more abstract. This story, lacking precise character of its own, is heard by people of highly varied character. They give it their own character.





2

2

他们赋予它的特征不仅因性别、年龄、种族、宗教和社会地位而异，而且在这些较粗略的分类中，根据个人的遗传和后天体质、能力、职业、职业发展、职业的突出方面、情绪和紧张程度，或他在所玩的任何人生游戏中的棋盘位置而有所不同。他从公共事务、几行印刷品、一些照片、轶事和他自己的一些偶然经历中了解到的东西，他通过既定的模式进行构思，并用自己的情感进行再现。他不会将个人问题作为更大环境的部分样本。他将自己对更大环境的故事视为私人生活的模仿放大。

The character they give it varies not only with sex and age, race and religion and social position, but within these cruder classifications, according to the inherited and acquired constitution of the individual, his faculties, his career, the progress of his career, an emphasized aspect of his career, his moods and tenses, or his place on the board in any of the games of life that he is playing. What reaches him of public affairs, a few lines of print, some photographs, anecdotes, and some casual experience of his own, he conceives through his set patterns and recreates with his own emotions. He does not take his personal problems as partial samples of the greater environment. He takes his stories of the greater environment as a mimic enlargement of his private life.

但不一定像他自己描述的那种私人生活。因为在他的私人生活中，选择范围很窄，他的大部分自我被压抑在视线之外，无法直接控制他的外在行为。因此，除了那些将自己生活的幸福投射到普遍的善意中，或将自己的不幸投射到怀疑和仇恨中的普通人之外，还有一些表面上快乐但在自己圈子之外的任何地方都很残忍的人，以及那些越憎恨家人、朋友和工作，就越对人类充满爱的人。

But not necessarily of that private life as he would describe it to himself. For in his private life the choices are narrow, and much of himself is squeezed down and out of sight where it cannot directly govern his outward behavior. And thus, beside the more average people who project the happiness of their own lives into a general good will, or their unhappiness into suspicion and hate, there are the outwardly happy people who are brutal everywhere but in their own circle, as well as the people who, the more they detest their families, their friends, their jobs, the more they overflow with love for mankind.

当你从一般性转向细节时，就会越来越明显地看到，人们处理事务的性格并不是固定不变的。也许他们不同的自我有共同的主干和共同的品质，但树枝和细枝却有多种形式。没有人会以相同的性格面对每一种情况。他的性格会因时间和记忆的积累而在某种程度上发生变化，因为他不是机器人。他的性格不仅会随着时间而变化，而且会随着环境而变化。传说南洋的一位孤独的英国人，他总是刮胡子，打着黑色领带去吃晚饭，这证明了他自己直觉的、文明的恐惧，害怕失去他已经获得的性格。日记、相册、纪念品、旧信件、旧衣服和对一成不变的例行公事的热爱也证明了我们意识到在赫拉克利特河中再踏两步是多么困难。

As you descend from generalities to detail, it becomes more apparent that the character in which men deal with their affairs is not fixed. Possibly their different selves have a common stem and common qualities, but the branches and the twigs have many forms. Nobody confronts every situation with the same character. His character varies in some degree through the sheer influence of time and accumulating memory, since he is not an automaton. His character varies, not only in time, but according to circumstance. The legend of the solitary Englishman in the South Seas, who invariably shaves and puts on a black tie for dinner, bears witness to his own intuitive and civilized fear of losing the character which he has acquired. So do diaries, and albums, and souvenirs, old letters, and old clothes, and the love of unchanging routine testify to our sense of how hard it is to step twice in the Heraclitan river.

没有任何一个自我总是在发挥作用。因此，在形成任何公众舆论时，自我所参与的程度非常重要。日本人要求获得在加利福尼亚定居的权利。显然，无论你认为这一要求是想种植水果还是想娶白人的女儿，都会有很大的不同。如果两个国家在争夺一块领土，那么人们是把谈判看作房地产交易、羞辱他们的企图，还是像通常笼罩这些争论的激动和挑衅的语言那样，认为是强奸，这非常重要。因为当我们想到柠檬或遥远的土地时，掌控本能的自我与我们在思考甚至可能作为愤怒的一家之主时出现的自我非常不同。在一种情况下，进入意见的私人情感是温和的，在另一种情况下，则是炽热的。因此，尽管“自身利益”决定观点这一说法真实可信，但这种说法并没有多大启发意义，除非我们知道众多自我中的哪一个自我选择并引导了如此构想的利益。

There is no one self always at work. And therefore it is of great importance in the formation of any public opinion, what self is engaged. The Japanese ask the right to settle in California. Clearly it makes a whole lot of difference whether you conceive the demand as a desire to grow fruit or to marry the white man's daughter. If two nations are disputing a piece of territory, it matters greatly whether the people regard the negotiations as a real estate deal, an attempt to humiliate them, or, in the excited and provocative language which usually enclouds these arguments, as a rape. For the self which takes charge of the instincts when we are thinking about lemons or distant acres is very different from the self which appears when we are thinking even potentially as the outraged head of a family. In one case the private feeling which enters into the opinion is tepid, in the other, red hot. And so while it is so true as to be mere tautology that "self-interest" determines opinion, the statement is not illuminating, until we know which self out of many selects and directs the interest so conceived.

宗教教义和民间智慧总是将每个人的个性区分开来。他们被称为高级和低级、精神和物质、神圣和肉体；尽管我们可能不完全接受这种分类，但我们不能不注意到存在区别。现代人可能会注意到，除了两个对立的自我之外，还有很多没有那么明显区别的自我。他会说神学家们的区分是武断的和外在的，因为许多不同的自我只要符合神学家的分类，就会被归为高级自我，但他仍然会认识到，这是人类本性多样性的真实线索。

Religious teaching and popular wisdom have always distinguished several personalities in each human being. They have been called the Higher and Lower, the Spiritual and the Material, the Divine and the Carnal; and although we may not wholly accept this classification, we cannot fail to observe that distinctions exist. Instead of two antithetic selves, a modern man would probably note a good many not so sharply separated. He would say that the distinction drawn by theologians was arbitrary and external, because many different selves were grouped together as higher provided they fitted into the theologian's categories, but he would recognize nevertheless that here was an authentic clue to the variety of human nature.

我们学会了注意多个自我，但不要急于对它们做出评判。我们明白，我们看到的是同一个身体，但往往是一个不同的人，这取决于他是在与社会地位平等的人、社会地位低下的人还是社会地位高的人打交道；取决于他是在与一个有资格结婚的女人做爱，还是与一个没有资格结婚的女人做爱；取决于他是在追求一个女人，还是认为自己是她的主人；取决于他是在和他的孩子、他的伙伴、他最信任的下属、能成就他或毁掉他的老板打交道；取决于他是在为生活必需品而奋斗，还是在取得成功；取决于他是在与一个友好的外国人打交道，还是在与一个被鄙视的人打交道；取决于他是处在极大的危险之中，还是处于绝对的安全之中；取决于他是独自一人在巴黎，还是在皮奥里亚与家人在一起。

We have learned to note many selves, and to be a little less ready to issue judgment upon them. We understand that we see the same body, but often a different man, depending on whether he is dealing with a social equal, a social inferior, or a social superior; on whether he is making love to a woman he is eligible to marry, or to one whom he is not; on whether he is courting a woman, or whether he considers himself her proprietor; on whether he is dealing with his children, his partners, his most trusted subordinates, the boss who can make him or break him; on whether he is struggling for the necessities of life, or successful; on whether he is dealing with a friendly alien, or a despised one; on whether he is in great danger, or in perfect security; on whether he is alone in Paris or among his family in Peoria.

当然，人们在性格的一致性方面差异很大，差异如此之大，以至于他们可能涵盖了像杰基尔博士那样的分裂灵魂与完全专一的布兰德、帕西法尔或堂吉诃德之间的所有差异。如果自我之间太不相关，我们就会不信任这个人；如果他们过于固执地坚持一条轨道，我们会觉得他枯燥、固执或古怪。在人物的储备中，孤立和自给自足的人的储备很贫乏，适应性强的人的储备则高度多样化，有各种各样的自我，从我们希望上帝看到的顶部自我，到我们自己不敢看到的底部自我。可能有八度代表家庭——父亲、耶和华、暴君——丈夫、东道主、男性——情人、好色之徒——代表职业——雇主、主人、剥削者——竞争对手、阴谋家、敌人——下属、朝臣、势利小人。有些角色从未出现在公众视野中。其他人只有在特殊情况下才会被召唤出来。但这些角色的形成取决于一个人对自己所处境况的想象。如果他敏感的环境恰好是上流社会，他就会模仿他认为合适的角色。那个角色往往会调节他的举止、讲话、话题选择和喜好。生活的喜剧大部分就在于此，在于人们如何想象他们的角色适合他们不熟悉的境况：发起人中的教授、扑克游戏中的执事、乡下的伦敦佬、真钻石中的人造钻石。

People differ widely, of course, in the consistency of their characters, so widely that they may cover the whole gamut of differences between a split soul like Dr. Jekyll's and an utterly singleminded Brand, Parsifal, or Don Quixote. If the selves are too unrelated, we distrust the man; if they are too inflexibly on one track we find him arid, stubborn, or eccentric. In the repertory of characters, meager for the isolated and the self-sufficient, highly varied for the adaptable, there is a whole range of selves, from that one at the top which we should wish God to see, to those at the bottom that we ourselves do not dare to see. There may be octaves for the family,—father, Jehovah, tyrant,—husband, proprietor, male,—lover, lecher,—for the occupation,—employer, master, exploiter,—competitor, intriguer, enemy,—subordinate, courtier, snob. Some never come out into public view. Others are called out only by exceptional circumstances. But the characters take their form from a man's conception of the situation in which he finds himself. If the environment to which he is sensitive happens to be the smart set, he will imitate the character he conceives to be appropriate. That character will tend to act as modulator of his bearing, his speech, his choice of subjects, his preferences. Much of the comedy of life lies here, in the way people imagine their characters for situations that are strange to them: the professor among promoters, the deacon at a poker game, the cockney in the country, the paste diamond among real diamonds.





3

3

在形成一个人的性格时，会受到各种难以区分的影响。其基本分析可能仍像公元前五世纪一样令人怀疑，当时希波克拉底提出了体液学说，区分了多血质、忧郁质、胆汁质和粘液质的性格，并将它们归因于血液、黑胆汁、黄胆汁和粘液。最新的理论，如坎农、阿德勒、肯普夫的理论，似乎遵循着同样的思路，从外在行为和内在意识到身体的生理学。但是，尽管技术有了很大的改进，但没有人会声称有确定的结论使我们能够将先天与后天分开，并将天生的性格与后天的性格区分开来。只有在约瑟夫·贾斯特罗所说的心理学贫民窟中，性格的解释才被视为一套固定的系统，供颅相学家、手相学家、算命师、读心师和一些政治教授使用。在那里你仍然会发现有人断言“中国人喜欢颜色，眉毛很高”，而“卡尔梅克人的头从上面凹陷，但侧面很大，在器官周围，有获取的倾向；这个民族的偷窃倾向等是被承认的。”

Into the making of a man's characters there enters a variety of influences not easily separated. The analysis in its fundamentals is perhaps still as doubtful as it was in the fifth century B. C. when Hippocrates formulated the doctrine of the humors, distinguished the sanguine, the melancholic, the choleric, and the phlegmatic dispositions, and ascribed them to the blood, the black bile, the yellow bile, and the phlegm.
