But they knew just as certainly, that there was in men a will to decide their own fate, and to find a peace that was not imposed by force. How could they reconcile the wish and the fact?

他们环顾四周。在希腊和意​​大利的城邦，他们发现了腐败、阴谋和战争的记录。在他们自己的城市，他们看到了派系斗争、虚伪和狂热。这不是民主理想能够繁荣的环境，也不是一群独立且同样有能力的人自发管理自己事务的地方。他们进一步观察，也许是受让·雅克·卢梭的启发，来到遥远而未受破坏的乡村。他们看到的东西足以让他们相信，那里就是理想家园。杰斐逊尤其感受到了这一点，杰斐逊比任何人都更能塑造美国的民主形象。正是从乡镇中产生了推动美国革命取得胜利的力量。正是从乡镇中产生了让杰斐逊的政党获得权力的选票。在马萨诸塞州和弗吉尼亚州的农业社区，如果你戴上可以消除奴隶制的眼镜，你就能用心灵之眼看到民主的形象。

They looked about them. In the city states of Greece and Italy they found a chronicle of corruption, intrigue and war. In their own cities they saw faction, artificiality, fever. This was no environment in which the democratic ideal could prosper, no place where a group of independent and equally competent people managed their own affairs spontaneously. They looked further, guided somewhat perhaps by Jean Jacques Rousseau, to remote, unspoiled country villages. They saw enough to convince themselves that there the ideal was at home. Jefferson in particular felt this, and Jefferson more than any other man formulated the American image of democracy. From the townships had come the power that had carried the American Revolution to victory. From the townships were to come the votes that carried Jefferson's party to power. Out there in the farming communities of Massachusetts and Virginia, if you wore glasses that obliterated the slaves, you could see with your mind's eye the image of what democracy was to be.

托克维尔说：“美国革命爆发了，人民主权的理论在乡镇中得到培育，并在整个州内盛行。”它当然占据了那些制定和推广民主刻板观念的人的思想。杰斐逊写道：“珍视人民是我们的原则。”但他所珍视的几乎都是小土地所有者：“那些在土地上劳作的人是上帝的选民，如果他真的有选民的话，上帝在他们心中寄托了实质性和真正的美德。正是在这种焦点上，上帝保持了神圣之火的活力，否则它可能会从地球上消失。广大农民的道德败坏是一种现象，任何时代或国家都没有提供过先例。”

"The American Revolution broke out," says de Tocqueville, "and the doctrine of the sovereignty of the people, which had been nurtured in the townships, took possession of the state." It certainly took possession of the minds of those men who formulated and popularized the stereotypes of democracy. "The cherishment of the people was our principle," wrote Jefferson. But the people he cherished almost exclusively were the small landowning farmers: "Those who labor in the earth are the chosen people of God, if ever He had a chosen people, whose breasts He has made his peculiar deposit for substantial and genuine virtue. It is the focus in which He keeps alive that sacred fire, which otherwise might escape from the face of the earth. Corruption of morals in the mass of cultivators is a phenomenon of which no age nor nation has furnished an example."

不管这句感叹词中有多少浪漫的回归自然的成分，其中也包含着实实在在的道理。杰斐逊认为，一群独立的农民比任何其他人类社会都更接近于满足自发民主的要求，他的想法是正确的。但是，如果你想要维护这一理想，你就必须将这些理想的社会与世间的丑恶隔离开来。如果农民要管理自己的事务，他们必须将事务限制在他们习惯管理的范围内。杰斐逊得出了所有这些合乎逻辑的结论。他反对制造业、对外贸易、海军、无形财产形式，在理论上，他反对任何不以小型自治团体为中心的政府形式。他那个时代也曾受到批评，其中一人评论道：“如果我们全身心地投入到自我责任中，并且实际上足够强大，能够抵御一切入侵者，我们可能会享受永恒的质朴，永远在自私、满足的冷漠的庇护下，冷漠而粗俗地生活。”

However much of the romantic return to nature may have entered into this exclamation, there was also an element of solid sense. Jefferson was right in thinking that a group of independent farmers comes nearer to fulfilling the requirements of spontaneous democracy than any other human society. But if you are to preserve the ideal, you must fence off these ideal communities from the abominations of the world. If the farmers are to manage their own affairs, they must confine affairs to those they are accustomed to managing. Jefferson drew all these logical conclusions. He disapproved of manufacture, of foreign commerce, and a navy, of intangible forms of property, and in theory of any form of government that was not centered in the small self-governing group. He had critics in his day: one of them remarked that "wrapt up in the fullness of self-consequence and strong enough, in reality, to defend ourselves against every invader, we might enjoy an eternal rusticity and live, forever, thus apathized and vulgar under the shelter of a selfish, satisfied indifference."





4

4

杰斐逊所塑造的民主理想包括理想的环境和精英阶层，这与他那个时代的政治科学并不冲突。它确实与现实相冲突。当这一理想被绝对化地表述出来时，部分是出于热情，部分是出于竞选目的，人们很快就忘记了这一理论最初是为非常特殊的条件而设计的。它成为了政治福音，并为各党派的美国人提供了看待政治的刻板印象。

The democratic ideal, as Jefferson moulded it, consisting of an ideal environment and a selected class, did not conflict with the political science of his time. It did conflict with the realities. And when the ideal was stated in absolute terms, partly through exuberance and partly for campaign purposes, it was soon forgotten that the theory was originally devised for very special conditions. It became the political gospel, and supplied the stereotypes through which Americans of all parties have looked at politics.

这一信条之所以被确立，是因为在杰斐逊时代，没有人能够设想出非自发和主观的公众舆论。因此，民主传统总是试图看到这样一个世界：人们只关心其原因和结果都在他们所居住的地区内发生的事务。民主理论从来没有能够在广阔而不可预测的环境背景下设想自己。镜子是凹面的。尽管民主人士认识到他们与外部事务有联系，但他们非常肯定地看到，与这个自给自足的群体之外的每一次接触都对最初设想的民主构成了威胁。这是一种明智的担忧。如果民主是自发的，民主的利益就必须保持简单、易懂和易于管理。如果信息的供应要留给偶然的经验，条件必须接近偏远乡村乡镇的条件。环境必须限制在每个人直接和确定的知识范围内。

That gospel was fixed by the necessity that in Jefferson's time no one could have conceived public opinions that were not spontaneous and subjective. The democratic tradition is therefore always trying to see a world where people are exclusively concerned with affairs of which the causes and effects all operate within the region they inhabit. Never has democratic theory been able to conceive itself in the context of a wide and unpredictable environment. The mirror is concave. And although democrats recognize that they are in contact with external affairs, they see quite surely that every contact outside that self-contained group is a threat to democracy as originally conceived. That is a wise fear. If democracy is to be spontaneous, the interests of democracy must remain simple, intelligible, and easily managed. Conditions must approximate those of the isolated rural township if the supply of information is to be left to casual experience. The environment must be confined within the range of every man's direct and certain knowledge.

民主主义者已经理解了舆论分析似乎表明的一点：在处理看不见的环境时，决策“显然是随意做出的，显然不应该如此”。因此，他总是试图以这样或那样的方式尽量减少看不见的环境的重要性。他害怕对外贸易，因为贸易涉及外国联系；他不信任制造业，因为它们会产生大城市并聚集人群；如果他仍然需要制造业，他希望得到保护以实现自给自足。当他在现实世界中找不到这些条件时，他热情地走进荒野，建立了远离外国联系的乌托邦社区。他的口号揭示了他的偏见。他主张自治、自决、独立。这些想法中没有一个带有自治团体边界之外的任何同意或社区概念。民主行动领域是一个有限的领域。在受保护的边界内，目标是实现自给自足并避免纠缠。这条规则并不局限于外交政策，但它在那里显而易见，因为国界之外的生活比国界之内的生活更明显地陌生。历史表明，民主国家在外交政策方面通常不得不在光荣孤立和违背其理想的外交之间做出选择。事实上，最成功的民主国家，瑞士、丹麦、澳大利亚、新西兰和美国直到最近，都没有欧洲意义上的外交政策。即使是像门罗主义这样的规则，也是出于希望用足够共和、没有外交政策的国家来补充两大洋的愿望。

The democrat has understood what an analysis of public opinion seems to demonstrate: that in dealing with an unseen environment decisions "are manifestly settled at haphazard, which clearly they ought not to be." So he has always tried in one way or another to minimize the importance of that unseen environment. He feared foreign trade because trade involves foreign connections; he distrusted manufactures because they produced big cities and collected crowds; if he had nevertheless to have manufactures, he wanted protection in the interest of self-sufficiency. When he could not find these conditions in the real world, he went passionately into the wilderness, and founded Utopian communities far from foreign contacts. His slogans reveal his prejudice. He is for Self-Government, Self-Determination, Independence. Not one of these ideas carries with it any notion of consent or community beyond the frontiers of the self-governing groups. The field of democratic action is a circumscribed area. Within protected boundaries the aim has been to achieve self-sufficiency and avoid entanglement. This rule is not confined to foreign policy, but it is plainly evident there, because life outside the national boundaries is more distinctly alien than any life within. And as history shows, democracies in their foreign policy have had generally to choose between splendid isolation and a diplomacy that violated their ideals. The most successful democracies, in fact, Switzerland, Denmark, Australia, New Zealand, and America until recently, have had no foreign policy in the European sense of that phrase. Even a rule like the Monroe Doctrine arose from the desire to supplement the two oceans by a glacis of states that were sufficiently republican to have no foreign policy.

尽管危险是专制统治的一个重要条件，甚至可以说是不可或缺的条件，但安全被视为民主制度发挥作用的必要条件。自给自足的社会前提必须尽可能少地受到干扰。不安全感意味着意外。这意味着有人在影响你的生活，而你无法控制他们，也无法与他们商量。这意味着有力量在肆意扰乱熟悉的日常生活，并带来新的问题，需要迅速做出不同寻常的决定。每个民主人士都深知危险的危机与民主是不相容的，因为他知道群众的惰性是如此之大，以至于要迅速采取行动，只有极少数人必须做出决定，其余的人则盲目地跟随。这并没有让民主人士成为不抵抗者，但却导致所有民主战争都是为了和平主义目标而战。即使战争实际上是征服战争，人们也真诚地相信它们是为保卫文明而战。

Whereas danger is a great, perhaps an indispensable condition of autocracy, security was seen to be a necessity if democracy was to work. There must be as little disturbance as possible of the premise of a self-contained community. Insecurity involves surprises. It means that there are people acting upon your life, over whom you have no control, with whom you cannot consult. It means that forces are at large which disturb the familiar routine, and present novel problems about which quick and unusual decisions are required. Every democrat feels in his bones that dangerous crises are incompatible with democracy, because he knows that the inertia of masses is such that to act quickly a very few must decide and the rest follow rather blindly. This has not made non-resistants out of democrats, but it has resulted in all democratic wars being fought for pacifist aims. Even when the wars are in fact wars of conquest, they are sincerely believed to be wars in defense of civilization.

这些试图圈占地球表面一部分土地的各种尝试并非出于懦弱、冷漠，或者像杰斐逊的一位批评者所说的，愿意生活在僧侣般的纪律之下。民主党人看到了一个令人眼花缭乱的可能性，即每个人都应该充分发挥自己的能力，摆脱人为的限制。凭借他们对政府艺术的了解，他们无法想象一个由自治个体组成的社会，就像他们之前的亚里士多德一样，只能想象一个封闭而简单的社会。因此，如果他们要得出所有人都能自发管理公共事务的结论，他们就别无选择。

These various attempts to enclose a part of the earth's surface were not inspired by cowardice, apathy, or, what one of Jefferson's critics called a willingness to live under monkish discipline. The democrats had caught sight of a dazzling possibility, that every human being should rise to his full stature, freed from man-made limitations. With what they knew of the art of government, they could, no more than Aristotle before them, conceive a society of autonomous individuals, except an enclosed and simple one. They could, then, select no other premise if they were to reach the conclusion that all the people could spontaneously manage their public affairs.





5

5

他们采纳这个前提是因为他们迫切希望这样做，但他们也得出了其他结论。因为要实现自发的自治，就必须有一个简单的自给自足的社区，所以他们理所当然地认为，一个人和另一个人一样有能力管理这些简单而自给自足的事务。当愿望是思想的基础时，这种逻辑是令人信服的。此外，全能公民的原则在乡镇中大多数实际应用中都是正确的。村里的每个人迟早都会尝试村里所做的一切事情。全能公民的职位由各行各业的人轮流担任。在民主刻板印象被普遍应用之前，全能公民的原则并没有出现严重的问题，因此人们将复杂的文明视为一个封闭的村庄。

Having adopted the premise because it was necessary to their keenest hope, they drew other conclusions as well. Since in order to have spontaneous self-government, you had to have a simple self-contained community, they took it for granted that one man was as competent as the next to manage these simple and self-contained affairs. Where the wish is father to the thought such logic is convincing. Moreover, the doctrine of the omnicompetent citizen is for most practical purposes true in the rural township. Everybody in a village sooner or later tries his hand at everything the village does. There is rotation in office by men who are jacks of all trades. There was no serious trouble with the doctrine of the omnicompetent citizen until the democratic stereotype was universally applied, so that men looked at a complicated civilization and saw an enclosed village.

个人公民不仅适合处理所有公共事务，而且始终具有公共精神，并具有不懈的兴趣。他在乡镇中具有足够的公共精神，在那里他认识每个人，并对每个人的事情感兴趣。对于乡镇来说足够的概念很容易转变为对于任何目的来说足够的概念，因为正如我们所指出的，定量思维并不符合刻板印象。但还有另一个循环。由于假设每个人都对重要事务有足够的兴趣，因此只有每个人都感兴趣的事务才显得重要。

Not only was the individual citizen fitted to deal with all public affairs, but he was consistently public-spirited and endowed with unflagging interest. He was public-spirited enough in the township, where he knew everybody and was interested in everybody's business. The idea of enough for the township turned easily into the idea of enough for any purpose, for as we have noted, quantitative thinking does not suit a stereotype. But there was another turn to the circle. Since everybody was assumed to be interested enough in important affairs, only those affairs came to seem important in which everybody was interested.

这意味着人们从头脑中未受质疑的画面中形成了他们对外部世界的印象。这些画面在他们脑海中被父母和老师刻板地塑造，很少被他们自己的经验所纠正。只有少数人有跨越州界的风流韵事。有理由出国的就更少了。大多数选民一生都生活在一个环境中，除了几份乏味的报纸、一些小册子、政治演讲、他们的宗教训练和谣言外，他们不得不想象更大的商业和金融环境、战争与和平。与基于随意想象的舆论相比，基于任何客观报道的舆论数量非常少。

This meant that men formed their picture of the world outside from the unchallenged pictures in their heads. These pictures came to them well stereotyped by their parents and teachers, and were little corrected by their own experience. Only a few men had affairs that took them across state lines. Even fewer had reason to go abroad. Most voters lived their whole lives in one environment, and with nothing but a few feeble newspapers, some pamphlets, political speeches, their religious training, and rumor to go on, they had to conceive that larger environment of commerce and finance, of war and peace. The number of public opinions based on any objective report was very small in proportion to those based on casual fancy.

因此，出于许多不同的原因，自给自足在形成时期是一种精神理想。乡镇的物理孤立、拓荒者的孤独、民主理论、新教传统和政治科学的局限性，所有这些都使人们相信，他们必须从自己的良心中提取政治智慧。从绝对原则中推导出法律会夺走他们如此多的自由能量，这并不奇怪。美国政治思想必须依靠其资本生存。在法制主义中，它找到了一套经过检验的规则，从中可以制定新的规则，而不必从经验中获得新的真理。这些公式变得如此神圣，以至于每一位优秀的外国观察家都对美国人民充满活力的实践能量与他们公共生活的静态理论主义之间的对比感到惊讶。对固定原则的坚定热爱正是实现自给自足的唯一已知途径。但这意味着任何一个社区的公众对外部世界的看法主要都是由一些刻板的形象组成的，这些形象按照从其法律和道德准则中推断出的模式排列，并受到当地经验所激发的感觉的激发。

And so for many different reasons, self-sufficiency was a spiritual ideal in the formative period. The physical isolation of the township, the loneliness of the pioneer, the theory of democracy, the Protestant tradition, and the limitations of political science all converged to make men believe that out of their own consciences they must extricate political wisdom. It is not strange that the deduction of laws from absolute principles should have usurped so much of their free energy. The American political mind had to live on its capital. In legalism it found a tested body of rules from which new rules could be spun without the labor of earning new truths from experience. The formulae became so curiously sacred that every good foreign observer has been amazed at the contrast between the dynamic practical energy of the American people and the static theorism of their public life. That steadfast love of fixed principles was simply the only way known of achieving self-sufficiency. But it meant that the public opinions of any one community about the outer world consisted chiefly of a few stereotyped images arranged in a pattern deduced from their legal and their moral codes, and animated by the feeling aroused by local experiences.

因此，民主理论从其对终极人类尊严的美好愿景出发，由于缺乏报告其环境的知识工具，被迫依靠选民身上积累的智慧和经验。用杰斐逊的话来说，上帝把人的胸膛变成了“他独特的储藏实质性和真正美德的地方”。这些被选中的人在他们自给自足的环境中掌握了所有的事实。环境是如此熟悉，以至于人们可以理所当然地认为人们谈论的是基本相同的事情。因此，唯一真正的分歧将是对相同事实的判断。没有必要保证信息来源。它们是显而易见的，所有人都可以平等地获得。也没有必要为最终的标准而烦恼。在自给自足的社会中，人们可以假设，或至少确实假设了同质的道德准则。因此，唯一存在意见分歧的地方是将公认的标准逻辑地应用于公认的事实。而且由于推理能力也得到了很好的标准化，推理中的错误很快就会在自由讨论中暴露出来。因此，在这些限制内，人们可以自由地获得真理。社会可以将其信息供应视为理所当然；其准则通过学校、教堂和家庭传递，从前提中得出推论的能力，而不是找到前提的能力，被视为智力训练的主要目的。

Thus democratic theory, starting from its fine vision of ultimate human dignity, was forced by lack of the instruments of knowledge for reporting its environment, to fall back upon the wisdom and experience which happened to have accumulated in the voter. God had, in the words of Jefferson, made men's breasts "His peculiar deposit for substantial and genuine virtue." These chosen people in their self-contained environment had all the facts before them. The environment was so familiar that one could take it for granted that men were talking about substantially the same things. The only real disagreements, therefore, would be in judgments about the same facts. There was no need to guarantee the sources of information. They were obvious, and equally accessible to all men. Nor was there need to trouble about the ultimate criteria. In the self-contained community one could assume, or at least did assume, a homogeneous code of morals. The only place, therefore, for differences of opinion was in the logical application of accepted standards to accepted facts. And since the reasoning faculty was also well standardized, an error in reasoning would be quickly exposed in a free discussion. It followed that truth could be obtained by liberty within these limits. The community could take its supply of information for granted; its codes it passed on through school, church, and family, and the power to draw deductions from a premise, rather than the ability to find the premise, was regarded as the chief end of intellectual training.

第十八章

CHAPTER XVIII

武力、庇护和特权的作用

THE ROLE OF FORCE, PATRONAGE AND PRIVILEGE





1

1

汉密尔顿写道：“正如人们所预见的那样，联邦的措施并未得到执行；各州的失职行为一步步发展到极点，最终导致国家政府的所有运转陷入停滞，并陷入可怕的停顿。”……因为“在我们的情况下，在联邦制下，要完全执行联邦制定的每一项重要措施，就需要十三个不同的主权意志的一致同意。”他问道：“各成员国的统治者……将负责判断措施本身是否适当。他们将考虑所提议或要求的事情是否符合他们的直接利益或目标；是否符合通过该措施带来的暂时便利或不便。所有这些都将以利害攸关和怀疑的态度进行，不了解国家情况和国家理由，而这些对于正确判断至关重要，并且对地方目标的强烈偏爱几乎肯定会误导决策。同样的过程必须在组成该机构的每个成员国重复进行；而由全体议会制定的计划的执行，将始终受到各部分不了解情况和偏见的意见的影响。那些熟悉人民议会程序的人，他们看到，在没有外部环境压力的情况下，让他们就重要问题达成和谐决议往往是多么困难，他们很容易想象，要让许多人民议会成员同意他们做出一致决定是多么不可能。这样的集会，在不同的时间、以不同的印象进行远距离审议，渴望在相同的观点和追求下进行合作。”

"IT has happened as was to have been foreseen," wrote Hamilton, "the measures of the Union have not been executed; the delinquencies of the States have, step by step, matured themselves to an extreme which has at length arrested all the wheels of the national government and brought them to an awful stand."… For "in our case the concurrence of thirteen distinct sovereign wills is requisite, under the confederation, to the complete execution of every important measure that proceeds from the Union." How could it be otherwise, he asked: "The rulers of the respective members… will undertake to judge of the propriety of the measures themselves. They will consider the conformity of the thing proposed or required to their immediate interests or aims; the momentary conveniences or inconveniences that would attend its adoption. All this will be done, and in a spirit of interested and suspicious scrutiny, without that knowledge of national circumstances and reasons of state which is essential to right judgment, and with that strong predilection in favor of local objects which can hardly fail to mislead the decision. The same process must be repeated in every member of which the body is constituted; and the execution of the plans framed by the councils of the whole, will always fluctuate on the discretion of the ill-informed and prejudiced opinion of every part. Those who have been conversant in the proceedings of popular assemblies, who have seen how difficult it often is, when there is no exterior pressure of circumstances, to bring them to harmonious resolutions on important points, will readily conceive how impossible it must be to induce a number of such assemblies, deliberating at a distance from each other, at different times, and under different impressions, long to cooperate in the same views and pursuits."

十年的风风雨雨，以及约翰·亚当斯所说的“只是外交集会”的国会，为革命领袖们提供了“具有启发性但又令人痛苦的教训”，让他们明白，当许多以自我为中心的社区陷入同一环境时会发生什么。因此，当他们于 1787 年 5 月前往费城，表面上是为了修改《邦联条例》，实际上是在完全反对 18 世纪民主的基本前提。这些领导人不仅有意识地反对当时的民主精神，正如麦迪逊所说，他们觉得“民主一直都是动荡和争斗的奇观”，而且他们决心在国家边界内尽可能地抵消在自给自足的环境中建立自治社区的理想。凹面民主的冲突和失败摆在他们眼前，在凹面民主中，人们自发地管理自己的所有事务。在他们看来，问题在于恢复政府，而不是民主。他们理解政府是制定国家决策并在全国范围内执行的权力；他们相信民主是地方和阶级根据其直接利益和目标坚持自决。

Over ten years of storm and stress with a congress that was, as John Adams said, "only a diplomatic assembly," had furnished the leaders of the revolution "with an instructive but afflicting lesson" in what happens when a number of self-centered communities are entangled in the same environment. And so, when they went to Philadelphia in May of 1787, ostensibly to revise the Articles of Confederation, they were really in full reaction against the fundamental premise of Eighteenth Century democracy. Not only were the leaders consciously opposed to the democratic spirit of the time, feeling, as Madison said, that "democracies have ever been spectacles of turbulence and contention," but within the national frontiers they were determined to offset as far as they could the ideal of self-governing communities in self-contained environments. The collisions and failures of concave democracy, where men spontaneously managed all their own affairs, were before their eyes. The problem as they saw it, was to restore government as against democracy. They understood government to be the power to make national decisions and enforce them throughout the nation; democracy they believed was the insistence of localities and classes upon self-determination in accordance with their immediate interests and aims.

他们在计算中没有考虑到这样一种知识组织的可能性，即不同的社区会同时根据同一种事实采取行动。我们刚刚开始设想这种可能性，适用于世界上某些新闻自由流通、语言通用的地区，而且仅限于生活的某些方面。工业和世界政治中自愿联邦制的整个概念仍然很初级，正如我们在自己的经验中所看到的，它只在实际政治中发挥了很小的作用。一个多世纪后，我们只能设想它激励几代人的智力努力，而宪法的作者根本没有理由设想它。为了建立国家政府，汉密尔顿和他的同事们必须制定计划，不是基于人们会因为有共同利益而合作的理论，而是基于如果特殊利益通过权力平衡保持平衡，人们就可以被统治的理论。麦迪逊说：“必须用野心来抵消野心。”

They could not consider in their calculations the possibility of such an organization of knowledge that separate communities would act simultaneously on the same version of the facts. We just begin to conceive this possibility for certain parts of the world where there is free circulation of news and a common language, and then only for certain aspects of life. The whole idea of a voluntary federalism in industry and world politics is still so rudimentary, that, as we see in our own experience, it enters only a little, and only very modestly, into practical politics. What we, more than a century later, can only conceive as an incentive to generations of intellectual effort, the authors of the Constitution had no reason to conceive at all. In order to set up national government, Hamilton and his colleagues had to make plans, not on the theory that men would cooperate because they had a sense of common interest, but on the theory that men could be governed, if special interests were kept in equilibrium by a balance of power. "Ambition," Madison said, "must be made to counteract ambition."

他们并不像某些作家所认为的那样，想要平衡各方利益，让政府陷入永久的僵局。他们想要使地方和阶级利益陷入僵局，以防止这些利益妨碍政府。麦迪逊写道：“在组建一个由人统治人的政府时，最大的困难在于：你必须首先让政府控制被统治者，其次，迫使政府控制自己。”因此，在一个非常重要的意义上，制衡原则是联邦主义领导人解决舆论问题的良方。他们认为，除了设计一种巧妙的机器来中和地方舆论之外，没有其他方法可以用“行政长官的温和影响”来取代“剑的血腥力量”。他们不懂得如何操纵大量选民，就像他们看不到在共同信息的基础上达成共同同意的可能性一样。确实，当汉密尔顿在 1800 年借助坦慕尼协会夺取纽约市控制权时，阿伦·伯尔给汉密尔顿上了一课，给他留下了深刻印象。但汉密尔顿在能够考虑到这一新发现之前就被杀了，而且，正如福特先生所说，伯尔的手枪炸毁了联邦党的脑袋。

They did not, as some writers have supposed, intend to balance every interest so that the government would be in a perpetual deadlock. They intended to deadlock local and class interest to prevent these from obstructing government. "In framing a government which is to be administered by men over men," wrote Madison, "the great difficulty lies in this: you must first enable the government to control the governed, and in the next place, oblige it to control itself." In one very important sense, then, the doctrine of checks and balances was the remedy of the federalist leaders for the problem of public opinion. They saw no other way to substitute "the mild influence of the magistracy" for the "sanguinary agency of the sword" except by devising an ingenious machine to neutralize local opinion. They did not understand how to manipulate a large electorate, any more than they saw the possibility of common consent upon the basis of common information. It is true that Aaron Burr taught Hamilton a lesson which impressed him a good deal when he seized control of New York City in 1800 by the aid of Tammany Hall. But Hamilton was killed before he was able to take account of this new discovery, and, as Mr. Ford says, Burr's pistol blew the brains out of the Federal party.





2

2

宪法制定时，“政治仍可通过绅士之间的协商和协议来管理”，汉密尔顿向绅士寻求政府支持。当地方偏见通过宪法制衡而达到平衡时，他们应该管理国家事务。毫无疑问，汉密尔顿因收养而属于这个阶级，因此对绅士有偏爱。但这本身不足以解释他的治国之道。当然，他对联盟的强烈热情是毋庸置疑的，我认为，说他建立联盟是为了保护阶级特权，而不是说他利用阶级特权建立了联盟，这是颠倒事实。汉密尔顿说：“我们必须以我们所发现的为人，如果我们希望他为公众服务，就必须激起他的热情。”他需要能够最迅速地将热情与国家利益联系起来的人来治理国家。这些人包括绅士、公共债权人、制造商、船运商和商人，历史上可能没有比汉密尔顿采取的一系列财政措施更好的例子来说明如何采用精明的手段来实现明确的目的，通过这些措施，汉密尔顿把地方知名人士团结在新政府中。

When the constitution was written, "politics could still be managed by conference and agreement among gentlemen" and it was to the gentry that Hamilton turned for a government. It was intended that they should manage national affairs when local prejudice had been brought into equilibrium by the constitutional checks and balances. No doubt Hamilton, who belonged to this class by adoption, had a human prejudice in their favor. But that by itself is a thin explanation of his statecraft. Certainly there can be no question of his consuming passion for union, and it is, I think, an inversion of the truth to argue that he made the Union to protect class privileges, instead of saying that he used class privileges to make the Union. "We must take man as we find him," Hamilton said, "and if we expect him to serve the public we must interest his passions in doing so." He needed men to govern, whose passions could be most quickly attached to a national interest. These were the gentry, the public creditors, manufacturers, shippers, and traders, and there is probably no better instance in history of the adaptation of shrewd means to clear ends, than in the series of fiscal measures, by which Hamilton attached the provincial notables to the new government.

尽管制宪会议是闭门进行的，尽管批准是“可能不超过六分之一的成年男性投票的结果”，但几乎没有任何掩饰。联邦党人主张联盟，而不是民主，甚至共和国这个词对乔治·华盛顿来说也是一种不愉快的声音，因为他已经担任了两年多的共和党总统。宪法是限制民众统治范围的一次坦率尝试；政府应该拥有的唯一民主机构是众议院，而众议院的选举权受到财产资格的严格限制。即便如此，人们认为众议院将是政府中如此放荡的一部分，因此它受到参议院、选举团、总统否决权和司法解释的仔细制约和平衡。

Although the constitutional convention worked behind closed doors, and although ratification was engineered by "a vote of probably not more than one-sixth of the adult males," there was little or no pretence. The Federalists argued for union, not for democracy, and even the word republic had an unpleasant sound to George Washington when he had been for more than two years a republican president. The constitution was a candid attempt to limit the sphere of popular rule; the only democratic organ it was intended the government should possess was the House, based on a suffrage highly limited by property qualifications. And even at that, the House, it was believed, would be so licentious a part of the government, that it was carefully checked and balanced by the Senate, the electoral college, the Presidential veto, and by judicial interpretation.

因此，当法国大革命在全世界激起民心的时候，1776 年的美国革命者们却受到了一部尽可能效仿英国君主制的宪法的约束。这种保守的反动无法持续下去。制定这一政策的人是少数，他们的动机受到怀疑，而当华盛顿退休时，士绅阶层的地位还不足以在不可避免的继承权斗争中生存下来。教父们最初的计划与当时的道德情感之间的差距太大了，一位优秀的政治家不能不利用这一点。

Thus at the moment when the French Revolution was kindling popular feeling the world over, the American revolutionists of 1776 came under a constitution which went back, as far as it was expedient, to the British Monarchy for a model. This conservative reaction could not endure. The men who had made it were a minority, their motives were under suspicion, and when Washington went into retirement, the position of the gentry was not strong enough to survive the inevitable struggle for the succession. The anomaly between the original plan of the Fathers and the moral feeling of the age was too wide not to be capitalized by a good politician.





3

3

杰斐逊将自己的当选称为“1800 年的伟大革命”，但更重要的是，这是一场思想上的革命。虽然没有改变任何重大政策，但建立了新的传统。因为杰斐逊是第一个教导美国人民将宪法视为民主工具的人，他塑造了美国人自此以后相互描述政治的形象、思想，甚至许多短语。这种思想上的胜利是如此彻底，以至于 25 年后，受到联邦党人家庭接待的托克维尔指出，即使是那些“因持续存在而感到恼火”的人，也常常听到“在公共场合赞美共和政府的魅力和民主制度的优势”。

Jefferson referred to his election as "the great revolution of 1800," but more than anything else it was a revolution in the mind. No great policy was altered, but a new tradition was established. For it was Jefferson who first taught the American people to regard the Constitution as an instrument of democracy, and he stereotyped the images, the ideas, and even many of the phrases, in which Americans ever since have described politics to each other. So complete was the mental victory, that twenty-five years later de Tocqueville, who was received in Federalist homes, noted that even those who were "galled by its continuance"—were not uncommonly heard to "laud the delights of a republican government, and the advantages of democratic institutions when they are in public."

制宪之父们尽管十分睿智，却未能看到，一部明显不民主的宪法不会长期被容忍。对民治的大胆否定必然会为像杰斐逊这样的人提供一个攻击的切入点，就其宪法观点而言，杰斐逊并不比汉密尔顿更愿意将政府移交给“未经提炼”的人民意志。联邦党领袖们都是有明确信念的人，他们直言不讳。他们的公开观点和私人观点之间几乎没有真正的差异。但杰斐逊的思想却充满矛盾，这不仅仅是因为其缺陷（汉密尔顿和他的传记作者认为），还因为他相信联盟，也相信自发民主，而他那个时代的政治学没有令人满意的方法来调和这两者。杰斐逊的思想和行动都混乱不堪，因为他有一个新奇而伟大的想法，而没有人全面地考虑过它。但是，尽管没有人清楚地理解人民主权，但它似乎意味着人类生活的巨大改善，以至于任何宪法都不能坦率地否认它。因此，坦率的否认从意识中被抹去，而这份表面上是有限宪政民主的真实例子的文件，却被谈论和认为是直接人民统治的工具。杰斐逊实际上已经到了相信联邦党人已经曲解宪法的地步，在他看来，他们不再是宪法的作者。因此，宪法在精神上被重写。部分是通过实际修订，部分是通过实践，如选举团的情况，但主要是通过另一套刻板印象来看待它，外表不再允许看起来像寡头政治。

The Constitutional Fathers with all their sagacity had failed to see that a frankly undemocratic constitution would not long be tolerated. The bold denial of popular rule was bound to offer an easy point of attack to a man, like Jefferson, who so far as his constitutional opinions ran, was not a bit more ready than Hamilton to turn over government to the "unrefined" will of the people. The Federalist leaders had been men of definite convictions who stated them bluntly. There was little real discrepancy between their public and their private views. But Jefferson's mind was a mass of ambiguities, not solely because of its defects, as Hamilton and his biographers have thought, but because he believed in a union and he believed in spontaneous democracies, and in the political science of his age there was no satisfactory way to reconcile the two. Jefferson was confused in thought and action because he had a vision of a new and tremendous idea that no one had thought out in all its bearings. But though popular sovereignty was not clearly understood by anybody, it seemed to imply so great an enhancement of human life, that no constitution could stand which frankly denied it. The frank denials were therefore expunged from consciousness, and the document, which is on its face an honest example of limited constitutional democracy, was talked and thought about as an instrument for direct popular rule. Jefferson actually reached the point of believing that the Federalists had perverted the Constitution, of which in his fancy they were no longer the authors. And so the Constitution was, in spirit, rewritten. Partly by actual amendment, partly by practice, as in the case of the electoral college, but chiefly by looking at it through another set of stereotypes, the facade was no longer permitted to look oligarchic.

美国人民开始相信他们的宪法是民主的工具，并以此对待它。他们将这一虚构归功于托马斯·杰斐逊的胜利，而这已成为一个伟大的保守主义虚构。可以合理地猜测，如果每个人都像宪法的作者那样看待宪法，宪法就会被暴力推翻，因为对宪法的忠诚和对民主的忠诚似乎是不相容的。杰斐逊通过教导美国人民将宪法视为民主的表达来解决这一悖论。他自己就此止步。但在大约二十五年的时间里，社会条件发生了如此巨大的变化，安德鲁·杰克逊进行了杰斐逊为之准备的传统的政治革命。

The American people came to believe that their Constitution was a democratic instrument, and treated it as such. They owe that fiction to the victory of Thomas Jefferson, and a great conservative fiction it has been. It is a fair guess that if everyone had always regarded the Constitution as did the authors of it, the Constitution would have been violently overthrown, because loyalty to the Constitution and loyalty to democracy would have seemed incompatible. Jefferson resolved that paradox by teaching the American people to read the Constitution as an expression of democracy. He himself stopped there. But in the course of twenty-five years or so social conditions had changed so radically, that Andrew Jackson carried out the political revolution for which Jefferson had prepared the tradition.









4

4

这场革命的政治核心是任人唯亲的问题。政府的创立者认为公职是一种财产，不容轻易侵犯，他们无疑希望公职能留在自己的社会阶层手中。但民主理论的主要原则之一就是全能公民的原则。因此，当人们开始将宪法视为民主工具时，官职常任制无疑会显得不民主。人们的自然野心与他们那个时代伟大的道德冲动不谋而合。杰斐逊推广了这一理念，但并未将其无情地付诸实践，在弗吉尼亚州总统任期内，因党派原因被罢免的情况相对较少。杰克逊开创了将公职转变为任人唯亲的做法。

The political center of that revolution was the question of patronage. By the men who founded the government public office was regarded as a species of property, not lightly to be disturbed, and it was undoubtedly their hope that the offices would remain in the hands of their social class. But the democratic theory had as one of its main principles the doctrine of the omnicompetent citizen. Therefore, when people began to look at the Constitution as a democratic instrument, it was certain that permanence in office would seem undemocratic. The natural ambitions of men coincided here with the great moral impulse of their age. Jefferson had popularized the idea without carrying it ruthlessly into practice, and removals on party grounds were comparatively few under the Virginian Presidents. It was Jackson who founded the practice of turning public office into patronage.

在我们看来，这听起来很奇怪，但短期轮换制被认为是一项伟大的改革。它不仅承认普通人的新尊严，将他们视为适合任何职位的人，不仅摧毁了少数社会阶层的垄断，似乎为人才打开了职业大门，而且“几个世纪以来，它一直被推崇为政治腐败的万能药”，是防止官僚主义产生的一种方式。公职人员快速更替的做法是将自给自足的村庄民主形象应用于广大地区。

Curious as it sounds to us, the principle of rotation in office with short terms was regarded as a great reform. Not only did it acknowledge the new dignity of the average man by treating him as fit for any office, not only did it destroy the monopoly of a small social class and appear to open careers to talent, but "it had been advocated for centuries as a sovereign remedy for political corruption," and as the one way to prevent the creation of a bureaucracy. The practice of rapid change in public office was the application to a great territory of the image of democracy derived from the self-contained village.

当然，它在国内没有取得与民主理论所基于的理想社会相同的结果。它产生了意想不到的结果，因为它建立了一个新的统治阶级来取代被淹没的联邦主义者。无意中，赞助对大选民的影响就像汉密尔顿的财政措施对上层阶级的影响一样。我们常常没有意识到我们政府的稳定在多大程度上归功于赞助。因为正是赞助使天生的领导者摆脱了对以自我为中心的社会的过度依恋，正是赞助削弱了地方精神，并通过某种和平合作将这些人聚集在一起，而这些人作为地方名人，如果没有共同利益意识，就会把联盟分裂开来。

Naturally it did not have the same results in the nation that it had in the ideal community on which the democratic theory was based. It produced quite unexpected results, for it founded a new governing class to take the place of the submerged federalists. Unintentionally, patronage did for a large electorate what Hamilton's fiscal measures had done for the upper classes. We often fail to realize how much of the stability of our government we owe to patronage. For it was patronage that weaned natural leaders from too much attachment to the self-centered community, it was patronage that weakened the local spirit and brought together in some kind of peaceful cooperation, the very men who, as provincial celebrities, would, in the absence of a sense of common interest, have torn the union apart.

但当然，民主理论并不打算产生一个新的统治阶级，它从未适应过这一事实。当民主党人想要废除官职垄断，实行轮换和短期任期时，他想到的是乡镇，在那里任何人都可以做公共服务，然后谦卑地回到自己的农场。一个特殊的政治家阶层的想法正是民主党人不喜欢的。但他无法拥有他喜欢的东西，因为他的理论源于一个理想的环境，而他生活在一个真实的环境中。他越深刻地感受到民主的道德冲动，就越不愿意看到汉密尔顿所说的深刻真理，即在远处和不同印象下进行审议的社区无法长期合作，共同追求相同的观点和追求。因为这个真理推迟了任何类似于在公共事务中充分实现民主的事情，直到获得共同同意的艺术得到根本性的改进。因此，虽然杰斐逊和杰克逊领导的革命产生了赞助，从而形成了两党制，创造了绅士统治的替代品，并建立了管理三权分立僵局的纪律，但所有这一切都是在无形中发生的。

But of course, the democratic theory was not supposed to produce a new governing class, and it has never accommodated itself to the fact. When the democrat wanted to abolish monopoly of offices, to have rotation and short terms, he was thinking of the township where anyone could do a public service, and return humbly to his own farm. The idea of a special class of politicians was just what the democrat did not like. But he could not have what he did like, because his theory was derived from an ideal environment, and he was living in a real one. The more deeply he felt the moral impulse of democracy, the less ready he was to see the profound truth of Hamilton's statement that communities deliberating at a distance and under different impressions could not long coöperate in the same views and pursuits. For that truth postpones anything like the full realization of democracy in public affairs until the art of obtaining common consent has been radically improved. And so while the revolution under Jefferson and Jackson produced the patronage which made the two party system, which created a substitute for the rule of the gentry, and a discipline for governing the deadlock of the checks and balances, all that happened, as it were, invisibly.

因此，轮换职位可能是表面上的理论，实际上职位在亲信之间来回变动。任期可能不是永久垄断，但职业政客却是永久垄断的。正如哈丁总统曾经说过的，政府可能很简单，但赢得选举却是一项复杂的工作。官员的薪水可能像杰斐逊的家常便饭一样节俭，但党组织的开支和胜利的果实却是宏伟的。民主的刻板印象控制着可见的政府；美国人民对其环境真实事实的修正、例外和适应必须是看不见的，即使每个人都知道这些。只有法律的文字、政客的演讲、政纲和正式的行政机构必须符合民主的原始形象。

Thus, rotation in office might be the ostensible theory, in practice the offices oscillated between the henchmen. Tenure might not be a permanent monopoly, but the professional politician was permanent. Government might be, as President Harding once said, a simple thing, but winning elections was a sophisticated performance. The salaries in office might be as ostentatiously frugal as Jefferson's home-spun, but the expenses of party organization and the fruits of victory were in the grand manner. The stereotype of democracy controlled the visible government; the corrections, the exceptions and adaptations of the American people to the real facts of their environment have had to be invisible, even when everybody knew all about them. It was only the words of the law, the speeches of politicians, the platforms, and the formal machinery of administration that have had to conform to the pristine image of democracy.





5

5

如果有人问一位哲学民主主义者，当公众舆论如此以自我为中心时，这些自给自足的社区如何合作，他会指出国会代表的代议制政府。没有什么比发现代议制政府的威望如何稳步下降，而总统的权力却在增长更让他惊讶的了。

If one had asked a philosophical democrat how these self-contained communities were to cooperate, when their public opinions were so self-centered, he would have pointed to representative government embodied in the Congress. And nothing would surprise him more than the discovery of how steadily the prestige of representative government has declined, while the power of the Presidency has grown.

一些批评家将此归因于只派遣当地名人前往华盛顿的习俗。他们认为，如果国会能由全国知名人士组成，首都的生活将会更加精彩。当然，如果即将退休的总统和内阁官员效仿约翰·昆西·亚当斯，那将是一件非常好的事情。但这些人的缺席并不能解释国会的困境，因为它的衰落始于它相对最杰出的政府部门。事实上，更可能的情况是相反的，国会不再吸引知名人士，因为它失去了对国家政策制定的直接影响。

Some critics have traced this to the custom of sending only local celebrities to Washington. They have thought that if Congress could consist of the nationally eminent men, the life of the capital would be more brilliant. It would be, of course, and it would be a very good thing if retiring Presidents and Cabinet officers followed the example of John Quincy Adams. But the absence of these men does not explain the plight of Congress, for its decline began when it was relatively the most eminent branch of the government. Indeed it is more probable that the reverse is true, and that Congress ceased to attract the eminent as it lost direct influence on the shaping of national policy.

我认为，造成这种世界性失信的主要原因在于，国会本质上是一群盲人，他们身处一个广阔而未知的世界。除了一些例外，宪法或代议制政府理论中承认的国会了解情况的唯一方法是交换各选区的意见。国会没有系统、充分和授权的方式来了解世界上正在发生的事情。理论认为，每个选区的最佳人选将选民的最佳智慧带到一个中心，而所有这些智慧加在一起就是国会所需要的智慧。现在，没有必要质疑表达和交换当地意见的价值。国会作为一个大陆国家的市场具有巨大的价值。在衣帽间、酒店大堂、国会山的寄宿公寓、国会女主人的茶话会以及偶尔进入国际化华盛顿的客厅，新的前景和更广阔的视野都被打开了。但即使应用这一理论，各地区也总是派出最聪明的人，当地印象的总和或组合也不足以成为国家政策的广泛基础，也根本不是控制外交政策的基础。由于大多数法律的实际影响都是微妙而隐蔽的，因此无法通过过滤当地经验和当地心态来了解它们。只有通过受控报道和客观分析才能了解它们。正如一家大工厂的负责人无法通过与工头交谈来了解工厂的效率，而必须检查只有会计师才能为他挖掘出的成本表和数据一样，立法者也无法通过拼凑当地图片来获得联邦状况的真实图景。他需要了解当地的情况，但除非他拥有校准它们的仪器，否则一幅图景与另一幅图景一样好，甚至好得多。

The main reason for the discredit, which is world wide, is, I think, to be found in the fact that a congress of representatives is essentially a group of blind men in a vast, unknown world. With some exceptions, the only method recognized in the Constitution or in the theory of representative government, by which Congress can inform itself, is to exchange opinions from the districts. There is no systematic, adequate, and authorized way for Congress to know what is going on in the world. The theory is that the best man of each district brings the best wisdom of his constituents to a central place, and that all these wisdoms combined are all the wisdom that Congress needs. Now there is no need to question the value of expressing local opinions and exchanging them. Congress has great value as the market-place of a continental nation. In the coatrooms, the hotel lobbies, the boarding houses of Capitol Hill, at the tea-parties of the Congressional matrons, and from occasional entries into the drawing rooms of cosmopolitan Washington, new vistas are opened, and wider horizons. But even if the theory were applied, and the districts always sent their wisest men, the sum or a combination of local impressions is not a wide enough base for national policy, and no base at all for the control of foreign policy. Since the real effects of most laws are subtle and hidden, they cannot be understood by filtering local experiences through local states of mind. They can be known only by controlled reporting and objective analysis. And just as the head of a large factory cannot know how efficient it is by talking to the foreman, but must examine cost sheets and data that only an accountant can dig out for him, so the lawmaker does not arrive at a true picture of the state of the union by putting together a mosaic of local pictures. He needs to know the local pictures, but unless he possesses instruments for calibrating them, one picture is as good as the next, and a great deal better.

总统确实通过发表国情咨文来协助国会。他之所以能这样做，是因为他掌管着一大批机构及其代理人，他们既要报告，又要采取行动。但他只告诉国会他想说的话。他不能被人阻拦，而审查哪些内容符合公众利益则由他决定。这是一种完全片面而棘手的关系，有时甚至荒谬至极，以至于国会为了获得一份重要文件，不得不感谢芝加哥一家报纸的辛勤工作，或者下属官员的蓄意轻率行为。立法者与必要事实的接触如此糟糕，以至于他们不得不依靠私人情报或合法的暴行——国会调查，在这种调查中，国会议员们缺乏合法的思考材料，开始疯狂而狂热地搜捕，甚至不止于吃人。

The President does come to the assistance of Congress by delivering messages on the state of the Union. He is in a position to do that because he presides over a vast collection of bureaus and their agents, which report as well as act. But he tells Congress what he chooses to tell it. He cannot be heckled, and the censorship as to what is compatible with the public interest is in his hands. It is a wholly one-sided and tricky relationship, which sometimes reaches such heights of absurdity, that Congress, in order to secure an important document has to thank the enterprise of a Chicago newspaper, or the calculated indiscretion of a subordinate official. So bad is the contact of legislators with necessary facts that they are forced to rely either on private tips or on that legalized atrocity, the Congressional investigation, where Congressmen, starved of their legitimate food for thought, go on a wild and feverish man-hunt, and do not stop at cannibalism.

除了这些调查结果很少、行政部门偶尔的通报、私人收集的感兴趣和不感兴趣的数据、国会议员阅读的报纸、期刊和书籍，以及向州际商务委员会、联邦贸易委员会和关税委员会等专家机构寻求帮助的新做法外，国会意见的形成是乱伦的。由此可见，要么国家立法是由少数知情人士准备的，并通过党派力量通过；要么立法被分解成一系列地方项目，每一项都是出于当地原因而制定的。关税表、海军造船厂、陆军哨所、河流和港口、邮局和联邦大楼、养老金和赞助：这些都被提供给凹陷社区，作为国家生活好处的有形证据。凹陷社区可以看到用联邦资金建造的白色大理石建筑，以提高当地房地产价值并雇用当地承包商，却无法判断政治分肥的累计成本。公平地说，在一个庞大的议会中，每个人只对自己的选区有实际了解，处理跨地区事务的法律会被大多数国会议员拒绝或接受，而没有任何创造性的参与。他们只参与制定那些可以作为一堆地方问题处理的法律。因为一个没有有效信息和分析手段的立法机构必须在盲目的规律性（偶尔会受到叛乱的影响）和互投赞成票之间摇摆不定。正是互投赞成票使规律性变得可以接受，因为通过互投赞成票，国会议员向更积极的选民证明，他正在关注他们所设想的利益。

Except for the little that these investigations yield, the occasional communications from the executive departments, interested and disinterested data collected by private persons, such newspapers, periodicals, and books as Congressmen read, and a new and excellent practice of calling for help from expert bodies like the Interstate Commerce Commission, the Federal Trade Commission, and the Tariff Commission, the creation of Congressional opinion is incestuous. From this it follows either that legislation of a national character is prepared by a few informed insiders, and put through by partisan force; or that the legislation is broken up into a collection of local items, each of which is enacted for a local reason. Tariff schedules, navy yards, army posts, rivers and harbors, post offices and federal buildings, pensions and patronage: these are fed out to concave communities as tangible evidence of the benefits of national life. Being concave, they can see the white marble building which rises out of federal funds to raise local realty values and employ local contractors more readily than they can judge the cumulative cost of the pork barrel. It is fair to say that in a large assembly of men, each of whom has practical knowledge only of his own district, laws dealing with translocal affairs are rejected or accepted by the mass of Congressmen without creative participation of any kind. They participate only in making those laws that can be treated as a bundle of local issues. For a legislature without effective means of information and analysis must oscillate between blind regularity, tempered by occasional insurgency, and logrolling. And it is the logrolling which makes the regularity palatable, because it is by logrolling that a Congressman proves to his more active constituents that he is watching their interests as they conceive them.

这不是国会议员个人的错，除非他对此沾沾自喜。最聪明、最勤奋的代表也不可能指望自己能理解他所投票表决的法案的一小部分。他所能做的最好的事情就是专注于少数法案，其余的则听从别人的意见。我知道国会议员在研究一个主题时，会像他们通过期末考试以来从未研究过的那样，喝很多大杯黑咖啡，用湿毛巾等等。他们必须挖掘信息，费尽心思整理和核实事实，而在任何有意识组织的政府中，这些事实都应该以适合决策的形式轻松获得。即使他们真的了解一个主题，他们的焦虑才刚刚开始。因为在国内，编辑、贸易委员会、中央联合工会和妇女俱乐部都省去了这些工作，准备通过当地的奇观来观察国会议员的表现。

This is no fault of the individual Congressman's, except when he is complacent about it. The cleverest and most industrious representative cannot hope to understand a fraction of the bills on which he votes. The best he can do is to specialize on a few bills, and take somebody's word about the rest. I have known Congressmen, when they were boning up on a subject, to study as they had not studied since they passed their final examinations, many large cups of black coffee, wet towels and all. They had to dig for information, sweat over arranging and verifying facts, which, in any consciously organized government, should have been easily available in a form suitable for decision. And even when they really knew a subject, their anxieties had only begun. For back home the editors, the board of trade, the central federated union, and the women's clubs had spared themselves these labors, and were prepared to view the Congressman's performance through local spectacles.





6

6

赞助使政治领袖与国家政府紧密相连，而无数种地方补贴和特权则使以自我为中心的社区紧密相连。赞助和利益融合并稳定了成千上万的特殊观点、地方不满和私人野心。只有另外两种选择。一种是通过恐怖和服从来统治，另一种是基于高度发达的信息、分析和自我意识系统的统治，以至于“对国家情况和国家原因的了解”对所有人都是显而易见的。专制制度正在衰落，自愿制度正处于其最初的发展阶段；因此，在计算大群体、国际联盟、工业政府或联邦州联盟之间的联合前景时，共同意识的材料存在程度决定了合作将在多大程度上依赖于武力，或者依赖于武力的较温和的替代方案，即赞助和特权。亚历山大·汉密尔顿等伟大的国家建设者的秘密在于，他们知道如何计算这些原则。

What patronage did to attach political chieftains to the national government, the infinite variety of local subsidies and privileges do for self-centered communities. Patronage and pork amalgamate and stabilize thousands of special opinions, local discontents, private ambitions. There are but two other alternatives. One is government by terror and obedience, the other is government based on such a highly developed system of information, analysis, and self-consciousness that "the knowledge of national circumstances and reasons of state" is evident to all men. The autocratic system is in decay, the voluntary system is in its very earliest development; and so, in calculating the prospects of association among large groups of people, a League of Nations, industrial government, or a federal union of states, the degree to which the material for a common consciousness exists, determines how far cooperation will depend upon force, or upon the milder alternative to force, which is patronage and privilege. The secret of great state-builders, like Alexander Hamilton, is that they know how to calculate these principles.

第十九章

CHAPTER XIX

新形式的旧形象：行会社会主义。

THE OLD IMAGE IN A NEW FORM: GUILD SOCIALISM.





1

1

每当以自我为中心的群体之间的争吵变得无法忍受时，过去的改革者们就会发现自己被迫在两个重大选择之间做出选择。他们可以走上通往罗马的道路，将罗马的和平强加给交战的部落。他们可以走上孤立、自治和自给自足的道路。他们几乎总是选择那条他们最近最少走过的道路。如果他们尝试过帝国的单调乏味，他们最珍视的是他们自己社区的简单自由。但是，如果他们看到这种简单的自由被地方主义的嫉妒所浪费，他们就会渴望一个强大国家的广阔秩序。

Whenever the quarrels of self-centered groups become unbearable, reformers in the past found themselves forced to choose between two great alternatives. They could take the path to Rome and impose a Roman peace upon the warring tribes. They could take the path to isolation, to autonomy and self-sufficiency. Almost always they chose that path which they had least recently travelled. If they had tried out the deadening monotony of empire, they cherished above all other things the simple freedom of their own community. But if they had seen this simple freedom squandered in parochial jealousies they longed for the spacious order of a great and powerful state.

无论他们做出何种选择，根本困难都是一样的。如果决策分散，他们很快就会陷入当地意见的混乱之中。如果决策集中，国家的政策就基于首都一小撮社会群体的意见。无论如何，武力都是必要的，以捍卫一个地方权利，对抗另一个地方权利，或对地方实施法律和秩序，或抵抗中央的阶级政府，或保卫整个社会，无论是集中的还是分散的，以抵御外来的野蛮人。

Whichever choice they made, the essential difficulty was the same. If decisions were decentralized they soon floundered in a chaos of local opinions. If they were centralized, the policy of the state was based on the opinions of a small social set at the capital. In any case force was necessary to defend one local right against another, or to impose law and order on the localities, or to resist class government at the center, or to defend the whole society, centralized or decentralized, against the outer barbarian.

现代民主和工业体系都诞生于反对国王、王室政府和详细经济监管制度的时代。在工业领域，这种反应表现为极端权力下放，即所谓的自由放任的个人主义。每项经济决策都由拥有相关财产所有权的人做出。由于几乎所有东西都归某人所有，所以会有人来管理一切。这是复仇的多元主权。

Modern democracy and the industrial system were both born in a time of reaction against kings, crown government, and a regime of detailed economic regulation. In the industrial sphere this reaction took the form of extreme devolution, known as laissez-faire individualism. Each economic decision was to be made by the man who had title to the property involved. Since almost everything was owned by somebody, there would be somebody to manage everything. This was plural sovereignty with a vengeance.

这是由任何人的经济哲学决定的经济政府，尽管它应该受制于政治经济的不可改变的规律，而这些规律最终必将产生和谐。它产生了许多辉煌的事物，但也产生了足够多的肮脏和可怕的事物，从而引发了逆流。其中之一就是托拉斯，它在工业内部建立了一种罗马式的和平，而在工业外部建立了一种罗马式的掠夺性帝国主义。人们转向立法机构寻求救济。他们援引以乡镇农民形象为基础的代议制政府来管理半主权公司。工人阶级转向劳工组织。随后出现了一个日益集中的时期，以及一种军备竞赛。托拉斯相互关联，行业工会联合起来，组成一个劳工运动，随着改革者试图将其力量与大企业抗衡，政治体系在华盛顿变得更加强大，在各州则变得更加弱小。

It was economic government by anybody's economic philosophy, though it was supposed to be controlled by immutable laws of political economy that must in the end produce harmony. It produced many splendid things, but enough sordid and terrible ones to start counter-currents. One of these was the trust, which established a kind of Roman peace within industry, and a Roman predatory imperialism outside. People turned to the legislature for relief. They invoked representative government, founded on the image of the township farmer, to regulate the semi-sovereign corporations. The working class turned to labor organization. There followed a period of increasing centralization and a sort of race of armaments. The trusts interlocked, the craft unions federated and combined into a labor movement, the political system grew stronger at Washington and weaker in the states, as the reformers tried to match its strength against big business.

在这一时期，几乎所有社会主义思想流派，从马克思主义左派到西奥多·罗斯福周围的新民族主义者，都将集中化视为演变的第一阶段，最终将导致政治国家吸收所有半主权商业权力。除了战争期间的几个月外，这种演变从未发生。这已经足够了，并且转向了反对杂食国家，支持几种新形式的多元化。但这一次，社会将回归的不是亚当·斯密的经济人和托马斯·杰斐逊的农民的原子个人主义，而是一种自愿团体的分子个人主义。

In this period practically all the schools of socialist thought from the Marxian left to the New Nationalists around Theodore Roosevelt, looked upon centralization as the first stage of an evolution which would end in the absorption of all the semi-sovereign powers of business by the political state. The evolution never took place, except for a few months during the war. That was enough, and there was a turn of the wheel against the omnivorous state in favor of several new forms of pluralism. But this time society was to swing back not to the atomic individualism of Adam Smith's economic man and Thomas Jefferson's farmer, but to a sort of molecular individualism of voluntary groups.

所有这些理论摇摆不定的有趣之处之一在于，它们都承诺一个没有人为了生存而必须遵循马基雅维利的世界。它们都是通过某种形式的强制手段建立起来的，它们都为了维持自身而实施强制手段，它们都因强制手段而被抛弃。然而，它们并不接受强制手段，无论是物质力量还是特殊地位、赞助或特权，作为其理想的一部分。个人主义者说，自我启蒙的利己主义将带来内部和外部的和平。社会主义者确信侵略动机将会消失。新多元主义者希望它们会消失。除了马基雅维利主义，强制手段在几乎所有社会理论中都是无稽之谈。由于强制手段荒谬、不可言说且难以控制，任何试图使人类生活合理化的人都会受到忽视强制手段的诱惑。

One of the interesting things about all these oscillations of theory is that each in turn promises a world in which no one will have to follow Machiavelli in order to survive. They are all established by some form of coercion, they all exercise coercion in order to maintain themselves, and they are all discarded as a result of coercion. Yet they do not accept coercion, either physical power or special position, patronage, or privilege, as part of their ideal. The individualist said that self-enlightened self-interest would bring internal and external peace. The socialist is sure that the motives to aggression will disappear. The new pluralist hopes they will. Coercion is the surd in almost all social theory, except the Machiavellian. The temptation to ignore it, because it is absurd, inexpressible, and unmanageable, becomes overwhelming in any man who is trying to rationalize human life.





2

2

聪明人有时会不择手段地逃避对武力作用的充分认识，这一点在 GDH Cole 先生的《基尔特社会主义》一书中有所体现。他说，现在的国家“主要是一种强制手段”；在基尔特社会主义社会中，虽然会有一个协调机构，但不会存在主权。他称这个机构为公社。

The lengths to which a clever man will sometimes go in order to escape a full recognition of the role of force is shown by Mr. G. D. H. Cole's book on Guild Socialism. The present state, he says, "is primarily an instrument of coercion;" in a guild socialist society there will be no sovereign power, though there will be a coordinating body. He calls this body the Commune.

然后他开始列举公社的权力，我们记得，公社主要不是强制手段。它解决价格纠纷。有时它确定价格，分配盈余或分摊损失。它分配自然资源，控制信贷发行。它还“分配公共劳动力”。它批准行会和公务员的预算。它征税。“所有收入问题”都属于它的管辖范围。它“分配”收入给社区的非生产成员。它是行会之间所有政策和管辖权问题的最终仲裁者。它通过宪法法律确定职能机构的职能。它任命法官。它赋予行会强制权力，并在涉及强制的地方批准其章程。它宣战和缔结和平。它控制武装部队。它是国家在国外的最高代表。它解决民族国家内部的边界问题。它建立新的职能机构，或将新的职能分配给旧机构。它管理警察。它制定一切必要的法律来规范个人行为和个人财产。

He then begins to enumerate the powers of the Commune, which, we recall, is to be primarily not an instrument of coercion. It settles price disputes. Sometimes it fixes prices, allocates the surplus or distributes the loss. It allocates natural resources, and controls the issue of credit. It also "allocates communal labor-power." It ratifies the budgets of the guilds and the civil services. It levies taxes. "All questions of income" fall within its jurisdiction. It "allocates" income to the non-productive members of the community. It is the final arbiter in all questions of policy and jurisdiction between the guilds. It passes constitutional laws fixing the functions of the functional bodies. It appoints the judges. It confers coercive powers upon the guilds, and ratifies their by-laws wherever these involve coercion. It declares war and makes peace. It controls the armed forces. It is the supreme representative of the nation abroad. It settles boundary questions within the national state. It calls into existence new functional bodies, or distributes new functions to old ones. It runs the police. It makes whatever laws are necessary to regulate personal conduct and personal property.

这些权力不是由一个公社行使的，而是由地方和省级公社组成的联邦结构行使的，最高层是全国公社。当然，科尔先生可以坚持认为这不是一个主权国家，但如果现在任何现代政府都享有强制权力，而他却忘记为之留出空间，我想不出还有什么。

These powers are exercised not by one commune, but by a federal structure of local and provincial communes with a National commune at the top. Mr. Cole is, of course, welcome to insist that this is not a sovereign state, but if there is a coercive power now enjoyed by any modern government for which he has forgotten to make room, I cannot think of it.

然而，他告诉我们，行会社会将是非强制性的：“我们希望建立一个新社会，其精神不是强制，而是免费服务。”因此，与大多数男人和女人一样，所有怀有这种希望的人都会仔细研究行会社会主义计划中的内容，该计划承诺将强制减少到最低限度，尽管今天的行会成员已经为他们的公社保留了最广泛的强制权力。人们立即承认，新社会不能通过普遍同意而建立。科尔先生太诚实了，不会逃避实现过渡所需的武力因素。虽然他显然无法预测可能会发生多少内战，但他很清楚，工会必须采取一段直接行动。

He tells us, however, that Guild society will be non-coercive: "we want to build a new society which will be conceived in the spirit, not of coercion, but of free service." Everyone who shares that hope, as most men and women do, will therefore look closely to see what there is in the Guild Socialist plan which promises to reduce coercion to its lowest limits, even though the Guildsmen of to-day have already reserved for their communes the widest kind of coercive power. It is acknowledged at once that the new society cannot be brought into existence by universal consent. Mr. Cole is too honest to shirk the element of force required to make the transition. And while obviously he cannot predict how much civil war there might be, he is quite clear that there would have to be a period of direct action by the trade unions.





3

3

但是，抛开过渡问题，抛开对未来行动的影响，当人们一路闯进应许之地时，让我们想象一下行会社会的存在。是什么让它作为一个非强制性的社会运行？

But leaving aside the problems of transition, and any consideration of what the effect is on their future action, when men have hacked their way through to the promised land, let us imagine the Guild Society in being. What keeps it running as a non-coercive society?

科尔先生对这个问题有两个答案。一个是正统的马克思主义答案，即废除资本主义财产将消除侵略动机。但他并不真的相信这一点，因为如果他相信，他就不会像普通马克思主义者一样关心工人阶级在掌握政权后如何管理政府。如果他的诊断是正确的，马克思主义者就完全正确了：如果疾病是资本家阶级，而且只是资本家阶级，那么在其灭绝之后，救赎自然就会到​​来。但科尔先生非常关心革命后的社会是由国家集体主义、行会或合作社、民主议会还是职能代表来管理。事实上，行会社会主义作为一种新的代议制政府理论引起了人们的关注。

Mr. Cole has two answers to this question. One is the orthodox Marxian answer that the abolition of capitalist property will remove the motive to aggression. Yet he does not really believe that, because if he did, he would care as little as does the average Marxian how the working class is to run the government, once it is in control. If his diagnosis were correct, the Marxian would be quite right: if the disease were the capitalist class and only the capitalist class, salvation would automatically follow its extinction. But Mr. Cole is enormously concerned about whether the society which follows the revolution is to be run by state collectivism, by guilds or cooperative societies, by a democratic parliament or by functional representation. In fact, it is as a new theory of representative government that guild socialism challenges attention.

行会成员并不指望资本主义财产权的消失会带来奇迹。他们确实期望，当然这是完全正确的，如果收入平等成为常态，社会关系将发生深刻变化。但据我所知，他们在这方面与正统的俄罗斯共产主义者不同：共产主义者提议通过无产阶级专政的力量建立平等，认为一旦人们在收入和服务上都平等了，他们就会失去侵略的动机。行会成员也提议通过武力建立平等，但他们足够精明，看到如果要维持平衡，他们必须提供维持平衡的机构。因此，行会成员相信他们所相信的是一种新的民主理论。

The guildsmen do not expect a miracle to result from the disappearance of capitalist property rights. They do expect, and of course quite rightly, that if equality of income were the rule, social relations would be profoundly altered. But they differ, as far as I can make out, from the orthodox Russian communist in this respect: The communist proposes to establish equality by force of the dictatorship of the proletariat, believing that if once people were equalized both in income and in service, they would then lose the incentives to aggression. The guildsmen also propose to establish equality by force, but are shrewd enough to see that if an equilibrium is to be maintained they have to provide institutions for maintaining it. Guildsmen, therefore, put their faith in what they believe to be a new theory of democracy.

科尔先生说，他们的目标是“使机制正确，并尽可能地调整它以表达人们的社会意愿”。这些意愿需要在“任何形式的社会行动”中通过自治获得自我表达的机会。这些话背后是真正的民主冲动，是提高人类尊严的愿望，以及传统的假设，即除非每个人的意志都参与到影响他的一切事务的管理中，否则这种人类尊严就会受到损害。因此，行会成员和早期的民主人士一样，都在寻找一个可以实现这种自治理想的环境。自卢梭和杰斐逊以来已经过去了一百多年，关注的中心已经从乡村转移到了城市。新民主主义者不能再从理想化的乡村小镇寻找民主的形象。他现在转向了车间。 “联合精神必须在最能体现的领域中得到自由发挥。这显然是工厂，因为人们有一起工作的习惯和传统。工厂是工业民主的自然和基本单位。这不仅意味着工厂必须尽可能自由地管理自己的事务，还意味着工厂的民主单位必须成为行会更大民主的基础，行会管理和政府的较大机构必须主要以工厂代表制原则为基础。”

Their object, says Mr. Cole, is "to get the mechanism right, and to adjust it as far as possible to the expression of men's social wills." These wills need to be given opportunity for self-expression in self-government "in any and every form of social action." Behind these words is the true democratic impulse, the desire to enhance human dignity, as well as the traditional assumption that this human dignity is impugned, unless each person's will enters into the management of everything that affects him. The guildsman, like the earlier democrat therefore, looks about him for an environment in which this ideal of self-government can be realized. A hundred years and more have passed since Rousseau and Jefferson, and the center of interest has shifted from the country to the city. The new democrat can no longer turn to the idealized rural township for the image of democracy. He turns now to the workshop. "The spirit of association must be given free play in the sphere in which it is best able to find expression. This is manifestly the factory, in which men have the habit and tradition of working together. The factory is the natural and fundamental unit of industrial democracy. This involves, not only that the factory must be free, as far as possible, to manage its own affairs, but also that the democratic unit of the factory must be made the basis of the larger democracy of the Guild, and that the larger organs of Guild administration and government must be based largely on the principle of factory representation."

当然，工厂是一个非常宽泛的词，科尔先生要求我们将其理解为矿山、造船厂、码头、车站和每个“自然生产中心”的地方。但从这个意义上讲，工厂与工业完全不同。科尔先生认为，工厂是一个人们真正进行个人接触的工作场所，一个足够小的环境，所有工人都可以直接了解。“如果要实现这种民主，就必须深入工会的每一个成员，并由他们直接行使民主。”这一点很重要，因为科尔先生和杰斐逊一样，都在寻求一个自然的政府单位。唯一自然的单位是一个完全熟悉的环境。现在，一个大型工厂、一个铁路系统、一个大型煤田，都不是这个意义上的自然单位。除非它是一个非常小的工厂，否则科尔先生真正考虑的是车间。在那里，人们可以被认为有“一起工作的习惯和传统”。工厂的其余部分、行业的其余部分都是推断的环境。

Factory is, of course, a very loose word, and Mr. Cole asks us to take it as meaning mines, shipyards, docks, stations, and every place which is "a natural center of production." But a factory in this sense is quite a different thing from an industry. The factory, as Mr. Cole conceives it, is a work place where men are really in personal contact, an environment small enough to be known directly to all the workers. "This democracy if it is to be real, must come home to, and be exercisable directly by, every individual member of the Guild." This is important, because Mr. Cole, like Jefferson, is seeking a natural unit of government. The only natural unit is a perfectly familiar environment. Now a large plant, a railway system, a great coal field, is not a natural unit in this sense. Unless it is a very small factory indeed, what Mr. Cole is really thinking about is the shop. That is where men can be supposed to have "the habit and tradition of working together." The rest of the plant, the rest of the industry, is an inferred environment.





4

4

任何人都可以看到，而且几乎每个人都会承认，纯粹的车间内部事务的自治是“一目了然”的事务管理。但是，关于车间内部事务的构成，会出现争议。显然，最大的利益，如工资、生产标准、采购物资、产品营销、更大的工作规划，绝不是纯粹的内部利益。车间民主有自由，但受到来自外部的巨大限制条件。它可以在一定程度上处理车间的工作安排，它可以处理个人的脾气和性情，它可以执行琐碎的工业正义，并在较大的个人纠纷中充当初审法庭。最重要的是，它可以作为一个单位来处理其他车间，甚至整个工厂。但孤立是不可能的。工业民主的单位完全卷入了外交事务。正是对这些外部关系的管理构成了行会社会主义理论的检验标准。

Anybody can see, and almost everybody will admit, that self-government in the purely internal affairs of the shop is government of affairs that "can be taken in at a single view." But dispute would arise as to what constitute the internal affairs of a shop. Obviously the biggest interests, like wages, standards of production, the purchase of supplies, the marketing of the product, the larger planning of work, are by no means purely internal. The shop democracy has freedom, subject to enormous limiting conditions from the outside. It can deal to a certain extent with the arrangement of work laid out for the shop, it can deal with the temper and temperament of individuals, it can administer petty industrial justice, and act as a court of first instance in somewhat larger individual disputes. Above all it can act as a unit in dealing with other shops, and perhaps with the plant as a whole. But isolation is impossible. The unit of industrial democracy is thoroughly entangled in foreign affairs. And it is the management of these external relations that constitutes the test of the guild socialist theory.

这些工厂必须由代议制政府管理，代议制政府按照联邦的顺序从车间到工厂，从工厂到行业，从行业到国家，中间由地区代表组成。但所有这些结构都源于车间，车间的所有独特优点都归因于车间。科尔先生断言，选择最终“协调”和“管理”车间的代表的代表是由真正的民主选举产生的。由于他们最初来自自治单位，整个联邦机构将受到自治精神和现实的启发。代表们将致力于实现工人“自己理解的实际意愿”，即车间个人所理解的意愿。

They have to be managed by representative government arranged in a federal order from the shop to the plant, the plant to the industry, the industry to the nation, with intervening regional grouping of representatives. But all this structure derives from the shop, and all its peculiar virtues are ascribed to this source. The representatives who choose the representatives who choose the representatives who finally "coordinate" and "regulate" the shops are elected, Mr. Cole asserts, by a true democracy. Because they come originally from a self-governing unit, the whole federal organism will be inspired by the spirit and the reality of self-government. Representatives will aim to carry out the workers' "actual will as understood by themselves," that is, as understood by the individual in the shops.

如果历史可以作为参考，那么一个完全按照这一原则运行的政府要么是永无休止的争论，要么是车间争斗的混乱局面。因为虽然车间工人可以对车间内部的事务有真正的看法，但他对该车间与工厂、行业和国家的关系的“意愿”却受到其他任何以自我为中心的意见所受到的所有限制，包括访问、刻板印象和自身利益。他在车间的经验充其量只能引起他整体的关注。他可以通过直接了解基本事实来获得对车间内部正确的看法。如果他对看不见的复杂环境中正确的看法是从单个车间的经验中概括出来的，那么他很可能是错误的。根据经验，行会代表会发现，就像今天的高级工会官员发现的那样，在他们必须决定的大量问题上，车间并没有“实际的意愿”。

A government run literally on this principle would, if history is any guide, be either a perpetual logroll, or a chaos of warring shops. For while the worker in the shop can have a real opinion about matters entirely within the shop, his "will" about the relation of that shop to the plant, the industry, and the nation is subject to all the limitations of access, stereotype, and self-interest that surround any other self-centered opinion. His experience in the shop at best brings only aspects of the whole to his attention. His opinion of what is right within the shop he can reach by direct knowledge of the essential facts. His opinion of what is right in the great complicated environment out of sight is more likely to be wrong than right if it is a generalization from the experience of the individual shop. As a matter of experience, the representatives of a guild society would find, just as the higher trade union officials find today, that on a great number of questions which they have to decide there is no "actual will as understood" by the shops.





5

5

然而，行会成员坚持认为，这种批评是盲目的，因为它忽略了一个伟大的政治发现。他们会说，你可能完全正确，认为商店的代表必须对商店没有意见的许多问题做出自己的决定。但你只是陷入了一个古老的谬论：你在寻找某个人来代表一群人。他是找不到的。唯一可能的代表是代表“某些特定职能”的人，因此每个人都必须帮助选择尽可能多的代表，“因为要执行的职能不同，基本职能也不同”。

The guildsmen insist, however, that such criticism is blind because it ignores a great political discovery. You may be quite right, they would say, in thinking that the representatives of the shops would have to make up their own minds on many questions about which the shops have no opinion. But you are simply entangled in an ancient fallacy: you are looking for somebody to represent a group of people. He cannot be found. The only representative possible is one who acts for "some particular function," and therefore each person must help choose as many representatives "as there are distinct essential groups of functions to be performed."

那么假设代表们不是代表车间工人发言，而是代表工人感兴趣的某些职能发言。请注意，如果他们不按照小组的意愿执行小组所理解的职能，他们就是不忠诚的。这些职能代表会面。他们的工作是协调和监管。假设车间之间存在意见冲突，那么每个人以什​​么标准来判断对方的提议，因为如果没有意见冲突，就没有必要进行协调和监管？

Assume then that the representatives speak, not for the men in the shops, but for certain functions in which the men are interested. They are, mind you, disloyal if they do not carry out the will of the group about the function, as understood by the group. These functional representatives meet. Their business is to coordinate and regulate. By what standard does each judge the proposals of the other, assuming, as we must, that there is conflict of opinion between the shops, since if there were not, there would be no need to coordinate and regulate?

现在，功能性民主的独特美德被认为是人们根据自己的利益坦诚投票，而人们认为他们从日常经验中知道这一点。他们可以在自给自足的团体内做到这一点。但在对外关系中，整个团体或其代表正在处理超越直接经验的问题。商店不会自发地对整个情况形成看法。因此，商店对其在行业和社会中的权利和义务的公众意见是教育或宣传的问题，而不是商店意识的自动产物。无论行会成员选举代表还是代表，他们都无法摆脱正统民主的问题。无论是整个团体还是当选的发言人，都必须将他的思维拓展到直接经验的范围之外。他必须对来自其他商店的问题以及来自整个行业边界之外的问题进行投票。商店的主要利益甚至不涵盖整个工业行业的职能。职业、大行业、地区、国家的功能是一种概念，而不是一种经验，需要想象、发明、教授和相信。即使你尽可能谨慎地定义功能，一旦你承认每个商店对该功能的看法不一定与其他商店的看法一致，你就是说一个利益集团的代表关心其他利益集团提出的建议。你是说他必须有共同的利益。投票给他，你选择的这个人不仅代表你对你的功能的看法，这是你第一手了解的全部，而且代表你对其他人对该功能的看法的看法。你的投票和正统民主党人一样不确定。

Now the peculiar virtue of functional democracy is supposed to be that men vote candidly according to their own interests, which it is assumed they know by daily experience. They can do that within the self-contained group. But in its external relations the group as a whole, or its representative, is dealing with matters that transcend immediate experience. The shop does not arrive spontaneously at a view of the whole situation. Therefore, the public opinions of a shop about its rights and duties in the industry and in society, are matters of education or propaganda, not the automatic product of shop-consciousness. Whether the guildsmen elect a delegate, or a representative, they do not escape the problem of the orthodox democrat. Either the group as a whole, or the elected spokesman, must stretch his mind beyond the limits of direct experience. He must vote on questions coming up from other shops, and on matters coming from beyond the frontiers of the whole industry. The primary interest of the shop does not even cover the function of a whole industrial vocation. The function of a vocation, a great industry, a district, a nation is a concept, not an experience, and has to be imagined, invented, taught and believed. And even though you define function as carefully as possible, once you admit that the view of each shop on that function will not necessarily coincide with the view of other shops, you are saying that the representative of one interest is concerned in the proposals made by other interests. You are saying that he must conceive a common interest. And in voting for him you are choosing a man who will not simply represent your view of your function, which is all that you know at first hand, but a man who will represent your views about other people's views of that function. You are voting as indefinitely as the orthodox democrat.





6

6

行会成员在自己的头脑中通过玩弄“功能”一词解决了如何构想共同利益的问题。他们想象一个社会，在这个社会中，世界上所有的主要工作都被分析为功能，而这些功能又和谐地综合起来。他们假设整个社会的目的基本一致，每个有组织的团体在实现这些目的方面的作用基本一致。因此，这是一种美好的情感，促使他们从一个天主教封建社会中兴起的机构中取名他们的理论。但他们应该记住，那个时代的智者所假设的功能方案不是由凡人制定的。目前尚不清楚行会成员认为该方案将如何制定并在现代世界中被接受。有时他们似乎认为该方案将从工会组织发展而来，有时他们则认为公社将定义团体的宪法功能。但他们是否相信团体定义自己的功能，在实际中会产生相当大的差异。

The guildsmen in their own minds have solved the question of how to conceive a common interest by playing with the word function. They imagine a society in which all the main work of the world has been analysed into functions, and these functions in turn synthesized harmoniously. They suppose essential agreement about the purposes of society as a whole, and essential agreement about the role of every organized group in carrying out those purposes. It was a nice sentiment, therefore, which led them to take the name of their theory from an institution that arose in a Catholic feudal society. But they should remember that the scheme of function which the wise men of that age assumed was not worked out by mortal man. It is unclear how the guildsmen think the scheme is going to be worked out and made acceptable in the modern world. Sometimes they seem to argue that the scheme will develop from trade union organization, at other times that the communes will define the constitutional function of the groups. But it makes a considerable practical difference whether they believe that the groups define their own functions or not.

无论如何，科尔先生认为，社会可以通过基于“不同的基本功能组”这一公认理念的社会契约来运作。如何识别这些不同的基本功能组？据我所知，科尔先生认为，功能是一群人感兴趣的事情。“功能民主的本质是，一个人应该考虑他感兴趣的功能。”现在，感兴趣这个词至少有两个含义。你可以用它来表示一个人参与其中，或者他的思想被占据。例如，约翰·史密斯可能对斯蒂尔曼离婚案非常感兴趣。他可能读过龙虾版的每一个新闻字。另一方面，年轻的盖伊·斯蒂尔曼的合法性受到威胁，可能根本不会费心。约翰·史密斯对一场不影响他“利益”的诉讼感兴趣，而盖伊对一场决定他整个人生历程的诉讼不感兴趣。恐怕科尔先生更倾向于约翰·史密斯。他正在回答一个“非常愚蠢的反对意见”，即按职能投票就是经常投票：“如果一个人对投票没有足够的兴趣，并且无法激起足够的兴趣来让他对十几个不同的问题进行投票，那么他就放弃了投票权，其结果并不比他盲目和毫无兴趣地投票更不民主。”

In either case, Mr. Cole assumes that society can be carried on by a social contract based on an accepted idea of "distinct essential groups of functions." How does one recognize these distinct essential groups? So far as I can make out, Mr. Cole thinks that a function is what a group of people are interested in. "The essence of functional democracy is that a man should count as many times over as there are functions in which he is interested." Now there are at least two meanings to the word interested. You can use it to mean that a man is involved, or that his mind is occupied. John Smith, for example, may have been tremendously interested in the Stillman divorce case. He may have read every word of the news in every lobster edition. On the other hand, young Guy Stillman, whose legitimacy was at stake, probably did not trouble himself at all. John Smith was interested in a suit that did not affect his "interests," and Guy was uninterested in one that would determine the whole course of his life. Mr. Cole, I am afraid, leans towards John Smith. He is answering the "very foolish objection" that to vote by functions is to be voting very often: "If a man is not interested enough to vote, and cannot be aroused to interest enough to make him vote, on, say, a dozen distinct subjects, he waives his right to vote and the result is no less democratic than if he voted blindly and without interest."

科尔先生认为，未受过教育的选民“放弃了投票权”。由此可见，受过教育的选民的投票表明了他们的利益，他们的利益决定了职能。“因此，布朗、琼斯和罗宾逊必须拥有的不只是一票，而是与他们感兴趣的需要联合行动的问题一样多的不同职能投票。”我非常怀疑科尔先生是否认为布朗、琼斯和罗宾逊应该有资格参加他们声称感兴趣的任何选举，或者是否认为没有透露姓名的其他人选择了他们有权感兴趣的职能。如果有人让我说出我认为科尔先生的想法，我会说他已经通过一个非常奇怪的假设来消除困难，即未受过教育的选民放弃了他的投票权；并得出结论：无论功能性投票是由更高权力安排的，还是“自下而上”安排的，原则是当一个人有兴趣时可以投票，只有受指示的人才会投票，因此该制度才会发挥作用。

Mr. Cole thinks that the uninstructed voter "waives his right to vote." From this it follows that the votes of the instructed reveal their interest, and their interest defines the function. "Brown, Jones, and Robinson must therefore have, not one vote each, but as many different functional votes as there are different questions calling for associative action in which they are interested." I am considerably in doubt whether Mr. Cole thinks that Brown, Jones and Robinson should qualify in any election where they assert that they are interested, or that somebody else, not named, picks the functions in which they are entitled to be interested. If I were asked to say what I believe Mr. Cole thinks, it would be that he has smoothed over the difficulty by the enormously strange assumption that it is the uninstructed voter who waives his right to vote; and has concluded that whether functional voting is arranged by a higher power, or "from below" on the principle that a man may vote when it interests him to vote, only the instructed will be voting anyway, and therefore the institution will work.

但是，有两种没有受过教育的选民。一种人不知道，但知道自己不知道。他通常是一个开明的人。他是放弃投票权的人。但也有一种人没有受过教育，不知道自己受过教育，也不在乎。如果政党机器运转正常，他总是可以被带到投票站。他的选票是机器的基础。而且，由于行会社会的公社对税收、工资、价格、信贷和自然资源拥有巨大的权力，因此，假设选举不会像我们自己的选举一样激烈，那将是荒谬的。

But there are two kinds of uninstructed voter. There is the man who does not know and knows that he does not know. He is generally an enlightened person. He is the man who waives his right to vote. But there is also the man who is uninstructed and does not know that he is, or care. He can always be gotten to the polls, if the party machinery is working. His vote is the basis of the machine. And since the communes of the guild society have large powers over taxation, wages, prices, credit, and natural resources, it would be preposterous to assume that elections will not be fought at least as passionately as our own.

人们展现兴趣的方式不会界定一个功能性社会的功能。还有另外两种定义功能的方式。一种是工会，他们为建立行会社会主义而奋斗。这样的斗争将使一群人团结在一起，形成某种功能性关系，这些群体将成为行会社会主义社会的既得利益者。其中一些人，如矿工和铁路工人，会非常强大，可能深深地执着于他们从与资本主义的斗争中学到的关于他们功能的观点。在社会主义国家下，某些处于有利地位的工会成为凝聚力和政府的中心，这并非不可能。但行会社会不可避免地会发现他们是一个难以处理的问题，因为直接行动会暴露他们的战略力量，至少他们的一些领导人不会轻易地在自由的祭坛上献出这种力量。为了“协调”他们，行会社会必须集中力量，而且我认为，很快人们就会发现，行会社会主义下的激进分子会要求建立足够强大的公社来定义行会的职能。

The way people exhibit their interest will not then delimit the functions of a functional society. There are two other ways that function might be defined. One would be by the trade unions which fought the battle that brought guild socialism into being. Such a struggle would harden groups of men together in some sort of functional relation, and these groups would then become the vested interests of the guild socialist society. Some of them, like the miners and railroad men, would be very strong, and probably deeply attached to the view of their function which they learned from the battle with capitalism. It is not at all unlikely that certain favorably placed trade unions would under a socialist state become the center of coherence and government. But a guild society would inevitably find them a tough problem to deal with, for direct action would have revealed their strategic power, and some of their leaders at least would not offer up this power readily on the altar of freedom. In order to "coordinate" them, guild society would have to gather together its strength, and fairly soon one would find, I think, that the radicals under guild socialism would be asking for communes strong enough to define the functions of the guilds.

但是，如果你要让政府（公社）定义职能，那么该理论的前提就不复存在了。它必须假设职能方案是显而易见的，以便凹形商店自愿与社会建立联系。如果每个选民的头脑中没有固定的职能方案，那么在行会社会主义下，他没有比在正统民主下更好的方法将以自我为中心的观点转化为社会判断。当然，不可能有这样的固定方案，因为即使科尔先生和他的朋友们设计了一个好的方案，所有权力都源于的商店民主也会根据他们所了解的情况和他们所能想象的情况来判断方案的运作情况。行会对同一方案的看法会有所不同。因此，在行会社会主义下，与其他地方一样，试图定义方案应该是什么，而不是方案是维持行会社会团结的骨架，而是政治的主要业务。如果我们可以允许科尔先生制定他的职能方案，我们几乎可以允许他做任何事情。不幸的是，他在他的前提中插入了他希望行会社会推论出的东西。

But if you are going to have the government (commune) define functions, the premise of the theory disappears. It had to suppose that a scheme of functions was obvious in order that the concave shops would voluntarily relate themselves to society. If there is no settled scheme of functions in every voter's head, he has no better way under guild socialism than under orthodox democracy of turning a self-centered opinion into a social judgment. And, of course, there can be no such settled scheme, because, even if Mr. Cole and his friends devised a good one, the shop democracies from which all power derives, would judge the scheme in operation by what they learn of it and by what they can imagine. The guilds would see the same scheme differently. And so instead of the scheme being the skeleton that keeps guild society together, the attempt to define what the scheme ought to be, would be under guild socialism as elsewhere, the main business of politics. If we could allow Mr. Cole his scheme of functions we could allow him almost everything. Unfortunately he has inserted in his premise what he wishes a guild society to deduce.





第二十章

CHAPTER XX

新的形象

A NEW IMAGE





1

1

我认为，这个教训相当明显。由于缺乏制度和教育，公众无法如此成功地报道环境，以至于公众生活的现实与以自我为中心的观点截然相反，公共利益在很大程度上完全逃避了公众舆论，只能由一个专业阶层来管理，而这个阶层的个人利益超越了地方范围。这个阶层是不负责任的，因为它根据不属于公共财产的信息采取行动，在公众无法想象的情况下采取行动，而且只能根据既成事实来追究它的责任。

THE lesson is, I think, a fairly clear one. In the absence of institutions and education by which the environment is so successfully reported that the realities of public life stand out sharply against self-centered opinion, the common interests very largely elude public opinion entirely, and can be managed only by a specialized class whose personal interests reach beyond the locality. This class is irresponsible, for it acts upon information that is not common property, in situations that the public at large does not conceive, and it can be held to account only on the accomplished fact.
