民主理论未能承认以自我为中心的观点不足以实现良好的政府，因此导致理论与实践之间永远存在冲突。根据该理论，人的充分尊严要求他的意志应该如科尔先生所说，在“任何形式的社会行动中”得到表达。人们认为，表达意志是人们强烈的激情，因为他们被认为本能地拥有治理的艺术。但从简单的经验来看，自决只是人类个性的众多利益之一。成为自己命运的主人是一种强烈的愿望，但它必须适应其他同样强烈的愿望，例如对美好生活、和平、减轻负担的愿望。在民主的最初假设中，人们认为每个人意志的表达不仅会自发地满足他对自我表达的渴望，还会满足他对美好生活的渴望，因为在美好生活中表达自我的本能是与生俱来的。

The democratic theory by failing to admit that self-centered opinions are not sufficient to procure good government, is involved in perpetual conflict between theory and practice. According to the theory, the full dignity of man requires that his will should be, as Mr. Cole says, expressed "in any and every form of social action." It is supposed that the expression of their will is the consuming passion of men, for they are assumed to possess by instinct the art of government. But as a matter of plain experience, self-determination is only one of the many interests of a human personality. The desire to be the master of one's own destiny is a strong desire, but it has to adjust itself to other equally strong desires, such as the desire for a good life, for peace, for relief from burdens. In the original assumptions of democracy it was held that the expression of each man's will would spontaneously satisfy not only his desire for self-expression, but his desire for a good life, because the instinct to express one's self in a good life was innate.

因此，重点始终放在表达意愿的机制上。民主的黄金国一直都是某种完美的环境，某种完美的投票和代表制度，每个人天生的善意和本能的政治才能都可以转化为行动。在有限的地区和短暂的时期内，环境是如此有利，也就是说，环境是如此孤立，机会如此丰富，以至于该理论行之有效，足以让人们相信它适用于所有时间和地点。然后，当孤立结束，社会变得复杂，人们不得不紧密地相互适应时，民主主义者花时间试图设计更完美的投票单位，希望他能以某种方式，如科尔先生所说，“使机制正确，并尽可能地适应人们的社会意愿。”但是，当民主理论家忙于此事时，他远离了人性的实际利益。他只关注一种利益：自治。人类对其他各种事物都感兴趣，比如秩序、权利、繁荣、视觉和声音，以及不感到无聊。只要自发民主不能满足他们的其他兴趣，那么在大多数人看来，自发民主在大多数时候都是空洞的。因为成功的自治艺术不是本能的，所以人们不会长期渴望自治本身。他们渴望自治是为了结果。这就是为什么自治的冲动总是作为对恶劣条件的抗议而最强烈的原因。

The emphasis, therefore, has always been on the mechanism for expressing the will. The democratic El Dorado has always been some perfect environment, and some perfect system of voting and representation, where the innate good will and instinctive statesmanship of every man could be translated into action. In limited areas and for brief periods the environment has been so favorable, that is to say so isolated, and so rich in opportunity, that the theory worked well enough to confirm men in thinking that it was sound for all time and everywhere. Then when the isolation ended, and society became complex, and men had to adjust themselves closely to one another, the democrat spent his time trying to devise more perfect units of voting, in the hope that somehow he would, as Mr. Cole says, "get the mechanism right, and adjust it as far as possible to men's social wills." But while the democratic theorist was busy at this, he was far away from the actual interests of human nature. He was absorbed by one interest: self-government. Mankind was interested in all kinds of other things, in order, in its rights, in prosperity, in sights and sounds and in not being bored. In so far as spontaneous democracy does not satisfy their other interests, it seems to most men most of the time to be an empty thing. Because the art of successful self-government is not instinctive, men do not long desire self-government for its own sake. They desire it for the sake of the results. That is why the impulse to self-government is always strongest as a protest against bad conditions.

民主的谬误在于它关注政府的起源，而不是过程和结果。民主主义者一直认为，如果政治权力能够以正确的方式获得，那将是有益的。他的全部注意力都集中在权力的来源上，因为他被这样的信念所催眠：最重要的事情是表达人民的意愿，首先因为表达是人类的最高利益，其次因为意愿本能是善良的。但是，在河流的源头进行任何监管都无法完全控制其行为，而民主主义者一直专注于寻找一种产生社会权力的良好机制，即一种良好的投票和代表机制，他们几乎忽视了人类的其他所有利益。因为无论权力如何产生，关键利益在于权力如何行使。决定文明质量的是权力的使用。而权力的使用无法从源头控制。

The democratic fallacy has been its preoccupation with the origin of government rather than with the processes and results. The democrat has always assumed that if political power could be derived in the right way, it would be beneficent. His whole attention has been on the source of power, since he is hypnotized by the belief that the great thing is to express the will of the people, first because expression is the highest interest of man, and second because the will is instinctively good. But no amount of regulation at the source of a river will completely control its behavior, and while democrats have been absorbed in trying to find a good mechanism for originating social power, that is to say a good mechanism of voting and representation, they neglected almost every other interest of men. For no matter how power originates, the crucial interest is in how power is exercised. What determines the quality of civilization is the use made of power. And that use cannot be controlled at the source.

如果你试图从源头上完全控制政府，你不可避免地会让所有重要决定都变得不可见。因为没有本能会自动做出带来美好生活的政治决定，实际行使权力的人不仅无法表达人民的意愿，因为在大多数问题上不存在意愿，而且他们根据选民看不到的意见行使权力。

If you try to control government wholly at the source, you inevitably make all the vital decisions invisible. For since there is no instinct which automatically makes political decisions that produce a good life, the men who actually exercise power not only fail to express the will of the people, because on most questions no will exists, but they exercise power according to opinions which are hidden from the electorate.

那么，如果你从民主哲学中根除政府是本能的，因此政府可以通过以自我为中心的观点来管理的整个假设及其所有后果，那么民主对人的尊严的信仰又会变成什么样子呢？它通过将自己与整个人格联系起来，而不是与人格的微不足道的方面联系起来，获得了新的生命力。因为传统的民主主义者冒着失去人的尊严的风险，认为人会本能地在明智的法律和良好的政府中表现出这种尊严。选民们没有这样做，所以民主主义者总是被意志坚定的人看作是有点愚蠢的。但是，如果你不把人的尊严挂在关于自治的假设上，而是坚持认为人的尊严需要一种生活水平，在这种水平上，他的能力得到适当的发挥，整个问题就变了。那么，你用来衡量政府的标准是，它是否提供了最低限度的健康、体面的住房、物质必需品、教育、自由、快乐、美，而不仅仅是它是否在牺牲所有这些东西的情况下，与人们头脑中浮现的以自我为中心的观点产生共鸣。在这些标准能够做到准确和客观的程度上，政治决策（这必然是相对较少人关心的问题）实际上与人们的利益有关。

If, then, you root out of the democratic philosophy the whole assumption in all its ramifications that government is instinctive, and that therefore it can be managed by self-centered opinions, what becomes of the democratic faith in the dignity of man? It takes a fresh lease of life by associating itself with the whole personality instead of with a meager aspect of it. For the traditional democrat risked the dignity of man on one very precarious assumption, that he would exhibit that dignity instinctively in wise laws and good government. Voters did not do that, and so the democrat was forever being made to look a little silly by tough-minded men. But if, instead of hanging human dignity on the one assumption about self-government, you insist that man's dignity requires a standard of living, in which his capacities are properly exercised, the whole problem changes. The criteria which you then apply to government are whether it is producing a certain minimum of health, of decent housing, of material necessities, of education, of freedom, of pleasures, of beauty, not simply whether at the sacrifice of all these things, it vibrates to the self-centered opinions that happen to be floating around in men's minds. In the degree to which these criteria can be made exact and objective, political decision, which is inevitably the concern of comparatively few people, is actually brought into relation with the interests of men.

在我们能够想象的任何时候，都不可能出现这样的前景：整个无形环境对所有人都如此清晰，以至于他们会自发地对整个政府事务形成合理的公众意见。即使有这样的前景，我们中是否有很多人愿意为此烦恼，或者愿意花时间对影响我们的“任何形式的社会行动”形成意见，这也是非常值得怀疑的。唯一不切实际的前景是，我们每个人在自己的领域将越来越多地根据无形世界的现实图景采取行动，我们将培养出越来越多擅长保持这些图景现实的人。在我们自己可能关注的相当狭窄的范围之外，社会控制取决于制定生活标准和审计方法，以此来衡量政府官员和工业主管的行为。我们自己无法像神秘的民主人士一直想象的那样，激励或指导所有这些行为。但我们可以通过坚持要求所有行为都应被清楚地记录下来，并客观地衡量其结果，来稳步增加我们对这些行为的实际控制。也许我应该说，我们可以逐步坚持下去。因为制定此类标准和此类审计才刚刚开始。

There is no prospect, in any time which we can conceive, that the whole invisible environment will be so clear to all men that they will spontaneously arrive at sound public opinions on the whole business of government. And even if there were a prospect, it is extremely doubtful whether many of us would wish to be bothered, or would take the time to form an opinion on "any and every form of social action" which affects us. The only prospect which is not visionary is that each of us in his own sphere will act more and more on a realistic picture of the invisible world, and that we shall develop more and more men who are expert in keeping these pictures realistic. Outside the rather narrow range of our own possible attention, social control depends upon devising standards of living and methods of audit by which the acts of public officials and industrial directors are measured. We cannot ourselves inspire or guide all these acts, as the mystical democrat has always imagined. But we can steadily increase our real control over these acts by insisting that all of them shall be plainly recorded, and their results objectively measured. I should say, perhaps, that we can progressively hope to insist. For the working out of such standards and of such audits has only begun.

第七部分：报纸

PART VII: NEWSPAPERS

第二十一章

CHAPTER XXI

购买公众

THE BUYING PUBLIC





1

1

人们必须走出去研究世界才能治理世界，这种观念在政治思想中只占很小一部分。这种观念之所以能被忽略，是因为从亚里士多德时代到民主前提确立的时代，以任何对政府有用的方式报道世界的方法都没有取得太大的进步。

THE idea that men have to go forth and study the world in order to govern it, has played a very minor part in political thought. It could figure very little, because the machinery for reporting the world in any way useful to government made comparatively little progress from the time of Aristotle to the age in which the premises of democracy were established.

因此，如果你问一位民主先驱，人民意志所依据的信息从何而来，他一定会对这个问题感到困惑。这听起来有点像你问他生命或灵魂从何而来。他几乎总是认为，人民意志始终存在；政治科学的职责是制定选票和代议制政府的发明。如果在适当的条件下，如在自给自足的村庄或自给自足的商店中，正确地制定和应用这些发明，这种机制就会以某种方式克服亚里士多德所观察到的注意力的短暂性，以及其范围的狭窄性，这是自给自足社区理论默认的。我们已经看到，即使在这个晚期，行会社会主义者仍然被这样一种观念所吸引：只要你能建立在正确的投票和代表单位上，一个复杂的合作联邦就有可能实现。

Therefore, if you had asked a pioneer democrat where the information was to come from on which the will of the people was to be based, he would have been puzzled by the question. It would have seemed a little as if you had asked him where his life or his soul came from. The will of the people, he almost always assumed, exists at all times; the duty of political science was to work out the inventions of the ballot and representative government. If they were properly worked out and applied under the right conditions, such as exist in the self-contained village or the self-contained shop, the mechanism would somehow overcome the brevity of attention which Aristotle had observed, and the narrowness of its range, which the theory of a self-contained community tacitly acknowledged. We have seen how even at this late date the guild socialists are transfixed by the notion that if only you can build on the right unit of voting and representation, an intricate cooperative commonwealth is possible.

民主党人坚信只要你能找到智慧，他们就一定有智慧，因此他们把公众舆论形成问题视为公民自由问题。“谁知道在自由开放的冲突中真理被贬低了？”假设没有人见过真理被贬低，那么我们是否应该相信真理是由冲突产生的，就像两根木棍摩擦生火一样？美国民主党人在其《权利法案》中体现了这一经典的自由主义学说，事实上，在这种学说背后，存在着几种关于真理起源的不同理论。一种是相信在意见竞争中，最真实的人会获胜，因为真理具有一种特殊的力量。如果让竞争持续足够长的时间，这种说法可能是正确的。当人们以这种方式争论时，他们想到的是历史的裁决，他们特别想到了异教徒在生前受到迫害，死后被奉为圣徒。弥尔顿提出的问题也基于这样一种信念：认识真理的能力是所有人与生俱来的，而自由传播的真理将赢得认可。它同样源于经验，经验表明，如果人们不能说出真理，他们就不可能发现真理，除非在一位不理解真相的警察的眼皮底下。

Convinced that the wisdom was there if only you could find it, democrats have treated the problem of making public opinions as a problem in civil liberties. "Who ever knew Truth put to the worse, in a free and open encounter?" Supposing that no one has ever seen it put to the worse, are we to believe then that the truth is generated by the encounter, like fire by rubbing two sticks? Behind this classic doctrine of liberty, which American democrats embodied in their Bill of Rights, there are, in fact, several different theories of the origin of truth. One is a faith that in the competition of opinions, the truest will win because there is a peculiar strength in the truth. This is probably sound if you allow the competition to extend over a sufficiently long time. When men argue in this vein they have in mind the verdict of history, and they think specifically of heretics persecuted when they lived, canonized after they were dead. Milton's question rests also on a belief that the capacity to recognize truth is inherent in all men, and that truth freely put in circulation will win acceptance. It derives no less from the experience, which has shown that men are not likely to discover truth if they cannot speak it, except under the eye of an uncomprehending policeman.

没有人会高估这些公民自由的实际价值，也没有人会高估维护这些自由的重要性。当这些自由受到威胁时，人类精神也会受到威胁，如果真的到了必须限制这些自由的时候，比如在战争期间，压制思想就会给文明带来危险，如果歇斯底里的人利用这种必要性，把战争的禁忌带入和平时期，文明就可能无法从战争的影响中恢复过来。幸运的是，大多数人都太宽容了，不会长时间地享受职业审判官的待遇，因为在那些不愿被恐吓的人的批评下，他们逐渐被揭露为心胸狭窄的生物，十分之九的时间里他们都不知道自己在说什么。

No one can possibly overestimate the practical value of these civil liberties, nor the importance of maintaining them. When they are in jeopardy, the human spirit is in jeopardy, and should there come a time when they have to be curtailed, as during a war, the suppression of thought is a risk to civilization which might prevent its recovery from the effects of war, if the hysterics, who exploit the necessity, were numerous enough to carry over into peace the taboos of war. Fortunately, the mass of men is too tolerant long to enjoy the professional inquisitors, as gradually, under the criticism of men not willing to be terrorized, they are revealed as mean-spirited creatures who nine-tenths of the time do not know what they are talking about.

但是，尽管公民自由具有根本重要性，但这种意义上的公民自由并不能保证现代世界的舆论。因为它总是假设，要么真理是自发的，要么在没有外部干扰的情况下存在获取真理的手段。但是当你面对一个看不见的环境时，这个假设就是错误的。关于遥远或复杂问题的真相并不是不言而喻的，而收集信息的机制是技术性的和昂贵的。然而，政治学，特别是民主政治学，从来没有充分摆脱亚里士多德政治学的原始假设，重新阐述其前提，以便政治思想能够解决如何让现代国家的公民看到看不见的世界的问题。

But in spite of its fundamental importance, civil liberty in this sense does not guarantee public opinion in the modern world. For it always assumes, either that truth is spontaneous, or that the means of securing truth exist when there is no external interference. But when you are dealing with an invisible environment, the assumption is false. The truth about distant or complex matters is not self-evident, and the machinery for assembling information is technical and expensive. Yet political science, and especially democratic political science, has never freed itself from the original assumption of Aristotle's politics sufficiently to restate the premises, so that political thought might come to grips with the problem of how to make the invisible world visible to the citizens of a modern state.

这种传统根深蒂固，直到最近，例如，我们的大学还在教授政治学，就好像报纸不存在一样。我指的不是新闻学院，因为它们是职业学校，旨在为男性和女性做好职业准备。我指的是面向未来的商人、律师、政府官员和广大公民的政治学。在那门科学中，对新闻界和大众信息来源的研究是没有地位的。这是一个奇怪的事实。对于任何不沉浸于政治学日常兴趣的人来说，几乎无法解释为什么没有一位美国政府学生、美国社会学家写过一本关于新闻采访的书。偶尔会提到新闻界，并声称新闻界不是，或者应该是“自由”和“真实的”。但我几乎找不到其他的。这种对专业人士的蔑视在公众舆论中找到了对应。普遍承认，新闻界是与看不见的环境接触的主要手段。几乎到处都有人认为，报刊应该自发地为我们做原始民主所想象的我们每个人都可以自发地为自己做的事情，即每天两次向我们呈现我们所感兴趣的整个外部世界的真实图景。

So deep is the tradition, that until quite recently, for example, political science was taught in our colleges as if newspapers did not exist. I am not referring to schools of journalism, for they are trade schools, intended to prepare men and women for a career. I am referring to political science as expounded to future business men, lawyers, public officials, and citizens at large. In that science a study of the press and the sources of popular information found no place. It is a curious fact. To anyone not immersed in the routine interests of political science, it is almost inexplicable that no American student of government, no American sociologist, has ever written a book on news-gathering. There are occasional references to the press, and statements that it is not, or that it ought to be, "free" and "truthful." But I can find almost nothing else. And this disdain of the professionals finds its counterpart in public opinions. Universally it is admitted that the press is the chief means of contact with the unseen environment. And practically everywhere it is assumed that the press should do spontaneously for us what primitive democracy imagined each of us could do spontaneously for himself, that every day and twice a day it will present us with a true picture of all the outer world in which we are interested.





2

2

这种坚持而古老的信念——真理不是挣来的，而是灵感的、启示的、无偿提供的——在我们作为报纸读者的经济偏见中表现得非常明显。我们期望报纸向我们提供真理，无论真理是多么无利可图。对于这种困难且往往危险的服务，我们认为它是根本，直到最近，我们仍期望支付铸币厂铸造的最小硬币。现在，我们已经习惯了在工作日支付两分甚至三分钱，而在星期天，为了一本插图百科全书和附带的杂耍娱乐节目，我们甚至不得不支付五分钱甚至一角钱。没有人会想一想他应该为他的报纸付钱。他期望真理的泉源会沸腾，但他不会签订任何涉及任何风险、成本或麻烦的法律或道德合同。他会在适合他的时候支付象征性的价格，在适合他的时候停止支付，在适合他的时候转向另一份报纸。有人说得非常对，报纸编辑每天都要重新选举。

This insistent and ancient belief that truth is not earned, but inspired, revealed, supplied gratis, comes out very plainly in our economic prejudices as readers of newspapers. We expect the newspaper to serve us with truth however unprofitable the truth may be. For this difficult and often dangerous service, which we recognize as fundamental, we expected to pay until recently the smallest coin turned out by the mint. We have accustomed ourselves now to paying two and even three cents on weekdays, and on Sundays, for an illustrated encyclopedia and vaudeville entertainment attached, we have screwed ourselves up to paying a nickel or even a dime. Nobody thinks for a moment that he ought to pay for his newspaper. He expects the fountains of truth to bubble, but he enters into no contract, legal or moral, involving any risk, cost or trouble to himself. He will pay a nominal price when it suits him, will stop paying whenever it suits him, will turn to another paper when that suits him. Somebody has said quite aptly that the newspaper editor has to be re-elected every day.

读者与报刊之间这种随意、片面的关系是我们文明的异常现象。没有其他事物能与之相比，因此很难将报刊与任何其他行业或机构进行比较。报刊并非纯粹的行业，部分原因是产品经常以低于成本的价格出售，但主要原因是社会对报刊采用一种道德标准，对贸易或制造业采用另一种道德标准。从道德上讲，报纸就像教堂或学校一样被评判。但如果你试图将报纸与教堂或学校进行比较，你就失败了；纳税人支付公立学校的费用，私立学校由学费资助，教堂则有补贴和募捐。你不能将新闻业与法律、医学或工程进行比较，因为在这些职业中，消费者都要为服务付费。如果以读者的态度来判断，自由媒体意味着报纸实际上是免费的。

This casual and one-sided relationship between readers and press is an anomaly of our civilization. There is nothing else quite like it, and it is, therefore, hard to compare the press with any other business or institution. It is not a business pure and simple, partly because the product is regularly sold below cost, but chiefly because the community applies one ethical measure to the press and another to trade or manufacture. Ethically a newspaper is judged as if it were a church or a school. But if you try to compare it with these you fail; the taxpayer pays for the public school, the private school is endowed or supported by tuition fees, there are subsidies and collections for the church. You cannot compare journalism with law, medicine or engineering, for in every one of these professions the consumer pays for the service. A free press, if you judge by the attitude of the readers, means newspapers that are virtually given away.

然而，批评报刊的人只是在表达社会的道德标准，而他们却希望这样的机构能够与学校、教堂和无私的职业处于同一水平。这再次说明了民主的凹面性。人们认为不需要人工获取信息。信息必须自然而然地出现，也就是说，免费，如果不是出自公民的内心，那么就是免费来自报纸。公民会为他的电话、他的火车票、他的汽车、他的娱乐付费。但他不会公开为他的新闻付费。

Yet the critics of the press are merely voicing the moral standards of the community, when they expect such an institution to live on the same plane as that on which the school, the church, and the disinterested professions are supposed to live. This illustrates again the concave character of democracy. No need for artificially acquired information is felt to exist. The information must come naturally, that is to say gratis, if not out of the heart of the citizen, then gratis out of the newspaper. The citizen will pay for his telephone, his railroad rides, his motor car, his entertainment. But he does not pay openly for his news.

然而，他会为让别人读到他的文章而付出高昂的代价。他会直接付钱做广告。他也会间接为别人的广告付费，因为这种付费隐藏在商品价格中，是他无法有效理解的隐形环境的一部分。公开支付一杯好冰淇淋的价格来购买全世界的新闻，会被视为一种侮辱，尽管公众在购买广告商品时会支付这么多甚至更多的费用。公众为媒体付费，但只有在付费是隐蔽的情况下。

He will, however, pay handsomely for the privilege of having someone read about him. He will pay directly to advertise. And he will pay indirectly for the advertisements of other people, because that payment, being concealed in the price of commodities is part of an invisible environment that he does not effectively comprehend. It would be regarded as an outrage to have to pay openly the price of a good ice cream soda for all the news of the world, though the public will pay that and more when it buys the advertised commodities. The public pays for the press, but only when the payment is concealed.





3

3

因此，发行量是达到目的的手段。只有当它能够卖给广告商时，它才成为一种资产，广告商通过间接向读者征税获得收入来购买它。广告商购买的发行量取决于他要卖什么。可能是“优质”的，也可能是“大众”的。总的来说，没有明显的分界线，因为对于大多数通过广告销售的商品而言，客户既不是极富的少数人，也不是极穷的人。他们是那些在基本生活必需品之外有足够的剩余，可以自行决定购买的人。因此，进入相当富裕家庭的报纸大体上是广告商最看好的。它也可能进入穷人家庭，但除了某些商品外，分析广告代理不会将这种发行量视为一项巨大的资产，除非像赫斯特先生的某些财产的情况那样，发行量巨大。

Circulation is, therefore, the means to an end. It becomes an asset only when it can be sold to the advertiser, who buys it with revenues secured through indirect taxation of the reader. The kind of circulation which the advertiser will buy depends on what he has to sell. It may be "quality" or "mass." On the whole there is no sharp dividing line, for in respect to most commodities sold by advertising, the customers are neither the small class of the very rich nor the very poor. They are the people with enough surplus over bare necessities to exercise discretion in their buying. The paper, therefore, which goes into the homes of the fairly prosperous is by and large the one which offers most to the advertiser. It may also go into the homes of the poor, but except for certain lines of goods, an analytical advertising agent does not rate that circulation as a great asset, unless, as seems to be the case with certain of Mr. Hearst's properties, the circulation is enormous.

如果报纸激怒了那些最希望通过广告接触到的读者，那么对于广告商来说，它就是一种糟糕的媒介。而且，由于没有人声称广告是慈善行为，广告商购买的刊物空间肯定会接触到他们的未来客户。人们不必花太多时间担心干货商未报道的丑闻。这些丑闻并不代表什么重大问题，而且这类事件并不像许多新闻批评家所认为的那样常见。真正的问题是，报纸的读者不习惯支付新闻采访的费用，他们只有将新闻转化为可以卖给制造商和商人的流通品才能从中获利。而最需要从中获利的是那些有最多钱可以花的人。这样的报业必然会尊重购买公众的观点。报纸就是为购买公众编辑和出版的，因为没有这种支持，报纸就无法生存。报纸可以藐视广告商，可以攻击强大的银行或牵引利益，但如果它疏远了购买公众，它就会失去其存在不可或缺的资产。

A newspaper which angers those whom it pays best to reach through advertisements is a bad medium for an advertiser. And since no one ever claimed that advertising was philanthropy, advertisers buy space in those publications which are fairly certain to reach their future customers. One need not spend much time worrying about the unreported scandals of the dry-goods merchants. They represent nothing really significant, and incidents of this sort are less common than many critics of the press suppose. The real problem is that the readers of a newspaper, unaccustomed to paying the cost of newsgathering, can be capitalized only by turning them into circulation that can be sold to manufacturers and merchants. And those whom it is most important to capitalize are those who have the most money to spend. Such a press is bound to respect the point of view of the buying public. It is for this buying public that newspapers are edited and published, for without that support the newspaper cannot live. A newspaper can flout an advertiser, it can attack a powerful banking or traction interest, but if it alienates the buying public, it loses the one indispensable asset of its existence.

前《纽约太阳晚报》记者约翰·L·吉文先生于 1914 年表示，在美国出版的 2300 多家日报中，约有 175 家在人口超过十万的城市出版。这些报纸构成了“综合新闻”的报刊。它们是收集重大事件新闻的主要报纸，甚至那些不读这 175 家报纸的人最终也依靠它们来了解外部世界的消息。因为它们组成了大型新闻协会，在新闻交流方面进行合作。因此，每个报刊不仅是自己读者的消息来源，也是其他城市报纸的本地记者。农村报刊和专业报刊大体上从这些主要报纸获取综合新闻。其中有些报纸比其他报纸丰富得多，因此，对于国际新闻，全国的整个报刊主要依靠新闻协会的报道和一些大都市日报的特别服务。

Mr. John L. Given, formerly of the New York Evening Sun, stated in 1914 that out of over two thousand three hundred dailies published in the United States, there were about one hundred and seventy-five printed in cities having over one hundred thousand inhabitants. These constitute the press for "general news." They are the key papers which collect the news dealing with great events, and even the people who do not read any one of the one hundred and seventy-five depend ultimately upon them for news of the outer world. For they make up the great press associations which cooperate in the exchange of news. Each is, therefore, not only the informant of its own readers, but it is the local reporter for the newspapers of other cities. The rural press and the special press by and large, take their general news from these key papers. And among these there are some very much richer than others, so that for international news, in the main, the whole press of the nation may depend upon the reports of the press associations and the special services of a few metropolitan dailies.

粗略地说，一般新闻采集的经济支撑来自十万以上人口的城市中较为富裕的地区为广告商品支付的价格。这些购买者由家庭成员组成，他们的收入主要来自贸易、商品销售、制造业指导和金融。他们是报纸广告最有利的客户群。他们拥有集中的购买力，其购买力可能比农民和工人的总购买力要小；但在日报覆盖的范围内，他们是最快速的资产。

Roughly speaking, the economic support for general news gathering is in the price paid for advertised goods by the fairly prosperous sections of cities with more than one hundred thousand inhabitants. These buying publics are composed of the members of families, who depend for their income chiefly on trade, merchandising, the direction of manufacture, and finance. They are the clientele among whom it pays best to advertise in a newspaper. They wield a concentrated purchasing power, which may be less in volume than the aggregate for farmers and workingmen; but within the radius covered by a daily newspaper they are the quickest assets.





4

4

此外，他们还有双重关注。他们不仅是广告商的最佳客户，他们本身也包括广告商。因此，报纸给公众留下的印象至关重要。幸运的是，公众意见并不统一。他们可能是“资本主义的”，但对资本主义是什么以及如何运作资本主义有不同的看法。除了在危险时期，这种可敬的观点存在足够的分歧，导致政策存在相当大的分歧。如果不是出版商本身通常都是这些城市社区的成员，并诚实地通过同事和朋友的视角看待世界，这些分歧会更大。

They have, moreover, a double claim to attention. They are not only the best customers for the advertiser, they include the advertisers. Therefore the impression made by the newspapers on this public matters deeply. Fortunately this public is not unanimous. It may be "capitalistic" but it contains divergent views on what capitalism is, and how it is to be run. Except in times of danger, this respectable opinion is sufficiently divided to permit of considerable differences of policy. These would be greater still if it were not that publishers are themselves usually members of these urban communities, and honestly see the world through the lenses of their associates and friends.

他们从事投机性业务，这种业务取决于总体贸易状况，更特别的是，这种业务的发行量不是基于与读者的婚姻契约，而是基于自由恋爱。因此，每个出版商的目标都是将自己的发行量从一群随意购买报摊商品的杂乱无章的买家转变为一群忠实的固定读者。考虑到现代新闻业的经济状况，一份真正能够依靠读者忠诚度的报纸是最独立的报纸。一群不离不弃的读者的力量比任何单个广告商所能拥有的力量都要强大，这种力量足以瓦解广告商联盟。因此，每当你发现一份报纸为了广告商而背叛读者时，你都可以相当肯定，要么出版商真诚地赞同广告商的观点，要么他认为，也许错误地认为，如果他公开抵制命令，就不能指望读者的支持。问题在于，读者不会为新闻支付现金，但会不会以忠诚度付费。

They are engaged in a speculative business, which depends on the general condition of trade, and more peculiarly on a circulation based not on a marriage contract with their readers, but on free love. The object of every publisher is, therefore, to turn his circulation from a medley of catch-as-catch-can news stand buyers into a devoted band of constant readers. A newspaper that can really depend upon the loyalty of its readers is as independent as a newspaper can be, given the economics of modern journalism. A body of readers who stay by it through thick and thin is a power greater than any which the individual advertiser can wield, and a power great enough to break up a combination of advertisers. Therefore, whenever you find a newspaper betraying its readers for the sake of an advertiser, you can be fairly certain either that the publisher sincerely shares the views of the advertiser, or that he thinks, perhaps mistakenly, he cannot count upon the support of his readers if he openly resists dictation. It is a question of whether the readers, who do not pay in cash for their news, will pay for it in loyalty.

第二十二章

CHAPTER XXII

忠实读者

THE CONSTANT READER





1

1

任何契约都不会规定购买者对报纸的忠诚度。在几乎所有其他企业中，期望获得服务的人都会签订协议来控制他一时兴起的想法。至少他会为所获得的东西付钱。在期刊出版中，最接近确定时间协议的方式是付费订阅，而我认为这并不是大都市日报经济的一个重要因素。读者是他忠诚度的唯一和日常评判者，不能以违反承诺或不提供支持为由起诉他。

THE loyalty of the buying public to a newspaper is not stipulated in any bond. In almost every other enterprise the person who expects to be served enters into an agreement that controls his passing whims. At least he pays for what he obtains. In the publishing of periodicals the nearest approach to an agreement for a definite time is the paid subscription, and that is not, I believe, a great factor in the economy of a metropolitan daily. The reader is the sole and the daily judge of his loyalty, and there can be no suit against him for breach of promise or nonsupport.

虽然一切都取决于读者的恒心，但甚至没有一个模糊的传统来提醒读者这一事实。读者的恒心取决于他当时的感觉或习惯。而这些不仅取决于新闻的质量，而且更经常取决于一些模糊的因素，在我们与新闻界的随意关系中，我们几乎不费吹灰之力去意识到这些因素。其中最重要的是，我们每个人都倾向于通过报纸对我们认为自己参与的那部分新闻的处理来判断报纸，如果我们要判断的话。报纸涉及大量我们经验之外的事件。但它也涉及一些我们经验范围内的事件。我们最常通过它对这些事件的处理来决定喜欢它还是不喜欢它，信任它还是拒绝在家里拥有这份报纸。如果报纸对我们认为我们知道的事情，我们的业务、我们的教堂、我们的政党，给出了令人满意的报道，那么它几乎肯定不会受到我们的猛烈批评。除了报纸版本与早餐桌上的人自己的观点相符之外，还有什么更好的标准呢？因此，大多数人倾向于以他们自己的身份，而不是普通读者的身份，而是以他们自己经历的问题的特殊辩护人的身份，要求报纸承担最严格的责任。

Though everything turns on the constancy of the reader, there does not exist even a vague tradition to call that fact to the reader's mind. His constancy depends on how he happens to feel, or on his habits. And these depend not simply on the quality of the news, but more often on a number of obscure elements that in our casual relation to the press, we hardly take the trouble to make conscious. The most important of these is that each of us tends to judge a newspaper, if we judge it at all, by its treatment of that part of the news in which we feel ourselves involved. The newspaper deals with a multitude of events beyond our experience. But it deals also with some events within our experience. And by its handling of those events we most frequently decide to like it or dislike it, to trust it or refuse to have the sheet in the house. If the newspaper gives a satisfactory account of that which we think we know, our business, our church, our party, it is fairly certain to be immune from violent criticism by us. What better criterion does the man at the breakfast table possess than that the newspaper version checks up with his own opinion? Therefore, most men tend to hold the newspaper most strictly accountable in their capacity, not of general readers, but of special pleaders on matters of their own experience.

除了利益相关方，很少有人能够检验报道的准确性。如果是本地新闻，而且有竞争，编辑知道他可能会听到那些认为他的报道不公平和不准确的人的消息。但如果是非本地新闻，随着主题逐渐淡出，纠正力度就会减弱。唯一能够纠正他们认为是另一个城市刊登的虚假报道的人是那些组织良好、雇佣宣传人员的团体的成员。

Rarely is anyone but the interested party able to test the accuracy of a report. If the news is local, and if there is competition, the editor knows that he will probably hear from the man who thinks his portrait unfair and inaccurate. But if the news is not local, the corrective diminishes as the subject matter recedes into the distance. The only people who can correct what they think is a false picture of themselves printed in another city are members of groups well enough organized to hire publicity men.

现在，值得注意的是，如果报纸的一般读者认为自己被新闻误导，则在法律上没有立足之地。只有受害方才能以诽谤或诽谤罪起诉，并且他必须证明自己受到了实质性伤害。法律体现了这样的传统，即一般新闻不是公众关注的问题，除非是被模糊地描述为不道德或煽动性的内容。

Now it is interesting to note that the general reader of a newspaper has no standing in law if he thinks he is being misled by the news. It is only the aggrieved party who can sue for slander or libel, and he has to prove a material injury to himself. The law embodies the tradition that general news is not a matter of common concern, except as to matter which is vaguely described as immoral or seditious.

但是，尽管新闻主体整体上不受无私读者的审查，但其中的内容却包含一些读者有非常明确的先入之见的内容。这些内容是读者判断的数据，而人们在阅读新闻时，如果没有这种个人标准，他们会根据准确性标准以外的其他标准来判断。他们在这里处理的主题对他们来说与虚构难以区分。真理的准则无法适用。如果新闻符合他们的刻板印象，他们不会对它感到困惑，如果他们感兴趣，他们会继续阅读。

But the body of the news, though unchecked as a whole by the disinterested reader, consists of items about which some readers have very definite preconceptions. Those items are the data of his judgment, and news which men read without this personal criterion, they judge by some other standard than their standard of accuracy. They are dealing here with a subject matter which to them is indistinguishable from fiction. The canon of truth cannot be applied. They do not boggle over such news if it conforms to their stereotypes, and they continue to read it if it interests them.





2

2

甚至在大城市，有些报纸的编辑原则是读者希望阅读有关他们自己的信息。这种理论认为，如果足够多的人经常在报纸上看到自己的名字，可以阅读有关他们的婚礼、葬礼、社交活动、国外旅行、分会会议、学校奖项、他们的五十岁生日、六十岁生日、银婚、郊游和蛤蜊聚会的信息，那么这些报纸的发行量就会稳定。

There are newspapers, even in large cities, edited on the principle that the readers wish to read about themselves. The theory is that if enough people see their own names in the paper often enough, can read about their weddings, funerals, sociables, foreign travels, lodge meetings, school prizes, their fiftieth birthdays, their sixtieth birthdays, their silver weddings, their outings and clambakes, they will make a reliable circulation.

这种报纸的经典公式包含在 1860 年 4 月 3 日，贺拉斯·格里利 (Horace Greeley) 写给“朋友弗莱彻”的一封信中，当时弗莱彻正准备创办一份乡村报纸：

The classic formula for such a newspaper is contained in a letter written by Horace Greeley on April 3, 1860, to "Friend Fletcher" who was about to start a country newspaper:

“I. 首先要明确一个概念，即普通人最感兴趣的对象是自己；其次才是邻居。亚洲和通戈群岛在他眼中远远落后于这些……不要让新教堂的建立、现有教堂的扩充、农场的出售、新房子的建造、磨坊的开张、商店的开张，或任何引起十几个家庭兴趣的事情发生，而没有在专栏中及时、简短地记录这些事实。如果一个农民砍伐了一棵大树，或者种出了一种巨大的甜菜，或者收获了丰收的小麦或玉米，请尽可能简洁、毫无例外地陈述这些事实。”

"I. Begin with a clear conception that the subject of deepest interest to an average human being is himself; next to that he is most concerned about his neighbors. Asia and the Tongo Islands stand a long way after these in his regard…. Do not let a new church be organized, or new members be added to one already existing, a farm be sold, a new house raised, a mill set in motion, a store opened, nor anything of interest to a dozen families occur, without having the fact duly, though briefly, chronicled in your columns. If a farmer cuts a big tree, or grows a mammoth beet, or harvests a bounteous yield of wheat or corn, set forth the fact as concisely and unexceptionally as possible."

正如李先生所说，成为“家乡的印刷日记”这一功能是每一份报纸无论在哪里出版都必须在一定程度上履行的。而在纽约这样的大城市，通过广播发行的一般报纸无法满足这一功能，因此存在着按照格里利模式为城市各部分出版的小报纸。在曼哈顿和布朗克斯区，地方日报的数量可能是一般报纸的两倍。此外，还有各种针对行业、宗教和民族的特别出版物作为补充。

The function of becoming, as Mr. Lee puts it, "the printed diary of the home town" is one that every newspaper no matter where it is published must in some measure fill. And where, as in a great city like New York, the general newspapers circulated broadcast cannot fill it, there exist small newspapers published on Greeley's pattern for sections of the city. In the boroughs of Manhattan and the Bronx there are perhaps twice as many local dailies as there are general newspapers. And they are supplemented by all kinds of special publications for trades, religions, nationalities.

这些日记是为那些认为自己的生活有趣的人出版的。但也有许多人觉得自己的生活很枯燥，他们希望像海达·高布勒一样，过上更刺激的生活。为他们出版了几份完整的报纸和其他报纸的部分版面，专门介绍一群虚构人物的个人生活，读者可以在自己的想象中安全地认同他们华丽的恶习。赫斯特先生对上流社会的不懈兴趣迎合了那些从不希望进入上流社会的人，但他们却能从模糊的感觉中获得一些提升，即他们是他们所读到的生活的一部分。在大城市里，“家乡印刷的日记”往往是一群上流人士印刷的日记。

These diaries are published for people who find their own lives interesting. But there are also great numbers of people who find their own lives dull, and wish, like Hedda Gabler, to live a more thrilling life. For them there are published a few whole newspapers, and sections of others, devoted to the personal lives of a set of imaginary people, with whose gorgeous vices the reader can in his fancy safely identify himself. Mr. Hearst's unflagging interest in high society caters to people who never hope to be in high society, and yet manage to derive some enhancement out of the vague feeling that they are part of the life that they read about. In the great cities "the printed diary of the home town" tends to be the printed diary of a smart set.

正如我们已经指出的，城市日报承担着向普通公民提供远方新闻的重任。但主要不是政治和社会新闻在维持发行量。人们对政治和社会新闻的兴趣是断断续续的，很少有出版商能仅依靠政治和社会新闻。因此，报纸还拥有各种其他功能，所有这些功能主要是为了吸引读者，而读者对于重大新闻没有能力进行批评。此外，在重大新闻方面，任何一个社区的竞争都不是很激烈。新闻服务将主要事件标准化；只有偶尔才会有重大新闻；显然，如此大规模的报道并没有太多的读者，而近年来，《纽约时报》对各种观点的人来说都是必不可少的。为了使自己与众不同并吸引稳定的读者群，大多数报纸必须走出一般新闻领域。他们深入社会各个层面，关注丑闻和犯罪，关注体育、图片、女演员、给失恋者的建议、高中笔记、女性页面、买家页面、烹饪收据、国际象棋、惠斯特、园艺、漫画、激烈的党派之争，这并不是因为出版商和编辑对新闻以外的一切感兴趣，而是因为他们必须找到某种方式来留住那些所谓充满热情的读者，一些新闻批评家认为这些读者只要求真相，不要求别的。

And it is, as we have already noted, the dailies of the cities which carry the burden of bringing distant news to the private citizen. But it is not primarily their political and social news which holds the circulation. The interest in that is intermittent, and few publishers can bank on it alone. The newspaper, therefore, takes to itself a variety of other features, all primarily designed to hold a body of readers together, who so far as big news is concerned, are not able to be critical. Moreover, in big news the competition in any one community is not very serious. The press services standardize the main events; it is only once in a while that a great scoop is made; there is apparently not a very great reading public for such massive reporting as has made the New York Times of recent years indispensable to men of all shades of opinion. In order to differentiate themselves and collect a steady public most papers have to go outside the field of general news. They go to the dazzling levels of society, to scandal and crime, to sports, pictures, actresses, advice to the lovelorn, highschool notes, women's pages, buyer's pages, cooking receipts, chess, whist, gardening, comic strips, thundering partisanship, not because publishers and editors are interested in everything but news, but because they have to find some way of holding on to that alleged host of passionately interested readers, who are supposed by some critics of the press to be clamoring for the truth and nothing but the truth.

报纸编辑处于一个奇怪的位置。他的事业依赖于广告商向读者征收的间接税；广告商的赞助取决于编辑将有效客户群体聚集在一起的技巧。这些客户根据他们的私人经验和刻板的期望做出判断，因为本质上他们对所读的大多数新闻没有独立的了解。如果判断不是不利的，编辑至少在支付范围内。但为了确保发行量，他不能完全依赖大环境的新闻。当然，他会尽可能有趣地处理这些新闻，但一般新闻的质量，尤其是关于公共事务的新闻，本身不足以让大量读者在日报之间做出区分。

The newspaper editor occupies a strange position. His enterprises depend upon indirect taxation levied by his advertisers upon his readers; the patronage of the advertisers depends upon the editor's skill in holding together an effective group of customers. These customers deliver judgment according to their private experiences and their stereotyped expectations, for in the nature of things they have no independent knowledge of most news they read. If the judgment is not unfavorable, the editor is at least within range of a circulation that pays. But in order to secure that circulation, he cannot rely wholly upon news of the greater environment. He handles that as interestingly as he can, of course, but the quality of the general news, especially about public affairs, is not in itself sufficient to cause very large numbers of readers to discriminate among the dailies.

报纸与公共信息之间这种有点不协调的关系反映在新闻工作者的薪水上。从理论上讲，报道是整个机构的基础，但却是报纸工作中薪水最低、最不受重视的部门。总的来说，有能力的人只是出于需要或为了积累经验而进入这个行业，并且明确希望尽快毕业。因为直截了当的报道并不是一个能带来很多回报的职业。新闻业的回报属于专业工作、具有编辑质量的署名信函、主管以及具有自己天赋和品味的人。毫无疑问，这是由于经济学家所说的能力租金。但这一经济原则在新闻业中发挥着如此特殊的暴力作用，以至于新闻采访本身并不能吸引到与其公共重要性似乎要求的大量训练有素、能力出众的人。我认为，有能力的人从事“直言不讳”的工作，目的是尽快离开，这是该行业从未充分发展那些赋予该职业声望和嫉妒自尊的企业传统的主要原因。因为正是这些企业传统产生了手艺自豪感，往往会提高入职标准，惩罚违反守则的行为，并给予人们力量来坚持自己的社会地位。

This somewhat left-handed relationship between newspapers and public information is reflected in the salaries of newspaper men. Reporting, which theoretically constitutes the foundation of the whole institution, is the most poorly paid branch of newspaper work, and is the least regarded. By and large, able men go into it only by necessity or for experience, and with the definite intention of being graduated as soon as possible. For straight reporting is not a career that offers many great rewards. The rewards in journalism go to specialty work, to signed correspondence which has editorial quality, to executives, and to men with a knack and flavor of their own. This is due, no doubt, to what economists call the rent of ability. But this economic principle operates with such peculiar violence in journalism that newsgathering does not attract to itself anything like the number of trained and able men which its public importance would seem to demand. The fact that the able men take up "straight reporting" with the intention of leaving it as soon as possible is, I think, the chief reason why it has never developed in sufficient measure those corporate traditions that give to a profession prestige and a jealous self-respect. For it is these corporate traditions which engender the pride of craft, which tend to raise the standards of admission, punish breaches of the code, and give men the strength to insist upon their status in society.





3

3

然而，所有这些都没有触及问题的根源。因为，尽管新闻业的经济学会降低新闻报道的价值，但我确信，这是一种错误的决定论，它会在这一点上放弃分析。记者的内在力量似乎如此强大，通过报道获得成功的非常有能力的人的数量如此之多，因此，相对而言，很少有人认真努力将这一职业提升到医学、工程或法律的水平，这其中一定有更深层次的原因。

Yet all this does not go to the root of the matter. For while the economics of journalism is such as to depress the value of news reporting, it is, I am certain, a false determinism which would abandon the analysis at that point. The intrinsic power of the reporter appears to be so great, the number of very able men who pass through reporting is so large, that there must be some deeper reason why, comparatively speaking, so little serious effort has gone into raising the vocation to the level say of medicine, engineering, or law.

厄普顿·辛克莱先生代表了美国大部分民众的意见，他声称，在他所谓的“黄铜支票”中，他发现了这个更深层次的原因：

Mr. Upton Sinclair speaks for a large body of opinion in America, when he claims that in what he calls "The Brass Check" he has found this deeper reason:

“你们每周的薪水信封里都会有一张铜支票——你们负责撰写、印刷和分发我们的报纸和杂志。这张铜支票是你们的耻辱的代价——你们将美丽的真理带到市场上出售，将人类纯洁的希望出卖给大企业的可憎妓院。”

"The Brass Check is found in your pay envelope every week—you who write and print and distribute our newspapers and magazines. The Brass check is the price of your shame—you who take the fair body of truth and sell it in the market place, who betray the virgin hopes of mankind into the loathsome brothel of Big Business."

由此看来，存在着大量已知的事实和一系列有根据的希望，而这些事实和希望却被富有的报业巨头们或多或少有意识的阴谋所滥用。如果这一理论是正确的，那么就会得出一个结论。那就是，在与大企业没有任何关系的媒体中，公正的事实是不可侵犯的。因为如果一家不受大企业控制甚至与大企业不友好的媒体以某种方式未能包含公正的事实，那么辛克莱先生的理论就存在问题。

It would seem from this that there exists a body of known truth, and a set of well founded hopes, which are prostituted by a more or less conscious conspiracy of the rich owners of newspapers. If this theory is correct, then a certain conclusion follows. It is that the fair body of truth would be inviolate in a press not in any way connected with Big Business. For if it should happen that a press not controlled by, and not even friendly with, Big Business somehow failed to contain the fair body of truth, something would be wrong with Mr. Sinclair's theory.

确实有这样的报刊。说来奇怪，辛克莱先生在提出补救措施时，并没有建议读者订阅最近的激进报纸。为什么不呢？如果美国新闻业的麻烦可以追溯到大企业的“金支票”，那么为什么补救措施不在于阅读那些根本不接受“金支票”的报纸呢？为什么要资助一家拥有“各种信仰或事业”的大型董事会的“全国新闻”，来印刷一份充满事实的报纸，“不管受到什么损害，钢铁托拉斯、世界产业工人联盟、标准石油公司或社会主义党？”如果麻烦来自大企业，即钢铁托拉斯、标准石油公司等，为什么不敦促每个人都阅读世界产业工人联盟或社会主义报纸呢？辛克莱先生没有说为什么不。但原因很简单。他无法说服任何人，甚至他自己，反资本主义报刊是资本主义报刊的补救措施。他在“金支票”理论和建设性建议中都忽视了反资本主义报刊。但是，如果你在诊断美国新闻业，你就不能忽视它。如果你关心的是“公正的事实”，你就不会犯下严重的逻辑错误，把你能在一组报纸中找到的所有不公平和谎言的例子汇总起来，而忽略你在另一组报纸中很容易找到的所有例子，然后将你调查的媒体的一个所谓共同特征归咎为谎言的原因。如果你要把新闻业的缺陷归咎于“资本主义”，你就必须证明，这些缺陷只有在资本主义控制的地方才存在。辛克莱先生不能做到这一点，这一点可以从以下事实中看出：虽然他在诊断中把一切都归咎于资本主义，但在他的处方中，他却忽视了资本主义和反资本主义。

There is such a press. Strange to say, in proposing a remedy Mr. Sinclair does not advise his readers to subscribe to the nearest radical newspaper. Why not? If the troubles of American journalism go back to the Brass Check of Big Business why does not the remedy lie in reading the papers that do not in any remote way accept the Brass Check? Why subsidize a "National News" with a large board of directors "of all creeds or causes" to print a paper full of facts "regardless of what is injured, the Steel Trust or the I. W. W., the Standard Oil Company or the Socialist Party?" If the trouble is Big Business, that is, the Steel Trust, Standard Oil and the like, why not urge everybody to read I. W. W. or Socialist papers? Mr. Sinclair does not say why not. But the reason is simple. He cannot convince anybody, not even himself, that the anti-capitalist press is the remedy for the capitalist press. He ignores the anti-capitalist press both in his theory of the Brass Check and in his constructive proposal. But if you are diagnosing American journalism you cannot ignore it. If what you care about is "the fair body of truth," you do not commit the gross logical error of assembling all the instances of unfairness and lying you can find in one set of newspapers, ignore all the instances you could easily find in another set, and then assign as the cause of the lying, the one supposedly common characteristic of the press to which you have confined your investigation. If you are going to blame "capitalism" for the faults of the press, you are compelled to prove that those faults do not exist except where capitalism controls. That Mr. Sinclair cannot do this, is shown by the fact that while in his diagnosis he traces everything to capitalism, in his prescription he ignores both capitalism and anti-capitalism.

人们本以为，无法将任何非资本主义报纸视为真实性和能力的典范，这会导致辛克莱先生及其支持者更加批判地审视他们的假设。例如，他们会问自己，公平的真相在哪里？大企业会卖弄事实，而反大企业似乎无法获得真相。因为我认为，这个问题指向了问题的核心，即什么是新闻的问题。

One would have supposed that the inability to take any non-capitalist paper as a model of truthfulness and competence would have caused Mr. Sinclair, and those who agree with him, to look somewhat more critically at their assumptions. They would have asked themselves, for example, where is the fair body of truth, that Big Business prostitutes, but anti-Big Business does not seem to obtain? For that question leads, I believe, to the heart of the matter, to the question of what is news.

第二十三章

CHAPTER XXIII

新闻的本质

THE NATURE OF NEWS





1

1

世界上所有记者即使整天工作，也不可能见证世界上发生的所有事情。记者的数量并不多。他们中没有一个人有能力同时出现在多个地方。记者不是千里眼，他们不会注视水晶球随意观察世界，他们没有思想转移的帮助。然而，如果不是标准化的例行工作，这些相对较少的记者能够报道的题材范围确实是一个奇迹。

ALL the reporters in the world working all the hours of the day could not witness all the happenings in the world. There are not a great many reporters. And none of them has the power to be in more than one place at a time. Reporters are not clairvoyant, they do not gaze into a crystal ball and see the world at will, they are not assisted by thought-transference. Yet the range of subjects these comparatively few men manage to cover would be a miracle indeed, if it were not a standardized routine.

报纸并不试图监视全人类。它们在某些地方派驻了观察员，如警察局、验尸官办公室、县书记官办公室、市政厅、白宫、参议院、众议院等。他们监视，或者更确切地说，在大多数情况下，他们属于一些协会，这些协会雇用人员监视“相对较少的地方，当任何人的生活偏离正常轨道，或发生值得一提的事件时，就会公布消息。”例如，假设约翰·史密斯成为一名经纪人。十年来，他一直过着平静的生活，除了他的客户和朋友，没有人会想到他。在报纸看来，他就像不存在一样。但在第十一年，他遭受了重大损失，最后，他的资源全部用完了，他召集了律师，安排了一项任务。律师把信件寄到县书记官办公室，那里的书记官在官方档案中做了必要的记录。报纸也紧随其后。当书记官在写史密斯的商业讣告时，一名记者从他身后瞥了一眼，几分钟后，记者们就知道了史密斯的麻烦，并且对他的商业状况了如指掌，就像他们十多年来每天都让一名记者守在他家门口一样。

Newspapers do not try to keep an eye on all mankind. They have watchers stationed at certain places, like Police Headquarters, the Coroner's Office, the County Clerk's Office, City Hall, the White House, the Senate, House of Representatives, and so forth. They watch, or rather in the majority of cases they belong to associations which employ men who watch "a comparatively small number of places where it is made known when the life of anyone… departs from ordinary paths, or when events worth telling about occur. For example, John Smith, let it be supposed, becomes a broker. For ten years he pursues the even tenor of his way and except for his customers and his friends no one gives him a thought. To the newspapers he is as if he were not. But in the eleventh year he suffers heavy losses and, at last, his resources all gone, summons his lawyer and arranges for the making of an assignment. The lawyer posts off to the County Clerk's office, and a clerk there makes the necessary entries in the official docket. Here in step the newspapers. While the clerk is writing Smith's business obituary a reporter glances over his shoulder and a few minutes later the reporters know Smith's troubles and are as well informed concerning his business status as they would be had they kept a reporter at his door every day for over ten years.

当吉文先生说报纸知道“史密斯的麻烦”和“他的商业状况”时，他并不是说他们像史密斯一样知道这些，或者像阿诺德·贝内特先生如果把史密斯写成三卷本小说的英雄一样知道这些。报纸只是在“几分钟内”知道县书记官办公室记录的赤裸裸的事实。这种公开的行为“揭露”了有关史密斯的消息。是否会跟进新闻是另一回事。关键在于，在一系列事件成为新闻之前，他们通常必须通过某种或多或少公开的行为让自己引人注目。通常也是以一种粗鲁的公开行为。史密斯的朋友可能多年来都知道他在冒险，如果史密斯的朋友健谈的话，谣言甚至可能传到了财经编辑那里。但除了这些都不能发表，因为这是诽谤之外，这些谣言中没有任何明确的东西可以作为故事的依据。必须发生一些具有明确形式的明确的事情。它可能是破产行为，也可能是火灾、碰撞、袭击、暴乱、逮捕、谴责、提出法案、演讲、投票、会议、知名公民表达的意见、报纸上的社论、销售、工资表、价格变动、建桥提案……必须有表现。事件的进程必须呈现某种可定义的形态，除非它处于某个方面成为既定事实的阶段，否则新闻不会脱离可能真相的海洋。

When Mr. Given says that the newspapers know "Smith's troubles" and "his business status," he does not mean that they know them as Smith knows them, or as Mr. Arnold Bennett would know them if he had made Smith the hero of a three volume novel. The newspapers know only "in a few minutes" the bald facts which are recorded in the County Clerk's Office. That overt act "uncovers" the news about Smith. Whether the news will be followed up or not is another matter. The point is that before a series of events become news they have usually to make themselves noticeable in some more or less overt act. Generally too, in a crudely overt act. Smith's friends may have known for years that he was taking risks, rumors may even have reached the financial editor if Smith's friends were talkative. But apart from the fact that none of this could be published because it would be libel, there is in these rumors nothing definite on which to peg a story. Something definite must occur that has unmistakable form. It may be the act of going into bankruptcy, it may be a fire, a collision, an assault, a riot, an arrest, a denunciation, the introduction of a bill, a speech, a vote, a meeting, the expressed opinion of a well known citizen, an editorial in a newspaper, a sale, a wage-schedule, a price change, the proposal to build a bridge…. There must be a manifestation. The course of events must assume a certain definable shape, and until it is in a phase where some aspect is an accomplished fact, news does not separate itself from the ocean of possible truth.





2

2

当然，对于事件何时具有可以报道的形式，存在着巨大的分歧。一个好的记者比一个雇佣文人更能发现新闻。如果他看到一栋有危险倾斜的建筑物，他不必等到它倒塌在街上才能识别出新闻。一位伟大的记者在听说某某勋爵正在询问气候时，猜出了下一任印度总督的名字。幸运的镜头是有的，但能拍到的人很少。通常，事件在明显的地方呈现的刻板形状揭示了新闻的走向。最明显的地方是人民事务触及公共权力的地方。De minimis non curat lex。正是在这些地方，婚姻、出生、死亡、合同、失败、到达、离开、诉讼、混乱、流行病和灾难才为人所知。

Naturally there is room for wide difference of opinion as to when events have a shape that can be reported. A good journalist will find news oftener than a hack. If he sees a building with a dangerous list, he does not have to wait until it falls into the street in order to recognize news. It was a great reporter who guessed the name of the next Indian Viceroy when he heard that Lord So-and-So was inquiring about climates. There are lucky shots but the number of men who can make them is small. Usually it is the stereotyped shape assumed by an event at an obvious place that uncovers the run of the news. The most obvious place is where people's affairs touch public authority. De minimis non curat lex. It is at these places that marriages, births, deaths, contracts, failures, arrivals, departures, lawsuits, disorders, epidemics and calamities are made known.

因此，首先，新闻不是社会状况的镜子，而是对突显出来的事物的报道。新闻不会告诉你种子在地里是如何发芽的，但它可能会告诉你第一颗嫩芽何时破土而出。它甚至可能会告诉你有人说地下的种子发生了什么。它可能会告诉你嫩芽没有在预期的时间发芽。因此，任何事件可以被确定、客观化、衡量和命名的点越多，新闻发生的点就越多。

In the first instance, therefore, the news is not a mirror of social conditions, but the report of an aspect that has obtruded itself. The news does not tell you how the seed is germinating in the ground, but it may tell you when the first sprout breaks through the surface. It may even tell you what somebody says is happening to the seed under ground. It may tell you that the sprout did not come up at the time it was expected. The more points, then, at which any happening can be fixed, objectified, measured, named, the more points there are at which news can occur.

因此，如果有一天立法机关在用尽了所有其他改善人类的方法之后，禁止棒球比赛计分，那么仍有可能进行某种比赛，裁判根据自己的公平观念决定比赛应该持续多长时间，每支球队应该在什么时候击球，谁应该被视为赢家。如果报纸报道了这场比赛，它将包括裁判判决的记录，加上记者对观众欢呼声的印象，以及充其量模糊地描述某些在球场上没有指定位置的人如何在没有标记的草地上走动几个小时。你越是试图想象如此荒谬的困境的逻辑，就越清楚，为了新闻采访的目的（更不用说玩游戏的目的），如果没有命名、计分和记录的设备和规则，就不可能做很多事情。由于这种机器远非完美，裁判的生活常常令人心烦意乱。许多关键的比赛他必须用眼睛来判断。如果有人认为值得拍摄每一场比赛，那么比赛的最后争议痕迹就可以消除，就像人们遵守规则时国际象棋中争议的痕迹已经消除一样。由于人眼反应迟钝，许多记者心中的疑问终于被动态画面打消了，他们不知道邓普西的哪一击击倒了卡彭蒂尔。

So, if some day a legislature, having exhausted all other ways of improving mankind, should forbid the scoring of baseball games, it might still be possible to play some sort of game in which the umpire decided according to his own sense of fair play how long the game should last, when each team should go to bat, and who should be regarded as the winner. If that game were reported in the newspapers it would consist of a record of the umpire's decisions, plus the reporter's impression of the hoots and cheers of the crowd, plus at best a vague account of how certain men, who had no specified position on the field moved around for a few hours on an unmarked piece of sod. The more you try to imagine the logic of so absurd a predicament, the more clear it becomes that for the purposes of newsgathering, (let alone the purposes of playing the game) it is impossible to do much without an apparatus and rules for naming, scoring, recording. Because that machinery is far from perfect, the umpire's life is often a distracted one. Many crucial plays he has to judge by eye. The last vestige of dispute could be taken out of the game, as it has been taken out of chess when people obey the rules, if somebody thought it worth his while to photograph every play. It was the moving pictures which finally settled a real doubt in many reporters' minds, owing to the slowness of the human eye, as to just what blow of Dempsey's knocked out Carpentier.

哪里有良好的记录机制，哪里的现代新闻服务就非常精确。证券交易所就有这样的机制，价格变动的消息会以可靠的准确性在行情显示机上闪现。选举结果也有记录机制，如果计票和制表工作做得好，全国选举的结果通常在选举当晚就能知道。在文明社会中，死亡、出生、结婚和离婚都会被记录下来，除非有隐瞒或疏忽，否则都会被准确知晓。这种机制只存在于工业和政府的某些方面，而且只存在于某些方面，对证券、货币和主要商品、银行结算、房地产交易、工资表的精确程度各不相同。进出口也有这种机制，因为它们要经过海关，可以直接记录。国内贸易，尤其是场外交易，其精确程度却大不相同。

Wherever there is a good machinery of record, the modern news service works with great precision. There is one on the stock exchange, and the news of price movements is flashed over tickers with dependable accuracy. There is a machinery for election returns, and when the counting and tabulating are well done, the result of a national election is usually known on the night of the election. In civilized communities deaths, births, marriages and divorces are recorded, and are known accurately except where there is concealment or neglect. The machinery exists for some, and only some, aspects of industry and government, in varying degrees of precision for securities, money and staples, bank clearances, realty transactions, wage scales. It exists for imports and exports because they pass through a custom house and can be directly recorded. It exists in nothing like the same degree for internal trade, and especially for trade over the counter.

我认为，人们会发现，新闻的确定性和记录系统之间存在着非常直接的关系。如果你回想一下改革者对新闻界的主要指控，你会发现，在这些话题中，报纸占据着棒球比赛中裁判的位置。所有关于心理状态的新闻都具有这种特征：所有关于个性、诚意、抱负、动机、意图、大众情感、民族情感、舆论、外国政府政策的描述也是如此。关于即将发生的事情的许多新闻也是如此。关于私人利润、私人收入、工资、工作条件、劳动效率、教育机会、失业、单调、健康、歧视、不公平、贸易限制、浪费、“落后民族”、保守主义、帝国主义、激进主义、自由、荣誉、正义的问题也是如此。所有这些都涉及充其量是断断续续记录的数据。这些数据可能因为审查制度或隐私传统而被隐藏，也可能因为没有人认为记录很重要、因为人们认为这是官僚作风或因为还没有人发明客观的测量系统而不存在。那么，当这些主题的新闻没有被完全忽视时，它必然会引起争议。没有被评分的事件要么被报道为个人和传统观点，要么就不是新闻。直到有人抗议、有人调查，或者有人公开（从这个词的词源意义上来说）提出问题，它们才会成形。

It will be found, I think, that there is a very direct relation between the certainty of news and the system of record. If you call to mind the topics which form the principal indictment by reformers against the press, you find they are subjects in which the newspaper occupies the position of the umpire in the unscored baseball game. All news about states of mind is of this character: so are all descriptions of personalities, of sincerity, aspiration, motive, intention, of mass feeling, of national feeling, of public opinion, the policies of foreign governments. So is much news about what is going to happen. So are questions turning on private profit, private income, wages, working conditions, the efficiency of labor, educational opportunity, unemployment, monotony, health, discrimination, unfairness, restraint of trade, waste, "backward peoples," conservatism, imperialism, radicalism, liberty, honor, righteousness. All involve data that are at best spasmodically recorded. The data may be hidden because of a censorship or a tradition of privacy, they may not exist because nobody thinks record important, because he thinks it red tape, or because nobody has yet invented an objective system of measurement. Then the news on these subjects is bound to be debatable, when it is not wholly neglected. The events which are not scored are reported either as personal and conventional opinions, or they are not news. They do not take shape until somebody protests, or somebody investigates, or somebody publicly, in the etymological meaning of the word, makes an issue of them.

这就是新闻代理人存在的根本原因。对于报道哪些事实和哪些印象拥有极大的自由裁量权，这让每一个有组织的团体都坚信，无论他们希望获得宣传还是避免宣传，自由裁量权都不能留给记者。雇佣一名站在团体和报纸之间的新闻代理人更为安全。雇佣了他之后，利用他的战略地位的诱惑就非常大了。 “战争爆发前不久，”弗兰克·科布先生说，“纽约的各家报纸对定期受雇和定期认证的新闻代理人进行了一次普查，发现大约有 1200 人。现在（1919 年）有多少人，我并不知道，但我知道的是，许多直接获取新闻的渠道已被关闭，公众的信息首先要通过宣传代理人进行过滤。大公司有宣传代理人，银行有宣传代理人，铁路有宣传代理人，所有商业和社会政治活动组织都有宣传代理人，他们是新闻传播的媒介。甚至政治家也有宣传代理人。”

This is the underlying reason for the existence of the press agent. The enormous discretion as to what facts and what impressions shall be reported is steadily convincing every organized group of people that whether it wishes to secure publicity or to avoid it, the exercise of discretion cannot be left to the reporter. It is safer to hire a press agent who stands between the group and the newspapers. Having hired him, the temptation to exploit his strategic position is very great. "Shortly before the war," says Mr. Frank Cobb, "the newspapers of New York took a census of the press agents who were regularly employed and regularly accredited and found that there were about twelve hundred of them. How many there are now (1919) I do not pretend to know, but what I do know is that many of the direct channels to news have been closed and the information for the public is first filtered through publicity agents. The great corporations have them, the banks have them, the railroads have them, all the organizations of business and of social and political activity have them, and they are the media through which news comes. Even statesmen have them."

如果报道的是显而易见的事实，新闻代理人只不过是个办事员。但是，由于就大多数重大新闻话题而言，事实并不简单，也一点也不明显，而是受选择和意见的影响，所以每个人都希望自己选择一些事实供报纸刊登，这是很自然的。宣传人员就是这样做的。这样做，他当然为记者省去了很多麻烦，因为他向记者展示了一幅清晰的画面，否则记者可能一头雾水。但由此可见，宣传人员为记者描绘的画面是他希望公众看到的画面。他是审查员和宣传员，只对他的雇主负责，只对符合雇主对他自身利益的看法的全部真相负责。

Were reporting the simple recovery of obvious facts, the press agent would be little more than a clerk. But since, in respect to most of the big topics of news, the facts are not simple, and not at all obvious, but subject to choice and opinion, it is natural that everyone should wish to make his own choice of facts for the newspapers to print. The publicity man does that. And in doing it, he certainly saves the reporter much trouble, by presenting him a clear picture of a situation out of which he might otherwise make neither head nor tail. But it follows that the picture which the publicity man makes for the reporter is the one he wishes the public to see. He is censor and propagandist, responsible only to his employers, and to the whole truth responsible only as it accords with the employers' conception of his own interests.

宣传人员的发展清楚地表明，现代生活的事实不会自发地形成一种可以被人知晓的形式。它们必须由某人来塑造，而由于在日常工作中记者无法塑造事实，而且由于几乎没有公正的情报组织，因此需要由相关方来满足对事实进行某种表述的需求。

The development of the publicity man is a clear sign that the facts of modern life do not spontaneously take a shape in which they can be known. They must be given a shape by somebody, and since in the daily routine reporters cannot give a shape to facts, and since there is little disinterested organization of intelligence, the need for some formulation is being met by the interested parties.





3

3

优秀的新闻代理人明白，他的事业的优点不算新闻，除非这些优点非常奇怪，以至于与日常生活格格不入。这并不是因为报纸不喜欢优点，而是因为当没有人期望发生任何事情时，说什么都没有发生是毫无意义的。因此，如果宣传人员希望获得免费宣传，那么他必须开始做点什么，说得更准确些。他安排了一个噱头：阻碍交通、戏弄警察，设法将他的客户或事业与已经是新闻的事件纠缠在一起。妇女参政主义者知道这一点，他们并不特别喜欢这种知识，但他们还是采取了行动，在赞成和反对的论点都毫无意义、人们即将安定下来将妇女参政运动视为美国生活中既定制度之一之后，他们仍然让妇女参政成为新闻话题。

The good press agent understands that the virtues of his cause are not news, unless they are such strange virtues that they jut right out of the routine of life. This is not because the newspapers do not like virtue, but because it is not worth while to say that nothing has happened when nobody expected anything to happen. So if the publicity man wishes free publicity he has, speaking quite accurately, to start something. He arranges a stunt: obstructs the traffic, teases the police, somehow manages to entangle his client or his cause with an event that is already news. The suffragists knew this, did not particularly enjoy the knowledge but acted on it, and kept suffrage in the news long after the arguments pro and con were straw in their mouths, and people were about to settle down to thinking of the suffrage movement as one of the established institutions of American life.

幸运的是，与女权主义者不同的是，妇女参政主义者有一个非常具体的目标，而且非常简单。投票权所象征的东西并不简单，这一点最有能力的支持者和最有能力的反对者都知道。但投票权是一项简单而熟悉的权利。现在，在劳资纠纷中，这可能是对报纸的指控中的主要内容，罢工权和投票权一样，非常简单。但特定罢工的原因和目标就像妇女运动的原因和目标一样，极其微妙。

Fortunately the suffragists, as distinct from the feminists, had a perfectly concrete objective, and a very simple one. What the vote symbolizes is not simple, as the ablest advocates and the ablest opponents knew. But the right to vote is a simple and familiar right. Now in labor disputes, which are probably the chief item in the charges against newspapers, the right to strike, like the right to vote, is simple enough. But the causes and objects of a particular strike are like the causes and objects of the woman's movement, extremely subtle.

让我们假设罢工前的条件很差。衡量邪恶的标准是什么？某种关于适当生活水平、卫生、经济保障和人类尊严的概念。该行业可能远低于社会理论标准，工人们可能太悲惨而无法抗议。条件可能高于标准，工人们可能会激烈抗议。标准充其量只是一个模糊的衡量标准。然而，我们假设条件低于标准，正如编辑所理解的那样。偶尔，他不会等工人威胁，而是在社会工作者的提示下，派记者去调查，并引起人们对恶劣条件的关注。他不一定能经常这样做。因为这些调查需要时间、金钱、特殊才能和大量版面。要使一份关于条件恶劣的报道可信，你需要很多栏的印刷品。为了讲述匹兹堡地区钢铁工人的真相，需要一队调查人员、大量的时间和几卷厚厚的印刷品。不可能想象任何日报会把制作《匹兹堡调查》或《教会间钢铁报告》视为自己的任务之一。需要如此费力才能获得的新闻超出了日报的资源范围。

Let us suppose the conditions leading up to a strike are bad. What is the measure of evil? A certain conception of a proper standard of living, hygiene, economic security, and human dignity. The industry may be far below the theoretical standard of the community, and the workers may be too wretched to protest. Conditions may be above the standard, and the workers may protest violently. The standard is at best a vague measure. However, we shall assume that the conditions are below par, as par is understood by the editor. Occasionally without waiting for the workers to threaten, but prompted say by a social worker, he will send reporters to investigate, and will call attention to bad conditions. Necessarily he cannot do that often. For these investigations cost time, money, special talent, and a lot of space. To make plausible a report that conditions are bad, you need a good many columns of print. In order to tell the truth about the steel worker in the Pittsburgh district, there was needed a staff of investigators, a great deal of time, and several fat volumes of print. It is impossible to suppose that any daily newspaper could normally regard the making of Pittsburgh Surveys, or even Interchurch Steel Reports, as one of its tasks. News which requires so much trouble as that to obtain is beyond the resources of a daily press.

恶劣条件本身并不是新闻，因为除了特殊情况外，新闻报道并不是对原始材料的第一手报道。它是对材料进行风格化后的报道。因此，如果卫生委员会报告某个工业区的死亡率异常高，恶劣条件就可能成为新闻。如果没有这种干预，事实就不会成为新闻，直到工人们组织起来并向雇主提出要求。即便如此，如果确定可以轻松解决，新闻价值也很低，无论条件本身是否在和解中得到改善。但如果劳资关系破裂为罢工或停工，新闻价值就会增加。如果停工涉及报纸读者直接依赖的服务，或者涉及违反秩序，新闻价值就更大。

The bad conditions as such are not news, because in all but exceptional cases, journalism is not a first hand report of the raw material. It is a report of that material after it has been stylized. Thus bad conditions might become news if the Board of Health reported an unusually high death rate in an industrial area. Failing an intervention of this sort, the facts do not become news, until the workers organize and make a demand upon their employers. Even then, if an easy settlement is certain the news value is low, whether or not the conditions themselves are remedied in the settlement. But if industrial relations collapse into a strike or lockout the news value increases. If the stoppage involves a service on which the readers of the newspapers immediately depend, or if it involves a breach of order, the news value is still greater.

潜在的麻烦通过某些容易识别的症状出现在新闻中，如要求、罢工、骚乱。从工人或公正的正义追求者的角度来看，要求、罢工和骚乱仅仅是一个对他们来说非常复杂的过程中的事件。但由于所有直接现实都不在记者和大多数报纸所依赖的特殊公众的直接经验范围内，因此他们通常必须等待以公开行为形式出现的信号。当这种信号出现时，比如工人罢工或警察传唤，它就会激发人们对罢工和骚乱的刻板印象。看不见的斗争没有自己的特色。它被抽象地注意到，然后这种抽象被读者和记者的直接经验所激发。显然，这与罢工者的经历截然不同。他们感受到，比如说，工头的脾气、机器令人神经紧张的单调、令人沮丧的糟糕空气、妻子的单调工作、孩子的发育迟缓、住房的肮脏。罢工的口号充满了这些感受。但记者和读者一开始只看到罢工和一些口号。他们把这些口号融入了感情。他们的感觉可能是，他们的工作没有保障，因为罢工者阻止了他们工作所需的商品，会出现短缺和价格上涨，这一切都非常不方便。这些也是现实。当他们给罢工的抽象新闻增添色彩时，事情的本质就是工人处于不利地位。也就是说，在现有的劳资关系制度的本质中，工人的不满或希望产生的新闻几乎总是会通过公开攻击生产来揭露。

The underlying trouble appears in the news through certain easily recognizable symptoms, a demand, a strike, disorder. From the point of view of the worker, or of the disinterested seeker of justice, the demand, the strike, and the disorder, are merely incidents in a process that for them is richly complicated. But since all the immediate realities lie outside the direct experience both of the reporter, and of the special public by which most newspapers are supported, they have normally to wait for a signal in the shape of an overt act. When that signal comes, say through a walkout of the men or a summons for the police, it calls into play the stereotypes people have about strikes and disorders. The unseen struggle has none of its own flavor. It is noted abstractly, and that abstraction is then animated by the immediate experience of the reader and reporter. Obviously this is a very different experience from that which the strikers have. They feel, let us say, the temper of the foreman, the nerve-racking monotony of the machine, the depressingly bad air, the drudgery of their wives, the stunting of their children, the dinginess of their tenements. The slogans of the strike are invested with these feelings. But the reporter and reader see at first only a strike and some catchwords. They invest these with their feelings. Their feelings may be that their jobs are insecure because the strikers are stopping goods they need in their work, that there will be shortage and higher prices, that it is all devilishly inconvenient. These, too, are realities. And when they give color to the abstract news that a strike has been called, it is in the nature of things that the workers are at a disadvantage. It is in the nature, that is to say, of the existing system of industrial relations that news arising from grievances or hopes by workers should almost invariably be uncovered by an overt attack on production.

因此，你会看到各种错综复杂的情况、发出信号的公开行为、发布信号的陈词滥调的公告，以及读者自己从直接影响他的经历中得出的意义。现在，读者对罢工的经历可能确实非常重要，但从引起罢工的核心问题的角度来看，这是奇怪的。然而，这种奇怪的意义自然是最有趣的。以想象的方式进入核心问题，对读者来说，就是走出自我，进入截然不同的生活。

You have, therefore, the circumstances in all their sprawling complexity, the overt act which signalizes them, the stereotyped bulletin which publishes the signal, and the meaning that the reader himself injects, after he has derived that meaning from the experience which directly affects him. Now the reader's experience of a strike may be very important indeed, but from the point of view of the central trouble which caused the strike, it is eccentric. Yet this eccentric meaning is automatically the most interesting. To enter imaginatively into the central issues is for the reader to step out of himself, and into very different lives.

因此，在报道罢工事件时，最简单的方法就是让新闻通过公开行为来揭露，并将事件描述为干扰读者生活的故事。这是读者注意力首先被唤起的地方，也是最容易引起读者兴趣的地方。在工人和改革者看来，报纸故意歪曲事实，其中很大一部分，我认为是关键部分，是揭露新闻的实际困难的直接结果，以及使遥远的事实变得有趣的情感困难的直接结果，除非如爱默生所说，我们能够“将它们视为我们熟悉经验的新版本”，并能够“立即着手将它们转化为我们的平行事实”。

It follows that in the reporting of strikes, the easiest way is to let the news be uncovered by the overt act, and to describe the event as the story of interference with the reader's life. That is where his attention is first aroused, and his interest most easily enlisted. A great deal, I think myself the crucial part, of what looks to the worker and the reformer as deliberate misrepresentation on the part of newspapers, is the direct outcome of a practical difficulty in uncovering the news, and the emotional difficulty of making distant facts interesting unless, as Emerson says, we can "perceive (them) to be only a new version of our familiar experience" and can "set about translating (them) at once into our parallel facts."

如果你研究一下媒体报道罢工事件的方式，你会发现，很多时候，这些问题很少出现在头条新闻中，很少出现在前几段中，有时甚至根本没有提到。另一个城市的劳资纠纷必须非常重要，新闻报道才会包含任何有关争议的明确信息。新闻的常规就是这样运作的，在政治问题和国际新闻方面也是如此，只是有所修改。新闻是对有趣的公开阶段的报道，报纸坚持这一常规的压力来自多方面。它来自只关注情况的刻板阶段的经济效益。它来自很难找到能看到他们没有学会看到的东西的记者。它来自几乎不可避免的困难，即找到足够的空间，即使是最好的记者也可以让一个非传统的观点变得可信。它来自迅速引起读者兴趣的经济需要，以及完全不引起读者兴趣或因描述不充分或笨拙的意外新闻而冒犯读者所涉及的经济风险。所有这些困难加在一起，使得编辑在面临危险问题时感到不确定，并自然而然地倾向于无可争辩的事实和更易于适应读者兴趣的处理方式。无可争辩的事实和容易的兴趣，就是罢工本身和读者的不便。

If you study the way many a strike is reported in the press, you will find, very often, that the issues are rarely in the headlines, barely in the leading paragraphs, and sometimes not even mentioned anywhere. A labor dispute in another city has to be very important before the news account contains any definite information as to what is in dispute. The routine of the news works that way, with modifications it works that way in regard to political issues and international news as well. The news is an account of the overt phases that are interesting, and the pressure on the newspaper to adhere to this routine comes from many sides. It comes from the economy of noting only the stereotyped phase of a situation. It comes from the difficulty of finding journalists who can see what they have not learned to see. It comes from the almost unavoidable difficulty of finding sufficient space in which even the best journalist can make plausible an unconventional view. It comes from the economic necessity of interesting the reader quickly, and the economic risk involved in not interesting him at all, or of offending him by unexpected news insufficiently or clumsily described. All these difficulties combined make for uncertainty in the editor when there are dangerous issues at stake, and cause him naturally to prefer the indisputable fact and a treatment more readily adapted to the reader's interest. The indisputable fact and the easy interest, are the strike itself and the reader's inconvenience.

在目前的行业组织中，所有更微妙、更深刻的真相都是非常不可靠的真相。它们涉及对生活水平、生产力、人权的判断，而这些判断在没有准确记录和定量分析的情况下是无休止地争论的。只要这些在行业中不存在，那么有关它的新闻就会像爱默生引用伊索克拉底的话所说的那样，“把鼹鼠变成山，把山变成鼹鼠。”如果行业没有宪法程序，也没有专家对证据和主张进行筛选，那么让读者感到耸人听闻的事实就是几乎每个记者都会寻找的事实。鉴于普遍存在的劳资关系，即使有会议或仲裁，但没有独立的事实筛选以供决定，报纸公众的问题往往不会成为行业的问题。因此，通过报纸上诉来审理纠纷会给报纸和读者带来负担，而这是他们无法也不应该承担的。只要真正的法律和秩序不存在，除非有意识地勇敢地加以纠正，否则大部分新闻都会对那些没有合法有序维护自己权利的人不利。来自行动现场的公告将记录由这种主张引起的麻烦，而不是导致这种主张的原因。原因是无形的。

All the subtler and deeper truths are in the present organization of industry very unreliable truths. They involve judgments about standards of living, productivity, human rights that are endlessly debatable in the absence of exact record and quantitative analysis. And as long as these do not exist in industry, the run of news about it will tend, as Emerson said, quoting from Isocrates, "to make of moles mountains, and of mountains moles." Where there is no constitutional procedure in industry, and no expert sifting of evidence and the claims, the fact that is sensational to the reader is the fact that almost every journalist will seek. Given the industrial relations that so largely prevail, even where there is conference or arbitration, but no independent filtering of the facts for decision, the issue for the newspaper public will tend not to be the issue for the industry. And so to try disputes by an appeal through the newspapers puts a burden upon newspapers and readers which they cannot and ought not to carry. As long as real law and order do not exist, the bulk of the news will, unless consciously and courageously corrected, work against those who have no lawful and orderly method of asserting themselves. The bulletins from the scene of action will note the trouble that arose from the assertion, rather than the reasons which led to it. The reasons are intangible.





4

4

编辑负责处理这些公报。他坐在办公室里阅读公报，很少看到事件本身的大部分内容。正如我们所看到的，他必须每天吸引至少一部分读者，因为如果竞争对手的报纸恰好符合他们的口味，他们会毫不留情地离开他。他承受着巨大的压力，因为报纸的竞争往往是几分钟的事情。每一份公报都需要迅速而复杂的判断。它必须被理解，与其他同样被理解的公报联系起来，并根据编辑对公众的可能兴趣来夸大或淡化它。如果没有标准化、没有刻板印象、没有常规判断、没有相当无情地忽视微妙之处，编辑很快就会兴奋得死去活来。最终的页面是确定的大小，必须在精确的时间准备好；每篇文章的标题只能有一定数量的标题，每个标题中的字母数也必须确定。总是存在着购买者的迫切需求、诽谤法和无尽麻烦的可能性。没有系统化，事情根本无法管理，因为标准化产品可以节省时间和精力，还可以部分保证不会失败。

The editor deals with these bulletins. He sits in his office, reads them, rarely does he see any large portion of the events themselves. He must, as we have seen, woo at least a section of his readers every day, because they will leave him without mercy if a rival paper happens to hit their fancy. He works under enormous pressure, for the competition of newspapers is often a matter of minutes. Every bulletin requires a swift but complicated judgment. It must be understood, put in relation to other bulletins also understood, and played up or played down according to its probable interest for the public, as the editor conceives it. Without standardization, without stereotypes, without routine judgments, without a fairly ruthless disregard of subtlety, the editor would soon die of excitement. The final page is of a definite size, must be ready at a precise moment; there can be only a certain number of captions on the items, and in each caption there must be a definite number of letters. Always there is the precarious urgency of the buying public, the law of libel, and the possibility of endless trouble. The thing could not be managed at all without systematization, for in a standardized product there is economy of time and effort, as well as a partial guarantee against failure.

正是在这里，各家报纸相互影响最为深刻。因此，当战争爆发时，美国报纸面临着一个他们以前没有经验的话题。某些日报有足够的钱支付电报费，率先获得新闻，新闻呈现方式成为整个新闻界的典范。但这种模式从何而来？它来自英国媒体，不是因为诺思克利夫拥有美国报纸，而是因为起初购买英文通讯更容易，而且后来，美国记者阅读英文报纸比阅读其他报纸更容易。伦敦是电报和新闻中心，正是在那里，一种报道战争的技术得以发展。在报道俄国革命时也发生了类似的事情。在那个例子中，俄罗斯和盟军的军事审查制度封锁了进入俄罗斯的渠道，而俄语的困难更是封锁了进入俄罗斯的渠道。但最重要的是，它无法进行有效的新闻报道，因为最难报道的是混乱，尽管它是一种不断发展的混乱。这使得俄罗斯新闻的制作权从赫尔辛基、斯德哥尔摩、日内瓦、巴黎和伦敦等地的源头落入了审查者和宣传者的手中。很长一段时间里，他们没有受到任何形式的审查。在他们变得可笑之前，他们从俄罗斯大漩涡的某些真实方面创造了一套刻板印象，让我们承认，这些刻板印象如此令人厌恶和恐惧，以至于新闻业最优秀的本能，即去看看、去报道的愿望，在很长一段时间内被压制了。

It is here that newspapers influence each other most deeply. Thus when the war broke out, the American newspapers were confronted with a subject about which they had no previous experience. Certain dailies, rich enough to pay cable tolls, took the lead in securing news, and the way that news was presented became a model for the whole press. But where did that model come from? It came from the English press, not because Northcliffe owned American newspapers, but because at first it was easier to buy English correspondence, and because, later, it was easier for American journalists to read English newspapers than it was for them to read any others. London was the cable and news center, and it was there that a certain technic for reporting the war was evolved. Something similar occurred in the reporting of the Russian Revolution. In that instance, access to Russia was closed by military censorship, both Russian and Allied, and closed still more effectively by the difficulties of the Russian language. But above all it was closed to effective news reporting by the fact that the hardest thing to report is chaos, even though it is an evolving chaos. This put the formulating of Russian news at its source in Helsingfors, Stockholm, Geneva, Paris and London, into the hands of censors and propagandists. They were for a long time subject to no check of any kind. Until they had made themselves ridiculous they created, let us admit, out of some genuine aspects of the huge Russian maelstrom, a set of stereotypes so evocative of hate and fear, that the very best instinct of journalism, its desire to go and see and tell, was for a long time crushed.





5

5

每一份报纸送到读者手中，都是经过一系列选择的结果，包括要印什么内容、印在什么位置、每篇内容占据多少版面、每篇内容的重点是什么。这里没有客观标准。只有惯例。以同一天早上在同一城市出版的两份报纸为例。一份报纸的标题是：“英国承诺向柏林提供援助，抵抗法国的侵略；法国公开支持波兰人。”第二份报纸的标题是“斯蒂尔曼夫人的另一种爱”。你喜欢哪一份报纸取决于你的品味，但并不完全取决于编辑的品味。这取决于他的判断，即什么内容会吸引某一群读者对他的报纸的半小时的注意力。现在，吸引注意力的问题绝不等同于以宗教教义或某种形式的道德文化所规定的视角来展示新闻。这是一个激发读者情感的问题，促使读者对他正在阅读的故事产生个人认同感。如果新闻不能提供机会让人们参与到它所描绘的斗争中，那么它就不可能吸引广大的观众。观众必须通过个人认同来参与新闻，就像参与戏剧一样。就像女主角遇到危险时每个人都屏住呼吸，帮助贝比·鲁斯挥动球棒一样，读者以更微妙的方式进入新闻。为了进入新闻，他必须在故事中找到一个熟悉的立足点，而这正是通过使用刻板印象提供给他的。他们告诉他，如果一个水管工协会被称为“联合体”，那么培养他的敌意是合适的；如果它被称为“一群主要的商人”，那么暗示着他会做出有利的反应。

Every newspaper when it reaches the reader is the result of a whole series of selections as to what items shall be printed, in what position they shall be printed, how much space each shall occupy, what emphasis each shall have. There are no objective standards here. There are conventions. Take two newspapers published in the same city on the same morning. The headline of one reads: "Britain pledges aid to Berlin against French aggression; France openly backs Poles." The headline of the second is "Mrs. Stillman's Other Love." Which you prefer is a matter of taste, but not entirely a matter of the editor's taste. It is a matter of his judgment as to what will absorb the half hour's attention a certain set of readers will give to his newspaper. Now the problem of securing attention is by no means equivalent to displaying the news in the perspective laid down by religious teaching or by some form of ethical culture. It is a problem of provoking feeling in the reader, of inducing him to feel a sense of personal identification with the stories he is reading. News which does not offer this opportunity to introduce oneself into the struggle which it depicts cannot appeal to a wide audience. The audience must participate in the news, much as it participates in the drama, by personal identification. Just as everyone holds his breath when the heroine is in danger, as he helps Babe Ruth swing his bat, so in subtler form the reader enters into the news. In order that he shall enter he must find a familiar foothold in the story, and this is supplied to him by the use of stereotypes. They tell him that if an association of plumbers is called a "combine" it is appropriate to develop his hostility; if it is called a "group of leading business men" the cue is for a favorable reaction.

正是这些因素的结合，才产生了创造舆论的力量。社论则起到了加强作用。有时，在新闻版面上的某种情况过于混乱而无法辨别时，社论会给读者提供线索，让读者参与进来。如果他想像我们大多数人一样，迅速抓住新闻，他就必须有这样的线索。他需要某种建议，告诉他，作为一个认为自己是某某的人，他应该在何处将自己的感受与他所读到的新闻结合起来。

It is in a combination of these elements that the power to create opinion resides. Editorials reinforce. Sometimes in a situation that on the news pages is too confusing to permit of identification, they give the reader a clue by means of which he engages himself. A clue he must have if, as most of us must, he is to seize the news in a hurry. A suggestion of some sort he demands, which tells him, so to speak, where he, a man conceiving himself to be such and such a person, shall integrate his feelings with the news he reads.

沃尔特·白芝浩写道：“据说，如果你能让一个中产阶级英国人思考‘天狼星里是否有蜗牛’，他很快就会对此有自己的看法。让他思考很难，但如果他真的思考了，他就不会固步自封，他会做出某种决定。当然，对于任何普通话题，情况都是如此。杂货商对外交政策有着完整的信念，年轻女士对圣礼有着完整的理论，他们对此都没有任何怀疑。”

"It has been said" writes Walter Bagehot, "that if you can only get a middleclass Englishman to think whether there are 'snails in Sirius,' he will soon have an opinion on it. It will be difficult to make him think, but if he does think, he cannot rest in a negative, he will come to some decision. And on any ordinary topic, of course, it is so.
