A grocer has a full creed as to foreign policy, a young lady a complete theory of the sacraments, as to which neither has any doubt whatever."

然而，那位杂货商会对他所买的杂货产生许多疑虑，而那位对圣礼十分确信的年轻女士，可能会对是否要嫁给这位杂货商，以及如果不嫁给这位杂货商，是否应该接受他的关注产生各种疑虑。能够保持消极态度意味着要么对结果不感兴趣，要么对竞争性选择有强烈的感觉。在外交政策或圣礼方面，人们对结果的兴趣非常强烈，而核实意见的手段却很少。这就是一般新闻读者的困境。如果他要读新闻，他必须感兴趣，也就是说，他必须进入情境并关心结果。但如果他这样做，他就不能保持消极态度，除非存在独立核实报纸给他的线索的手段，否则他感兴趣的事实本身就可能使他难以达成最接近真相的意见平衡。他越是热情地参与其中，他就越倾向于不仅对不同的观点感到不满，而且对令人不安的新闻也感到不满。这就是为什么许多报纸发现，在诚实地激起读者的党派偏见之后，即使编辑认为事实需要改变立场，它也无法轻易改变立场。如果必须改变立场，就必须以最精湛的技巧和细腻的手段来处理这一转变。通常报纸不会尝试如此危险的行为。让该主题的新闻逐渐减少并消失，从而通过扼杀它来扑灭火焰，这样更容易、更安全。

Yet that same grocer will have many doubts about his groceries, and that young lady, marvelously certain about the sacraments, may have all kinds of doubts as to whether to marry the grocer, and if not whether it is proper to accept his attentions. The ability to rest in the negative implies either a lack of interest in the result, or a vivid sense of competing alternatives. In the case of foreign policy or the sacraments, the interest in the results is intense, while means for checking the opinion are poor. This is the plight of the reader of the general news. If he is to read it at all he must be interested, that is to say, he must enter into the situation and care about the outcome. But if he does that he cannot rest in a negative, and unless independent means of checking the lead given him by his newspaper exists, the very fact that he is interested may make it difficult to arrive at that balance of opinions which may most nearly approximate the truth. The more passionately involved he becomes, the more he will tend to resent not only a different view, but a disturbing bit of news. That is why many a newspaper finds that, having honestly evoked the partisanship of its readers, it can not easily, supposing the editor believes the facts warrant it, change position. If a change is necessary, the transition has to be managed with the utmost skill and delicacy. Usually a newspaper will not attempt so hazardous a performance. It is easier and safer to have the news of that subject taper off and disappear, thus putting out the fire by starving it.

第二十四章

CHAPTER XXIV

新闻、真相和结论

NEWS, TRUTH, AND A CONCLUSION





1

1

当我们开始对新闻界进行越来越精确的研究时，我们持有的假设将发挥很大作用。如果我们与辛克莱先生及其大多数反对者一样，认为新闻和真相是同一个事物的两个词，那么我相信我们将一事无成。我们将证明报纸在这一点上撒了谎。我们将证明辛克莱先生在那一点上的叙述是撒谎的。我们将证明当辛克莱先生说某人撒谎时，他撒了谎，当辛克莱先生说某人撒谎时，他撒了谎。我们将发泄我们的感情，但我们会把它们发泄到空气中。

As we begin to make more and more exact studies of the press, much will depend upon the hypothesis we hold. If we assume with Mr. Sinclair, and most of his opponents, that news and truth are two words for the same thing, we shall, I believe, arrive nowhere. We shall prove that on this point the newspaper lied. We shall prove that on that point Mr. Sinclair's account lied. We shall demonstrate that Mr. Sinclair lied when he said that somebody lied, and that somebody lied when he said Mr. Sinclair lied. We shall vent our feelings, but we shall vent them into air.

在我看来，最有说服力的假设是，新闻和真相不是一回事，必须明确区分。新闻的作用是报道事件，真相的作用是揭露隐藏的事实，将它们相互关联，并描绘出一幅人们可以采取行动的现实图景。只有在社会条件变得可识别和可衡量的时候，真相和新闻才会重合。这只是整个人类兴趣领域中相对较小的一部分。在这个领域，也只有在这个领域，对新闻的检验才足够准确，足以使歪曲或压制的指控不仅仅是党派判断。报纸六次声称列宁已死，而报纸所掌握的唯一信息是一份来自一个一再被证明不可靠的消息来源的关于他已死的报道，这没有任何辩护、任何减轻罪责的理由、任何借口。在这种情况下，新闻不是“列宁死了”，而是“赫尔辛基说列宁死了”。报纸可以被要求承担责任，不让列宁的死讯超过新闻来源的可靠性；如果说编辑最有责任心的话，那就是他们对消息来源可靠性的判断。但是，当涉及到处理俄罗斯人民想要什么的故事时，就没有这样的标准了。

The hypothesis, which seems to me the most fertile, is that news and truth are not the same thing, and must be clearly distinguished. The function of news is to signalize an event, the function of truth is to bring to light the hidden facts, to set them into relation with each other, and make a picture of reality on which men can act. Only at those points, where social conditions take recognizable and measurable shape, do the body of truth and the body of news coincide. That is a comparatively small part of the whole field of human interest. In this sector, and only in this sector, the tests of the news are sufficiently exact to make the charges of perversion or suppression more than a partisan judgment. There is no defense, no extenuation, no excuse whatever, for stating six times that Lenin is dead, when the only information the paper possesses is a report that he is dead from a source repeatedly shown to be unreliable. The news, in that instance, is not "Lenin Dead" but "Helsingfors Says Lenin is Dead." And a newspaper can be asked to take the responsibility of not making Lenin more dead than the source of the news is reliable; if there is one subject on which editors are most responsible it is in their judgment of the reliability of the source. But when it comes to dealing, for example, with stories of what the Russian people want, no such test exists.

我认为，缺乏这些精确的测试，是新闻职业的本质所在，其他任何解释都无法解释。新闻职业需要的精确知识非常少，不需要出色的能力或训练就能掌握。其余的则由新闻工作者自行决定。一旦新闻工作者离开县书记官办公室明确记录的约翰·史密斯破产的区域，所有固定的标准就都消失了。约翰·史密斯失败的原因、他的人性弱点、导致他破产的经济状况的分析，所有这些都可以用一百种不同的方式来讲述。应用心理学没有一门学科，就像医学、工程学甚至法律中有一门学科一样，在新闻工作者从新闻转向模糊的真相领域时，它有权指导他的思想。没有准则来指导他自己的思想，也没有准则来强迫读者或出版商做出判断。他对真相的看法只是他自己的看法。他如何能证明他所看到的真相呢？他无法证明这一点，就像辛克莱·刘易斯先生无法证明自己说出了有关大街的全部真相一样。他越了解自己的弱点，就越愿意承认，在没有客观检验的情况下，他自己的观点在某种程度上是基于他自己的刻板印象、按照他自己的准则以及他自己兴趣的紧迫性而构建的。他知道自己是通过主观的视角看待世界的。他无法否认，正如雪莱所说，他也是一座五彩缤纷的玻璃穹顶，玷污了永恒的白色光芒。

The absence of these exact tests accounts, I think, for the character of the profession, as no other explanation does. There is a very small body of exact knowledge, which it requires no outstanding ability or training to deal with. The rest is in the journalist's own discretion. Once he departs from the region where it is definitely recorded at the County Clerk's office that John Smith has gone into bankruptcy, all fixed standards disappear. The story of why John Smith failed, his human frailties, the analysis of the economic conditions on which he was shipwrecked, all of this can be told in a hundred different ways. There is no discipline in applied psychology, as there is a discipline in medicine, engineering, or even law, which has authority to direct the journalist's mind when he passes from the news to the vague realm of truth. There are no canons to direct his own mind, and no canons that coerce the reader's judgment or the publisher's. His version of the truth is only his version. How can he demonstrate the truth as he sees it? He cannot demonstrate it, any more than Mr. Sinclair Lewis can demonstrate that he has told the whole truth about Main Street. And the more he understands his own weaknesses, the more ready he is to admit that where there is no objective test, his own opinion is in some vital measure constructed out of his own stereotypes, according to his own code, and by the urgency of his own interest. He knows that he is seeing the world through subjective lenses. He cannot deny that he too is, as Shelley remarked, a dome of many-colored glass which stains the white radiance of eternity.

正是由于这种认识，他的自信才得以缓和。他可能拥有各种道德勇气，有时确实如此，但他缺乏对某种技术的坚定信念，而正是这种技术最终将物理科学从神学控制中解放出来。正是逐渐发展出一种不可辩驳的方法，才使物理学家获得了与世界所有权力相对抗的思想自由。他的证据如此清晰，他的证据如此明显优于传统，以至于他最终摆脱了一切控制。但记者在自己的良心或事实上没有这样的支持。雇主和读者的意见对他施加的控制，不是偏见对真理的控制，而是一种意见对另一种意见的控制，而后者显然并不不那么真实。在加里法官断言工会将摧毁美国机构与冈珀先生断言工会是人权机构之间，选择在很大程度上必须由信仰的意愿来支配。

And by this knowledge his assurance is tempered. He may have all kinds of moral courage, and sometimes has, but he lacks that sustaining conviction of a certain technic which finally freed the physical sciences from theological control. It was the gradual development of an irrefragable method that gave the physicist his intellectual freedom as against all the powers of the world. His proofs were so clear, his evidence so sharply superior to tradition, that he broke away finally from all control. But the journalist has no such support in his own conscience or in fact. The control exercised over him by the opinions of his employers and his readers, is not the control of truth by prejudice, but of one opinion by another opinion that it is not demonstrably less true. Between Judge Gary's assertion that the unions will destroy American institutions, and Mr. Gomper's assertion that they are agencies of the rights of man, the choice has, in large measure, to be governed by the will to believe.

平息这些争议，并将它们降到可以作为新闻报道的程度，这不是记者能够完成的任务。记者有可能也有必要让人们认识到他们的观点所依据的真相的不确定性，并通过批评和鼓动，促使社会科学对社会事实做出更有用的表述，并促使政治家建立更明显的机构。换句话说，新闻界可以为扩大可报道的真相而斗争。但是，由于当今社会真相的组织方式，新闻界无法从一期到下一期提供民主舆论理论所要求的知识量。这并不是由于激进报纸的新闻质量所显示的“黄铜支票”，而是由于新闻界面对的是一个统治力量记录不完善的社会。新闻界本身可以记录这些力量的理论是错误的。它通常只能记录机构运作为其记录的内容。其余一切都是争论和观点，随着人类心灵的变迁、自我意识和勇气而波动。

The task of deflating these controversies, and reducing them to a point where they can be reported as news, is not a task which the reporter can perform. It is possible and necessary for journalists to bring home to people the uncertain character of the truth on which their opinions are founded, and by criticism and agitation to prod social science into making more usable formulations of social facts, and to prod statesmen into establishing more visible institutions. The press, in other words, can fight for the extension of reportable truth. But as social truth is organized to-day, the press is not constituted to furnish from one edition to the next the amount of knowledge which the democratic theory of public opinion demands. This is not due to the Brass Check, as the quality of news in radical papers shows, but to the fact that the press deals with a society in which the governing forces are so imperfectly recorded. The theory that the press can itself record those forces is false. It can normally record only what has been recorded for it by the working of institutions. Everything else is argument and opinion, and fluctuates with the vicissitudes, the self-consciousness, and the courage of the human mind.

如果新闻界并非如辛克莱先生所言，普遍邪恶，阴谋诡计多端，那么它就比民主理论迄今承认的要脆弱得多。它太脆弱了，无法承担人民主权的全部重担，无法自发提供民主人士所希望的与生俱来的真相。当我们期望它提供这样一种真相时，我们采用的判断标准是错误的。我们误解了新闻的有限性和社会的无限复杂性；我们高估了自己的忍耐力、公共精神和全面的能力。我们假设人们对无趣的真相有胃口，而任何诚实分析我们自己的品味都无法发现这种胃口。

If the press is not so universally wicked, nor so deeply conspiring, as Mr. Sinclair would have us believe, it is very much more frail than the democratic theory has as yet admitted. It is too frail to carry the whole burden of popular sovereignty, to supply spontaneously the truth which democrats hoped was inborn. And when we expect it to supply such a body of truth we employ a misleading standard of judgment. We misunderstand the limited nature of news, the illimitable complexity of society; we overestimate our own endurance, public spirit, and all-round competence. We suppose an appetite for uninteresting truths which is not discovered by any honest analysis of our own tastes.

那么，如果报纸要承担起传达人类整个公共生活的责任，以便每个成年人都能对每个有争议的话题发表意见，那么它们就失败了，注定会失败，而且可以想象，它们在未来的任何时间都将继续失败。我们不可能假设一个由劳动分工和权力分配所驱动的世界能够由全民普遍意见所统治。这种理论在不知不觉中将单个读者设定为理论上无所不能的人，并让媒体承担起完成代议制政府、工业组织和外交未能完成的任务。在二十四小时内，媒体对每个人施加三十分钟的影响，被要求创造一种名为舆论的神秘力量，以弥补公共机构的不足。媒体常常错误地假装它能够做到这一点。它付出了巨大的道德代价，鼓励民主仍然局限于其原有的前提，期望报纸自发地为每一个政府机构、每一个社会问题提供信息机制，而这些机制通常不会自己提供。机构未能为自己提供知识工具，已成为一堆“问题”，而这些问题应该由全体民众、全体读者来解决。

If the newspapers, then, are to be charged with the duty of translating the whole public life of mankind, so that every adult can arrive at an opinion on every moot topic, they fail, they are bound to fail, in any future one can conceive they will continue to fail. It is not possible to assume that a world, carried on by division of labor and distribution of authority, can be governed by universal opinions in the whole population. Unconsciously the theory sets up the single reader as theoretically omnicompetent, and puts upon the press the burden of accomplishing whatever representative government, industrial organization, and diplomacy have failed to accomplish. Acting upon everybody for thirty minutes in twenty-four hours, the press is asked to create a mystical force called Public Opinion that will take up the slack in public institutions. The press has often mistakenly pretended that it could do just that. It has at great moral cost to itself, encouraged a democracy, still bound to its original premises, to expect newspapers to supply spontaneously for every organ of government, for every social problem, the machinery of information which these do not normally supply themselves. Institutions, having failed to furnish themselves with instruments of knowledge, have become a bundle of "problems," which the population as a whole, reading the press as a whole, is supposed to solve.

换言之，新闻界已被视为直接民主的机构，其职责范围更广，而且日复一日地承担着通常归因于创议、全民公决和罢免的职能。舆论法庭日夜开放，随时为一切事物制定法律。这是行不通的。当你考虑到新闻的性质时，这甚至不可想象。因为，正如我们所见，新闻的精确性与事件记录的精确性成正比。除非事件能够被命名、衡量、塑造和具体化，否则它要么无法呈现新闻的特征，要么会受到观察的偶然性和偏见的影响。

The press, in other words, has come to be regarded as an organ of direct democracy, charged on a much wider scale, and from day to day, with the function often attributed to the initiative, referendum, and recall. The Court of Public Opinion, open day and night, is to lay down the law for everything all the time. It is not workable. And when you consider the nature of news, it is not even thinkable. For the news, as we have seen, is precise in proportion to the precision with which the event is recorded. Unless the event is capable of being named, measured, given shape, made specific, it either fails to take on the character of news, or it is subject to the accidents and prejudices of observation.

因此，总体而言，有关现代社会的新闻质量是其社会组织的一个指标。制度越好，所有相关利益就越多地得到正式代表，问题越能得到理清，引入的客观标准越多，事件就越能完美地呈现为新闻。在最好的情况下，新闻界是制度的仆人和守护者；在最坏的情况下，它只是少数人利用社会混乱来达到自己目的的一种手段。在制度无法发挥作用的程度上，不道德的记者可能会浑水摸鱼，而有良心的记者则必须冒着不确定性的风险进行赌博。

Therefore, on the whole, the quality of the news about modern society is an index of its social organization. The better the institutions, the more all interests concerned are formally represented, the more issues are disentangled, the more objective criteria are introduced, the more perfectly an affair can be presented as news. At its best the press is a servant and guardian of institutions; at its worst it is a means by which a few exploit social disorganization to their own ends. In the degree to which institutions fail to function, the unscrupulous journalist can fish in troubled waters, and the conscientious one must gamble with uncertainties.

报刊不能代替机构。它就像探照灯的光束，不停地移动，把一个又一个事件从黑暗中带入视野。人们不能仅凭这束光来完成世界的工作。他们不能通过事件、事件和爆发来统治社会。只有当他们靠自己稳定的光来工作时，报刊在他们身上时，才能揭示出一种足够清晰的形势，以便做出民意决定。问题比报刊更深，解决办法也是如此。它存在于基于分析和记录系统的社会组织中，以及该原则的所有推论中；存在于放弃全能公民理论中，存在于决策分散中，存在于通过可比记录和分析来协调决策中。如果在管理中心有一个运行审计，使那些做这项工作的人和那些监督这项工作的人能够理解工作，那么当问题出现时，就不仅仅是盲人的碰撞了。然后，新闻也是通过情报系统向新闻界披露的，而情报系统同时也对新闻界进行了制约。

The press is no substitute for institutions. It is like the beam of a searchlight that moves restlessly about, bringing one episode and then another out of darkness into vision. Men cannot do the work of the world by this light alone. They cannot govern society by episodes, incidents, and eruptions. It is only when they work by a steady light of their own, that the press, when it is turned upon them, reveals a situation intelligible enough for a popular decision. The trouble lies deeper than the press, and so does the remedy. It lies in social organization based on a system of analysis and record, and in all the corollaries of that principle; in the abandonment of the theory of the omnicompetent citizen, in the decentralization of decision, in the coordination of decision by comparable record and analysis. If at the centers of management there is a running audit, which makes work intelligible to those who do it, and those who superintend it, issues when they arise are not the mere collisions of the blind. Then, too, the news is uncovered for the press by a system of intelligence that is also a check upon the press.

这是激进的做法。因为媒体的麻烦，就像代议制政府（无论是领土型还是功能型政府）的麻烦，就像资本主义、合作型还是共产主义工业的麻烦，都源于一个共同的根源：自治的人民未能通过发明、创造和组织知识机制来超越他们的偶然经验和偏见。正是因为他们被迫在没有可靠的世界观的情况下采取行动，政府、学校、报纸和教会才在对抗民主的更明显缺陷、对抗暴力偏见、冷漠、偏爱奇异琐事而非枯燥重要事物以及对杂耍和三条腿小牛的渴望方面取得了如此微小的进展。这是民选政府的主要缺陷，是其传统中固有的缺陷，我相信，它的所有其他缺陷都可以追溯到这一点。

That is the radical way. For the troubles of the press, like the troubles of representative government, be it territorial or functional, like the troubles of industry, be it capitalist, cooperative, or communist, go back to a common source: to the failure of self-governing people to transcend their casual experience and their prejudice, by inventing, creating, and organizing a machinery of knowledge. It is because they are compelled to act without a reliable picture of the world, that governments, schools, newspapers and churches make such small headway against the more obvious failings of democracy, against violent prejudice, apathy, preference for the curious trivial as against the dull important, and the hunger for sideshows and three legged calves. This is the primary defect of popular government, a defect inherent in its traditions, and all its other defects can, I believe, be traced to this one.

第八部分：组织情报

PART VIII: ORGANIZED INTELLIGENCE

第二十五章

CHAPTER XXV

进入楔形

THE ENTERING WEDGE





1

1

如果补救措施有趣，查尔斯·麦卡锡、罗伯特·瓦伦丁和弗雷德里克·W·泰勒等美国先驱者就不必如此努力地争取听证会了。但他们为什么要斗争，以及为什么政府研究、工业审计、预算等机构是改革中的丑小鸭，这是很清楚的。他们逆转了有趣的公众意见形成的过程。他们没有呈现一个偶然的事实、一大堆刻板印象和戏剧性的认同，而是打破了戏剧，打破了刻板印象，为人们提供了一幅事实的图景，这对他们来说是陌生的，也是非个人化的。当这并不痛苦时，它就会变得乏味，而那些感到痛苦的人，即贸易政客和有很多事情要隐瞒的党派人士，往往会利用公众感到的乏味，以消除他们感到的痛苦。

If the remedy were interesting, American pioneers like Charles McCarthy, Robert Valentine, and Frederick W. Taylor would not have had to fight so hard for a hearing. But it is clear why they had to fight, and why bureaus of governmental research, industrial audits, budgeting and the like are the ugly ducklings of reform. They reverse the process by which interesting public opinions are built up. Instead of presenting a casual fact, a large screen of stereotypes, and a dramatic identification, they break down the drama, break through the stereotypes, and offer men a picture of facts, which is unfamiliar and to them impersonal. When this is not painful, it is dull, and those to whom it is painful, the trading politician and the partisan who has much to conceal, often exploit the dullness that the public feels, in order to remove the pain that they feel.





2

2

然而，每一个复杂的社会都寻求过特殊人物、占卜者、牧师、长老的帮助。我们自己的民主，虽然是建立在普遍能力理论的基础上的，也寻求过律师来管理政府，帮助管理工业。人们认识到，受过专门训练的人在某种程度上比业余爱好者头脑中自发产生的真理体系更倾向于更广泛的真理体系。但经验表明，传统律师的装备不足以提供帮助。大社会通过应用技术知识，迅速发展到庞大的规模。它是由学会使用精确测量和定量分析的工程师建造的。人们开始发现，它不能由那些对是非进行推理思考的人来管理。它只能由创造它的技术来控制。然后，逐渐地，更开明的指导思想者开始聘请受过训练或自己受过训练的专家，让管理这个大社会的人能够理解这个大社会的某些部分。这些人有各种各样的称谓，比如统计员、会计师、审计师、工业顾问、各种工程师、科学经理、人事管理员、研究人员、“科学家”，有时他们也被称为普通的私人秘书。他们各自都带来了自己的专业术语，还有文件柜、卡片目录、图表、活页小玩意，最重要的是，他们身上都体现了完美理想的高管形象：坐在一张平顶办公桌前，面前放着一张打字纸，就以随时可以让他拒绝或批准的形式呈现的政策问题做出决定。

Yet every complicated community has sought the assistance of special men, of augurs, priests, elders. Our own democracy, based though it was on a theory of universal competence, sought lawyers to manage its government, and to help manage its industry. It was recognized that the specially trained man was in some dim way oriented to a wider system of truth than that which arises spontaneously in the amateur's mind. But experience has shown that the traditional lawyer's equipment was not enough assistance. The Great Society had grown furiously and to colossal dimensions by the application of technical knowledge. It was made by engineers who had learned to use exact measurements and quantitative analysis. It could not be governed, men began to discover, by men who thought deductively about rights and wrongs. It could be brought under human control only by the technic which had created it. Gradually, then, the more enlightened directing minds have called in experts who were trained, or had trained themselves, to make parts of this Great Society intelligible to those who manage it. These men are known by all kinds of names, as statisticians, accountants, auditors, industrial counsellors, engineers of many species, scientific managers, personnel administrators, research men, "scientists," and sometimes just as plain private secretaries. They have brought with them each a jargon of his own, as well as filing cabinets, card catalogues, graphs, loose-leaf contraptions, and above all the perfectly sound ideal of an executive who sits before a flat-top desk, one sheet of typewritten paper before him, and decides on matters of policy presented in a form ready for his rejection or approval.

整个发展过程与其说是自发的创造性进化，倒不如说是盲目的自然选择。政治家、行政人员、政党领袖、志愿协会的负责人发现，如果他一天要讨论二十多个不同的主题，就必须有人指导他。他开始吵着要备忘录。他发现自己读不懂邮件。他要求有人用铅笔勾掉重要信件中有趣的句子。他发现自己无法消化桌上堆积如山的打字报告。他要求摘要。他发现自己读不懂一连串没完没了的数字。他拥抱了那些给这些数字制作彩色图片的人。他发现自己真的分不清机器与机器。他雇佣工程师挑选机器，告诉他它们的价格和用途。他卸下了一个又一个负担，就像一个人在努力搬动笨重的负载时，先脱下帽子，然后脱下外套，然后脱下衣领一样。

This whole development has been the work, not so much of a spontaneous creative evolution, as of blind natural selection. The statesman, the executive, the party leader, the head of a voluntary association, found that if he had to discuss two dozen different subjects in the course of the day, somebody would have to coach him. He began to clamor for memoranda. He found he could not read his mail. He demanded somebody who would blue-pencil the interesting sentences in the important letters. He found he could not digest the great stacks of type-written reports that grew mellow on his desk. He demanded summaries. He found he could not read an unending series of figures. He embraced the man who made colored pictures of them. He found that he really did not know one machine from another. He hired engineers to pick them, and tell him how much they cost and what they could do. He peeled off one burden after another, as a man will take off first his hat, then his coat, then his collar, when he is struggling to move an unwieldy load.





3

3

然而奇怪的是，尽管他知道自己需要帮助，但他迟迟没有向社会科学家求助。化学家、物理学家、地质学家受到的欢迎要早得多，也更友好。他们设立了实验室，并提供了诱因，因为他们很快就意识到战胜自然的胜利。但以人性为问题的科学家则不同。原因有很多：最主要的是，他几乎没有什么胜利可展示。他之所以如此少，是因为除非他处理历史，否则他无法在向公众提供理论之前证明自己的理论。物理学家可以提出假设，进行测试，数百次修改假设，如果经过所有这些，他错了，没有人需要为此付出代价。但社会科学家无法提供实验室测试的保证，如果听从了他的建议，结果错了，后果可能是无法估量的。从本质上讲，他要承担更大的责任，也更不确定。

Yet curiously enough, though he knew that he needed help, he was slow to call in the social scientist. The chemist, the physicist, the geologist, had a much earlier and more friendly reception. Laboratories were set up for them, inducements offered, for there was quick appreciation of the victories over nature. But the scientist who has human nature as his problem is in a different case. There are many reasons for this: the chief one, that he has so few victories to exhibit. He has so few, because unless he deals with the historic past, he cannot prove his theories before offering them to the public. The physical scientist can make an hypothesis, test it, revise the hypothesis hundreds of times, and, if after all that, he is wrong, no one else has to pay the price. But the social scientist cannot begin to offer the assurance of a laboratory test, and if his advice is followed, and he is wrong, the consequences may be incalculable. He is in the nature of things far more responsible, and far less certain.

但不仅如此。在实验科学中，学生已经克服了思想和行动的两难境地。他将行动样本带到一个安静的地方，在那里可以随意重复，并在闲暇时进行检查。但社会科学家却经常陷入两难境地。如果他呆在图书馆里，有闲暇思考，他就必须依靠通过官方报告、报纸和采访得到的极其随意和贫乏的印刷记录。如果他走进正在发生事情的“世界”，他必须经历一段漫长的、往往是浪费时间的学徒期，才能被允许进入正在做出决定的圣殿。他不能做的是，只要适合他，就立即行动，然后又退出。没有特权听众。实务人士观察到，社会科学家只是从外部了解他所知道的事情，至少部分是从内部了解，认识到社会科学家的假设不是能够通过实验室证明的事物的本质，而且只有在“现实”世界中才有可能得到验证，因此，对那些不同意他的公共政策观点的社会科学家的评价相当低。

But more than that. In the laboratory sciences the student has conquered the dilemma of thought and action. He brings a sample of the action to a quiet place, where it can be repeated at will, and examined at leisure. But the social scientist is constantly being impaled on a dilemma. If he stays in his library, where he has the leisure to think, he has to rely upon the exceedingly casual and meager printed record that comes to him through official reports, newspapers, and interviews. If he goes out into "the world" where things are happening, he has to serve a long, often wasteful, apprenticeship, before he is admitted to the sanctum where they are being decided. What he cannot do is to dip into action and out again whenever it suits him. There are no privileged listeners. The man of affairs, observing that the social scientist knows only from the outside what he knows, in part at least, from the inside, recognizing that the social scientist's hypothesis is not in the nature of things susceptible of laboratory proof, and that verification is possible only in the "real" world, has developed a rather low opinion of social scientists who do not share his views of public policy.

社会科学家在内心深处也这样评价自己。他对自己的工作缺乏内在的确定性。他只是半信半疑，而且由于什么都不确定，他找不到任何令人信服的理由来坚持自己的思想自由。根据他自己的良心，他究竟能为此主张什么呢？他所获得的数据不确定，他缺乏验证手段。他身上最优秀的品质也令人沮丧。因为如果他真的具有批判精神和科学精神，他就不可能成为教条主义者，为了一个他不确定的理论而与校董、学生、公民联合会和保守派媒体进行世界末日决战。如果你要走向世界末日决战，你就必须为上帝而战，但政治学家总是有点怀疑上帝是否召唤了他。

In his heart of hearts the social scientist shares this estimate of himself. He has little inner certainty about his own work. He only half believes in it, and being sure of nothing, he can find no compelling reason for insisting on his own freedom of thought. What can he actually claim for it, in the light of his own conscience? His data are uncertain, his means of verification lacking. The very best qualities in him are a source of frustration. For if he is really critical and saturated in the scientific spirit, he cannot be doctrinaire, and go to Armageddon against the trustees and the students and the Civic Federation and the conservative press for a theory of which he is not sure. If you are going to Armageddon, you have to battle for the Lord, but the political scientist is always a little doubtful whether the Lord called him.

因此，如果社会科学如此多的内容是辩护性的而非建设性的，那么解释就在于社会科学的机会，而不是“资本主义”。物理学家通过制定出一种能够得出无法压制或忽视的结论的方法，摆脱了教权主义。他们说服了自己，获得了尊严，并且知道他们在为何而战。社会科学家在制定出自己的方法后，将获得尊严和力量。他将通过把大社会领导者对分析工具的需求转化为机会来做到这一点，通过分析工具，一种看不见的、可理解的现象得以显现。

Consequently if so much of social science is apologetic rather than constructive, the explanation lies in the opportunities of social science, not in "capitalism." The physical scientists achieved their freedom from clericalism by working out a method that produced conclusions of a sort that could not be suppressed or ignored. They convinced themselves and acquired dignity, and knew what they were fighting for. The social scientist will acquire his dignity and his strength when he has worked out his method. He will do that by turning into opportunity the need among directing men of the Great Society for instruments of analysis by which an invisible and made intelligible.

但就目前的情况来看，社会科学家从大量不相关的材料中收集数据。社会过程是断断续续地记录下来的，通常是作为行政事故。一份提交给国会的报告、一场辩论、一项调查、一份法律摘要、一份人口普查、一项关税、一份税表；这些材料，就像皮尔当人的头骨一样，必须通过巧妙的推理拼凑起来，学生才能对他所研究的事件有任何印象。虽然它涉及同胞的有意识生活，但它往往令人沮丧地晦涩难懂，因为试图概括的人几乎没有监督他的数据收集方式。想象一下，医学研究是由那些很少去医院、被剥夺动物实验机会、被迫从病人的故事、护士的报告（每个护士都有自己的诊断系统）和国内税收局编制的关于药剂师超额利润的统计数据中得出结论的学生进行的。社会科学家通常必须从执行法律的官员或试图辩护、说服、主张或证明的官员头脑中不加批判地形成的范畴中找出他能做的。学生知道这一点，为了防止这种情况发生，他们发展了学术研究的这一分支，即对哪些地方可以忽略自己的信息进行了精心的怀疑。

But as things go now, the social scientist assembles his data out of a mass of unrelated material. Social processes are recorded spasmodically, quite often as accidents of administration. A report to Congress, a debate, an investigation, legal briefs, a census, a tariff, a tax schedule; the material, like the skull of the Piltdown man, has to be put together by ingenious inference before the student obtains any sort of picture of the event he is studying. Though it deals with the conscious life of his fellow citizens, it is all too often distressingly opaque, because the man who is trying to generalize has practically no supervision of the way his data are collected. Imagine medical research conducted by students who could rarely go into a hospital, were deprived of animal experiment, and compelled to draw conclusions from the stories of people who had been ill, the reports of nurses, each of whom had her own system of diagnosis, and the statistics compiled by the Bureau of Internal Revenue on the excess profits of druggists. The social scientist has usually to make what he can out of categories that were uncritically in the mind of an official who administered some part of a law, or who was out to justify, to persuade, to claim, or to prove. The student knows this, and, as a protection against it, has developed that branch of scholarship which is an elaborated suspicion about where to discount his information.

这是一种美德，但是当它只是对社会科学不健康立场的一种纠正时，它就变得非常单薄了。因为学者注定要尽可能精明地猜测为什么在不清楚的情况下会发生某事或某事。但是，作为代表之间的调解人以及作为管理的镜子和衡量标准的专家，对事实的控制却截然不同。他不再是从行动者提供给他的事实中进行概括的人，而是成为为行动者准备事实的人。这是他战略地位的深刻变化。他不再站在外面，咀嚼忙碌的事务人员提供的东西，而是站在决策的前面而不是后面。今天的顺序是，事务人员找到事实，并根据事实做出决定；然后，一段时间后，社会科学家推断出他做出或没有做出明智决定的极好理由。这种事后关系是学术性的，在这个好词的坏意义上。真正的顺序应该是，公正的专家首先为行动者寻找和表述事实，然后通过对他所理解的决策和他所组织的事实进行比较，做出其所能做出的明智决定。

That is a virtue, but it becomes a very thin virtue when it is merely a corrective for the unwholesome position of social science. For the scholar is condemned to guess as shrewdly as he can why in a situation not clearly understood something or other may have happened. But the expert who is employed as the mediator among representatives, and as the mirror and measure of administration, has a very different control of the facts. Instead of being the man who generalizes from the facts dropped to him by the men of action, he becomes the man who prepares the facts for the men of action. This is a profound change in his strategic position. He no longer stands outside, chewing the cud provided by busy men of affairs, but he takes his place in front of decision instead of behind it. To-day the sequence is that the man of affairs finds his facts, and decides on the basis of them; then, some time later, the social scientist deduces excellent reasons why he did or did not decide wisely. This ex post facto relationship is academic in the bad sense of that fine word. The real sequence should be one where the disinterested expert first finds and formulates the facts for the man of action, and later makes what wisdom he can out of comparison between the decision, which he understands, and the facts, which he organized.





4

4

对于自然科学而言，这种战略地位的变化开始缓慢，然后迅速加速。曾经有一段时间，发明家和工程师是浪漫的、半饥不饱的局外人，被当作怪人对待。商人和工匠知道他们手艺的所有奥秘。然后这些奥秘变得更加神秘，最后工业开始依赖于肉眼无法看到、只有受过训练的头脑才能想象的物理定律和化学组合。科学家从拉丁区的高贵阁楼搬进了办公楼和实验室。因为只有他才能构建出工业所依赖的现实的工作形象。从这种新的关系中，他得到的和付出的一样多，也许更多：纯科学的发展速度比应用科学快，尽管它的经济支持、大量灵感，甚至更多的相关性，都来自与实际决策的不断接触。但自然科学仍然受到巨大的限制，即决策者只能依靠常识来指导他们。他们在没有科学帮助的情况下管理着一个被科学家复杂化的世界。他们再次不得不处理他们无法理解的事实，正如他们曾经不得不请工程师一样，现在他们不得不请统计学家、会计师和各种各样的专家。

For the physical sciences this change in strategic position began slowly, and then accelerated rapidly. There was a time when the inventor and the engineer were romantic half-starved outsiders, treated as cranks. The business man and the artisan knew all the mysteries of their craft. Then the mysteries grew more mysterious, and at last industry began to depend upon physical laws and chemical combinations that no eye could see, and only a trained mind could conceive. The scientist moved from his noble garret in the Latin Quarter into office buildings and laboratories. For he alone could construct a working image of the reality on which industry rested. From the new relationship he took as much as he gave, perhaps more: pure science developed faster than applied, though it drew its economic support, a great deal of its inspiration, and even more of its relevancy, from constant contact with practical decision. But physical science still labored under the enormous limitation that the men who made decisions had only their commonsense to guide them. They administered without scientific aid a world complicated by scientists. Again they had to deal with facts they could not apprehend, and as once they had to call in engineers, they now have to call in statisticians, accountants, experts of all sorts.

这些实践型的学生是新社会科学的真正先驱。他们“与驱动轮紧密相连”，从科学和行动的这种实践互动中，两者都将受益匪浅：行动通过澄清其信念而受益；信念通过不断的行动检验而受益。我们正处于最初的开端。但如果承认所有大型人类协会形式都必须包含那些会认识到需要专家报告其特定环境的人，那么想象力就有了一个可以发挥作用的前提。我认为，在专家人员之间交换技术和结果时，我们可以看到社会科学实验方法的开始。当每个学区和预算、卫生部门、工厂和关税表成为彼此的知识材料时，可比经验的数量就开始接近真正的实验的规模。在 48 个州、2400 个城市、277,000 所学校、270,000 家制造企业、27,000 个矿场和采石场，只要记录下来并可供查阅，就有丰富的经验。而且，还有机会进行试验和犯错，风险很小，任何合理的假设都可以得到公平的检验，而不会动摇社会的基础。

These practical students are the true pioneers of a new social science. They are "in mesh with the driving wheels" and from this practical engagement of science and action, both will benefit radically: action by the clarification of its beliefs; beliefs by a continuing test in action. We are in the earliest beginnings. But if it is conceded that all large forms of human association must, because of sheer practical difficulty, contain men who will come to see the need for an expert reporting of their particular environment, then the imagination has a premise on which to work. In the exchange of technic and result among expert staffs, one can see, I think, the beginning of experimental method in social science. When each school district and budget, and health department, and factory, and tariff schedule, is the material of knowledge for every other, the number of comparable experiences begins to approach the dimensions of genuine experiment. In forty-eight states, and 2400 cities, and 277,000 school houses, 270,000 manufacturing establishments, 27,000 mines and quarries, there is a wealth of experience, if only it were recorded and available. And there is, too, opportunity for trial and error at such slight risk that any reasonable hypothesis might be given a fair test without shaking the foundations of society.

造成这种分歧的不仅是一些工业主管和一些不得不寻求帮助的政治家，还有市政研究局、立法参考图书馆、企业和工会及公共事业的专门游说团体，还有妇女选民联盟、消费者联盟、制造商协会等志愿组织、数百个行业协会和公民联盟、《国会探照灯》和《调查》等出版物以及普通教育委员会等基金会。但并非所有人都不关心此事。这不是重点。所有这些组织都开始表明，需要在普通公民和他所处的广阔环境之间介入某种形式的专业知识。

The wedge has been driven, not only by some directors of industry and some statesmen who had to have help, but by the bureaus of municipal research, the legislative reference libraries, the specialized lobbies of corporations and trade unions and public causes, and by voluntary organizations like the League of Women Voters, the Consumers' League, the Manufacturers' Associations: by hundreds of trade associations, and citizens' unions; by publications like the Searchlight on Congress and the Survey; and by foundations like the General Education Board. Not all by any means are disinterested. That is not the point. All of them do begin to demonstrate the need for interposing some form of expertness between the private citizen and the vast environment in which he is entangled.

第二十六章

CHAPTER XXVI

情报工作

INTELLIGENCE WORK





1

1

民主的实践已经超越了其理论。因为该理论认为，成年选民共同做出的决定是基于他们内心的意愿。但正如理论上看不见的统治阶层逐渐形成一样，也出现了大量建设性的适应，这些适应在民主的形象中也未得到体现。人们已经找到了代表许多通常看不见的利益和职能的方法。

THE practice of democracy has been ahead of its theory. For the theory holds that the adult electors taken together make decisions out of a will that is in them. But just as there grew up governing hierarchies which were invisible in theory, so there has been a large amount of constructive adaptation, also unaccounted for in the image of democracy. Ways have been found to represent many interests and functions that are normally out of sight.

我们在法院理论中对此最为清楚，我们解释法院的立法权和否决权时，认为有些利益需要保护，而这些利益可能会被民选官员遗忘。但是，人口普查局在统计、分类和关联人、事和变化时，也代表了环境中看不见的因素。地质调查局使矿产资源显而易见，农业部在国家委员会中代表每个农民只看到其中很小一部分的因素。学校当局、关税委员会、领事服务、国内税收局代表了个人、思想和事物，而选举永远不会自动代表这些个人、思想和事物。儿童局是选民通常看不到的一系列利益和职能的代言人，因此无法自发成为选民舆论的一部分。因此，婴儿死亡率的比较统计数据的印刷往往会导致婴儿死亡率的下降。在公布之前，市政官员和选民们并没有在他们心中为这些婴儿留下任何位置。统计数据让这些婴儿的情况显而易见，就像这些婴儿选出一位市议员来表达他们的不满一样。

We are most conscious of this in our theory of the courts, when we explain their legislative powers and their vetoes on the theory that there are interests to be guarded which might be forgotten by the elected officials. But the Census Bureau, when it counts, classifies, and correlates people, things, and changes, is also speaking for unseen factors in the environment. The Geological Survey makes mineral resources evident, the Department of Agriculture represents in the councils of the nation factors of which each farmer sees only an infinitesimal part. School authorities, the Tariff Commission, the consular service, the Bureau of Internal Revenue give representation to persons, ideas, and objects which would never automatically find themselves represented in this perspective by an election. The Children's Bureau is the spokesman of a whole complex of interests and functions not ordinarily visible to the voter, and, therefore, incapable of becoming spontaneously a part of his public opinions. Thus the printing of comparative statistics of infant mortality is often followed by a reduction of the death rate of babies. Municipal officials and voters did not have, before publication, a place in their picture of the environment for those babies. The statistics made them visible, as visible as if the babies had elected an alderman to air their grievances.

美国政府在国务院设有一个远东事务司。它是干什么用的？日本和中国政府都在华盛顿设有大使。难道他们没有资格代表远东发言吗？他们是远东的代表。然而，没有人会否认，通过咨询这些大使，美国政府可以了解它需要了解的所有远东信息。即使他们尽可能坦诚，他们仍然是有限的信息渠道。因此，为了补充这些渠道，我们在东京和北京设有大使馆，在许多地方设有领事代理。我想，还有一些秘密特工。这些人应该将通过远东事务司的报告发送给国务卿。那么，国务卿对远东事务司有什么期望呢？我知道有人希望它花掉拨款。但有些国务卿得不到特殊启示，于是他们向自己的部门寻求帮助。他们最不希望找到的就是一个为美国立场辩护的巧妙论据。

In the State Department the government maintains a Division of Far Eastern Affairs. What is it for? The Japanese and the Chinese Governments both maintain ambassadors in Washington. Are they not qualified to speak for the Far East? They are its representatives. Yet nobody would argue that the American Government could learn all that it needed to know about the Far East by consulting these ambassadors. Supposing them to be as candid as they know how to be, they are still limited channels of information. Therefore, to supplement them we maintain embassies in Tokio and Peking, and consular agents at many points. Also, I assume, some secret agents. These people are supposed to send reports which pass through the Division of Far Eastern Affairs to the Secretary of State. Now what does the Secretary expect of the Division? I know one who expected it to spend its appropriation. But there are Secretaries to whom special revelation is denied, and they turn to their divisions for help. The last thing they expect to find is a neat argument justifying the American position.

他们要求专家们把远东问题带到国务卿的办公桌上，把所有要素都联系起来，就好像国务卿与远东本身接触一样。专家必须翻译、简化、概括，但结果的推论必须适用于东方，而不仅仅是报告的前提。如果国务卿是称职的，他最不能容忍的就是专家们怀疑他们有“政策”。他不想从他们那里知道他们是否喜欢日本对华政策。他想知道不同阶层的中国人、日本人、英国人、法国人、德国人和俄罗斯人对此有何看法，以及他们可能会根据自己的想法做什么。他希望把所有这些情况都反映给他，作为他做决定的基础。该部门越能忠实地代表日本或美国大使或太平洋海岸的参议员和众议员没有代表的东西，他就越能成为一个优秀的国务卿。他可能决定采用太平洋海岸的政策，但他对日本的看法将沿袭日本的立场。

What they demand is that the experts shall bring the Far East to the Secretary's desk, with all the elements in such relation that it is as if he were in contact with the Far East itself. The expert must translate, simplify, generalize, but the inference from the result must apply in the East, not merely on the premises of the report. If the Secretary is worth his salt, the very last thing he will tolerate in his experts is the suspicion that they have a "policy." He does not want to know from them whether they like Japanese policy in China. He wants to know what different classes of Chinese and Japanese, English, Frenchmen, Germans, and Russians, think about it, and what they are likely to do because of what they think. He wants all that represented to him as the basis of his decision. The more faithfully the Division represents what is not otherwise represented, either by the Japanese or American ambassadors, or the Senators and Congressmen from the Pacific coast, the better Secretary of State he will be. He may decide to take his policy from the Pacific Coast, but he will take his view of Japan from Japan.





2

2

世界上最好的外交服务是知识的汇集和政策的控制最完美地分离的，这绝非偶然。战争期间，许多英国大使馆和英国外交部几乎总是有一些人，无论是常任官员还是特别任命的官员，他们都非常成功地忽视了当时盛行的战争思想。他们抛弃了赞成和反对的繁文缛节，抛弃了偏爱的国籍、讨厌的事物和怀揣未发表的演说。他们把这些留给了政治领袖。但在一家美国大使馆，我曾听到一位大使说，他从不向华盛顿报告任何不能让国内人民高兴的事情。他迷住了所有遇到他的人，帮助了许多滞留的战争工人，当他揭幕一座纪念碑时，他表现得非常出色。

It is no accident that the best diplomatic service in the world is the one in which the divorce between the assembling of knowledge and the control of policy is most perfect. During the war in many British Embassies and in the British Foreign Office there were nearly always men, permanent officials or else special appointees, who quite successfully discounted the prevailing war mind. They discarded the rigmarole of being pro and con, of having favorite nationalities, and pet aversions, and undelivered perorations in their bosoms. They left that to the political chiefs. But in an American Embassy I once heard an ambassador say that he never reported anything to Washington which would not cheer up the folks at home. He charmed all those who met him, helped many a stranded war worker, and was superb when he unveiled a monument.

他没有理解专家的权力取决于将自己与决策者分开，取决于他自己对所作的决定毫不关心。像大使一样，采取某种路线并干预决策的人很快就会被忽视。他就是这样，只是问题那一边的又一个。因为当他开始过于关心时，他开始看到他希望看到的东西，而事实上，他不再看到他应该看到的东西。他代表看不见的东西。他代表不是选民的人、不明显的选民职能、看不见的事件、哑巴、未出生的人、事物与人之间的关系。他拥有无形的选民群体。而无形的东西不能用来形成政治多数，因为投票归根结底是力量的考验，是升华的战斗，而专家并不代表眼前的力量。但他可以通过扰乱力量的排列来行使力量。通过使无形变为有形，他为那些运用物质力量的人提供了新的环境，在他们心中植入思想和情感，使他们失去原有的地位，从而以最深刻的方式影响了决策。

He did not understand that the power of the expert depends upon separating himself from those who make the decisions, upon not caring, in his expert self, what decision is made. The man who, like the ambassador, takes a line, and meddles with the decision, is soon discounted. There he is, just one more on that side of the question. For when he begins to care too much, he begins to see what he wishes to see, and by that fact ceases to see what he is there to see. He is there to represent the unseen. He represents people who are not voters, functions of voters that are not evident, events that are out of sight, mute people, unborn people, relations between things and people. He has a constituency of intangibles. And intangibles cannot be used to form a political majority, because voting is in the last analysis a test of strength, a sublimated battle, and the expert represents no strength available in the immediate. But he can exercise force by disturbing the line up of the forces. By making the invisible visible, he confronts the people who exercise material force with a new environment, sets ideas and feelings at work in them, throws them out of position, and so, in the profoundest way, affects the decision.

人们不可能长期以他们知道与他们所设想的环境相矛盾的方式行事。如果他们执意要以某种方式行事，他们就必须重新设想环境，他们必须审查，合理化。但是，如果他们面前有一个如此突出的事实，以至于他们无法解释，那么他们有三种选择。他们可以固执地忽视它，尽管他们会在这个过程中陷入困境，会过度扮演自己的角色并遭遇不幸。他们可以考虑它但拒绝采取行动。他们付出的代价是内心的不适和沮丧。或者，我认为这是最常见的情况，他们会调整自己的整个行为以适应扩大的环境。

Men cannot long act in a way that they know is a contradiction of the environment as they conceive it. If they are bent on acting in a certain way they have to reconceive the environment, they have to censor out, to rationalize. But if in their presence, there is an insistent fact which is so obtrusive that they cannot explain it away, one of three courses is open. They can perversely ignore it, though they will cripple themselves in the process, will overact their part and come to grief. They can take it into account but refuse to act. They pay in internal discomfort and frustration. Or, and I believe this to be the most frequent case, they adjust their whole behavior to the enlarged environment.

认为专家让别人做决定，所以他是一个无能的人，这种想法与经验完全相反。决策中的因素越微妙，专家所拥有的不负责任的权力就越大。而且，他将来肯定会比以前行使更多的权力，因为选民和行政人员越来越无法了解相关事实。所有管理机构都倾向于组织研究和信息机构，这些机构将伸出触角并不断扩张，就像世界上所有军队的情报部门一样。但专家仍然是人。他们将享有权力，他们的诱惑是任命自己为审查员，从而吸收决策的真正职能。除非他们的职能得到正确界定，否则他们往往会传递他们认为合适的事实，并传递他们批准的决定。简而言之，他们往往会成为一个官僚机构。

The idea that the expert is an ineffectual person because he lets others make the decisions is quite contrary to experience. The more subtle the elements that enter into the decision, the more irresponsible power the expert wields. He is certain, moreover, to exercise more power in the future than ever he did before, because increasingly the relevant facts will elude the voter and the administrator. All governing agencies will tend to organize bodies of research and information, which will throw out tentacles and expand, as have the intelligence departments of all the armies in the world. But the experts will remain human beings. They will enjoy power, and their temptation will be to appoint themselves censors, and so absorb the real function of decision. Unless their function is correctly defined they will tend to pass on the facts they think appropriate, and to pass down the decisions they approve. They will tend, in short, to become a bureaucracy.

唯一的制度保障是尽可能将执行人员与调查人员完全分开。这两个机构应该是平行但又截然不同的人员队伍，以不同的方式招募，如果可能的话，从不同的资金中支付工资，对不同的负责人负责，本质上对彼此的个人成功不感兴趣。在工业中，审计师、会计师和检查员应该独立于经理、主管、工头，我相信，随着时间的推移，我们将会看到，为了将工业置于社会控制之下，记录机制必须独立于董事会和股东。

The only institutional safeguard is to separate as absolutely as it is possible to do so the staff which executes from the staff which investigates. The two should be parallel but quite distinct bodies of men, recruited differently, paid if possible from separate funds, responsible to different heads, intrinsically uninterested in each other's personal success. In industry, the auditors, accountants, and inspectors should be independent of the manager, the superintendents, foremen, and in time, I believe, we shall come to see that in order to bring industry under social control the machinery of record will have to be independent of the boards of directors and the shareholders.





3

3

但在建立工业和政治情报部门时，我们并非从一片空白开始。而且，除了坚持这种基本的职能分离外，过于精确地坚持该原则在任何特定情况下应采取的形式也是很麻烦的。有些人相信情报工作，并会采纳它；有些人不理解它，但没有它就无法开展工作；有些人会抵制它。但只要该原则在每个社会机构的某个地方都有立足之地，它就会取得进展，而开始的方式就是开始。例如，在联邦政府中，没有必要理清行政混乱和一个世纪发展中不合逻辑的重复，以便为华盛顿急需的情报局找到一个整洁的地方。在选举之前，你可以承诺勇敢地冲进缺口。但当你气喘吁吁地到达那里时，你会发现每一个荒谬之处都带有习惯、强烈的利益和亲密的国会议员。从各个方面发起攻击，你就会与每一种反动力量交战。正如诗人所说，你上战场，你总会倒下。你可以在这里砍掉一个过时的局，在那里砍掉一群职员，你可以合并两个局。到那时，你就会忙于关税和铁路，改革时代就结束了。此外，为了实现真正合乎逻辑的政府改组，正如所有候选人总是承诺的那样，你必须激起比你平息的更多的激情。任何新的计划，假设你已经准备好了，都需要官员来执行。不管人们对公职人员有什么看法，即使是苏维埃俄罗斯也很高兴能把许多老官员带回来；如果这些老官员受到太无情的对待，就会破坏乌托邦本身。

But in building the intelligence sections of industry and politics, we do not start on cleared ground. And, apart from insisting on this basic separation of function, it would be cumbersome to insist too precisely on the form which in any particular instance the principle shall take. There are men who believe in intelligence work, and will adopt it; there are men who do not understand it, but cannot do their work without it; there are men who will resist. But provided the principle has a foothold somewhere in every social agency it will make progress, and the way to begin is to begin. In the federal government, for example, it is not necessary to straighten out the administrative tangle and the illogical duplications of a century's growth in order to find a neat place for the intelligence bureaus which Washington so badly needs. Before election you can promise to rush bravely into the breach. But when you arrive there all out of breath, you find that each absurdity is invested with habits, strong interests, and chummy Congressmen. Attack all along the line and you engage every force of reaction. You go forth to battle, as the poet said, and you always fall. You can lop off an antiquated bureau here, a covey of clerks there, you can combine two bureaus. And by that time you are busy with the tariff and the railroads, and the era of reform is over. Besides, in order to effect a truly logical reorganization of the government, such as all candidates always promise, you would have to disturb more passions than you have time to quell. And any new scheme, supposing you had one ready, would require officials to man it. Say what one will about officeholders, even Soviet Russia was glad to get many of the old ones back; and these old officials, if they are too ruthlessly treated, will sabotage Utopia itself.

没有善意，任何行政计划都行不通，没有教育，对奇怪做法的善意就不可能实现。更好的方法是，在现有机制中，只要你能找到机会，就引入一些机构，这些机构可以每周、每月照镜子。这样，你就可以希望让机器的操作者、负责的首领和外部公众都能看到它。当官员开始看清自己时——或者更确切地说，当局外人、首领和下属都开始看到同样的事实，如果你愿意的话，同样的谴责事实，阻碍就会减少。改革者认为某个部门效率低下只是他的观点，在部门眼中，这种观点并不像它自己的观点那么好。但是，如果分析和记录该部门的工作，然后与其他部门和私营公司进行比较，争论就会转移到另一个层面。

No administrative scheme is workable without good will, and good will about strange practices is impossible without education. The better way is to introduce into the existing machinery, wherever you can find an opening, agencies that will hold up a mirror week by week, month by month. You can hope, then, to make the machine visible to those who work it, as well as to the chiefs who are responsible, and to the public outside. When the office-holders begin to see themselves,—or rather when the outsiders, the chiefs, and the subordinates all begin to see the same facts, the same damning facts if you like, the obstruction will diminish. The reformer's opinion that a certain bureau is inefficient is just his opinion, not so good an opinion in the eyes of the bureau, as its own. But let the work of that bureau be analysed and recorded, and then compared with other bureaus and with private corporations, and the argument moves to another plane.

华盛顿有十个部门代表内阁。那么假设每个部门都有一个常设情报部门。那么，要达到有效性，需要哪些条件呢？最重要的是，情报官员应该独立于负责该部门的国会委员会和部长；他们不应该卷入决策或行动中。那么，独立性主要取决于三个方面：资金、任期和获取事实的渠道。因为很明显，如果某个国会或部门官员可以剥夺他们的资金、解雇他们或关闭档案，那么工作人员就成了他们的傀儡。

There are ten departments at Washington represented in the Cabinet. Suppose, then, there was a permanent intelligence section for each. What would be some of the conditions of effectiveness? Beyond all others that the intelligence officials should be independent both of the Congressional Committees dealing with that department, and of the Secretary at the head of it; that they should not be entangled either in decision or in action. Independence, then, would turn mainly on three points on funds, tenure, and access to the facts. For clearly if a particular Congress or departmental official can deprive them of money, dismiss them, or close the files, the staff becomes its creature.





4

4

资金问题既重要又困难。如果一个研究机构每年都依赖于国会的救济金，那么它就不可能真正自由，而国会可能嫉妒或吝啬。然而，资金的最终控制权不能从立法机构手中夺走。财务安排应确保工作人员免受左撇子、小丑和骑手攻击，免受狡猾破坏，同时应为增长提供保障。工作人员应该根深蒂固，以至于对其存在的攻击必须公开进行。也许，它可能在联邦宪章的背后工作，设立一个信托基金，并根据情报局所属部门的拨款情况，在几年内按比例浮动。无论如何，这不会涉及大笔资金。信托基金可以支付一定最低限度工作人员的管理费用和资本费用，浮动比例可以支付扩大费用。无论如何，拨款应该像支付任何长期债务一样，避免意外。与通过宪法修正案或发行政府债券相比，这是一种“束缚国会手脚”的不太严重的方法。国会可以废除宪章。但它必须废除它，而不是给它设置障碍。

The question of funds is both important and difficult. No agency of research can be really free if it depends upon annual doles from what may be a jealous or a parsimonious congress. Yet the ultimate control of funds cannot be removed from the legislature. The financial arrangement should insure the staff against left-handed, joker and rider attack, against sly destruction, and should at the same time provide for growth. The staff should be so well entrenched that an attack on its existence would have to be made in the open. It might, perhaps, work behind a federal charter creating a trust fund, and a sliding scale over a period of years based on the appropriation for the department to which the intelligence bureau belonged. No great sums of money are involved anyway. The trust fund might cover the overhead and capital charges for a certain minimum staff, the sliding scale might cover the enlargements. At any rate the appropriation should be put beyond accident, like the payment of any long term obligation. This is a much less serious way of "tying the hands of Congress" than is the passage of a Constitutional amendment or the issuance of government bonds. Congress could repeal the charter. But it would have to repeal it, not throw monkey wrenches into it.

任期应为终身，退休后可领取丰厚的退休金，休假年限用于高级学习和培训，只有在经过专业同事的试用后才能被解雇。适用于任何非盈利性知识分子职业的条件也应适用于此。如果这项工作要引人注目，从事这项工作的人必须有尊严、有保障，至少在高层，还要有思想自由，而这种自由只有在人们不太直接参与实际决策的地方才能找到。

Tenure should be for life, with provision for retirement on a liberal pension, with sabbatical years set aside for advanced study and training, and with dismissal only after a trial by professional colleagues. The conditions which apply to any non-profit-making intellectual career should apply here. If the work is to be salient, the men who do it must have dignity, security, and, in the upper ranks at least, that freedom of mind which you find only where men are not too immediately concerned in practical decision.

组织法中应规定查阅材料的权限。该局应有权审查所有文件，并质询任何官员或局外人。这种持续的调查与现在已成为我们政府常见特征的耸人听闻的立法调查和断断续续的钓鱼调查完全不同。该局应有权向部门提出会计方法建议，如果建议被拒绝或在被接受后遭到违反，则可根据其章程向国会提出上诉。

Access to the materials should be established in the organic act. The bureau should have the right to examine all papers, and to question any official or any outsider. Continuous investigation of this sort would not at all resemble the sensational legislative inquiry and the spasmodic fishing expedition which are now a common feature of our government. The bureau should have the right to propose accounting methods to the department, and if the proposal is rejected, or violated after it has been accepted, to appeal under its charter to Congress.

首先，每个情报局都将成为国会和国防部之间的纽带，在我看来，这种纽带比内阁官员同时出现在众议院和参议院更佳，尽管一个提议绝不会排斥另一个。情报局将成为国会对其政策执行情况的监督。它将成为国防部对国会批评的回应。然后，由于国防部的运作将永远可见，国会也许将不再需要那些因不信任和错误的三权分立原则而产生的细致立法，而这些立法使有效的行政管理变得非常困难。

In the first instance each intelligence bureau would be the connecting link between Congress and the Department, a better link, in my judgment, than the appearance of cabinet officers on the floor of both House and Senate, though the one proposal in no way excludes the other. The bureau would be the Congressional eye on the execution of its policy. It would be the departmental answer to Congressional criticism. And then, since operation of the Department would be permanently visible, perhaps Congress would cease to feel the need of that minute legislation born of distrust and a false doctrine of the separation of powers, which does so much to make efficient administration difficult.





5

5

但是，当然，这十个局不可能各自独立工作。他们之间的相互关系是实现“协调”的最佳机会，而人们对此知之甚多，见之甚少。显然，各参谋部需要尽可能采用可比的测量标准。他们会交换记录。这样，如果陆军部和邮政局都购买木材、雇用木匠或建造砖墙，他们就不必通过同一机构进行，因为这可能意味着繁琐的过度集中；但他们将能够对相同的事情使用相同的衡量标准，意识到比较，并被视为竞争对手。这种竞争越多越好。

But, of course, each of the ten bureaus could not work in a watertight compartment. In their relation one to another lies the best chance for that "coordination" of which so much is heard and so little seen. Clearly the various staffs would need to adopt, wherever possible, standards of measurement that were comparable. They would exchange their records. Then if the War Department and the Post Office both buy lumber, hire carpenters, or construct brick walls they need not necessarily do them through the same agency, for that might mean cumbersome over-centralization; but they would be able to use the same measure for the same things, be conscious of the comparisons, and be treated as competitors. And the more competition of this sort the better.

因为竞争的价值是由衡量竞争的标准的价值决定的。因此，我们不应该问自己是否相信竞争，而应该问自己是否相信竞争者所竞争的东西。没有一个理智的人会希望“废除竞争”，因为当最后一丝竞争的痕迹消失时，社会努力将由机械地服从惯例组成，少数人会受到本土灵感的缓和。然而，没有人希望在每个人与所有人的残酷斗争中将竞争推向其合乎逻辑的结论。问题在于选择竞争的目标和游戏规则。几乎总是最明显、最明显的衡量标准将决定游戏规则：比如金钱、权力、声望、掌声或凡勃伦先生的“炫耀性浪费”。我们的文明通常提供哪些其他衡量标准？它如何衡量我们一直呼吁的效率、生产力、服务？

For the value of competition is determined by the value of the standards used to measure it. Instead, then, of asking ourselves whether we believe in competition, we should ask ourselves whether we believe in that for which the competitors compete. No one in his senses expects to "abolish competition," for when the last vestige of emulation had disappeared, social effort would consist in mechanical obedience to a routine, tempered in a minority by native inspiration. Yet no one expects to work out competition to its logical conclusion in a murderous struggle of each against all. The problem is to select the goals of competition and the rules of the game. Almost always the most visible and obvious standard of measurement will determine the rules of the game: such as money, power, popularity, applause, or Mr. Veblen's "conspicuous waste." What other standards of measurement does our civilization normally provide? How does it measure efficiency, productivity, service, for which we are always clamoring?

总的来说，没有衡量标准，因此，也没有那么多为实现这些理想而进行的竞争。因为高尚动机与低俗动机之间的差异，并不像人们常常声称的那样，是利他主义与自私之间的差异。它是为容易理解的目标而行动，还是为晦涩难懂的目标而行动之间的差异。劝一个人比他的邻居赚取更多的利润，他就知道要瞄准什么。劝他为社会提供更多服务，他怎么能确定什么服务是社会的呢？标准是什么，衡量标准是什么？一种主观的感觉，某人的观点。在和平时期告诉一个人，他应该为国家服务，你说的是一句虔诚的陈词滥调，在战争时期告诉他，服务这个词就有了意义；这是一系列具体的行为，如入伍、购买债券、节省食物或每年工作一美元，他把每一项服务都明确视为一个具体目的的一部分，即在前线部署一支比敌人规模更大、装备更精良的军队。

By and large there are no measures, and there is, therefore, not so much competition to achieve these ideals. For the difference between the higher and the lower motives is not, as men often assert, a difference between altruism and selfishness. It is a difference between acting for easily understood aims, and for aims that are obscure and vague. Exhort a man to make more profit than his neighbor, and he knows at what to aim. Exhort him to render more social service, and how is he to be certain what service is social? What is the test, what is the measure? A subjective feeling, somebody's opinion. Tell a man in time of peace that he ought to serve his country and you have uttered a pious platitude, Tell him in time of war, and the word service has a meaning; it is a number of concrete acts, enlistment, or buying bonds, or saving food, or working for a dollar a year, and each one of these services he sees definitely as part of a concrete purpose to put at the front an army larger and better armed, than the enemy's.

因此，你越能分析管理并找出可比较的要素，你越能为想要提升的品质发明量化指标，你就越能将竞争转化为理想的结果。如果你能设计出正确的指数，你就可以在商店中的个体工人之间、商店之间、工厂之间、学校之间、政府部门之间、军团之间、师之间、船只之间、州之间、县之间、城市之间建立竞争；指数越好，竞争就越有用。

So the more you are able to analyze administration and work out elements that can be compared, the more you invent quantitative measures for the qualities you wish to promote, the more you can turn competition to ideal ends. If you can contrive the right index numbers you can set up a competition between individual workers in a shop; between shops; between factories; between schools; between government departments; between regiments; between divisions; between ships; between states; counties; cities; and the better your index numbers the more useful the competition.





6

6

材料交换的可能性是显而易见的。政府的每个部门都在随时要求获取其他部门可能已经获得的信息，尽管形式可能略有不同。比如说，国务院需要知道墨西哥石油储量的范围、它们与世界其他地区石油供应的关系、墨西哥石油土地的现有所有权、石油对正在建造或计划建造的军舰的重要性、不同领域的比较成本。今天它如何获得这些信息？这些信息可能分散在内政部、司法部、商务部、劳工部和海军部。要么是国务院的一名职员在参考书中查找墨西哥石油，而这些信息可能准确也可能不准确，要么是某人的私人秘书打电话给另一个人的私人秘书，要求提供备忘录，而随着时间的推移，一个黑人信使带着一大堆难以理解的报告到来。国务院应该能够要求自己的情报局以适合于需要解决的外交问题的方式收集事实。外交情报局将从中央清算所获得这些事实。

The possibilities that lie in the exchange of material are evident. Each department of government is all the time asking for information that may already have been obtained by another department, though perhaps in a somewhat different form. The State Department needs to know, let us say, the extent of the Mexican oil reserves, their relation to the rest of the world's supply, the present ownership of Mexican oil lands, the importance of oil to warships now under construction or planned, the comparative costs in different fields. How does it secure such information to-day? The information is probably scattered through the Departments of Interior, Justice, Commerce, Labor and Navy. Either a clerk in the State Department looks up Mexican oil in a book of reference, which may or may not be accurate, or somebody's private secretary telephones somebody else's private secretary, asks for a memorandum, and in the course of time a darkey messenger arrives with an armful of unintelligible reports. The Department should be able to call on its own intelligence bureau to assemble the facts in a way suited to the diplomatic problem up for decision. And these facts the diplomatic intelligence bureau would obtain from the central clearing house.

这个机构很快就会成为最特别的信息中心。里面的人会意识到政府的真正问题是什么。他们将处理定义、术语、统计技术和逻辑问题；他们将具体地涉及整个社会科学领域。很难理解为什么所有这些材料，除了一些外交和军事机密外，不应该向该国的学者公开。正是在那里，政治学家会找到真正的难题和真正的研究成果供他的学生进行。这项工作不必全部在华盛顿完成，但可以参考华盛顿来完成。因此，中央机构将具备一所国立大学的素质。工作人员可以从大学毕业生中招募到局里。他们将研究在国立大学馆长和遍布全国的教师协商后选定的论文。如果该协会具有应有的灵活性，那么作为常任工作人员的补充，大学将不断聘用临时和专业人员，并从华盛顿调来交流讲师。这样，工作人员的培训和招聘就可以同步进行。研究本身的一部分将由学生完成，大学里的政治学将与美国政治联系起来。

This establishment would pretty soon become a focus of information of the most extraordinary kind. And the men in it would be made aware of what the problems of government really are. They would deal with problems of definition, of terminology, of statistical technic, of logic; they would traverse concretely the whole gamut of the social sciences. It is difficult to see why all this material, except a few diplomatic and military secrets, should not be open to the scholars of the country. It is there that the political scientist would find the real nuts to crack and the real researches for his students to make. The work need not all be done in Washington, but it could be done in reference to Washington. The central agency would, thus, have in it the makings of a national university. The staff could be recruited there for the bureaus from among college graduates. They would be working on theses selected after consultation between the curators of the national university and teachers scattered over the country. If the association was as flexible as it ought to be, there would be, as a supplement to the permanent staff, a steady turnover of temporary and specialist appointments from the universities, and exchange lecturers called out from Washington. Thus the training and the recruiting of the staff would go together. A part of the research itself would be done by students, and political science in the universities would be associated with politics in America.





7

7

原则的主要内容同样适用于州政府、城市和农村县。比较和交换工作可以由州、市和县局联盟进行。在这些联盟内，可以组织任何理想的区域组合。只要会计系统具有可比性，就可以避免大量重复。区域协调尤其可取。因为法律边界通常与有效环境不一致。然而，它们有一定的习惯基础，如果打乱它们，代价将不菲。通过协调信息，几个行政区域可以协调决策自主权与合作。例如，纽约市已经是一个难以从市政厅管理的单位。然而，对于许多目的，如健康和交通，大都会区是真正的行政单位。然而，在那个地区，有大城市，如扬克斯、泽西市、帕特森、伊丽莎白、霍博肯、贝永。它们不可能全部由一个中心管理，但它们应该共同发挥作用。最终，也许像西德尼和比阿特丽斯·韦伯所建议的某些地方政府灵活方案可能是合适的解决方案。但第一步是协调，不是决策和行动的协调，而是信息和研究的协调。让各个市政当局的官员根据相同的事实看待他们共同的问题。

In its main outlines the principle is equally applicable to state governments, to cities, and to rural counties. The work of comparison and interchange could take place by federations of state and city and county bureaus. And within those federations any desirable regional combination could be organized. So long as the accounting systems were comparable, a great deal of duplication would be avoided. Regional coordination is especially desirable. For legal frontiers often do not coincide with the effective environments. Yet they have a certain basis in custom that it would be costly to disturb. By coordinating their information several administrative areas could reconcile autonomy of decision with cooperation. New York City, for example, is already an unwieldy unit for good government from the City Hall. Yet for many purposes, such as health and transportation, the metropolitan district is the true unit of administration. In that district, however, there are large cities, like Yonkers, Jersey City, Paterson, Elizabeth, Hoboken, Bayonne. They could not all be managed from one center, and yet they should act together for many functions. Ultimately perhaps some such flexible scheme of local government as Sidney and Beatrice Webb have suggested may be the proper solution. But the first step would be a coordination, not of decision and action, but of information and research. Let the officials of the various municipalities see their common problems in the light of the same facts.





8

8

否认这种政治和工业界情报局网络可能会成为累赘和永久的烦恼是毫无意义的。人们很容易想象它对那些寻找轻松工作的人、学究和爱管闲事的人的吸引力。人们可以看到官僚作风、堆积如山的文件、令人厌烦的问卷、每份文件七份、签注、延误、文件丢失、使用表格 136 而不是表格 2gb、文件被退回，因为用铅笔代替墨水，或者用黑色墨水代替红色墨水。工作可能做得很糟糕。没有万无一失的机构。

It would be idle to deny that such a net work of intelligence bureaus in politics and industry might become a dead weight and a perpetual irritation. One can easily imagine its attraction for men in search of soft jobs, for pedants, for meddlers. One can see red tape, mountains of papers, questionnaires ad nauseam, seven copies of every document, endorsements, delays, lost papers, the use of form 136 instead of form 2gb, the return of the document because pencil was used instead of ink, or black ink instead of red ink. The work could be done very badly. There are no fool-proof institutions.

但是，如果可以假设整个政府部门、工厂、办公室和大学之间都有流通，人员流通、数据流通和批评流通，那么干腐病的风险就不会那么大。说这些情报局会使生活复杂化也不正确。相反，它们会倾向于简化，揭示出现在人类无法处理的复杂性。目前基本上看不见的政府系统是如此复​​杂，以至于大多数人已经放弃尝试去理解它，因为他们不去尝试，所以他们倾向于认为它相对简单。相反，它是难以捉摸的、隐蔽的、不透明的。使用情报系统意味着每单位结果所需的人员减少，因为通过让每个人都能获得各自的经验，它将减少反复试验的次数；并且通过使社会过程可见，它将帮助人员进行自我批评。如果把特别调查委员会、大陪审团、地方检察官、改革组织和困惑的公职人员在试图从一片混乱中找到出路的过程中所花费的时间考虑在内，这并不需要大量额外的官员。

But if one could assume that there was circulation through the whole system between government departments, factories, offices, and the universities; a circulation of men, a circulation of data and of criticism, the risks of dry rot would not be so great. Nor would it be true to say that these intelligence bureaus will complicate life. They will tend, on the contrary, to simplify, by revealing a complexity now so great as to be humanly unmanageable. The present fundamentally invisible system of government is so intricate that most people have given up trying to follow it, and because they do not try, they are tempted to think it comparatively simple. It is, on the contrary, elusive, concealed, opaque. The employment of an intelligence system would mean a reduction of personnel per unit of result, because by making available to all the experience of each, it would reduce the amount of trial and error; and because by making the social process visible, it would assist the personnel to self-criticism. It does not involve a great additional band of officials, if you take into account the time now spent vainly by special investigating committees, grand juries, district attorneys, reform organizations, and bewildered office holders, in trying to find their way through a dark muddle.

如果对民意和民主理论与现代环境关系的分析在原则上是正确的，那么我认为人们无法逃避这样的结论：这种情报工作是改善环境的线索。我指的不是本章中的几条建议。它们只是例证。制定技术的任务掌握在受过训练的人手中，甚至他们今天也无法完全预见形式，更不用说细节了。现在记录的社会现象数量很少，分析工具非常粗糙，概念往往模糊且未经批判。但我认为，已经做了足够多的工作来证明，看不见的环境可以得到有效的报道，可以以一种不影响他们偏见的方式向不同的人群报道，并能够克服他们的主观主义。

If the analysis of public opinion and of the democratic theories in relation to the modern environment is sound in principle, then I do not see how one can escape the conclusion that such intelligence work is the clue to betterment. I am not referring to the few suggestions contained in this chapter. They are merely illustrations. The task of working out the technic is in the hands of men trained to do it, and not even they can to-day completely foresee the form, much less the details. The number of social phenomena which are now recorded is small, the instruments of analysis are very crude, the concepts often vague and uncriticized. But enough has been done to demonstrate, I think, that unseen environments can be reported effectively, that they can be reported to divergent groups of people in a way which is neutral to their prejudice, and capable of overcoming their subjectivism.

如果这是真的，那么在制定智力原则的过程中，人们将找到克服自治的核心困难的方法，即处理看不见的现实的困难。由于这一困难，任何自治社区都不可能调和其孤立的需要与广泛接触的必要性，调和地方决策的尊严和个性与安全和广泛协调，在不牺牲责任的情况下确保有效的领导人，在不试图就所有问题达成普遍的公众意见的情况下获得有用的公众意见。只要没有办法建立看不见的事件的共同版本、单独行动的共同措施，那么唯一可行的民主形象，即使在理论上，也是一种基于一个孤立的社区的民主，根据亚里士多德的著名格言，这些人的政治能力受到视野范围的限制。

If that is true, then in working out the intelligence principle men will find the way to overcome the central difficulty of self-government, the difficulty of dealing with an unseen reality. Because of that difficulty, it has been impossible for any self-governing community to reconcile its need for isolation with the necessity for wide contact, to reconcile the dignity and individuality of local decision with security and wide coordination, to secure effective leaders without sacrificing responsibility, to have useful public opinions without attempting universal public opinions on all subjects. As long as there was no way of establishing common versions of unseen events, common measures for separate actions, the only image of democracy that would work, even in theory, was one based on an isolated community of people whose political faculties were limited, according to Aristotle's famous maxim, by the range of their vision.

但现在有一条出路，虽然路途漫长，但总归是一条出路。这条出路与芝加哥市民（他们的眼睛和耳朵并不比雅典人好）能够远距离看到和听到声音的出路基本相同。今天，减少设想环境与实际环境之间的差异是可能的，如果投入更多的劳动，这种可能性将更大。随着这一目标的实现，联邦制将越来越多地通过同意而不是强制手段发挥作用。因为虽然联邦制是自治团体之间唯一可能的联合方式，但只要联合不是基于正确和普遍接受的联邦事务理念，联邦制就会走向帝国集权或地方无政府状态。这些理念不是自发产生的。必须通过基于分析的概括将它们拼凑起来，并且必须通过研究发明和测试用于分析的工具。

But now there is a way out, a long one to be sure, but a way. It is fundamentally the same way as that which has enabled a citizen of Chicago, with no better eyes or ears than an Athenian, to see and hear over great distances. It is possible to-day, it will become more possible when more labor has gone into it, to reduce the discrepancies between the conceived environment and the effective environment. As that is done, federalism will work more and more by consent, less and less by coercion. For while federalism is the only possible method of union among self-governing groups, federalism swings either towards imperial centralization or towards parochial anarchy wherever the union is not based on correct and commonly accepted ideas of federal matters. These ideas do not arise spontaneously. They have to be pieced together by generalization based on analysis, and the instruments for that analysis have to be invented and tested by research.

任何选举手段、任何选区操纵、任何财产制度的改变都不能触及问题的根源。你不可能从人类身上榨取比他们本身更多的政治智慧。任何改革，无论多么轰动，都是真正激进的，如果它没有自觉地提供一种克服基于个人经验局限性的人类意见主观主义的方法。有些政府、投票和代表制度比其他制度榨取的更多。但最终知识必须不是来自良心，而是来自良心所面对的环境。当人们按照智慧原则行事时，他们会出去寻找事实并创造智慧。当他们忽视它时，他们会进入自己的内心，只发现那里的东西。他们只会加深偏见，而不是增加知识。

No electoral device, no manipulation of areas, no change in the system of property, goes to the root of the matter. You cannot take more political wisdom out of human beings than there is in them. And no reform, however sensational, is truly radical, which does not consciously provide a way of overcoming the subjectivism of human opinion based on the limitation of individual experience. There are systems of government, of voting, and representation which extract more than others. But in the end knowledge must come not from the conscience but from the environment with which that conscience deals. When men act on the principle of intelligence they go out to find the facts and to make their wisdom. When they ignore it, they go inside themselves and find only what is there. They elaborate their prejudice, instead of increasing their knowledge.

第二十七章

CHAPTER XXVII

向公众发出呼吁

THE APPEAL TO THE PUBLIC





1

1

在现实生活中，没有人会按照他可以对每个公共问题发表公众意见的理论行事，尽管这一事实常常被掩盖，因为一个人认为没有公共问题，因为他没有公众意见。但在我们的政治理论中，我们继续比布莱斯勋爵的意图更字面地思考，“舆论的作用是连续的”，即使“它的作用……只涉及广泛的原则”。然后，因为我们试图认为自己有连续的意见，却完全不确定什么是广泛的原则，我们很自然地会以痛苦的哈欠迎接一个似乎需要阅读更多政府报告、更多统计数据、更多曲线和更多图表的争论。因为所有这些首先都和党派言论一样令人困惑，而且更不有趣。

IN real life no one acts on the theory that he can have a public opinion on every public question, though this fact is often concealed where a person thinks there is no public question because he has no public opinion. But in the theory of our politics we continue to think more literally than Lord Bryce intended, that "the action of Opinion is continuous," even though "its action… deals with broad principles only." And then because we try to think of ourselves having continuous opinions, without being altogether certain what a broad principle is, we quite naturally greet with an anguished yawn an argument that seems to involve the reading of more government reports, more statistics, more curves and more graphs. For all these are in the first instance just as confusing as partisan rhetoric, and much less entertaining.

任何计划都无法满足人们的需要，因为人们认为，在阅读了所有情报局的出版物后，全国所有公民都会对大量实际问题保持警惕、知情和热切，而这些问题从来都不能很好地融入任何广泛的原则中。我并不是在做这样的假设。情报局主要是行动者、负责决策的代表和工作人员的工具，如果它不能帮助他们，那么最终对任何人都没有帮助。但是，只要它能帮助他们了解他们所处的工作环境，它就能让他们的工作变得显而易见。这样一来，他们对公众就更加负责了。

The amount of attention available is far too small for any scheme in which it was assumed that all the citizens of the nation would, after devoting themselves to the publications of all the intelligence bureaus, become alert, informed, and eager on the multitude of real questions that never do fit very well into any broad principle. I am not making that assumption. Primarily, the intelligence bureau is an instrument of the man of action, of the representative charged with decision, of the worker at his work, and if it does not help them, it will help nobody in the end. But in so far as it helps them to understand the environment in which they are working, it makes what they do visible. And by that much they become more responsible to the general public.

因此，目的不是让每个公民都背负专家对所有问题的见解，而是将这一负担从公民身上转移到负责任的管理者身上。情报系统当然具有作为一般信息来源和每日新闻制约因素的价值。但那是次要的。它的实际用途是作为政治和工业领域代议制政府和行政管理的辅助。对会计师、统计学家、秘书等专业记者的帮助的需求并非来自公众，而是来自那些不能再凭经验行事的公共事务人员。从本质上讲，情报系统是一种更好地处理公共事务的工具，而不是一种更好地了解公共事务做得有多糟糕的工具。

The purpose, then, is not to burden every citizen with expert opinions on all questions, but to push that burden away from him towards the responsible administrator. An intelligence system has value, of course, as a source of general information, and as a check on the daily press. But that is secondary. Its real use is as an aid to representative government and administration both in politics and industry. The demand for the assistance of expert reporters in the shape of accountants, statisticians, secretariats, and the like, comes not from the public, but from men doing public business, who can no longer do it by rule of thumb. It is in origin and in ideal an instrument for doing public business better, rather than an instrument for knowing better how badly public business is done.





2

2

作为一名普通公民，作为一名主权选民，没有人能够试图消化这些文件。但作为争议的一方，作为立法机构的委员，作为政府、企业或工会的官员，作为工业委员会的成员，关于具体问题的报告将越来越受欢迎。对某些事业感兴趣的普通公民将像现在一样加入自愿社团，这些社团雇用工作人员研究文件，并制作报告，以制衡官僚机构。新闻工作者、专家和政治学家将对这些材料进行一些研究。但局外人，我们每个人都是现代生活除少数方面以外的所有方面的局外人，既没有时间，也没有注意力，没有兴趣，也没有具体判断的能力。社会的日常管理必须依靠内部人员在健全的条件下工作。

As a private citizen, as a sovereign voter, no one could attempt to digest these documents. But as one party to a dispute, as a committeeman in a legislature, as an officer in government, business, or a trade union, as a member of an industrial council, reports on the specific matter at issue will be increasingly welcome. The private citizen interested in some cause would belong, as he does now, to voluntary societies which employed a staff to study the documents, and make reports that served as a check on officialdom. There would be some study of this material by newspaper men, and a good deal by experts and by political scientists. But the outsider, and every one of us is an outsider to all but a few aspects of modern life, has neither time, nor attention, nor interest, nor the equipment for specific judgment. It is on the men inside, working under conditions that are sound, that the daily administrations of society must rest.

外界公众只能根据事件发生后的结果和事件发生前的程序来判断这些条件是否合理。公众舆论得以持续行动的广泛原则本质上是程序原则。局外人可以请专家告诉他相关事实是否得到了充分考虑；在大多数情况下，他无法自己决定什么是相关的，什么是应有的考虑。局外人也许可以判断是否充分听取了与决定有关的团体的意见，投票（如果有的话）是否诚实地进行，也许可以判断结果是否被诚实地接受。当新闻表明有值得关注的事情时，他可以观察程序。如果程序的正常结果与他对美好生活的理想相冲突，他可以质疑程序本身是否正确。但如果他在每种情况下都试图用自己来代替程序，像戏剧危机中的天赐叔叔一样引入公众舆论，他就会弄巧成拙。他不会连续地跟上任何思路。

The general public outside can arrive at judgments about whether these conditions are sound only on the result after the event, and on the procedure before the event. The broad principles on which the action of public opinion can be continuous are essentially principles of procedure. The outsider can ask experts to tell him whether the relevant facts were duly considered; he cannot in most cases decide for himself what is relevant or what is due consideration. The outsider can perhaps judge whether the groups interested in the decision were properly heard, whether the ballot, if there was one, was honestly taken, and perhaps whether the result was honestly accepted. He can watch the procedure when the news indicates that there is something to watch. He can raise a question as to whether the procedure itself is right, if its normal results conflict with his ideal of a good life. But if he tries in every case to substitute himself for the procedure, to bring in Public Opinion like a providential uncle in the crisis of a play, he will confound his own confusion. He will not follow any train of thought consecutively.

因为在各种复杂问题上向公众呼吁的做法几乎总是意味着希望通过争取大多数没有机会知道的人来逃避那些知情人士的批评。判决取决于谁的声音最大或最迷人，谁是最熟练或最厚颜无耻的宣传人员，谁最能获得报纸上最多的版面。因为即使编辑对“另一方”一丝不苟地公平，公平还不够。可能还有其他几个方面，任何有组织的、有资金的和活跃的党派都没有提到。

For the practice of appealing to the public on all sorts of intricate matters means almost always a desire to escape criticism from those who know by enlisting a large majority which has had no chance to know. The verdict is made to depend on who has the loudest or the most entrancing voice, the most skilful or the most brazen publicity man, the best access to the most space in the newspapers. For even when the editor is scrupulously fair to "the other side," fairness is not enough. There may be several other sides, unmentioned by any of the organized, financed and active partisans.

被党派呼吁借用公众意见所困扰的普通公民，也许很快就会发现，这些呼吁不是对他智慧的赞美，而是对他善良本性的侮辱，是对他证据意识的侮辱。由于他的公民教育考虑到了他所处环境的复杂性，他会关心程序的公平性和健全性，甚至在大多数情况下，他也会希望他选出的代表能为他注意这一点。他将拒绝接受这些决定的负担，在大多数情况下，他会拒绝那些急于取胜、从会议桌前匆匆忙忙地向记者提供第一手消息的人。

The private citizen, beset by partisan appeals for the loan of his Public Opinion, will soon see, perhaps, that these appeals are not a compliment to his intelligence, but an imposition on his good nature and an insult to his sense of evidence. As his civic education takes account of the complexity of his environment, he will concern himself about the equity and the sanity of procedure, and even this he will in most cases expect his elected representative to watch for him. He will refuse himself to accept the burden of these decisions, and will turn down his thumbs in most cases on those who, in their hurry to win, rush from the conference table with the first dope for the reporters.

只有坚持问题在经过程序之前不会提交给他，现代国家的忙碌公民才有可能希望以一种可理解的方式处理这些问题。因为，正如党派人士所言，问题几乎总是由他观察到的一系列错综复杂的事实组成，周围是一大堆充满情绪的陈词滥调。按照当时的流行做法，他会从会议室走出来，坚持说他想要的是一些能满足灵魂的想法，如正义、福利、美国主义、社会主义。在这些问题上，外人有时会感到恐惧或钦佩，但绝不会感到评判。在他能对论点做任何事情之前，必须先把论点中的脂肪煮出来。

Only by insisting that problems shall not come up to him until they have passed through a procedure, can the busy citizen of a modern state hope to deal with them in a form that is intelligible. For issues, as they are stated by a partisan, almost always consist of an intricate series of facts, as he has observed them, surrounded by a large fatty mass of stereotyped phrases charged with his emotion. According to the fashion of the day, he will emerge from the conference room insisting that what he wants is some soulfilling idea like Justice, Welfare, Americanism, Socialism. On such issues the citizen outside can sometimes be provoked to fear or admiration, but to judgment never. Before he can do anything with the argument, the fat has to be boiled out of it for him.





3

3

可以通过让代表在某人（主席或调解人）在场的情况下进行讨论来实现这一点，该人会迫使讨论处理专家提供的分析。这是任何处理远距离事务的代表机构的基本组织。党派的声音应该存在，但党派应该发现自己面对的是没有亲自参与的人，他们掌握足够的事实，并具有辩证技能，能够从刻板印象、模式和阐述中分辨出什么是真实的看法。这是苏格拉底式的对话，苏格拉底用尽了所有精力来突破词语，找到意义，甚至更多，因为现代生活中的辩证法必须由探索过环境和人类思想的人来完成。

That can be done by having the representative inside carry on discussion in the presence of some one, chairman or mediator, who forces the discussion to deal with the analyses supplied by experts. This is the essential organization of any representative body dealing with distant matters. The partisan voices should be there, but the partisans should find themselves confronted with men, not personally involved, who control enough facts and have the dialectical skill to sort out what is real perception from what is stereotype, pattern and elaboration. It is the Socratic dialogue, with all of Socrates's energy for breaking through words to meanings, and something more than that, because the dialectic in modern life must be done by men who have explored the environment as well as the human mind.

例如，钢铁行业存在着一场严重的争端。双方都发表了充满最高理想的宣言。在这个阶段，唯一值得尊重的舆论是坚持召开会议的舆论。对于声称其事业太正义而不能被会议玷污的一方来说，他们几乎不会得到同情，因为凡人中没有这样的事业。也许那些反对会议的人并不是这么说的。也许他们说对方太邪恶了；他们不能和叛徒握手。舆论所能做的就是组织政府官员举行听证会，听取邪恶的证据。它不能相信党派的话。但假设同意召开一次会议，假设有一位中立的主席，他随时听候公司、工会和劳工部的顾问专家的差遣。
