There is, for example, a grave dispute in the steel industry. Each side issues a manifesto full of the highest ideals. The only public opinion that is worth respect at this stage is the opinion which insists that a conference be organized. For the side which says its cause is too just to be contaminated by conference there can be little sympathy, since there is no such cause anywhere among mortal men. Perhaps those who object to conference do not say quite that. Perhaps they say that the other side is too wicked; they cannot shake hands with traitors. All that public opinion can do then is to organize a hearing by public officials to hear the proof of wickedness. It cannot take the partisans' word for it. But suppose a conference is agreed to, and suppose there is a neutral chairman who has at his beck and call the consulting experts of the corporation, the union, and, let us say, the Department of Labor.

加里法官非常真诚地表示，他的工人工资很高，没有过度劳累，然后开始概述俄罗斯从彼得大帝时代到沙皇被谋杀的历史。福斯特先生站起来，同样真诚地表示，工人受到剥削，然后开始概述从拿撒勒的耶稣到亚伯拉罕·林肯的人类解放史。此时，主席要求情报人员提供工资表，以便用一张显示不同阶层工资的表格来代替“高薪”和“受剥削”这两个词。 加里法官认为他们所有人都薪水很高吗？他认为是的。福斯特先生认为他们所有人都受到剥削吗？不，他认为 C、M 和 X 组受到剥削。他所说的“受剥削”是什么意思？他的意思是他们没有得到足够的生活工资。加里法官说，他们确实受到剥削。主席问，一个人用这份工资能买到什么。福斯特先生说，什么也买不到。加里法官说，他需要的一切。主席查阅了政府的预算和价格统计数据。他裁定 X 可以满足平均预算，但 C 和 M 不能。加里法官发出通知，称他认为官方统计数据不合理。预算太高，价格却下降了。福斯特先生也发出了例外通知。预算太低，价格却上涨了。主席裁定，这一点不属于会议的管辖范围，官方数据仍然有效，加里法官的专家和福斯特先生的专家应向联邦情报局常务委员会提出上诉。

Judge Gary states with perfect sincerity that his men are well paid and not overworked, and then proceeds to sketch the history of Russia from the time of Peter the Great to the murder of the Czar. Mr. Foster rises, states with equal sincerity that the men are exploited, and then proceeds to outline the history of human emancipation from Jesus of Nazareth to Abraham Lincoln. At this point the chairman calls upon the intelligence men for wage tables in order to substitute for the words "well paid" and "exploited" a table showing what the different classes are paid. Does Judge Gary think they are all well paid? He does. Does Mr. Foster think they are all exploited? No, he thinks that groups C, M, and X are exploited. What does he mean by exploited? He means they are not paid a living wage. They are, says Judge Gary. What can a man buy on that wage, asks the chairman. Nothing, says Mr. Foster. Everything he needs, says Judge Gary. The chairman consults the budgets and price statistics of the government. He rules that X can meet an average budget, but that C and M cannot. Judge Gary serves notice that he does not regard the official statistics as sound. The budgets are too high, and prices have come down. Mr. Foster also serves notice of exception. The budget is too low, prices have gone up. The chairman rules that this point is not within the jurisdiction of the conference, that the official figures stand, and that Judge Gary's experts and Mr. Foster's should carry their appeals to the standing committee of the federated intelligence bureaus.

然而，法官加里说，如果我们改变这些工资标准，我们就会破产。主席问道，破产是什么意思？拿出你的账簿。法官加里说，我不能，它们是私人的。主席说，私人的东西我们不感兴趣，因此，他向公众发表声明，宣布 C 组和 M 组工人的工资远低于官方最低生活工资，法官加里拒绝提高工资，理由是他拒绝说明。经过这样的程序，就可以形成一种赞美意义上的公众舆论。

Nevertheless, says Judge Gary, we shall be ruined if we change these wage scales. What do you mean by ruined, asks the chairman, produce your books. I can't, they are private, says Judge Gary. What is private does not interest us, says the chairman, and, therefore, issues a statement to the public announcing that the wages of workers in groups C and M are so-and-so much below the official minimum living wage, and that Judge Gary declines to increase them for reasons that he refuses to state. After a procedure of that sort, a public opinion in the eulogistic sense of the term can exist.

专家调解的价值不在于它树立意见以胁迫党派，而在于它瓦解了党派之争。加里法官和福斯特先生可能仍然像刚开始时一样不相信，尽管他们不得不用不同的语气说话。但几乎所有没有个人纠缠的人都会避免被纠缠。因为这种辩证法解开了纠缠不清的刻板印象和口号，而他的反应是如此迅速。

The value of expert mediation is not that it sets up opinion to coerce the partisans, but that it disintegrates partisanship. Judge Gary and Mr. Foster may remain as little convinced as when they started, though even they would have to talk in a different strain. But almost everyone else who was not personally entangled would save himself from being entangled. For the entangling stereotypes and slogans to which his reflexes are so ready to respond are by this kind of dialectic untangled.





4

4

在许多具有重大公共意义的话题上，以及在不同程度上，在更私人的问题上，不同的人记忆和情感的线索都陷入了混乱。同一个词会表示许多不同的想法：情感从它们所属的图像转移到与这些图像的名称相似的名称。在思想中未被批判的部分，仅仅通过叮当声、接触和连续，就会产生大量的联想。有零散的情感依恋，有曾经是名字和面具的词语。在梦境、遐想和恐慌中，我们发现了一些混乱，足以看到天真的心灵是如何组成的，以及当它没有被清醒的努力和外部阻力所约束时，它是如何表现的。我们看到，没有比尘土飞扬的旧阁楼更自然的秩序了。事实、思想和情感之间经常存在着矛盾，就像歌剧院里的情况一样，如果把所有的服装都堆成一堆，把所有的乐谱都混在一起，那么蝴蝶夫人就会穿着女武神的服装，满怀诗意地等待浮士德的归来。“在圣诞节的时候，”一篇社论说，“往日的回忆软化了人心。当思绪回到童年时，神圣的教义就会重新被记起。透过半快乐半悲伤的回忆，现在与上帝同在的亲人，看世界似乎并不那么糟糕。没有一颗心能不受神秘影响……这个国家充斥着红色宣传——但有充足的绳索、肌肉和灯柱……当这个世界运转时，自由的精神将在人类的心中燃烧。”

On many subjects of great public importance, and in varying degree among different people for more personal matters, the threads of memory and emotion are in a snarl. The same word will connote any number of different ideas: emotions are displaced from the images to which they belong to names which resemble the names of these images. In the uncriticized parts of the mind there is a vast amount of association by mere clang, contact, and succession. There are stray emotional attachments, there are words that were names and are masks. In dreams, reveries, and panic, we uncover some of the disorder, enough to see how the naive mind is composed, and how it behaves when not disciplined by wakeful effort and external resistance. We see that there is no more natural order than in a dusty old attic. There is often the same incongruity between fact, idea, and emotion as there might be in an opera house, if all the wardrobes were dumped in a heap and all the scores mixed up, so that Madame Butterfly in a Valkyr's dress waited lyrically for the return of Faust. "At Christmas-tide" says an editorial, "old memories soften the heart. Holy teachings are remembered afresh as thoughts run back to childhood. The world does not seem so bad when seen through the mist of half-happy, half-sad recollections of loved ones now with God. No heart is untouched by the mysterious influence…. The country is honeycombed with red propaganda—but there is a good supply of ropes, muscles and lampposts… while this world moves the spirit of liberty will burn in the breast of man."

在脑海中找到这些短语的人需要帮助。他需要一个苏格拉底来分离这些单词，盘问他直到他定义它们，并将单词变成思想的名称。使它们意味着一个特定的对象，而不是其他任何东西。因为这些紧张的音节通过原始联想在他的脑海中联系在一起，并被他对圣诞节的记忆、他作为保守派的愤慨以及他作为革命传统继承者的激动所捆绑在一起。有时咆哮声太大太久远，无法快速解开。有时，就像在现代心理治疗中一样，记忆层层回溯到婴儿时期，必须将它们分开并命名。

The man who found these phrases in his mind needs help. He needs a Socrates who will separate the words, cross-examine him until he has defined them, and made words the names of ideas. Made them mean a particular object and nothing else. For these tense syllables have got themselves connected in his mind by primitive association, and are bundled together by his memories of Christmas, his indignation as a conservative, and his thrills as the heir to a revolutionary tradition. Sometimes the snarl is too huge and ancient for quick unravelling. Sometimes, as in modern psychotherapy, there are layers upon layers of memory reaching back to infancy, which have to be separated and named.

命名的效果，即说劳动群体 C 和 M（而不是 X）的报酬过低，而不是说劳动被剥削的效果，是深刻的。感知恢复了其身份，它们所引起的情感是特定的，因为它不再通过与从圣诞节到莫斯科的一切的大规模和偶然联系而得到强化。具有自己名称和经过仔细审查的情感的解开的想法更容易通过问题中的新数据进行纠正。它已经嵌入整个人格中，与整个自我有某种联系：挑战将在整个灵魂中回荡。在彻底批评之后，这个想法不再是我 ，而是那个 。它被客观化了，它遥不可及。它的命运与我的命运无关，而是与我所行动的外部世界的命运有关。

The effect of naming, the effect, that is, of saying that the labor groups C and M, but not X, are underpaid, instead of saying that Labor is Exploited, is incisive. Perceptions recover their identity, and the emotion they arouse is specific, since it is no longer reinforced by large and accidental connections with everything from Christmas to Moscow. The disentangled idea with a name of its own, and an emotion that has been scrutinized, is ever so much more open to correction by new data in the problem. It had been imbedded in the whole personality, had affiliations of some sort with the whole ego: a challenge would reverberate through the whole soul. After it has been thoroughly criticized, the idea is no longer me but that . It is objectified, it is at arm's length. Its fate is not bound up with my fate, but with the fate of the outer world upon which I am acting.





5

5

这种再教育将有助于使我们的公众舆论与环境相适应。这就是消除庞大的审查、定型和戏剧化手段的方法。如果很容易了解相关环境，批评家、教师、医生就可以解开思想的谜团。但是，如果环境对分析师和他的学生来说都一样模糊，那么任何分析技术都不够用。需要情报工作。在政治和工业问题上，批评家本身可以做一些事情，但除非他能指望从专家记者那里得到对环境的有效描述，否则他的辩证法就走不远。

Re-education of this kind will help to bring our public opinions into grip with the environment. That is the way the enormous censoring, stereotyping, and dramatizing apparatus can be liquidated. Where there is no difficulty in knowing what the relevant environment is, the critic, the teacher, the physician, can unravel the mind. But where the environment is as obscure to the analyst as to his pupil, no analytic technic is sufficient. Intelligence work is required. In political and industrial problems the critic as such can do something, but unless he can count upon receiving from expert reporters a valid picture of the environment, his dialectic cannot go far.

因此，尽管在这里，就像在大多数其他事情中一样，“教育”是终极解决方案，但这种教育的价值将取决于知识的发展。而我们对人类制度的了解仍然极其贫乏和印象主义。社会知识的收集总体上仍然是杂乱无章的；它不会成为行动的正常伴随物，而这必然会成为行动的正常伴随物。然而，可以肯定的是，信息的收集不会是为了最终的用途。之所以收集信息，是因为现代决策需要这样做。但在收集信息的过程中，会积累大量的数据，政治科学可以将其转化为概括，并为学校构建出一幅概念性的世界图景。当这幅图景成形时，公民教育就可以成为应对看不见的环境的准备。

Therefore, though here, as in most other matters, "education" is the supreme remedy, the value of this education will depend upon the evolution of knowledge. And our knowledge of human institutions is still extraordinarily meager and impressionistic. The gathering of social knowledge is, on the whole, still haphazard; not, as it will have to become, the normal accompaniment of action. And yet the collection of information will not be made, one may be sure, for the sake of its ultimate use. It will be made because modern decision requires it to be made. But as it is being made, there will accumulate a body of data which political science can turn into generalization, and build up for the schools into a conceptual picture of the world. When that picture takes form, civic education can become a preparation for dealing with an unseen environment.

当教师掌握了社会制度的工作模型后，他可以利用它让学生敏锐地意识到自己的思维是如何处理不熟悉的事实的。除非他有这样的模型，否则教师无法指望让人们充分做好面对他们将要发现的世界的准备。他能做的是让他们做好准备，以更成熟的思维方式来应对这个世界。他可以通过案例教学法，教会学生检查信息来源的习惯。例如，他可以教学生在报纸上查找电报的发稿地点、记者姓名、新闻社名称、声明的授权机构、声明的背景。他可以教学生自问记者是否看到了他所描述的内容，并记住记者如何描述过去的其他事件。他可以教学生审查制度的性质、隐私的概念，并向他提供过去宣传的知识。通过正确使用历史，他可以让他意识到刻板印象，并培养对印刷文字所唤起的意象进行内省的习惯。通过比较历史和人类学课程，他可以培养终身的认识，即代码如何将特殊的模式强加于想象力。他可以教人们发现自己在编造寓言、戏剧化关系和拟人化抽象。他可以向学生展示他如何将自己与这些寓言联系起来，如何产生兴趣，以及如何选择在持有特定观点时采取的英雄、浪漫、经济的态度。对错误的研究不仅具有最高程度的预防作用，而且可以作为对真理研究的激励性介绍。随着我们的思想越来越深刻地意识到自己的主观主义，我们会发现客观方法的热情，而这种热情是其他方法所没有的。我们清楚地看到了我们的偏见的巨大危害和随意的残忍，而通常我们不应该看到这一点。而消除偏见，虽然一开始会很痛苦，因为它与我们的自尊有关，但一旦成功，就会带来极大的解脱和自豪感。注意力的范围会大大扩大。随着现有范畴的消失，一个僵硬、简单的世界观就瓦解了。场景变得生动而充实。随之而来的是情感上的激励，促使人们由衷地欣赏科学方法，否则这种激励很难激发，也不可能维持下去。偏见要容易得多，也更有趣。因为如果你把科学原理当作一直被接受的东西来教授，那么它们作为一门学科的主要优点，即客观性，就会使它们变得乏味。但一开始要把它们当作战胜思想迷信的胜利来教授，追逐和征服的兴奋可能会让学生从自我束缚的经历过渡到好奇心成熟的阶段，他的理智也获得了激情。

As a working model of the social system becomes available to the teacher, he can use it to make the pupil acutely aware of how his mind works on unfamiliar facts. Until he has such a model, the teacher cannot hope to prepare men fully for the world they will find. What he can do is to prepare them to deal with that world with a great deal more sophistication about their own minds. He can, by the use of the case method, teach the pupil the habit of examining the sources of his information. He can teach him, for example, to look in his newspaper for the place where the dispatch was filed, for the name of the correspondent, the name of the press service, the authority given for the statement, the circumstances under which the statement was secured. He can teach the pupil to ask himself whether the reporter saw what he describes, and to remember how that reporter described other events in the past. He can teach him the character of censorship, of the idea of privacy, and furnish him with knowledge of past propaganda. He can, by the proper use of history, make him aware of the stereotype, and can educate a habit of introspection about the imagery evoked by printed words. He can, by courses in comparative history and anthropology, produce a life-long realization of the way codes impose a special pattern upon the imagination. He can teach men to catch themselves making allegories, dramatizing relations, and personifying abstractions. He can show the pupil how he identifies himself with these allegories, how he becomes interested, and how he selects the attitude, heroic, romantic, economic which he adopts while holding a particular opinion. The study of error is not only in the highest degree prophylactic, but it serves as a stimulating introduction to the study of truth. As our minds become more deeply aware of their own subjectivism, we find a zest in objective method that is not otherwise there. We see vividly, as normally we should not, the enormous mischief and casual cruelty of our prejudices. And the destruction of a prejudice, though painful at first, because of its connection with our self-respect, gives an immense relief and a fine pride when it is successfully done. There is a radical enlargement of the range of attention. As the current categories dissolve, a hard, simple version of the world breaks up. The scene turns vivid and full. There follows an emotional incentive to hearty appreciation of scientific method, which otherwise it is not easy to arouse, and is impossible to sustain. Prejudices are so much easier and more interesting. For if you teach the principles of science as if they had always been accepted, their chief virtue as a discipline, which is objectivity, will make them dull. But teach them at first as victories over the superstitions of the mind, and the exhilaration of the chase and of the conquest may carry the pupil over that hard transition from his own self-bound experience to the phase where his curiosity has matured, and his reason has acquired passion.

第二十八章

CHAPTER XXVIII

诉诸理性

THE APPEAL TO REASON





1

1

我曾为这本书写过几个结尾，但后来又都扔掉了。所有这些结尾都笼罩着最后一章的宿命，似乎每个想法都找到了自己的位置，所有作者没有忘记的谜团都解开了。在政治中，英雄不会从此过上幸福的生活，也不会完美地结束自己的一生。没有结局章节，因为政治中的英雄面前的未来比他身后的历史还要多。最后一章只是作者想象礼貌的读者已经开始偷偷看手表的地方。

I HAVE written, and then thrown away, several endings to this book. Over all of them there hung that fatality of last chapters, in which every idea seems to find its place, and all the mysteries, that the writer has not forgotten, are unravelled. In politics the hero does not live happily ever after, or end his life perfectly. There is no concluding chapter, because the hero in politics has more future before him than there is recorded history behind him. The last chapter is merely a place where the writer imagines that the polite reader has begun to look furtively at his watch.





2

2

当柏拉图说到他应该总结的时候，他的自信变成了怯场，因为他觉得说出他内心关于理性在政治中的地位听起来是多么荒谬。《理想国》第五卷中的这些句子甚至连柏拉图都难以说出；它们是如此纯粹和鲜明，以至于人们既不能忘记它们，也不能靠它们生活。所以他让苏格拉底对格劳孔说，他将因说出“什么样的最小变化才能使一个国家转变为更真实的形式”而被笑死，因为他“很想说出，如果不是太夸张的话”的想法是“直到哲学家成为国王，或者这个世界的国王和王子拥有哲学的精神和力量，政治伟大和智慧融为一体……城市永远不会停止邪恶，——不会，人类也不会……”

When Plato came to the point where it was fitting that he should sum up, his assurance turned into stage-fright as he thought how absurd it would sound to say what was in him about the place of reason in politics. Those sentences in book five of the Republic were hard even for Plato to speak; they are so sheer and so stark that men can neither forget them nor live by them. So he makes Socrates say to Glaucon that he will be broken and drowned in laughter for telling "what is the least change which will enable a state to pass into the truer form," because the thought he "would fain have uttered if it had not seemed too extravagant" was that "until philosophers are kings, or the kings and princes of this world have the spirit and power of philosophy, and political greatness and wisdom meet in one… cities will never cease from ill,—no, nor the human race…"

他刚说出这些可怕的话，就意识到这是完美的忠告，并为自己的想法无法企及的宏伟感到尴尬。于是他赶紧补充说，当然，“真正的领航员”将被称为“喋喋不休的人、观星者、一无是处的人”。但是，这种若有所思的承认，虽然可以保护他免受希腊人对他缺乏幽默感的指控，但却为严肃的想法提供了令人羞辱的结尾。他变得挑衅起来，警告阿德曼图斯，他必须“把哲学家的无用归咎于那些不使用哲学家的人，而不是他们自己的过错。领航员不应该谦卑地请求水手们听从他的指挥——这不是自然规律。”带着这种傲慢的姿态，他匆匆拿起理性的工具，消失在学院里，把世界留给了马基雅维利。

Hardly had he said these awful words, when he realized they were a counsel of perfection, and felt embarrassed at the unapproachable grandeur of his idea. So he hastens to add that, of course, "the true pilot" will be called "a prater, a star-gazer, a good-for-nothing." But this wistful admission, though it protects him against whatever was the Greek equivalent for the charge that he lacked a sense of humor, furnished a humiliating tailpiece to a solemn thought. He becomes defiant and warns Adeimantus that he must "attribute the uselessness" of philosophers "to the fault of those who will not use them, and not to themselves. The pilot should not humbly beg the sailors to be commanded by him—that is not the order of nature." And with this haughty gesture, he hurriedly picked up the tools of reason, and disappeared into the Academy, leaving the world to Machiavelli.

因此，在理性与政治的第一次重大交锋中，理性的策略是愤怒地退却。但与此同时，正如柏拉图告诉我们的那样，船在海上。自柏拉图写作以来，海上有许多船只，而今天，无论我们的信念是明智还是愚蠢，我们都不能仅仅因为一个人知道如何“关注年份、季节、天空、星星和风，以及属于他的艺术的一切”就称他为真正的领航员。他不能忽视让那艘船顺利航行所需的一切。因为船上有叛乱者，他不能说：这对我们所有人来说都很糟糕……我不应该处理叛乱，这不符合自然规律……我不应该考虑叛乱……我知道如何航行……我不知道如何驾驶一艘满载水手的船……如果他们不认为我是掌舵人，我也没办法。我们都会触礁，他们将为自己的罪孽受到惩罚；我确信我更了解……

Thus, in the first great encounter between reason and politics, the strategy of reason was to retire in anger. But meanwhile, as Plato tells us, the ship is at sea. There have been many ships on the sea, since Plato wrote, and to-day, whether we are wise or foolish in our belief, we could no longer call a man a true pilot, simply because he knows how to "pay attention to the year and seasons and sky and stars and winds, and whatever else belongs to his art." He can dismiss nothing which is necessary to make that ship sail prosperously. Because there are mutineers aboard, he cannot say: so much the worse for us all… it is not in the order of nature that I should handle a mutiny… it is not in the order of philosophy that I should consider mutiny… I know how to navigate… I do not know how to navigate a ship full of sailors… and if they do not see that I am the man to steer, I cannot help it. We shall all go on the rocks, they to be punished for their sins; I, with the assurance that I knew better….





3

3

每当我们在政治上诉诸理性时，这个寓言中的困难就会重现。因为用理性的方法来处理一个不讲道理的世界本身就很困难。即使你和柏拉图一样认为真正的领航员知道什么对船最好，你也必须记住，他并不是那么容易被识别的，而且这种不确定性让大部分船员不相信。根据定义，船员不知道他所知道的，而领航员被星星和风迷住了，不知道如何让船员认识到他所知道的东西的重要性。在海上叛乱期间，没有时间让每个水手成为专家中的专家。领航员也没有时间咨询他的船员，看看他是否真的像他认为的那样聪明。因为教育需要几年的时间，紧急情况只需要几个小时。那么，告诉领航员，真正的补救措施是，例如，一种能让水手更好地掌握证据的教育，那就完全是学术性的了。你只能告诉陆地上的船长这一点。在危机中，唯一的建议是使用枪支，或发表演讲，喊出激动人心的口号，提出妥协，使用任何可用的快速手段来平息叛乱，证据就是证据。只有在岸上，人们计划进行多次航行，他们才有能力，也必须为了自己的救赎，处理那些需要很长时间才能消除的原因。他们将在几年和几代人的时间里处理，而不仅仅是在紧急情况下。没有什么比区分假危机和真危机更能考验他们的智慧了。因为当空气中弥漫着恐慌，一个危机接踵而至，真实的危险与想象的恐惧混杂在一起时，根本没有机会建设性地运用理性，任何秩序很快就会显得比任何混乱都好。

Whenever we make an appeal to reason in politics, the difficulty in this parable recurs. For there is an inherent difficulty about using the method of reason to deal with an unreasoning world. Even if you assume with Plato that the true pilot knows what is best for the ship, you have to recall that he is not so easy to recognize, and that this uncertainty leaves a large part of the crew unconvinced. By definition the crew does not know what he knows, and the pilot, fascinated by the stars and winds, does not know how to make the crew realize the importance of what he knows. There is no time during mutiny at sea to make each sailor an expert judge of experts. There is no time for the pilot to consult his crew and find out whether he is really as wise as he thinks he is. For education is a matter of years, the emergency a matter of hours. It would be altogether academic, then, to tell the pilot that the true remedy is, for example, an education that will endow sailors with a better sense of evidence. You can tell that only to shipmasters on dry land. In the crisis, the only advice is to use a gun, or make a speech, utter a stirring slogan, offer a compromise, employ any quick means available to quell the mutiny, the sense of evidence being what it is. It is only on shore where men plan for many voyages, that they can afford to, and must for their own salvation, deal with those causes that take a long time to remove. They will be dealing in years and generations, not in emergencies alone. And nothing will put a greater strain upon their wisdom than the necessity of distinguishing false crises from real ones. For when there is panic in the air, with one crisis tripping over the heels of another, actual dangers mixed with imaginary scares, there is no chance at all for the constructive use of reason, and any order soon seems preferable to any disorder.

只有在长期稳定的前提下，人们才有可能遵循理性的方法。这并不是因为人类无能，也不是因为诉诸理性是空想，而是因为政治主题上的理性发展才刚刚开始。我们在政治上的理性观念仍然是庞大而单薄的概括，过于抽象和粗略，无法提供实际指导，除非总量大到足以抵消个人特质并表现出很大的一致性。政治上的理性在预测个人行为方面尤其不成熟，因为在人类行为中，最小的初始变化往往会产生最复杂的差异。也许这就是为什么当我们试图在处理突发情况时仅仅坚持诉诸理性时，我们会被打败并被笑死。

It is only on the premise of a certain stability over a long run of time that men can hope to follow the method of reason. This is not because mankind is inept, or because the appeal to reason is visionary, but because the evolution of reason on political subjects is only in its beginnings. Our rational ideas in politics are still large, thin generalities, much too abstract and unrefined for practical guidance, except where the aggregates are large enough to cancel out individual peculiarity and exhibit large uniformities. Reason in politics is especially immature in predicting the behavior of individual men, because in human conduct the smallest initial variation often works out into the most elaborate differences. That, perhaps, is why when we try to insist solely upon an appeal to reason in dealing with sudden situations, we are broken and drowned in laughter.





4

4

因为我们拥有的理性本身的发展速度比采取行动的速度要慢。因此，在政治科学的现状下，一种情况在被清楚地理解之前就倾向于转变为另一种情况，因此，政治批评大多是事后诸葛亮，其他的就不多。无论是在发现未知事物时，还是在传播已被证实的事物时，都存在时间差异，政治哲学家应该比以往任何时候都更加关注这一差异。我们已经开始研究看不见的环境对我们观点的影响，主要是在格雷厄姆·沃拉斯先生的启发下。我们目前还不了解政治中的时间因素，除了一点点经验法则，尽管它与任何建设性建议的可行性有着最直接的关系。例如，我们可以看到，任何计划的相关性在某种程度上都取决于行动所需的时间长度。因为时间的长短将决定计划假设的数据是否真的保持不变。这里有一个因素，现实和经验丰富的人确实会考虑到，这有助于以某种方式将他们与机会主义者、空想家、庸人和学究区分开来。但目前我们还不知道时间计算是如何以任何系统的方式进入政治的。

For the rate at which reason, as we possess it, can advance itself is slower than the rate at which action has to be taken. In the present state of political science there is, therefore, a tendency for one situation to change into another, before the first is clearly understood, and so to make much political criticism hindsight and little else. Both in the discovery of what is unknown, and in the propagation of that which has been proved, there is a time-differential, which ought to, in a much greater degree than it ever has, occupy the political philosopher. We have begun, chiefly under the inspiration of Mr. Graham Wallas, to examine the effect of an invisible environment upon our opinions. We do not, as yet, understand, except a little by rule of thumb, the element of time in politics, though it bears most directly upon the practicability of any constructive proposal. We can see, for example, that somehow the relevancy of any plan depends upon the length of time the operation requires. Because on the length of time it will depend whether the data which the plan assumes as given, will in truth remain the same. There is a factor here which realistic and experienced men do take into account, and it helps to mark them off somehow from the opportunist, the visionary, the philistine and the pedant. But just how the calculation of time enters into politics we do not know at present in any systematic way.

在我们更清楚地理解这些问题之前，我们至少可以记住，存在一个在理论上极其困难、在实践上也极为重要的问题。这将帮助我们珍惜柏拉图的理想，而不赞同他关于不听从理性的人的乖僻的草率结论。在政治上服从理性是困难的，因为你试图让两个进程一起前进，而这两个进程目前还具有不同的步调和速度。在理性变得微妙和具体之前，政治的直接斗争将继续需要一定数量的天生的智慧、力量和无法证实的信念，而这些是理性既不能提供也不能控制的，因为生活的事实太过单一，超出了理性的理解能力。社会科学的方法还很不完善，以至于在许多严肃的决定和大多数随意的决定中，目前还没有选择，只能按照直觉的提示与命运赌一把。

Until we understand these matters more clearly, we can at least remember that there is a problem of the utmost theoretical difficulty and practical consequence. It will help us to cherish Plato's ideal, without sharing his hasty conclusion about the perversity of those who do not listen to reason. It is hard to obey reason in politics, because you are trying to make two processes march together, which have as yet a different gait and a different pace. Until reason is subtle and particular, the immediate struggle of politics will continue to require an amount of native wit, force, and unprovable faith, that reason can neither provide nor control, because the facts of life are too undifferentiated for its powers of understanding. The methods of social science are so little perfected that in many of the serious decisions and most of the casual ones, there is as yet no choice but to gamble with fate as intuition prompts.

但是，我们可以把对理性的信仰变成直觉之一。我们可以用我们的智慧和力量为理性找到立足点。在我们对世界的描绘背后，我们可以试图看到更长事件持续时间的远景，只要有可能摆脱紧迫的现实，就让这段更长的时间来控制我们的决定。然而，即使我们有这种让未来发挥作用的意愿，我们还是一次又一次地发现，我们不知道如何根据理性的指示行事。理性准备指示的人类问题数量很少。

But we can make a belief in reason one of those intuitions. We can use our wit and our force to make footholds for reason. Behind our pictures of the world, we can try to see the vista of a longer duration of events, and wherever it is possible to escape from the urgent present, allow this longer time to control our decisions. And yet, even when there is this will to let the future count, we find again and again that we do not know for certain how to act according to the dictates of reason. The number of human problems on which reason is prepared to dictate is small.





5

5

然而，这种慈善行为源自自我认知，以及我们这个群居物种中没有一个人在渴望一个更加友好的世界，这种信念是无可争辩的。人们彼此之间做出的许多鬼脸动作都只是随着脉搏的跳动而消失，因此它们并非全部都重要。在如此多不确定因素、如此多行动必须基于猜测的情况下，对单纯体面的储备要求是巨大的，我们必须像善意会起作用一样生活。我们无法证明它在每个例子中都会起作用，也无法证明为什么仇恨、不宽容、怀疑、偏执、保密、恐惧和撒谎是反对公众舆论的七宗罪。我们只能坚持认为，它们在诉诸理性时毫无用处，从长远来看，它们是一种毒药；如果我们坚持一种比我们自己的困境和生命更持久的世界观，我们就会对这些产生强烈的偏见。

There is, however, a noble counterfeit in that charity which comes from self-knowledge and an unarguable belief that no one of our gregarious species is alone in his longing for a friendlier world. So many of the grimaces men make at each other go with a flutter of their pulse, that they are not all of them important. And where so much is uncertain, where so many actions have to be carried out on guesses, the demand upon the reserves of mere decency is enormous, and it is necessary to live as if good will would work. We cannot prove in every instance that it will, nor why hatred, intolerance, suspicion, bigotry, secrecy, fear, and lying are the seven deadly sins against public opinion. We can only insist that they have no place in the appeal to reason, that in the longer run they are a poison; and taking our stand upon a view of the world which outlasts our own predicaments, and our own lives, we can cherish a hearty prejudice against them.

如果我们不让恐惧和狂热深深地影响我们，以至于我们因为对人类的未来失去信心而恼怒地举手投降，对长远的未来失去兴趣，那么我们就能做得更好。这种绝望是没有理由的，因为正如詹姆斯所说，我们的命运所依赖的所有假设都 像以往一样充满意义。我们已经看到了残酷，而且因为它很奇怪，所以它不是决定性的。1914 年至 1919 年，那只是柏林、莫斯科、凡尔赛，而不是我们夸张地说的世界末日。人们越是现实地面对残酷和歇斯底里，他们就越有权说，人们因为又一场大战而相信智慧、勇气和努力永远无法为所有人创造美好的生活，这并不是愚蠢的。

We can do this all the better if we do not allow frightfulness and fanaticism to impress us so deeply that we throw up our hands peevishly, and lose interest in the longer run of time because we have lost faith in the future of man. There is no ground for this despair, because all the ifs on which, as James said, our destiny hangs, are as pregnant as they ever were. What we have seen of brutality, we have seen, and because it was strange, it was not conclusive. It was only Berlin, Moscow, Versailles in 1914 to 1919, not Armageddon, as we rhetorically said. The more realistically men have faced out the brutality and the hysteria, the more they have earned the right to say that it is not foolish for men to believe, because another great war took place, that intelligence, courage and effort cannot ever contrive a good life for all men.

尽管恐怖十分严重，但并非普遍现象。有腐败的，也有廉洁的。有混乱的，也有奇迹的。有弥天大谎。也有人有意愿揭露谎言。这不是判断，而是一种情绪，当人们否认某些人曾经是，更多的人，最终是足够多的人，可能会是。你可以对从未发生过的事情感到绝望。你可以对有三个脑袋感到绝望，尽管萧伯纳甚至拒绝对此感到绝望。但你不能对人类所表现出的任何人类品质可能存在的可能性感到绝望。如果在这十年的所有罪恶中，你还没有看到你想增加的男人和女人，以及已知的时刻，上帝自己也帮不了你。

Great as was the horror, it was not universal. There were corrupt, and there were incorruptible. There was muddle and there were miracles. There was huge lying. There were men with the will to uncover it. It is no judgment, but only a mood, when men deny that what some men have been, more men, and ultimately enough men, might be. You can despair of what has never been. You can despair of ever having three heads, though Mr. Shaw has declined to despair even of that. But you cannot despair of the possibilities that could exist by virtue of any human quality which a human being has exhibited. And if amidst all the evils of this decade, you have not seen men and women, known moments that you would like to multiply, the Lord himself cannot help you.
